(**Product attributes can be picture swatches (product-attributes-for-shop v0.1.6, core v0.5.554).** New `IMAGE` control type: values are offered as picture tiles on the storefront filter, with the picture stored in the existing `swatch` column (hex for SWATCH, media url for IMAGE) rather than a new one. New `migrations/003_image_control_type.sql` (CHECK widened only), `lib/media-folder.ts` filing pictures under `shop / attributes / <attribute name>` because a value is shop-wide vocabulary rather than one product's, `lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts` on `core.media-reference-rewriters`, and a shared `SwatchImagePicker`. `requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.426 → 0.5.493 and `shop` 0.1.38 → 0.1.65 - see the module's "Picture swatches" entry.) (**GLB files that carry their own animation now play it in the 3D viewer (working tree, product-3d-views-for-shop, unreleased).** `parseRaw()` keeps `gltf.animations` on the returned scene so the clips survive `loadModel`'s clone, and `Viewer3d.tsx` drives them with an `AnimationMixer` + `Clock` in the existing rAF loop, gated on the reduced-motion check but not on the touch latch - see the module's "Baked GLB animations" entry.) (**Attribute values can be added from the product and variation editors (working tree, product-attributes-for-shop 0.1.5, unreleased).** New `AddValueBox` under each attribute on the product's Attributes tab and a `+ New value…` option in each Variations-tab cell, both POSTing `attributes/[id]/values` with the new `reuseExisting: true` flag (duplicate label returns the existing row rather than 409; the response now carries the whole value). Values stay shop-wide on purpose and are written immediately rather than on the product's Save - see the module's "Values added in context" entry.) (**Media pickers are folder-aware and open at the product's folder (working tree, shop + shop-variations + product-3d-views-for-shop).** Shop's `MediaPickerModal` and the 3D `Model3dPickerModal` browse per-folder with breadcrumb/subfolders/all-folder search; new look-only `findProductMediaFolderId` in shop, `GET` on shop's `media-folder` route, new 3D module route `GET .../models/folder` - see the product image filing and 3D column entries.) (**Every 3D format is now lit by one lighting model (working tree, product-3d-views-for-shop, unreleased).** New exported `normaliseMaterials(root, format)` in `lib/three/load-model.ts`, called from `parse()` so it runs once per file on the cached master, before any clone is handed out. Only GLTFLoader returns PBR materials; OBJLoader, FBXLoader and TDSLoader all return `MeshPhongMaterial`, which does not conserve energy (no 1/pi on the diffuse term, so roughly 3x the light for the same albedo under `addLights`) and is not driven by `scene.environment`/`environmentIntensity` on the same terms - hence "some models are much brighter" and a sitewide environment slider that moved the GLBs and not the rest. Phong and Lambert are converted to `MeshStandardMaterial`: `name` carried across (the fabric configurator's contract - see `applyFabricPaint`), `roughness` derived from `shininess` via `sqrt(2/(shininess+2))` clamped to [0.05, 1], `metalness` hard 0 (never guessed - metalness 1 kills the diffuse term and renders the part black), plus colour, emissive, the eight shared texture slots and the base flags (`flatShading`/`vertexColors` matter, OBJLoader sets both from the file). Standard, Physical, Basic (KHR_materials_unlit) and the Line/Points materials OBJLoader returns for non-mesh geometry are left alone. OBJ is a special case: it never gets its `.mtl`, so its materials are the loader's invention rather than the file's intent, and are given a house default of `0xcccccc` at roughness 0.6 - pure white is the one albedo that always clips. Source materials are memoised so one shared material converts once. Covered by new `lib/three/normalise-materials.test.ts` (16 tests). Editor help text and the wiki now say OBJ shows in plain grey.) (**The per-product Viewer brightness slider now has a live preview under it (product-3d-views-for-shop v0.1.33).** Ticking **Set a brightness just for this product** mounts a real `Viewer3d` beneath the slider, on the product's own first model (else the first variation's), lit by the whole sitewide config with the override dropped over the top - so the brightness can be judged rather than guessed. Three changes: the admin settings route returns the whole `P3dConfig` as `site` rather than two fields; `Viewer3d` mirrors `settings.exposure` onto the live renderer in its own effect, since its build effect deliberately ignores `settings` and a rebuild per slider step would re-download the model; `Product3dEditor` keeps the tree's models in one `treeModels` state so the list and the preview both derive from it. Preview is mounted only while the override is ticked.) (**Removing a 3D model no longer deletes a file something else is using (product-3d-views-for-shop v0.1.32).** New `p3d_models.owns_media` bool (migration `005_owns_media.sql`, default false, backfilled from `media_key LIKE '%/3d/%'`); `deleteModelCascade` deletes the `Media` row and blob only when the row owns the file and no other row names it by media id, key or url. Fixes a live data loss: one object attached to a product and a variation is two rows, and removing either used to delete the object. Also stops a file picked from the media library being deleted out of the owner's library. Tested in `lib/db/models.test.ts`.) (**A material part can be given a fixed colour and a texture rotation (working tree, product-3d-views-for-shop, unreleased).** Two new per-slot fields on `FabricConfig` (`lib/db/fabric-config.ts`), both zod-defaulted so saved configs read back unchanged: `colourManual` and `rotationDeg`. **Colour from** now offers **Manual** (sentinel `MANUAL_COLOUR_ID = '__manual_colour'`, `lib/fabric/constants.ts`, alongside the new shared `parseHexColour`): the part is painted one flat `#rrggbb` typed by the admin instead of following a shopper's option, for a frame or a leg the shopper gets no say in. **Rotation** (degrees, on every texture-driven part) turns that part's texture about the middle of its tile, for a grain or weave that came out of the modelling software lying the wrong way round. `FabricBundle` slots gained `colour: string | null` and `rotationDeg`; `applyFabricPaint` (`lib/three/load-model.ts`) drops the material's baseColour map and copies the colour in for a flat part, and adds the turn to the texture's existing rotation with `center` at 0.5/0.5 for a textured one. Resolver, admin preview and the thumbnail stage all go through the same bundle, so the preview matches the storefront. No migration - the config is one jsonb blob.) (**Viewer brightness can now be set per product (working tree, product-3d-views-for-shop v0.1.30, unreleased).** New table `p3d_product_settings` (migration `004_product_settings.sql`): one row per parent product, `config` jsonb of viewer-setting overrides - today only `exposure` (nullable; null = sitewide value). `lib/db/product-settings.ts` (`P3dProductConfigSchema`, `applyProductOverrides`) merges it over the sitewide config in the gallery provider and the fabric admin route, so viewer, thumbnails and material-configurator preview all see one resolved `P3dConfig`. Admin API `GET/PUT /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/settings` (gate `shop.products`). UI: "Viewer brightness" panel on the product editor 3D views tab, debounced save-as-you-go, greyed while sitewide colour handling is None; sitewide Brightness stays as the catalogue default. Backup round-trip PASS for real.) (**The 3D "Fabric configurator" is now the "Material configurator", and a part's swatch size can be typed in by hand.** Admin-copy rename only in `product-3d-views-for-shop/components/admin/FabricConfigPanel.tsx` (heading, intro, "Material parts", "+ Add material part", "Save material configuration", detect/save messages, "texture scale measured") - the product covers wood, laminate and metal finishes, not just cloth, and the old wording read as fabric-only. Every stored name is unchanged (`FabricConfig`, `p3d_fabric_configs`, `lib/fabric/*`), so no migration and no data touched. Alongside it, the per-slot **Size from** dropdown gained **Manual**: `sizeAttributeId` may now hold the sentinel `MANUAL_SIZE_ID` (`'__manual'`, new leaf file `lib/fabric/constants.ts`, kept out of `lib/db/fabric-config.ts` so the client panel does not pull prisma into the bundle) with the typed value in the new `sizeManual` slot field (zod-defaulted `''`, so every saved config reads back unchanged). `composeFabricBundle` reads `sizeManual` through the same `parseSwatchCm` as an attribute label, empty → repeat 1. **Overall height from** took the same treatment (`heightAttributeId` accepts the sentinel, value in the new `heightManual`), and with every measurement now typeable the panel's old `attributes.length === 0` early-return is **gone** - a site without product-attributes installed can configure the lot by hand, and a new material part defaults to Manual when there are no attributes to offer. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.29**, core **v0.5.544** (re-pin).) **The beside option layout dropped its choices onto their own line the moment they wrapped.** A flex container breaks its lines from each item's *hypothetical* size (content width, so the whole unwrapped button row) and only shrinks what already landed on the line - so the choices div was measured at full width, found not to fit beside the name, and pushed below it: the stacked layout `beside` exists to avoid. `flex: 1 1 0` + `min-width: 0` on it (beside only) bases it at zero, so it always shares the line and wraps inside itself. The name also moved from `align-items: center` to `flex-start` + `padding-top: 0.5rem` (the pill's own top padding plus border), so it heads the first row rather than floating against the middle of a multi-line stack. Released: shop-variations **v0.1.43**, core **v0.5.545** (re-pin).) **The beside option layout kept its wrapped rows in a column beside the name, wasting the space under it.** v0.5.545 stopped the choices being pushed below the name, but they were still a flex item, so every wrapped row started under the first choice. Flex cannot do what this needs in either direction - measured at full unwrapped width it drops below the name, and once beside it a flex container is a block formatting context, so a float shoves it aside whole instead of letting it flow around. The name is now `float: left` in a `flow-root` container with the choices inline-level, so the first row clears the name and every row after it runs the full width, text wrapping around an image. Knock-ons: the choices' `gap` moves onto the buttons as margins (`gap` does nothing to inline layout), buttons take `vertical-align: top` so an image swatch cannot drag its row about, and containment is `flow-root` not `overflow: hidden` - hidden would clip the image swatch's hover peek. Released: shop-variations **v0.1.44**, core **v0.5.546** (re-pin). Previously:   **Download links now open in a new tab.** `DownloadItem` (`product-downloads-for-shop/components/public/DownloadsPanel.tsx`) gained `target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"` - the response's `Content-Disposition: attachment` already stops the browser navigating, same tab or new, so the old behaviour just dropped the shopper off the product page for nothing. Released: product-downloads-for-shop **v0.1.3**, core **v0.5.542** (re-pin). Also: **the two chiro-plus chair rows already broken by the earlier stale-key bug were repaired directly against the live Deskwell DB** (`pdl_files.media_key`/`url`/`media_provider` reset to match their `Media` row - the exact write `withFreshStorage` makes, done by hand because a shopper had no reason to wait for the deploy).) **The Shop: Variant Options block can put an option's name beside its choices, not just above.** New Option name position field (radio, above/beside, default above) on `ShopVariantOptions` threads a `labelPlacement` prop through `VariantOptionsPart` to `OptionControl`: beside drops the name's bottom margin and wraps name+choices in one wrapping flex row, for narrow columns where the stacked default runs the page long. Purely additive - default keeps every existing layout looking exactly as it did. No schema change. Released: shop-variations **v0.1.42**, core **v0.5.543** (re-pin). Previously:  **A product rename could quietly take its own downloads offline, and now heals itself.** Renaming a product (dwoffice's chiro-plus chair, adding "24 hour") renames its core media folder, which rewrites the storage key and nanoid of every file inside - core updates its own `Media` row for the move but `pdl_files` had copied `media_provider`/`media_key`/`url` off it at upload time and never learns the address changed, so the public download route kept reading a key the Worker had nothing under (confirmed live: old key 404, current `Media.key` 200). New `withFreshStorage()` (`product-downloads-for-shop/lib/db/heal.ts`) resolves a file's `media_id` against the live `Media` row before the public GET reads bytes or the admin DELETE removes them, uses the current key/url if it drifted, and writes the repair back to `pdl_files` - best-effort, so a lost race just heals again on the next request. No admin action needed; a stale download fixes itself the next time anyone clicks it. The DELETE side matters separately - deleting by a dead key would have left the real bytes orphaned and billed forever. `p3d_models`/`svr_uploads` cache the same three columns beside a `media_id` and carry the same latent exposure (0 stale rows found on Deskwell today, unlike `pdl_files`'s 2/2) - not fixed, flagged only. No schema change, so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger; tsc + eslint clean. Released: product-downloads-for-shop **v0.1.2**, core **v0.5.540** (re-pin). Previously: **Spin-model mode now actually leaves the shadow where it is (p3d 0.1.26, working tree).** v0.1.21's `spinModel` had two faults its own label promised away: v0.1.24 "pinned" the shadow by freezing the shadow map (`renderer.shadowMap.autoUpdate=false`), which anchored it by petrifying its SHAPE - the silhouette never followed the turning model - and a shopper's drag still drove OrbitControls' azimuth, so dragging orbited the camera and the whole world (floor shadow included) turned in view: the shadow travelled with the model, the exact thing the mode exists to stop. Fix inverts both. In spin mode the shadow map stays LIVE (light and floor never move, so the shadow stays anchored while its silhouette follows the model); the once-bake moves to camera-orbit mode instead, where the world genuinely never moves (saves the per-frame shadow pass for free). The camera azimuth is locked (`min/maxAzimuthAngle = getAzimuthalAngle()`) and horizontal pointer drag turns the pivot directly in `Viewer3d` (2π per stage height, the same ratio OrbitControls uses, with a release glide decayed by `dampingFactor`); vertical drag still tilts, pinch/zoom/pan untouched; `spinModel` now governs the drag as well as the idle spin, so `Settings3dTab` no longer gates it behind `autoRotate`. Two more real bugs fixed in the same sweep: `loadModel`'s `.clone(true)` SHARED materials across clones (three shares material references on clone), so `applyFabricPaint` on one viewer mutated the cached master - fabric colour leaked onto thumbnails of the same file and the next clone arrived pre-painted; materials are now deep-cloned per clone (textures still shared - nothing mutates a texture in place). And `Viewer3d`'s repaint effect could stamp a STALE colour over a newer pick when the older colour's slower texture fetch resolved after the newer near-instant cached one; the paint now `prefetchTexture`s first and re-checks `cancelled` before stamping. Previous entry: **The 3D viewer no longer rebuilds itself from scratch every time a shopper changes a colour - the actual reason an option change took seconds, which the preload shipped an hour earlier only partly addressed.** `Gallery3dStage` rendered `<PaintedStage key={item.productId}>`, and a colour change **is** a different variant child - so every colour pick handed React a new key and remounted the whole subtree: `Viewer3d` unmounted (`renderer.dispose`, `disposeModel`, `disposeEnvironment`) and rebuilt from nothing - new `WebGLRenderer`, a **freshly generated PMREM environment** (the `environments` WeakMap is keyed by renderer, so a new renderer regenerates it), the model re-cloned with its geometry and every texture re-uploaded to the GPU, re-framed, shadow catcher rebuilt - all to change one material's `map`. Worse, it made `Viewer3d`'s repaint-in-place effect (written precisely so "a seat-colour change must not tear down and rebuild the WebGL context") **unreachable for the exact case it exists for**, since the component never survived long enough to run it. The key was originally there to reset `slots` to null "for free" and dodge a set-state-in-effect lint trip (recorded in the v0.1.8 entry below) - a tidiness win that cost the whole context. **Fix: drop the key.** `PaintedStage` now persists across variation changes; `Viewer3d`'s build effect is keyed on `[item.url, item.format]`, so it rebuilds only when the model FILE genuinely changes (a headrest-style swap) and a plain colour change repaints in place. Dropping the key also removes the null-reset, which is better behaviour anyway: the previous colours stay on screen while the new bundle is in flight (the model is already correct, only its fabric is changing), where blanking to unpainted read as the model breaking and coming back. Added alongside: a module-scoped `bundleCache` (`Map<"parent|child", Promise<FabricBundle|null>>`) behind `fetchBundle`, so flicking back to a colour already seen paints from memory instead of re-resolving server-side; it holds the promise so two quick picks of one child share a request, and deletes the entry on failure so a connection blip is not cached for the visit. **Process note: the v0.1.23 preload was a real but SECONDARY cost** - it removed the swatch fetch + decode and left the rebuild untouched, so the shopper-visible delay barely moved and the user reported it again unchanged. The lesson is the one this module keeps re-teaching: the expensive thing was not on the path being optimised, and reading the render path end-to-end (what remounts, and why) would have found it before a line of preload code was written. The preload is kept - it still earns its place on first load and on a genuine model swap. tsc + eslint clean, 36 module unit tests pass; no schema change so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.25**, core **v0.5.533** (re-pin). Previously: **The 3D viewer's "spin the model" mode now pins the shadow to the floor, which is the only thing that made the setting visible at all.** `spinModel` as shipped in v0.1.21 turned the pivot under a scene-level light with a **live** shadow map - so the shadow re-projected the turning silhouette every frame and travelled round with the model, which is visually indistinguishable from the camera orbiting a static model+shadow (a transparent background and an invisible `ShadowMaterial` plane leave no fixed reference to tell the two apart). Reported as "enabling it doesn't appear to change anything", and correct - to the eye it genuinely did not. Fix is two lines in `Viewer3d.tsx`: when `shadowsEnabled && spinModel`, set `renderer.shadowMap.autoUpdate = false` + `needsUpdate = true` immediately after `addShadowCatcher`, so the first frame bakes the shadow map once and it never updates again. The model then rotates **within** a shadow anchored to the floor. Deliberately non-physical (a real object's shadow does turn with it) - legibility of the spin is the entire point of the setting - and it saves a shadow-map pass per frame. `spinModel` off is untouched (live shadow map, camera orbit, byte-identical). Label and README reworded from "the shadow sweeps with it" to "leave its shadow where it is", since the first wording described the bug. No schema change (jsonb config), backup gate not triggered; tsc + eslint clean. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.24**, core **v0.5.532** (re-pin only). Previously: **A product's 3D models and fabric colours now preload in the background after the page has settled, so changing a variation option shows the new model/colour near-instantly instead of after a few seconds' load.** `product-3d-views-for-shop` already caches parsed models (`cache`) and fabric master textures (`textureCache`) at module scope in `lib/three/load-model.ts`, both keyed by url and shared across viewer mounts - so the per-switch lag was purely the first fetch + parse/decode of a url not yet cached. New: `prefetchModel(url, format)` (warms `cache` without the `.clone(true)` a real load does) and `prefetchTexture(url)` (wraps `loadTexture`) in `load-model.ts`, both best-effort/error-swallowing (the cache never keeps a rejection, so a real load still retries + reports). New client orchestrator `lib/preload.ts` (`preloadProductAssets(payload, signal)`): dedupes model urls off `payload.items` and warms them at concurrency 3, then - only for a fabric-configured product - fetches the new swatch-list endpoint and warms each distinct texture, abortable throughout. New **public** route `GET /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/swatches?parent=` → `{urls: string[]}`, the distinct http(s) swatch urls the product's fabric colour options could paint (`getFabricConfig` + `listColourOptions`, deduped, 5-min public cache, `{urls:[]}` on error) - it scales with distinct colours (a handful), NOT variation count (can be hundreds), which is the whole reason it is one light endpoint rather than the storefront prefetching one `/fabric/[child]` resolve per child through the throttled 60s module route. Wired via a one-shot effect in `Gallery3dThumbs` (`components/public/Gallery3d.tsx`) scheduled on `requestIdleCallback` (1.2s `setTimeout` fallback for Safari) so it trails first paint, aborted on unmount; a real pick landing mid-preload shares the same cached promise, so preloading runs ahead of the shopper, never against them. No schema/migration/`lib/backup` change, so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger; tsc + eslint clean, 36 module unit tests pass. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.23**, core **v0.5.531** (re-pin). Previously: **The 3D viewer can now supersample to sharpen fine detail (e.g. a fine fabric weave) that looked grainy or choppy when the whole model was on screen.** New `superSampling` number on `product-3d-views-for-shop`'s viewer config (`lib/config.ts`, min 1 max 2, default 1 = historic behaviour), applied in `Viewer3d.tsx` as a multiplier on top of the down-capped device pixel ratio: `renderer.setPixelRatio(Math.min(devicePixelRatio, pixelRatioCap) * superSampling)`. `pixelRatioCap` only caps **downward** (min against the device ratio), so on a plain 1x monitor the render was stuck at 1x and a fine weave aliased to a shimmer whenever the model was small on screen - MSAA (`antialias`) smooths only the silhouette, and the earlier anisotropy pass (`applyMaxAnisotropy`, v0.1.20) fixes only grazing-angle wash, so neither touched this. Rendering above screen resolution and downsampling is the actual cure for shaded-surface aliasing. Cost is quadratic (2 = 4x the pixels), so it is a **Fine-detail sharpening** slider under Speed in `Settings3dTab.tsx`, capped at 2. Applies to the main stage viewer only (thumbnails untouched). Config is jsonb so no schema/migration change and the backup round-trip gate did not trigger; tsc + eslint clean, 36 module unit tests pass. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.22**, core **v0.5.530** (re-pin). Previously: **The 3D viewer's idle auto-rotate can now spin the model itself under a fixed light, so its shadow moves with it, instead of only orbiting the camera round a still model.** New `spinModel` boolean on `product-3d-views-for-shop`'s viewer config (`lib/config.ts`, default `false` = historic camera-orbit behaviour) with a **Spin the model itself, not the camera around it** checkbox in the 3D settings tab (`components/admin/Settings3dTab.tsx`, disabled unless auto-rotate is on, since it only governs the idle spin). `Viewer3d.tsx` derives `wantsMotion` once (auto-rotate on AND not reduced-motion), then either keeps `controls.autoRotate` (camera orbit, light + `ShadowMaterial` catcher plane hold still) or, when `spinModel`, leaves `controls.autoRotate` off and turns `pivot.rotation.y` per frame by a step matched to OrbitControls' own auto-rotation rate - the pivot is the model, the light and ground plane are scene-level, so the shadow sweeps with the turn (shadow camera reach is already sized off the model's largest dimension, so a full turn stays in-frame). First shopper touch stops both paths as before. Thumbnails unaffected (they already spin their pivot via the separate `thumbnailAutoRotate`). Config is jsonb so no schema/migration change and the backup round-trip gate did not trigger; tsc + eslint clean. Released: product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.21**, core re-pin. Previously: **The fabric configurator now paints whichever 3D model a shopper's chosen variation actually carries, instead of one shared admin-picked default.** Dropped the "Default model" dropdown and the structural `models[]` rules (a headrest-style model swap is now just a different file attached to that variation, no rule needed) from `product-3d-views-for-shop`'s fabric config (`lib/db/fabric-config.ts` - `FabricConfigSchema` lost `models`/`defaultModelId`, keeping only `heightAttributeId`/`modelHeights`/`slots`). `composeFabricBundle` (`lib/fabric/resolve.ts`) is now handed the model to draw and its height directly (pure, unit-tested unchanged in shape) rather than picking one out of a lookup; `resolveFabricForChild` gained a `parentProductId` param and resolves the variation's own attached model via `getModelsForProductTree`, falling back to the parent's. **The one trap**: `modelHeights` is keyed by `p3d_models` row id, but the same GLB is attached once per variation (many rows, one url) - the shown variation's row id is never the id its height was measured against, so the resolver now reads `modelHeights` **by file url**, not row id, or every variation's weave would silently sit at repeat 1. Previously: **Variant-import provider hooks are now batched per parent, not per row.** The final per-row DB ceiling after v0.5.519: shop-variations' `variant-field-provider` point gained an optional `beginImport(productId, childIds)` lifecycle (`variant-field-providers.ts`), so a provider preloads its state once per parent and `csv.ts` threads that ctx into every `applyImportedRow(…, ctx)`. `product-attributes-for-shop` (v0.1.4) preloads all children's current attribute values (`getVariantAttributeValues`), added change detection (only writes when the resolved value id differs) and a per-import label cache; `product-3d-views-for-shop` (v0.1.14) preloads all children's models in one query and diffs against ctx instead of a per-row `getModelsForProducts` read (diff logic unchanged). Ctx miss = new variant created mid-import = empty current state, so brand-new variants still get their values written; fully back-compatible with a provider that has no `beginImport`. Behaviour covered by each provider's `variant-field-provider.test.ts`. Pins: shop-variations v0.1.38, product-attributes-for-shop v0.1.4, product-3d-views-for-shop v0.1.14. **Earlier same day: A Google Sheet Pull now shows live "X of Y" progress, can be Continued if it stalls, and its Push/Pull/Open/Logs controls moved off the settings page onto the Products page.** Two asks, one build. **(1) Resumable, live-progress Pull.** The old Pull ran the whole pipeline inside one request's `after()`, capped at the module dispatcher's un-overridable **60s ceiling** (`app/api/m/[module]/[...path]/route.ts`) - a big catalogue died mid-variations and the UI just showed a static "Pulling…". A Pull is now a **job the browser drives one bounded batch at a time** (new `gsp_pull_job` table, migration `002_pull_job.sql`; `lib/pull-job.ts` data layer; `lib/pull-run.ts` stepper). `POST /pull` now only reads+validates the sheet, snapshots both grids into the job row, and returns `{pullJobId}` - no `after()`. The browser then loops `POST /pull/step`, each call doing one slice and returning a live snapshot: **PRODUCTS** (one blocking `processImportJob` on the whole products CSV, its live per-row count read from the linked `shp_import_jobs` row via `GET /pull/status`) → **DELETIONS** (status pass + `planPullDeletions` + product/variation deletes, one step) → **VARIATIONS** (time-boxed step: chunks of 10 rows through `importVariationsCsv`, cursor written after every chunk, new chunks started until a 35s in-step budget is spent - replaced the fixed 60-rows-per-step batch, which on the live dwoffice catalogue took >60s, got killed by the dispatcher before its single cursor write, and wedged the Pull at "0 of 83" through every Continue) → finalize (writes the two `gsp_sync_log` rows, stamps last-pull, clears the grid snapshot). Every phase is idempotent (products match by SKU/slug compare-first, variations upsert by value-set, deletes are by-id no-ops once gone), so a **Continue** after a failed step or a closed tab just replays from the saved cursor - `GET /pull/status` (no id) returns the latest unfinished job for the Continue prompt; `POST /pull/cancel` abandons one. `POST /pull` 409s if an unfinished job already exists. Residual: PRODUCTS and DELETIONS are single (coarse) steps, so a catalogue with >60s of pure products import or deletion-planning can still time out a step - but each is idempotent, so Continue chips away (already-imported rows become fast no-ops); only variations, the actual Deskwell failure, are finely chunked. **(2) Controls moved to the Products page.** Shop's `ProductsScreen` now renders a `toolbarExtras` slot beside its header buttons, resolved server-side in `products/page.tsx` from a **new `shop.products-toolbar` extension point** (generic host infra - empty on a plain shop, same pattern as `shop.product-editor-sections`). google-sheet contributes `GoogleSheetProductsToolbar` (`components/ProductsToolbar.tsx`): a single **Google Sheet ▾** dropdown (Open sheet / Push / Pull / Sheet logs), shown only once a sheet is connected, that opens the Pull preview→confirm→live-progress→Continue flow and the Recent-syncs log as modals. The settings tab (`SettingsTab.tsx`) is now setup-only (connection, create/reset sheet, cost-price toggle) and points at the Products page for the rest. Versions: **shop 0.1.60→0.1.61** (publishes the toolbar point), **google-sheet-products-for-shop 0.1.7→0.1.8** (`requiresModules shop` bumped to 0.1.61). Backup gate triggered by the new table: schema-coverage backstop green (all `gsp_pull_job` types - TEXT/JSONB/TIMESTAMP(3)/INTEGER - supported, no sequences), **backup round-trip real PASS (3/3, not skipped)**. tsc + eslint clean. Unreleased - both module working trees want the version bumps, module-repo commits and a `modules.json` re-pin at release. Previously: **A Google Sheet Pull (and a plain CSV re-import) now only writes the rows that actually changed, instead of rewriting the whole catalogue on every run.** Follow-on from the previous entry's fix: even with the image-rewrite skip in place, a re-sync was still an unconditional write per row - `processImportJob` (`shop/lib/import-engine.ts`) called `updateProduct` plus `setProductCategories`/`setProductTags`/`setProductCollections`/`setProductMedia` for **every** matched product on **every** run, because a CSV row carries every column regardless of whether the owner touched it; `upsertVariantForCombination` (`shop-variations/lib/variants-service.ts`) did the same for every matched variant's price/sku/barcode/stock/weight. On a real catalogue that's a write (and an `updated_at` bump) per row per Pull whether or not anything changed - the direct cause of "pulling takes ages" once the earlier image/60s fix was in. Both now **compare against the current DB row first and skip the write when it already matches**: `productFieldsUnchanged`/`sameIdSet`/`sameIdOrder`/`sameMedia` (import-engine.ts) gate the product's own fields and its categories/tags/collections/media independently, so a row that changed its price but not its categories only pays for the price write. `upsertVariantForCombination` gained the same gate for a **matched** (not freshly-created) variant, and now returns `changed: boolean` so `importVariationsCsv` can report an honest "updated" count - a row is only counted as updated if something it owns (fields or image) actually wrote, not just because the sheet listed it. A provider-only change (a 3D file, a `product-attributes-for-shop` value) isn't reflected in that count, since those providers own their own change detection (3D already skipped no-op writes; attributes wasn't touched - out of scope, flagged as a smaller residual cost). No schema change, so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger. tsc + eslint clean, `vitest run` on both modules green (27 tests). Released: shop **v0.1.60**, shop-variations **v0.1.34**, core **v0.5.514** (re-pin only - `google-sheet-products-for-shop` untouched this round, stays v0.1.7). Previously: **A Google Sheet Pull now finishes the variations before it says "done", stops dying on big catalogues, and no longer emails a report every time.** Three defects on one Pull, all confirmed against the live Deskwell site (`gsp_sync_log`: 17 of the last 19 Pulls logged Products COMPLETED but **no** Variations row - the variations pass was being killed, not throwing, since no FAILED row was written either). Root cause: `importVariationsCsv` (`shop-variations/lib/csv.ts`) re-wrote **every** variant's image on **every** Pull unconditionally - `setProductMedia` + `reorganiseProductMedia`, the latter a storage-provider round-trip per image - even when only a 3D URL changed and the picture was untouched. On Deskwell's one product with 92 variations that is 92 needless network trips, which tipped the whole `after()` run past the module dispatcher's un-overridable **60s ceiling** (`app/api/m/[module]/[...path]/route.ts`), so the variations upsert (and with it the 3D-files/attribute providers **and** the Variations sync-log write) never completed. Meanwhile the UI polled the **first** fresh PULL log - always the Products row, written before variations run - and announced "Pull complete" while variants were still being written (or already dead). And `processImportJob` fired shop's `IMPORT_COMPLETE` email on every Pull. Three fixes, each in the module that owns the concern, no schema change: **(1)** `importVariationsCsv` prefetches each variant's current primary image once per parent (one `shp_product_media` query) and **skips the media rewrite+re-file entirely when the cell already matches** - semantically a no-op, but it was the dominant cost; a changed/empty/invalid cell behaves exactly as before. **(2)** `processImportJob` (`shop/lib/import-engine.ts`) gained `opts?: { notify?: boolean }` (default keeps the emailed report for a direct CSV upload); the Pull passes `notify:false`, so a sync reports through the log, not the inbox. **(3)** the settings-tab poll (`google-sheet-products-for-shop/components/SettingsTab.tsx`) now waits for the **Variations** COMPLETED log (the last thing a Pull writes) or a FAILED row, and says "still running - check Recent syncs" on timeout rather than claiming success. Every product FK cascades except `shp_order_items.product_id` (ON DELETE SET NULL), so a delete keeps order history; both delete routes turn a foreign-key violation into a friendly 409. **Known gap:** deleting a product that carries shop-variations options leaves its hidden variant-child `shp_products` rows orphaned - cross-module cleanup is the variations module's job, flagged as a follow-up. No schema change, so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger; shop module working tree, unreleased. Previously: **Three shop-variations changes: unbuyable option choices now vanish instead of greying out, dependent options wait for the whole chain above them, and the Variations grid does bulk delete.** (1) `OptionControl` (`VariantParts.tsx`, shared by the granular storefront blocks and the `DetailSlotPartsClient` slot) now filters each option's values to `sel.isAvailable(option.id, v.id) || chosen === v.id` before rendering, so a value with no buyable variant given the current partial choice drops out of the dropdown / pill / swatch row entirely rather than showing struck-through-and-disabled - the shopper only ever meets choices that lead somewhere. The currently-chosen value is kept even when a change to an option above it makes it unreachable, so the control never blanks out from under them (that rare active-but-unavailable case keeps the old disabled styling). (2) `isOptionVisible(payload, selection, index)` (`lib/selection-logic.ts`) changed from gating on **the immediately-previous** option to gating on **every** option before `index` (`payload.options.slice(0, index).every((prev) => !!selection[prev.id])`), so a flagged dependent option only reveals once the whole chain ahead of it is chosen, not merely its neighbour; the admin tickbox label (`VariationsPanel.tsx`) is now "Only show once every option above it is chosen". An empty slice is vacuously true, so the first option stays dormant exactly as before, and both storefront render paths pick the change up through the shared helper. (3) The Variations grid gained a per-row tickbox in the sticky first column plus a select-all (with indeterminate) in its header - a `selected: Set<string>` pruned to live rows on every reload - and a **Delete selected (N)** button in the bulk-controls row, backed by a new `POST admin/products/[id]/delete-variants` route (`{variantIds: string[]}`, gate `shop.products`) → `deleteVariants(parentId, ids)` in `variants-service.ts`, which verifies each id belongs to the parent before `deleteProduct`ing its hidden child (the same cascade the single-row Delete and clear-all take). No schema change - pure code + manifest wiring, so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger. shop-variations **v0.1.27**. Previously: **A product with a very large option matrix no longer leaves the Variations tab blank.** Building the variant matrix for a product with hundreds of combinations (deskwell's 22×22×2 = 968 chair) used to try to create every hidden child product in a single request and get killed at the module route's 60s ceiling - a half-built matrix, stray child products (`createProduct` committed, then the kill before `createVariant`), and a Variations tab that stayed blank because `VariationsPanel`'s load `fetch` silently swallowed the resulting 500. `generateMatrix` (`lib/variants-service.ts`) now works to a **30s time budget** (`MATRIX_BATCH_MS`): it builds what it can, returns `{created, removed, total, done}` with `done:false` when the budget ran out - checked only **between** combos so a combo is never left half-made, and guarding the removal phase too - and the client `generate()` (`VariationsPanel.tsx`) **auto-loops** the request until `done`, refreshing between batches so the count climbs in view. One press builds the lot; closing the tab part-way leaves a resumable gap the existing "Continue building options" button fills (resumption is a cheap in-memory skip of combos that already exist). `total` is now the count that exists *now*, not the matrix's eventual size. The v0.1.22 cap removal ("unbounded") is what exposed this - it dropped the old `maxVariants` throw without ever teaching generation to batch. Also: `VariationsPanel` no longer renders a silent blank when the payload fails before first data - it shows an error with a **Try again** button (`loadFailed` state). shop-variations **v0.1.26**. Previously: **Shop variation options can now reveal in order - a dependent option stays hidden until the one before it is chosen.** Any product option from the **second onward** can be flagged "only show once the option above is chosen" (a checkbox on the option card in the Variations tab, `VariationsPanel.tsx`, gated on `oi > 0` and labelled with the previous option's name). On the storefront a flagged option is held back until the option immediately before it by display order has a value chosen, so a shopper works through them one step at a time - pick Frame, and only then does Glass appear, and so on. It is pure progressive disclosure: the variant matrix, `resolveVariant` and add-to-cart availability are all untouched, only which controls are on screen change. One new pure helper, **`isOptionVisible(payload, selection, index)`** (`lib/selection-logic.ts`), surfaced on the selection hook as `sel.isOptionVisible(index)` and applied in **both** storefront render paths (`VariantOptionsPart` in `VariantParts.tsx` and `VariantSlotPurchaseClient` in `DetailSlotPartsClient.tsx`, plus the RSC halves that delegate to them). The gate **chains** - if the option before is itself hidden and unchosen this one stays hidden too - and is **dormant on the first option** (nothing before it to wait on), so a flag left on an option later dragged to the front simply does nothing rather than hiding it forever. Backed by a new `svr_options.requires_previous_option` BOOLEAN column (default false), migration `003_requires_previous_option.sql` (idempotent `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`, mirrored into 001 for fresh installs), read/written through `mapOption`/`updateOption` and the `PATCH admin/options/[id]` route (`requiresPreviousOption` boolean). Backup round-trip re-run for the new column: real PASS, not skipped. No release yet - change sits in the module working tree. Previously: **Optimising, renaming or resizing a shop product's image no longer breaks it.** The media library can move a blob to a fresh storage key and url without changing the item's identity - optimise re-encodes to WebP, resize/crop/replace/rename all shift the key - and core rewrote every reference it owned for the move except the ones it did not know about. Product images and variation image swatches keep the media item's **url** in the shop's own tables (`shp_product_media.url`, `svr_option_values.swatch`), and core's `rewriteMediaReferencesInContent` only ever reached Puck page/layout builder JSON, so an optimise pass left every one of those columns pointing at a blob it had just deleted - the storefront 404ing while the library looked perfectly healthy, which is exactly what a bulk optimise did. Fixed with a new **`core.media-reference-rewriters`** extension point (`lib/media/reference-rewriters.ts`, contract + `getMediaReferenceRewriters`): a module that stores media urls in its own tables registers one async rewriter taking `{oldUrl,newUrl,oldKey,newKey}`, and `rewriteMediaReferencesInContent` runs every registered one as its final step - so optimise, resize, crop, replace and rename all reach module data now, not just the page builder. Shop's rewriter (`modules/shop/lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts`) repoints `shp_product_media.url` and `shp_digital_files.url`; shop-variations' (`modules/shop-variations/lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts`) repoints `svr_option_values.swatch` - both by **url equality**, because the column holds the whole url verbatim (the product/swatch editors save the picker's `Media.url` unchanged), so `= oldUrl` cannot touch an unrelated row and a hex colour swatch is never matched. A rewriter is allowed to throw: core runs it **before** it deletes the superseded blob (`repointMediaToBlob`/`moveOrRenameMedia`), so a failure aborts with the old url still serving rather than silently 404ing. Versions: core 0.5.493, shop 0.1.55 (`requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.493), shop-variations 0.1.23 (`requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.493). No schema change - pure code + manifest wiring - so the backup round-trip gate did not trigger. **This stops future breakage; it does not repair images already broken by an earlier optimise** - the old→new url mapping is gone once the old blob was deleted, so a separate best-effort heal is still owed. Previously: **A Google Sheet mirror of the shop catalogue, and the CSV round-trip bugs it forced out of shop first.** New module **google-sheet-products-for-shop** (`gsp_`): the owner Pushes the catalogue to a Google Sheet Cactus creates, bulk-edits it, and Pulls it back after a diff preview - two human-pressed buttons, no crons, no background sync. It is a **transport adapter, not a data mapper**: it moves grids between Google and shop's own CSV export/import and shop-variations' `exportVariationsCsv`/`importVariationsCsv`, writing zero product-field mapping and adding no columns to `shp_*`/`svr_*`. `drive.file` scope only (non-sensitive, no Google verification), which is *why* the module creates its own sheet rather than accepting a link; owner registers their own Google OAuth client; the Testing-mode 7-day-refresh-token trap is surfaced inline and as a plain-English refresh error. Pull runs `processImportJob` → a **status pass** (the engine ignores the `status` column, so ACTIVE-in-a-cell was a silent no-op) → an **archive pass** (rows missing from the sheet are archive-*candidates*, opt-in per row, never deleted - archive keeps order history) → variations, products-before-variations enforced in code. The preview dry-runs the same validation the engines apply so its counts match the result. **Phase 0 was three silent-data-loss bugs on a plain shop CSV export→import round trip, fixed in shop because they are shop's own** (this module just turned a rare manual round trip into a routine one, which is what made them dangerous): `tax_class` exported empty nulled every product's tax class (now exports the real code via `getTaxClassCodesByIds`); media flattened to `IMAGE` and dropped alt text (now type-prefixed `TYPE:url` cells + a new `image_alt` column, backwards-compatible, via `serializeMedia`/`parseMediaCells`); and export silently truncated at 100 products (listProducts' public-list clamp) which, with archive-on-missing, would have offered to archive product 101 onward - now paginated via `collectPaged`, clamp untouched. Pure round-trip test in shop (`lib/csv-roundtrip.test.ts`, 13 cases); backup round-trip re-run for the two new `gsp_` tables (real PASS). **Released**: shop CSV fixes shipped as **shop v0.1.56** (the version numbers drifted twice mid-build - 0.1.52 and 0.1.55 were both taken by other agents' work before this landed), the module as **v0.1.0** at `cactus-foundation-modules/google-sheet-products-for-shop`, registered in `modules.json` and pinned in core **v0.5.495**. `requiresModules shop >= 0.1.56` (the release that carries the CSV fixes) + `shop-variations >= 0.1.15` (a hard dependency); `requiresCoreVersion 0.5.486` (a safe floor - the module uses only long-standing core APIs; core is 0.5.495). Previously: **The product gallery now leads with the 3D model instead of burying it at the end.** A product that carries a 3D view was showing its photos first and the 3D thumbnail last, and opening the big stage on a flat photo - so the one thing a shopper could actually spin was the last thing they'd find. In all three galleries (`ProductGallery`, and shop-variations' `VariantSlotGalleryClient` + `ShopVariantGallery`) the contributed `extras.map` now renders **before** the photo thumbnails, so the 3D thumbnail leads the strip; and `Gallery3dThumbs` picks its first visible item once on first paint, so the stage opens on the model. Order and opening-view only - the host still owns the strip and the pick, the `stale` hand-back is unchanged, and a `ledWithModel` mount guard keeps a later variation change from yanking the stage off a photo the shopper chose. Versions: shop **v0.1.54**, shop-variations **v0.1.21** (in two steps - v0.1.20 did the hand-placed block, v0.1.21 the slot gallery), product-3d-views-for-shop **v0.1.6**, core **0.5.491**. Purely additive to the modules' own dirty trees at the time (a shop CSV import feature was left uncommitted and untouched). Previously: **A 3D Viewer settings tab, and the hosted-panel plumbing that let it be a sub-tab of someone else's page without a line of module code in core.** Site owners can now tune the shop's 3D viewer - shadows, tone mapping, background, the light rig, the orbit/zoom feel, and a speed group - from **admin > Shop > 3D Viewer**. Three repos, one feature, because putting it *there* rather than in a top-level Settings tab (the owner's call, option 1.b) hit a real gap: core collapsed every hosted settings panel to `Record<slot, ReactNode>` and threw the manifest `label` away, and a tab strip cannot draw a tab it has no label for. So core now forwards hosted panels in **two shapes** - the old merged node (for GoCardless, which just drops into shop's Payments section) and a new `hostedSettingsPanels` keeping each panel's `id`/`label` (for anything that wants its own tab) - both defined in `lib/modules/hosted-settings.ts`, and `host` is finally in the manifest zod schema it had been quietly relying on. Shop publishes a second slot, `shop.settings-sub-tabs`, appending each contributed panel as its own labelled sub-tab; the module's "3D Viewer" panel lands there. **Every setting defaults to the exact value the module hardcoded before the tab existed** (`P3D_CONFIG_DEFAULTS`), stored on a new `p3d_settings` singleton and carried to the storefront inside `P3dPayload.settings` (no client fetch, resolved only when a product has a model), so an install that never opens the tab renders byte-identical. Shadows are a real build, not a flag - a `ShadowMaterial` catcher plane at the model's base, the key light turned caster, meshes set to cast - and are the main viewer's alone, never the 64px thumbnails. **The through-line, again: the isolation held.** A shop-only owner with no add-ons sees an empty slot render nothing - no extra tab, no diff - which is the litmus for whether a "generic" core/shop change earned its place. Backup round-trip re-run for the new table: real PASS, not skipped. Versions: core 0.5.490, shop 0.1.53 (`requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.490), module v0.1.5 (`requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.490, `requiresModules` shop >= 0.1.53). Previously: **Every metal was rendering black, and two confident diagnoses walked straight past it.** `addLights` never set `scene.environment`, and **a PBR metal has no diffuse term - it is nothing but reflection**, so with nothing to reflect, Deskwell's polished chrome chair base rendered black on the site and silver in every desktop viewer. Fixed with three's procedural `RoomEnvironment` (module v0.1.4, core re-pin v0.5.485): chrome base brightness **9.3 -> 180.5**, measured against the real module code, and **the model file is irrelevant to it**. **The process lesson outweighs the fix.** Chasing "the fabric looks wrong" produced two wrong answers in a row: first that `KHR_texture_transform` should be *inverted* (it should not - that would make each weave tile 34.5cm, and it **rendered plausibly**, which is precisely what made it dangerous), then a tiling figure derived from the **global UV span** when the mesh is unwrapped into islands and only **per-triangle texel density** carries meaning. Both survived because the picture looked believable. What broke it open was the user reporting "the chair base is the wrong colour" - a symptom no file theory could explain, because no file can make chrome black. **Rules this earns: (1) when a PBR model looks wrong, check `scene.environment` FIRST - it is the one setting that silently changes an entire class of material; (2) a plausible render is not evidence, measure a number; (3) when a user pushes back twice on a diagnosis, re-derive it rather than re-explain it.** The flat weave *is* genuinely a file defect (0.088 -> 0.478 only when the spurious transform is stripped; the env map does nothing for it, 0.088 -> 0.096) - two independent bugs wearing one symptom, which is why each fix alone "did not work" and looked like a failure. Previously: **Three product-page bugs that all looked like something else.** (1) **A black chair rendered snow-white.** The GLB was blameless - its fabric texture is a correctly dark anthracite JPEG. Core's CSP allowed `blob:` under `img-src` but not `connect-src`, and three's GLTFLoader **fetches** the object URL it mints for each embedded texture, so `connect-src` is the directive consulted and every texture failed. glTF defaults an untextured `baseColorFactor` to white; the fabric was the only material on that chair taking its colour from a texture, so it alone went white while the arms and base looked right. Fixed in `proxy.ts` (v0.5.484). **The lesson: the directive follows the *fetch mechanism*, not the cargo's media type.** (2) **Thumbnails spun the model, not the scene** - `frameModel` centred the model but callers turned `model.rotation.y`, and `T*R*S` means that pivots on the *file's* origin, 4.79 units of swing against a ±1.46 view. Now returns a `Group` pivot with the model centred inside it (module v0.1.3). (3) **The gallery arrows shipped in shop v0.1.48 and almost nobody saw them**: shop-variations replaces the gallery wholesale on any product with options, and never adopted `GalleryThumbStrip` - so exactly the products with the most photos kept the bare scrolling row. Adopted in shop-variations v0.1.15, `requiresModules: shop` → 0.1.48. **The through-line: a feature that ships behind an extension point is not shipped until every provider of that point has taken it up** - shop's own CSS comment and this file both recorded the gap and it still sat there. All three were confirmed against the live Deskwell page and fixed under a probe, not by reasoning alone. Previously: **Landing the product-downloads trio, and the version lie under it.** `modules.json` pins **shop v0.1.50** (publishing `shop.product-detail-tabs`) and adds **product-downloads-for-shop v0.1.1**, which was built, released and documented but never registered - so it could not be installed, while the README and wiki already told site owners it could. The point's code had been sitting uncommitted in the shop checkout all along, which is why the docs describing it went public first: **documentation was pushed for source that was untracked**, the exact trap `reference_shared_tree_staging_hazards` records, walked into again. The defect that fell out of fixing it is the one worth keeping: product-downloads' manifest named `requiresModules: shop >= 0.1.47`, the shop of the day it was written against, and the point did not ship until 0.1.50. A min version naming a release **without** the feature is not a version check - the module installs with a thumbs-up, the tab never renders, and nothing anywhere says why. Corrected forward in module v0.1.1 rather than by rewriting the published v0.1.0 tag (same call as `product-3d-views-for-shop` v0.1.1 before it). **Rule this keeps re-teaching: a version number written while a dependency is still moving is a guess, so re-read the dependency's actual released version at release time, never at authoring time.** Previously: **Replace the file, keep the item.** `POST /api/admin/media/[id]/replace` + a Replace button on every media item (card hover 🔄, detail-panel footer, context menu). The job people were doing by hand - upload the new picture, delete the old one - silently broke every page, product and setting pointing at the old one, because those hold an id/url that stops resolving. So this keeps the row and swaps only the bytes: same id, name, folder, alt text, tags. Which is a job the library already knew how to do - `optimiseMediaInPlace` and `persistDerivedImage` (crop/reshape/resize) have been doing it for a while - so the win was extracting **`repointMediaToBlob`** as the one owner of the tail all of them share (repoint the row → rewrite Puck refs → delete the superseded blob last, and only if the key actually moved), rather than writing a fourth copy of the fiddly bits for Replace to get subtly wrong. Both upload paths are wired, so a 40 MB photograph replaces as happily as a 40 KB icon: `/upload-url` gained an optional `replaceId` that hands back the key `planMediaReplacement` dictates, and `[id]/replace` takes either the multipart file or the already-PUT blob. The one refusal is a 409: an **exact-named** item (the shop's product images) can only be replaced by a file of its own type, because its name is its key, and a new extension would move the url that the shop holds in its own table and reference-rewriting never reaches - the image would vanish from the storefront while sitting perfectly intact in the library. Previously: **Resize in the media library, and a lazy-load switch that had nowhere to enter.** Two media jobs. **Resize** (`[id]/resize` + `bulk-resize`, `MediaResizeDialog.tsx`) is the ratio changer's sibling: that one changes an image's shape by padding, this one keeps the shape and scales it down. Geometry is a pure `planResize` (`lib/media/resize-plan.ts`, unit-tested like `aspect-plan`) whose one rule is that the box is a **ceiling, not a target** - an image already inside it is returned as a `changed:false` skip rather than upscaled, because enlarging invents no detail and only costs bytes. Output dimensions are re-measured off the encoded bytes, not read from the plan: `fit:'inside'` preserves the source ratio and can land a pixel under the box, the same trap `changeMediaAspectRatio` already documents. Persistence is the shared `persistDerivedImage`, so replace-in-place keeps the id, the exact-name key and therefore every reference held outside Puck content. `Media` carries no width/height columns, so the dialog reads `naturalWidth` off the preview purely to tell the user what they're getting. **`SiteConfig.lazyLoadImages`** (Settings → Media) was the harder half, because there was no way in: `lib/puck/config.tsx` is bundled into the client editor and is contractually hook-free, so it can reach neither prisma nor a context, and `loading` is not expressible as a CSS variable the way `--img-radius` is. The channel is **Puck's own `metadata`** - `<Render metadata>` lands on `puck.metadata`, per render rather than per module (no cross-request leak), arriving through the same door as `puck.isEditing`. `lib/puck/renderMetadata.ts` resolves it server-side off the `cache()`d `getSiteConfig`; the helper blocks actually call is `lib/puck/imgLoading.ts`, which imports **nothing at all** because anything reaching prisma from there would follow config.tsx into the browser bundle. Every RSC `Render` call site passes it (public layout's header/footer, renderInfoPage + renderLayoutWithContent, not-found, both status pages, layout-preview). The helper defaults to lazy on absent metadata, which is what makes the editor a no-op: it is handed none, so its markup is byte-identical to before. **Every core content image obeys it** - Image block, Quote photo, Card cover, Panel image, logo strip. The Image block shipped exempt in v0.5.475 (it can be the first thing on a page, and lazy-loading the LCP element measurably delays it) and the exemption was removed on the owner's call in v0.5.476. The reasoning was sound but it is the site owner's trade to make, not one to bake in: with the switch on (the default) a hero Image block is lazy, so the help text names the cost and points at the switch as the first thing to try when the top of a page feels slow. A blanket exemption also made the switch untrue to its own label. Module blocks own their own `<img>`s and don't consult it. Backup round-trip re-run for the new column: real PASS, not skipped. Previously: **Shop's own download route: a sanitised filename, an honest length, and a count that waits for the bytes.** `GET /downloads/[token]` built its response out of three things it had no business trusting. `Content-Disposition` interpolated `shp_digital_files.filename` raw - a value `app/api/admin/digital-files` writes verbatim from the admin's `file.name` - so a double quote closed the parameter early and a CR/LF ended the header and began another; operator-supplied rather than attacker-supplied, which is not a reason to leave a header injection in. `Content-Length` came off the `size` column instead of the response actually being relayed, so a row disagreeing with its bytes truncated the transfer or left the browser waiting for a tail that was never coming. And `incrementDownloadCount` fired before a byte moved, so a transfer that died on a train still cost the customer one of their limited downloads. Shop now owns `lib/download-name.ts` (+ `download-name.test.ts`): the same code-point sanitiser and RFC 6266 `filename`/`filename*` pair as `product-downloads-for-shop`, **copied rather than imported**, because shop cannot depend on a module that depends on shop. Single-argument here - shop has only the uploaded name, no separate plain-English one, so there is no extension to re-append. Length is relayed from upstream or omitted (chunked beats corrupt); the count moved into the stream's `flush()`, which runs when the body ends normally and not at all when the client gives up, and swallows its own error because the bytes are already delivered by then and erroring the tail would break a download that worked. `nosniff` joins the attachment while the header block is open, which matters more here than in the sibling: this route's allowlist is by *declared* MIME type, and the declared type is exactly what a browser reserves the right to overrule. Previously: **Downloadable literature on a product, and a tab point to hang it from.** New module **product-downloads-for-shop** (`pdl_`) attaches manuals, spec sheets and drawings to a product, each named in plain English, shown free to anyone under a **Downloads** tab. It needed somewhere to go: the product page's tab strip was a closed set of four hardcoded branches in `ShopDetailTabsRsc`, so shop v0.1.50 publishes **`shop.product-detail-tabs`** (`lib/detail-tabs.ts`) - additive, modelled on `shop.gallery-media`, resolved once per page in `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx` and carried on `DetailPartContext.detailTabs` because `detail-parts.tsx` is dual-compiled into the client editor bundle and cannot reach prisma. `label`/`order` live on the provider object, not the manifest, since the manifest's copy is zod-stripped at install and only restored on the next deploy. Two things about the module are not choices: downloads go **through the server** (4 MB), because the Worker types an upload from its key's extension and 415s anything that is not a raster image or a 3D model - the direct path is closed to a PDF; and they are **served back through the module**, because core builds a key's extension from the MIME subtype, so a .docx lands under `.vnd.openxmlformats-...` and `<a download>` is ignored cross-origin. `lib/download-name.ts` therefore owns `Content-Disposition` (owner's name + the original's extension, so the name cannot choose the extension), unit-tested because the obvious character class for it hides a range that eats exclamation marks and strips no control character at all. The public route gates on `status === 'ACTIVE' && !catalogueHidden` (a uuid is unguessable, not access-controlled) and reads by provider+key via `downloadMedia`, so a moved Worker does not kill every link the way it does shop's digital files. Previously: **A stranded push now retries itself.** A module update or core update ships by pushing a commit and expecting Vercel's webhook to build it - normally true, but nothing ever retried when it wasn't: a missed delivery left the commit sitting unbuilt, the module row still promoted to a version whose code had never shipped, and the site quietly serving the previous build with no error anywhere. The only tell was a module's stored manifest sitting one version behind its recorded version, since the manifest is only rewritten by a build. Root cause found live on the Deskwell site: `product-3d-views-for-shop` and `shop-variations` had each been bumped, but the push carrying both never built. `startDeferredRedeploy`'s `captureOrTrigger` (`lib/deploy/redeploy.ts`) now polls for the push's own build first (so nothing double-deploys) and, only if none appears, starts one itself via `ensureVercelRedeploy`. Fixing the fallback surfaced a second, latent bug in the trigger itself: Vercel's redeploy API inherits the source deployment's commit sha unless told otherwise, so a naive retry would have quietly rebuilt the *old* commit and reported success. `createRedeploy` (`lib/vercel/deploy.ts`) now passes `withLatestCommit: true` - a no-op whenever the last deployment is already HEAD (every normal redeploy), and the difference between fixing this and rebuilding the same bug when it wasn't. Previously: **Product options open unchosen, and can be reset.** `firstPreselect` picked the first buyable variant the moment a product page loaded, so a combination the shopper had never chosen sat in the controls looking chosen, priced as though it were theirs, with a live buy button over it - a medium in green because that is what happened to be sitting there. The opening selection is now `{}` on both entry paths, which surfaced a latent bug behind the preselect: `VariantPricePart`'s "Out of stock" tested `hasOptions && !inStock`, and `inStock` is false whenever no variant resolves, so with nothing chosen *every* options product would have announced itself sold out. It now gates on `allOptionsChosen` too. A `ResetOptionsLink` renders after the last option in both hosts (the granular block and the detail slot), clearing options but deliberately not personalisation - that is the shopper's typing, not a click they can redo. Previously: **3D uploads actually upload, and a 3D column on the Variations tab.** The 3D module let you pick a 50 MB model and then posted it through a serverless route, where Vercel 413s any body over ~4.5 MB *before* the handler runs - and that 413's body is not JSON, so `res.json()` threw and `?? 'Upload failed'` was the only thing the admin ever saw. Every model worth selling died there; the feature had never worked for a real file. Models now take the **direct-to-Worker path** photographs already use: `MODEL_EXTENSION_TYPES` (`lib/media/limits.ts`, mirrored in the Worker's `EXTENSION_TYPES`) types the five formats, `extensionForMimeType` consults it first (a model type is not derivable from its subtype - `model/gltf-binary` must land as `.glb`; the old `application/octet-stream` produced `.octet-stream`, a key naming no type, which the Worker refuses), and both caps rose 25 → 50 MB in step. The module signs its own keys rather than using core's `/upload-url`, because only it knows the `…/3d` folder and the parent-tree ownership rule; core's `/record` stays image-only. **Every install must redeploy its Worker** before models upload - the client turns the old Worker's 415 into a plain "redeploy" message. Fallbacks say what is wrong instead of failing blankly: a non-S3 provider names its 4 MB ceiling and the fix. Separately, **`shop-variations.variant-columns`** lets a module hang a column on the variants grid; `product-3d-views-for-shop` uses it for a drag-and-drop **3D** column beside Image. The grid learned about *columns*, not about 3D - teaching it 3D would have put one module's UI inside another it does not depend on. Cells must be client components (only client references cross to the client panel), get `childProductId` (the bit only shop-variations knows), and save themselves rather than via the editor's Save button, because a 40 MB file held as a pending edit is a lie. Fifty variants share one fetch via a module-scoped store, not fifty identical requests. Previously: **3D models on the shop, and a second, additive gallery extension point to carry them.** `shop.gallery-media` (shop v0.1.43, `modules/shop/lib/gallery-media.ts`) exists because `shop.product-detail-parts` is winner-takes-all: shop-variations already claims Gallery on every product with options, so a would-be second claimant could never reach the products that most need 3D. The new point is additive - a module contributes extra thumbnails and a stage takeover, shop supplies the strip and its own class names and never learns what the item is - so every provider resolves rather than only the first, and one whose `load` throws is dropped and logged rather than taking the product page down. Resolved once per page in `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx` and carried on `DetailPartContext.galleryExtras` by the injector, **not** awaited inside the part: `wrapResponsiveRender` calls a block's `render` as a plain function. `load` is server-only and its payload crosses the RSC boundary (so JSON-serialisable); `Thumbs`/`Stage` are client components, because a function cannot make that crossing - which is why narrowing to the chosen variation is the provider's own job. All three galleries render extras: shop's `ProductGallery`, shop-variations' `VariantSlotGalleryClient` (passing the chosen child id, the bit shop cannot know) and its granular `ShopVariantGallery` (which covers shop's slot, so it is the only strip on those layouts). New module **product-3d-views-for-shop** (`p3d_`) rides it: a variation IS a hidden child `shp_products` row, so a model keys off a plain product id and the module needs no notion of variants - shop-variations stays optional, probed with `to_regclass` per `product-attributes-for-shop`'s bridge. **DWG and USDZ are rejected at upload**: DWG has no JS loader at all and USDZ is Apple-AR-only, so neither can drive an inline viewer and accepting them would store a file nothing could draw. Every thumbnail on a page shares **one** WebGL context (blitted to 2D canvases) - a context each hits the browser's ~8-16 cap and silently blanks the oldest. `three` joins core's dependencies, which is how `leaflet`, `imapflow` and the watermark-remover package already work. v0.1.0 was published naming `requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.464 before a parallel agent released that version without `three`; corrected forward to v0.1.1 naming 0.5.465 rather than rewriting a published tag. Also: **the material configurator can now be scaled by overall WIDTH instead of overall height (product-3d-views-for-shop, v0.1.57)** - `FabricConfig` gains `scaleAxis: 'height' | 'width'` (zod default `'height'`, so every saved config reads back unchanged) and `modelWidths`, the panel measures and stores both bbox extents on every Detect/save so switching axis needs no re-read, and `tileRepeat`'s terms are renamed `{realCm, modelUnits}` since the ratio is axis-agnostic. One or the other, never both.) (**Shop: Variant Options gains a "Colour & image previews" setting (shop-variations).** New Puck field `swatchPreview: 'show' | 'hide'` (default `show`) on the Product Detail block, independent of `swatchDisplay`. On `show` a hover chip pops a bigger look at a colour/image choice - the picture at 200x200, or a 160x90 block of the colour, which the 16px dot never conveyed; the old image-only hover peek (`ImageSwatchThumb`) is folded into one `ValuePeek`/`ValuePreview` pair. In the swatch-only look the preview sits ABOVE the value's name in the same chip. The accordion layout dropped `overflow: hidden` from each section - it was slicing every preview off at the section border - and the header/panel round their own corners instead.) (**Twilio v0.1.22: settings page redesigned into five sub-tabs, plus nine new features.** `TwilioSettingsTab` split into Account / Phone numbers / Call handling / Texting / Alerts & data via the core `TabStrip`; `TwilioForwardingSection` now edits one number at a time with an unsaved-changes marker. New: live Test connection, voicemail + missed-call email alerts, auto-text to missed callers, holiday closure dates, send-a-test-text, voicemail transcription, withheld-caller handling, nightly recording retention sweep (first cron job in this module), an optional second forwarding number, and a rolling twelve-month bank-holiday importer covering England and Wales, Scotland, Northern Ireland, the Republic of Ireland and the United States. Module migration `008_call_features_and_settings.sql` adds six `tw_forwarding_rules` columns, two `tw_voicemails` transcription columns and the new `tw_settings` singleton table. Backup round-trip re-run green (3/3) on the OVH VPS.) (**Product: Tabs strip gains its own background.** `bgColour` (light + dark arms in one `light-dark()` value via core `SiteColourField`) and `bgOpacity` (0-100) on `shopDetailTabsPuckComponent`; opacity is folded into each arm as a `color-mix`, and the block emits `--spd-tabnav-bg` (over transparent, the shell's fill) plus `--spd-tabnav-fade` (the same colour composited onto the page background, used by the edge fades/arrows so a see-through colour isn't painted twice). Blank colour = previous behaviour exactly. Also fixed: on a small phone the scroll-spy could light a tab sitting off the right-hand edge of the scrolling strip - `ProductSectionTabs` now scrolls the active pill into view on `active` change.) (**Product 3D views: material calibration now keyed by model file, not by row.** `FabricConfig.modelHeights`/`modelWidths` stored a measured bounding-box extent per `p3d_models` id; detaching and re-attaching the same model across a product's variations writes fresh rows, which stranded every measurement and dropped the whole product to `repeat: 1` - silently, since the colours still painted, so a changed swatch size appeared to do nothing. Both maps are now keyed by the model's url in `components/admin/FabricConfigPanel.tsx`, read through the new pure `measuredUnitsFor()` in `lib/fabric/resolve.ts` (legacy id keys still translated through the product tree while their rows exist; stranded keys dropped on the panel's next load). product-3d-views-for-shop 0.1.59 -> 0.1.60. An existing config only recovers once its material configurator is opened and saved again.) (**Product 3D views: calibration keys are the UNSIGNED model url.** v0.1.60 keyed `modelHeights`/`modelWidths` by the url as the admin panel received it, but `getAdminModels` signs every url (`?t=<expiry>.<token>`) so the browser may fetch it, while the storefront resolver reads the plain `p3d_models.url` - so the two never matched and every fabric surface stayed at `repeat: 1`. New `modelScaleKey()` in `lib/fabric/calibration.ts` strips the query; applied when writing (`FabricConfigPanel`) and when reading (`measuredUnitsFor`, `isCalibrated`), so configs already saved with signed keys come right on read without a second save. Also stops the key rotting when the asset token expires. product-3d-views-for-shop 0.1.60 -> 0.1.61.) **Push keeps the owner's spreadsheet formulas.** `pushProductsTab`/`pushVariationsTab` no longer `clearTab`+`writeGrid`: new `lib/push-grid.ts` (`pushGrid`) reads the tab first via new `readGridWithFormulas` (`spreadsheets.get?includeGridData` with a `fields` mask for `userEnteredValue,effectiveValue`), plans which formulas may survive with new pure `lib/formula-preserve.ts`, writes the grid RAW as before, clears only the rows/columns the catalogue has given up (new `clearRange`), then restores the surviving formulas with new `writeFormulaRuns` (`values:batchUpdate` at USER_ENTERED - the module's only interpreted write, and it only ever receives formula text already in the sheet). A formula survives only when its row index, column index and computed result are all unchanged; anything else flattens to the database value. Columns to the right of the pushed grid are never written or cleared any more, so helper columns and ARRAYFORMULAs live there safely. Unit-tested in `lib/formula-preserve.test.ts` (19 cases).

Flat factual inventory of the platform's routes, models, permissions, modules, env vars, components, scripts, and config - the current state, not a changelog. Per-release history lives in git and the GitHub releases. Update the affected sections plus this date after any substantive change.

---

## Core Application

### Routes

Pages (public):

- `/` - `app/(public)/page.tsx` - redirects to `/setup` until setup completes; renders the InfoPage set as `homepageId` (draft only for admins, with draft banner), else a welcome card with siteName/tagline/description. `force-dynamic`.
- `/[slug]` - `app/(public)/[slug]/page.tsx` - renders an InfoPage by slug; drafts 404 for non-admins; `generateMetadata` (title, metaDescription, OG image), `generateStaticParams` for published slugs, `revalidate = false`. On an InfoPage miss, falls back to a module's public index via `resolveModulePublicPage(slug, [])` (InfoPage always wins a collision) - calls `getSessionFromCookie()` first so that fallback path always renders dynamically rather than being cached under `revalidate = false`.
- `/[slug]/[...path]` - `app/(public)/[slug]/[...path]/page.tsx` - generic catch-all for a module's public sub-pages, via `resolveModulePublicPage`. `force-dynamic`.
- `/[slug]/feed.xml` - `app/(public)/[slug]/feed.xml/route.ts` - delegates to a module's `feed.xml` route via `dispatchModulePublicRoute`; a dedicated literal segment because `route.ts` can't share a folder with the `[...path]` page catch-all. `force-dynamic`.
- `/[slug]/[a]/feed.xml`, `/[slug]/[a]/[b]/feed.xml` - `app/(public)/[slug]/[a]/feed.xml/route.ts`, `app/(public)/[slug]/[a]/[b]/feed.xml/route.ts` - generic nested-feed delegates (Boards' per-board and per-sub-board RSS), same passthrough pattern one and two segments deeper. `force-dynamic`.
- `/logged-out` - `app/(public)/logged-out/page.tsx` - client page, 3-second countdown then redirect to `/`.
- `/page-preview/[id]` - `app/(public)/page-preview/[id]/page.tsx` - draft preview of an InfoPage; requires session + `pages.read`; always renders `builderData` with a fixed preview bar; noindex.
- `/layout-preview/[id]` - `app/layout-preview/[id]/page.tsx` - preview of a Layout; requires `layouts.manage` (was `isAdmin`, i.e. the protected role only - so the Preview button 404'd for every non-Admin role that had been granted layouts.manage); renders with the type-matched Puck RSC config plus placeholder content blocks; noindex. Outside the `(public)` group so header/footer are not applied.
- `app/(public)/layout.tsx` - public shell: resolves header/footer Layouts via `resolveThemeLayout`, injects design-token CSS + Google Fonts link, `AosInit`, `ConsentBanner` when enabled, favicon override from `faviconMediaId` (plus a `prefers-color-scheme: dark` icon from `faviconDarkMediaId` when set), and threads `logoDarkUrl` into the header/footer template context for the dark-mode logo swap.
- `app/layout.tsx` - root layout: Instrument Sans + JetBrains Mono fonts, theme flash-prevention inline script (`localStorage cactus-theme` → `data-theme` attribute), consent-init inline script (`cactus-consent` cookie → `window.__cactusConsent`, deny-by-default). Now uses `generateMetadata`/`generateViewport` (not a static `metadata` export) reading `resolveBranding()` (`lib/config/branding.ts`, React-`cache()`d) so the site's icons + app name + theme colour apply on EVERY route (fixing the default-cactus-favicon fallback); a custom favicon fully replaces the cactus svg/png/ico set (+ optional dark variant via `prefers-color-scheme`). The web-app manifest is generated dynamically by `app/manifest.ts` (`force-dynamic`, reads `resolveBranding`, served at `/manifest.webmanifest`); the old static `public/site.webmanifest` was removed.
- `app/not-found.tsx` - 404 page; renders the resolved `notFound` Layout via Puck if published, else a plain 404 card. `force-dynamic`.
- `app/robots.ts` - dynamic robots.txt; disallow-all when no site URL, `hideFromCrawlers`, or status ≠ live; else allow with disallows for `/cactus-admin/`, `/setup/`, `/cactus-status/`, `/api/`.
