- Hosted settings panels (`host` on a `settingsTabs` entry): a `settingsTabs` entry that sets `host: "<slot-name>"` is **not** a top-level Settings tab. `app/cactus-admin/config/page.tsx` resolves and renders it server-side (via `moduleSettingsTabComponents`) into **two shapes** (both defined in `lib/modules/hosted-settings.ts`), passed through `ConfigPageClient` to each module settings tab: `hostedSettingsSlots: Record<slot, ReactNode>` (the panels for a slot merged into one node - for a host that just drops them into a section of its own UI) and `hostedSettingsPanels: Record<slot, {id, label, node}[]>` (the same panels kept separate, each still carrying its manifest `id`/`label` - for a host that gives each panel its own tab, which needs the label up front). A host takes whichever it needs; both are always passed. `host` is now declared in the manifest zod schema (`lib/modules/manifest.ts`, optional). `app/cactus-admin/layout.tsx` skips `host`-ed tabs when building the command-palette `moduleSettingsTabs` list (no `/config?tab=` destination exists). Live uses: gocardless-instant-bank-pay-for-shop's "Instant Bank Pay" panel sets `host: "shop.payments"` (merged shape), rendering inside **admin > Shop > Payments** below the Stripe/PayPal cards; product-3d-views-for-shop's "3D Viewer" panel sets `host: "shop.settings-sub-tabs"` (labelled shape), rendering as its own sub-tab in **admin > Shop**. Both slot names are owned/rendered by the shop module (`modules/shop/components/admin/ShopSettingsTab.tsx`); core stays module-agnostic. An empty slot renders nothing, so a shop with no add-ons installed shows no extra tab.

Settings keys stored in the database = the SiteConfig columns (types and defaults listed in the Database Schema section). `designTokens` (Json) holds the v2 design-token object (defaults in `lib/design/tokens.ts:DEFAULT_DESIGN_TOKENS`: primary #2c7558/#459578, secondary white/#0f172a, system-ui font, heading sizes 2.5rem→1rem, link colours, status accents info #3b82f6 / success #16a34a / warning #f59e0b / error #ef4444 with brighter dark siblings, blockPadding 1.5rem, tabletBreakpoint 1024px, mobileBreakpoint 640px). `consentBannerConfig` (Json) holds `ConsentBannerConfig` (defaults in `lib/consent/types.ts`: disabled, bottom-bar, four categories necessary/preferences/analytics/marketing, reConsentDays 365, retention null, versions 0).

Client-side storage keys used by the admin: `localStorage cactus-theme`, `localStorage cactus-sidebar-collapsed`, `localStorage cactus-sidebar-sections-collapsed`, `localStorage cactus-sidebar-favourites`, `localStorage cactus-sidebar-recents`, `sessionStorage cactus-core-update-check`, `sessionStorage cactus-module-update-check-<id>` (both 10-minute throttles).

Credentials/env vars are never stored in the database; they are written to Vercel project env vars via `/api/admin/env` (read-only display in local mode).

### Puck Integration

- Library: `@puckeditor/core` ^0.22. Editor components (`<Puck>`) are client-only, lazy-loaded with `ssr: false`; public rendering uses `<Render>` from `@puckeditor/core/rsc`.
- **Custom field widgets reach `config.tsx` through a registry, never a direct import** (`lib/puck/fields/registry.tsx` + `lib/puck/fields/editor.ts`). The 14 sidebar widgets are all `'use client'` and `ResponsiveValueField` imports the Puck editor entrypoint, so importing one from `config.tsx` (which has no `'use client'`) opens a client boundary in the RSC graph and drags the whole editor, plus its vendored TipTap/ProseMirror, into every public page's bundle. `registry.tsx` exports server-safe proxies typed via `import type` (erased, no runtime edge); `editor.ts` (`'use client'`) holds the only real imports and is imported solely by `PuckEditor.tsx` / `LayoutPuckEditor.tsx`, which call `registerEditorFields()` at module scope. The same registry also carries the RichTextBlock `renderMenu` renderer (`RichTextMenuWithLink`), not just sidebar field widgets, for the same bundle-isolation reason - it imports the Puck editor runtime. `lib/puck/fields/registry.test.ts` fails if the two lists drift or if anyone reinstates a direct import - without it a missing registration renders the field as nothing, silently.
- Central config: `lib/puck/config.tsx` (safe for both editor and RSC paths; no hooks/browser APIs). Exports: `puckConfig` (default, full-page editor), `puckRscConfig`, `footerPuckConfig(+Rsc)`, `layoutPuckConfig(+Rsc)` (adds `ContentSlot`), `headerPuckConfig(+Rsc)`, `fullPagePuckConfig(+Rsc)` (aliases of puckConfig). RSC variants swap `SiteLogo` to an RSC renderer and replace the `richtext` field type with textarea (TipTap JSON is converted to HTML via `@tiptap/html` for RSC rendering).
- Root ("nothing selected") fields, right sidebar: `puckConfig.root` (pages) and `headerPuckConfig.root`/`footerPuckConfig.root` define real fields, rendered via each config's own `root.render`. `puckConfig.root` gained `bg` (`PageBgColorField`, none/colour) and `paddingY` (none/sm/md/lg, padding above the first Section and below the last) - deliberately no page-level `maxWidth`, since every `Section` already owns its own maxWidth/full-bleed background and a shared root wrapper would clip it. `layoutPuckConfig.root` and `getModuleLayoutPuckConfig(type).root` still define no fields, so Puck falls back to its built-in `{title: text}` root field (`@puckeditor/core`'s `defaultPageFields`) - which would duplicate the Title/Name field our own Settings tab already owns, so `LayoutPuckEditor.tsx` passes `overrides={{fields: hideRootFieldsOverride}}` (`lib/puck/tabs/rootFieldsOverride.tsx`) whenever the active config has no `root.fields`, hiding just the field body (Puck always renders the "Page" breadcrumb header regardless). `PuckEditor.tsx` (pages) needs no such override since `puckConfig.root.fields` is always real.
- Core blocks by category - Layout: Section (background/overlay/padding/max-width/sticky/border/shadow/opacity + slot; `bgType: 'grid-scan'` renders a decorative graph-paper grid + looping scan-beam sweep behind nested content, purely cosmetic; **outer `overflow` is now conditional** - only `hidden` when the section actually clips to an edged box (borderRadius≠none, bg image, overlay scrim, boxShadow, grid-scan), otherwise `visible` so a `position:sticky` descendant - e.g. a sticky image column inside a nested Grid - isn't trapped by an overflow context it doesn't need), Grid2/Grid3/Grid4 (fixed-column-count variants, ratios, per-column align/width, `stackColumns` mobile|tablet|never - `GridBlock` derives a `stackMode` from it (falling back to the legacy `stackAtTablet:'on'`→tablet, else `mobile` for a normal grid / `never` for one already managing its own per-breakpoint columns) and emits `data-stack="<mode>"` on every grid; `buildTokenStyles` keys the collapse rules off it - `mobile` stacks to one column at the mobile breakpoint (with the 3/4→2-col tablet step), `tablet` stacks across the whole tablet band and below, `never` holds the columns at every width. The stack rules outrank a grid's own scoped `[data-grid-id]` override, so an explicit stack choice stacks even a Manual-width grid. Per-column widths (`col{n}Width`) now only apply in Manual `columnSizes` mode (per breakpoint), so switching the preset back to Equal drops stale custom widths immediately instead of a lingering width silently winning, per-column `col{n}Sticky` off|on + `col{n}StickyOffset` - `on` pins that column's grid track (`position:sticky`, `top:offset`, `align-self:start` so the box stays content-height inside the full-height row and has room to travel) while the taller sibling scrolls; the track carries `data-col-sticky` and the block emits media rules dropping it back to `position:static` once the grid stacks (per `stackMode`: mobile band when `mobile`/`tablet`, plus the tablet band when `tablet`; never when `never`), so a pinned image just sits in normal flow on small screens. NB the sticky must live on the track div itself, not a nested block wrapped in a Section: the per-block visibility/slot wrapper between the track and a nested block is content-height, which caps a sticky descendant's travel to zero, per-column "scale to width" (wraps that column's content in `lib/puck/components/ScaleToFit.tsx` - a client component that measures natural size + applies `transform:scale(min(1,colWidth/naturalWidth))` so any content, incl. fixed-size icon widgets like ThemeToggle/cart, shrinks to fit; transform-origin follows `col*Align`) - **no longer its own field**: `GridBlock` derives it (`colScaled`) from whether that column's `col*WidthShrunk` has a value, since a column's rendered width only ever changes at runtime via the shrink-on-scroll override; the standalone `col*Scale` radio (Grid2/3/4 and the legacy dynamic `Grid`) was removed, 2/3/4 slots respectively - split from a single dynamic "Grid" so Puck's Outline panel only ever lists the slots that variant actually has; legacy dynamic `Grid` stays registered as a safety net but is unlisted in every picker), Group (flex row/column + slot; gained `columns` responsive select auto|1-6 (`ResponsiveSelectField`) - `auto`/blank keeps the default flex-wrap flow (every legacy Group byte-identical), a number switches the slot wrapper to an equal-width CSS grid `repeat(N, minmax(0,1fr))` that reflows per breakpoint via `responsiveMediaCssFor` on the same `.group-rsp-<id>` class, so an arbitrary child count sits N-per-row and can differ desktop/tablet/mobile (e.g. 3/2/1) - the flow the fixed-track Grid2/3/4 can't do since they cap at 4 one-child tracks and orphan the odd item when a 3-track grid drops to 2 at tablet; grid branch skips the header-centring `nth-child` style), Split (ratio columns, legacy zones/DropZone API not slot fields; `ratio` gained an `auto` option 2026-07-16 - `grid-template-columns: fit-content(60%) 1fr`, sizing the left track to whatever width its content actually declares and giving the slack to the right, capped at 60% so a greedy left column can't starve the right one and floored at its min-content. Only content with a *definite* width has anything to hug - a left column of ordinary prose has no natural width and simply takes the 60%. First consumer: shop's Default Product Detail starter, whose square gallery sizes itself against the viewport height and so wants a column that hugs the photo rather than centring it in a fixed fraction), Spacer, Divider. Typography: Heading (gained `revealAnimation: 'none'|'stagger-lines'` - splits `text` on `\n` into per-line clipped spans that rise in on mount, independent of the existing scroll-triggered `aosFields` also on this block; `text` field is `textarea` to allow multi-line entry; `level` gained a `display` option - the largest level, above h2, renders as a real `<h1>` with a `cactus-display` class, styled from `themeStyle.display` tokens; also gained `highlightText` + `highlightMark` - `highlightText` is a substring that gets recoloured in `--color-primary` and wrapped in a non-italic `<em>`, and when `highlightMark: 'underline'` also carries a chunky mustard bar sitting UNDER the word (a thick `text-decoration: underline`, 0.16em / `skip-ink: none` / small offset - deliberately under the glyphs not behind them, and a solid `--color-heading-mark` token / `#E3A857` fallback rather than a translucent one so a tinted hero background can't bleed through and turn it olive) (works inside `stagger-lines` too, applied per line via the shared `renderHighlight` helper); also gained a swatch/manual colour picker (`color` is now `SiteColourField allowManual` - swatch/custom/None/typed CSS colour, legacy `dark`/`muted`/`brand` still resolve, empty = per-level heading token), whole-heading linking (`href` wraps the tag in a colour-inheriting block `<a data-heading-link>`), an optional hover underline on linked headings (`hoverUnderline` yes/no + `hoverUnderlineColor` swatch, scoped `<style>` on the id, defaults to `currentColor`), and vertical positioning (`minHeight` none/sm 240/md 400/lg 600/screen 100vh + `verticalAlign` top/middle/bottom - a set height makes the wrapper a flex column and drops the tag's bottom margin so centring is true); also gained `fitOneLine` ("Keep on one line (shrink text to fit)", no/yes, default no) - wraps the heading's content in `lib/puck/components/HeadingFitText.tsx`, a client component that measures the text's natural one-line width against the room the heading has and scales it down to fit, bringing the box height down with it; the Menu block's `fitOneLine` trick, see the dated notes at the top), TextBlock (gained `size` base/md/lg, `maxWidth` none/prose 46ch/wide 60ch and `color` secondary/muted/dark - defaults preserve the old full-width secondary-colour 1rem look; used together they turn a plain paragraph into a constrained "lede" that wraps to multiple lines like the concept), RichTextBlock (TipTap), Quote (quote/attribution/padding + optional photo; the photo is now rendered INSIDE the `<blockquote>` - first child of a flex row that also holds the text, so it sits between the left accent border and the quote - where it used to be a sibling `<img>` to the left of the whole panel, outside it. `imageSize` sets the photo's width (sm 72 / md 112 / lg 160), new `imageHeight` number field overrides its height in px (blank or 0 = square, i.e. the old behaviour; a circle shape with an unequal height renders as an ellipse, which is the point of asking), `imageShape` circle/rounded/square. All photo fields stay hidden by `resolveFields` until `mediaUrl` is set), Caption (text/align/padding, styled from `themeStyle.caption` tokens via a `cactus-caption` class - small label/footnote text usable anywhere, not just form-field labels). Actions: ButtonLink (label/href/variant/align/padding, plus six Custom-only props; 2026-07-14: `variant` gained a fourth option `custom` alongside primary/secondary/outline. The three presets take their colours from the Styles → Buttons design tokens; `custom` ignores those and paints from the block's own `bgColor`/`textColor`/`hoverBgColor`/`hoverTextColor` (each a `SiteColourField` - palette swatches + native colour picker + free-text CSS colour) and `borderWidth` (`BUTTON_BORDER_OPTIONS`: none/1px/2px/3px/4px) with `borderColor`. Any custom colour left blank falls back to the matching primary token, so a freshly-switched custom button is identical to the primary it came from; a border width chosen with no colour picked paints `currentColor`, never transparent. `resolveFields` strips all six colour/border props unless `variant === 'custom'`, and strips `borderColor` until a width is picked, so only applicable options show. Hover for `custom` is a block-scoped `a[data-btn-link="<id>"]:hover{…!important}` rule emitted by the block itself - the global hover rules in `lib/design/tokens.ts` are keyed on `[data-variant="primary"|"secondary"|"outline"]` and deliberately never match `custom`; `!important` beats the inline base style, same reason those rules carry it. `align` (2026-07-14) is a responsive select (`ResponsiveSelectField`, left/center/right) emitting `text-align` on the wrapper `div[data-btn-id]` via `responsiveMediaCssFor`, with the `<a>` staying `display:inline-block`; blank resolves to `inherit`, which for an inherited property is the same as declaring nothing, so buttons saved before the field existed keep taking their container's alignment rather than being yanked left), Phone (2026-07-15, `PhoneBlock` - click-to-call number. Registered in `puckConfig` (page/infopage), `layoutPuckConfig` (infoPage + generic layouts, in the `actions` category), `headerPuckConfig` (`actions` category) and `footerPuckConfig` (`site` category, `noGutterDefault`) - so it appears in the page/infopage editor and in every layout-editor type (header/footer/infoPage/statusPage/generic), not just the plain layout config. RSC parity automatic via the shared render + the `...components` spreads in `puckRscConfig`/`layoutPuckRscConfig`/`headerPuckRscConfig`/`footerPuckRscConfig`. `number` free-text (kept legible with spaces/brackets) is stripped to `[\d+]` with a single leading `+` for the `tel:` href; optional `label` overrides the displayed text (blank shows the number). `showIcon` none|mobile|always injects an inline phone SVG - `mobile` hides it by default and un-hides under `mobileMediaQuery()` via a block-scoped `[data-phone-id]` style. `mobileIconOnly` no|yes (2026-07-15): when the icon shows on phones, drops the number text under `mobileMediaQuery()` (a `[data-phone-text]{display:none}` rule) so only the dial glyph remains on mobile - the `<a>`'s `aria-label` still carries the number so taps and screen readers keep it; hidden by `resolveFields` unless `showIcon` puts an icon on mobile. Full typography set to recreate a heading-styled number: `align` responsive select, `size` sm/base/md/lg/xl/xxl (`PHONE_SIZE_MAP`), `weight` normal/medium/semibold/bold (`PHONE_WEIGHT_MAP`), `transform` none/uppercase/capitalize/lowercase, `letterSpacing` (`UnitValueField` em/px), `fontFamily` (`SiteFontField`, non-system Google families hoisted via `googleFontHrefForFamily()` + `<link precedence>`), `color`/`hoverColor` (`SiteColourField allowManual`). Underline: `underline` no|yes (base) and `hoverUnderline` ''(no change)|underline|none, with shared `underlineColor` + `underlineThickness` + `underlineOffset` (`UnitValueField`) that `resolveFields` shows when EITHER base or hover underline is on (so a hover-only underline - the common "underline the number when you point at it" look - can still be fully styled). **The underline is painted on the number `[data-phone-text]` span, not the `<a>`** (2026-07-15 fix): the `<a>` is pinned to `text-decoration:none !important` and the span carries `text-decoration-line/color/thickness/offset`, because the global `a:hover{text-decoration:underline}` in globals.css was re-underlining the link on hover at the browser's default thickness and wiping out a chosen thickness/colour (and decoration on the inline-flex link didn't reach the text reliably). Hover toggles the span's decoration via `a[data-phone-link]:hover [data-phone-text]{…}`; hover colour stays on the link (`:hover{color…!important}`). `fitOneLine` no|yes (2026-07-15) wraps the icon+number in `HeadingFitText` (same client shrink-to-fit as the Heading/Menu blocks; link is `display:block` so it has a full width to measure against). Vertical positioning (2026-07-15) mirrors Heading: `minHeight` (`BLOCK_HEIGHT_OPTIONS` incl. fill/screen, responsive) + `verticalAlign` top/middle/bottom turn the wrapper into a flex column (`PHONE_VALIGN_MAP`), desktop inline + tablet/mobile via `responsiveMediaCssFor` on `[data-phone-id]`, `blockFillCssResponsive` for fill; `verticalAlign` hidden by `resolveFields` until a height is set. **Icon visibility is stylesheet-only** (2026-07-15 fix): the icon span carries NO inline `display` - `showIcon: mobile` sets `display:none` at base + `inline-flex` under `mobileMediaQuery()`; an earlier inline `display:none` outranked the media rule so the icon never appeared on phones. `mobileIconOnly` yes drops `[data-phone-text]` under the mobile breakpoint so only the glyph shows (aria-label keeps the number). Plus the standard padding/sticky/aos/visibility fields), CTABanner. Media: ImageBlock, VideoEmbed (YouTube/Vimeo), Embed (iframe). Content: Hero, Eyebrow (pill label + optional pulsing dot; pill shape now `var(--radius-pill, 9999px)` instead of a hardcoded `9999`, shared with Badge), Card, ImageChipPanel (single `<img>` + a repeatable `chips` array field, each rendered via the standalone `Chip` component at one of 5 corner positions - deliberately an array field rather than a Puck slot, since Puck wraps each slot child in its own drag-handle `_DropZone-item` box which breaks a Chip's `position:absolute` in the editor canvas even though it renders correctly live; array-field items have no such wrapper so this block is WYSIWYG-correct in both; gained a "holo frame" set of settings - `framePadding` (none/sm/md/lg inner gutter that insets the `<img>` and rounds it to `calc(panelRadius - 6px)`), `frameBg` (none/subtle/gradient panel fill behind the inset image), `gridPattern` (reuses the Section block's `cactus-section-grid-scan` graph-paper background) and `scanEffect` (reuses `cactus-section-scan-beam` looping sweep) - the image carries no z-index so the grid stays in the background and the scan beam + chips paint over it via DOM order), Callout (info/success/warning/error boxes - colours read the `--status-{key}`/`-bg`/`-title` vars from Styles → Colours → Status boxes, falling back to the original built-in hexes), Badge (blue/yellow/red/gray colours read `--badge-{key}-bg`/`-text` from Styles → Colours → Badges, falling back to the original hardcoded pastel hexes; `primary` option unchanged, still `--color-primary-subtle`; pill shape now `var(--radius-pill, 9999px)` instead of a hardcoded `9999`), Trustline (repeatable icon+text row, 6 built-in icons), Chip (small label+value card, static-in-flow or floating over a `position:relative` parent via 5 corner presets - fine as a freestanding block, but composing several as siblings inside a `Section`'s image slot is the broken pattern ImageChipPanel replaces), Accordion, FeatureList (gained `iconStyle` emoji|glyph - `glyph` swaps the leading emoji for a 46px solid `--color-primary` rounded square holding a white line-icon from the new `GLYPH_ICONS` map (share/tag/compass/check/shield/clock/star/truck, selected per-item via `item.icon`) and renders larger Fraunces `<h3>` titles + 48ch body; `emoji` default is byte-identical to before; `.cactus-feature-glyph-row` in globals.css adds a hover lift), SpecPanel (windowed "spec sheet" card - dot title-bar + `rows` array field of `{label, value, highlight?, badge?}`; `highlight: 'true'` renders the value in bold `--color-primary`, `badge` renders a green `--color-success` pill; reuses ImageChipPanel's shadow/radius knobs), Ticker (full-bleed teal marquee band - `items` array of `{text}` + `speed` slow/normal/fast; items are duplicated in render and the `.cactus-ticker` class scrolls to `translateX(-50%)` for a seamless loop via the `cactus-ticker` keyframe, Fraunces phrases with mustard `·` separators; respects the global reduced-motion block), Stats, Logos, SocialLinks. Site: SiteHeader (gained `alignment` field - left/center/space-between/space-around - to control horizontal menu item alignment when wrapping to multiple lines; gained the full MenuBlock nav-styling set for its built-in menu: `itemFontFamily` (SiteFontField), `hoverColor`/`hoverBackground`, `activeColor`/`activeFontWeight`/`activeUnderline`(+colour/thickness/offset, extras hidden via `resolveFields` unless underline on) and `showDropdowns` hover|click - all passed through to `MenuBlockClient`), SiteLogo, Copyright, MenuBlock (gained `alignment` field - left/center/space-between/space-around - to control horizontal menu item alignment when wrapping to multiple lines; gained 3 fluid min/max fields - `itemSpacingFluid`/`letterSpacingFluid`/`itemFontSizeFluid`, each `{min, max}` plain text inputs rendered side-by-side by the new `MinMaxPairField` custom Puck field - built into a `clamp(min, preferred, max)` via `fluidClamp()` (`lib/puck/responsiveValue.ts`) that hits `min` at the site's mobile breakpoint and `max` at its tablet breakpoint, continuously shrinking item gap/letter-spacing/font-size as the viewport narrows so a horizontal menu can stay on one line instead of wrapping; empty min/max falls back to the existing `spacing`/`itemFontSize` presets untouched; applied in `MenuBlock`'s vertical branch, `MenuBlockClient` (horizontal, live), and `MenuBlockEditorPreview` (both orientations) for editor/live parity; gained `hoverColor`, `activeColor`, `activeUnderline` (none|underline) + `activeUnderlineColor` (`SiteColourField` swatches; underline-colour field hidden via `resolveFields` unless underline on) - active = exact-path match (`isActiveHref` in `MenuBlockClient.tsx`, relative hrefs only, trailing-slash/query/hash normalised) detected client-side via `usePathname`, active links carry `aria-current="page"`; underline is `text-decoration` 2px thickness / 4px offset, taking the text colour when no separate underline colour set; vertical menus route each anchor through the exported `MenuVerticalLink` client component so hover/active work there too, since the RSC branch can't know the path; gained `itemFontFamily` (new `SiteFontField` custom field - site fonts from Appearance → Styles listed first under "Your fonts" via new cached `useSiteFonts` hook, then the Google Fonts catalogue searchable, or any typed CSS font-family value; empty inherits the site font) - non-system Google families load via a React-hoisted `<link rel="stylesheet" precedence="default">` built by new `googleFontHrefForFamily()` in `lib/design/tokens.ts` (wght 400-700), emitted from `MenuBlockClient`, the vertical RSC branch and the editor preview, so a font picked only on the block still loads without being in the site tokens; `POPULAR_FONTS`/`MAX_FONT_SEARCH_RESULTS` moved from the Styles page into shared `lib/design/font-options.ts`; audit fixes: "Dropdowns open on" now actually works - `showDropdowns` reaches `MenuBlockClient` and `click` mode toggles dropdowns on click (parent-with-children click prevents navigation, closes on outside mousedown via a per-item document listener) instead of hover; `itemColor` converted from free-text to `SiteColourField` swatches (matches SiteHeader, dark-mode-safe); new `hoverBackground` swatch field replaces the hardcoded `--color-primary-subtle` hover pill (which stays as the fallback), wiring up the previously-dead prop; new `activeFontWeight` select ('' = same as items) and `activeUnderlineThickness`/`activeUnderlineOffset` text fields (bare numbers treated as px via `cssLen()`, defaults 2px/4px, hidden with the underline extras); editors now pass `alignment` to `MenuBlockEditorPreview` so the canvas honours it like the live site), LoginButton, ThemeToggle (gained a `style` select - `segmented` icon pill (default), `expand` icon+hover menu, `dropdown` icon+click menu, `text` label pill, `switch` sun/moon two-state slider, `cycle` single icon click-to-step - passed to `ThemeToggleClient`), CookieSettingsLink. Members (MEMBERS_SPEC.md Phase 7): `MembersLogin`/`MembersRegister` (embed the real login/register client forms inline anywhere), `MembersAccountLink` (sign-in/register ↔ my-account/sign-out, the header-friendly member equivalent of `LoginButton` - also registered in `headerPuckConfig`), `MemberGate`/`TrustedMemberGate` (slot-field gates - any member vs `member.trusted`), `MembersProfile` (viewer's own avatar/name/bio). Editor renders always show a fixed preview (no member session to check under an admin editing session); live rendering is async Server Components in `lib/puck/components/MembersBlocksRsc.tsx` (`await connection()` then `getMemberFromCookie()`), swapped in via `rscComponents`/`layoutPuckRscConfig`/`headerPuckRscConfig` - kept out of `config.tsx` itself so the `next/headers`-dependent import chain never reaches the editor's client bundle. Modules category is populated from generated `lib/puck/module-components.ts` (currently: `ContactForm`).
- `headerPuckConfig` block palette (2026-07-13, ImageBlock added 2026-07-15): beyond the chrome/structure blocks (SiteLogo, MenuBlock, LoginButton, ThemeToggle, MembersAccountLink, Grid2/3/4, Group, Spacer, Divider) the header editor now also offers Heading, TextBlock, RichTextBlock (Text category), ButtonLink (Actions category) and ImageBlock (new Media category) - so an owner can put a phone number, strapline, "Call us" button or a logo/badge image in the header. These are static content blocks pulled straight from `puckConfig.components`; `headerPuckRscConfig` picks them up automatically via its `...headerPuckConfig.components` spread (no RSC data override needed, unlike SiteLogo/MembersAccountLink), so editor/frontend markup stays identical.
- `footerPuckConfig` gained a Media category (2026-07-15) holding `ImageBlock` (wrapped in `noGutterDefault` like the footer's other static content blocks, since the footer root already applies its own 1.5rem gutter) - previously the footer editor had no way to place a standalone image at all (only `SiteLogo`).
- Video and Embed blocks are http(s) only (2026-07-23): `toEmbedUrl` returns null for any other protocol and `Embed` runs its `src` through `isHttpUrl` (`lib/utils.ts`) before rendering, so a `javascript:` or `data:text/html` address is refused with the block's own "could not parse" / "must be a valid http(s) address" notice rather than reaching an `<iframe>` and executing in the site's own origin. Those two notices also moved off hardcoded hex (`#fef2f2`/`#b91c1c`) onto `--color-error-bg`/`--color-error`, so they are legible in dark mode.
- Header true-centering (composable header only, `headerRootRender`/`headerPuckConfig`): a Grid column set to "Centre" (`col*Align: 'center'`) or a 3-item space-distributed Group (`justify` between/around/evenly) centres its element on the header's own centre line via a header-scoped `position:absolute; left:50%` `<style>` rule emitted by `GridBlock`/`GroupBlock`. **Fixed 2026-07-08**: `GridBlock`'s column wrapper divs now carry an explicit `gridColumn: i+1` - without it, a centred (absolutely-positioned) middle column was skipped by CSS Grid's auto-placement, so any later column (e.g. a "Right" one) collapsed into the vacated track instead of holding its own position; reproduced live on the "Centred Navigation" starter header before the fix, confirmed resolved by DOM measurement after. Gated by the unconditional `data-header-root` marker on `headerRootRender`'s `<header>` plus its `position:relative` content wrapper (the absolute containing block); inert in the footer/page content where that marker is absent. Group's "exactly 3 items" gate is pure CSS (`:nth-child(2):nth-last-child(2)`) as the item count isn't reachable in render. NOT visually confirmed (static checks only).
- SiteLogo sizing: the logo `<img>` height comes from a shared `--header-cell-height` custom property set by the `cellHeight`/`cellHeightShrunk` fields ("Element height"/"Element height when shrunk", renamed from `logoHeight`/`logoHeightShrunk`); the shrink override swaps the property under `HEADER_SHRUNK_SELECTOR`. `SiteLogoClient` (editor) and `SiteLogoRsc` (live) both fall back to the old `logoHeight`/`logoHeightShrunk` keys, so `SiteHeaderBlock` (passes `logoHeight`) and pre-rename saved data need no migration. `scripts/migrate-sitelogo-cell-height.mjs` is a dry-run-default cleanup remap, not applied.
- RichTextBlock styling (2026-07-14, extended 2026-07-15): `richTextColourCss(id, { textColor, linkColor, linkHoverColor, bulletIcon, bulletColor })` (exported from `config.tsx`) emits a scoped `.puck-richtext[data-richtext-id="<id>"]` `<style>` block from BOTH the editor render (`RichTextBlock` in config.tsx) and the published render (`RichTextBlockRsc` in config.rsc.tsx, which imports the helper) so they stay identical. **Signature changed 2026-07-15** from `(id, colour)` to `(id, opts)` - only two call sites, both updated. Rules generated: `textColor` recolours `p,ul,ol,li,h1..h6,blockquote` (leaves links alone by design); `linkColor` → `a{color}`; `linkHoverColor` → `a:hover{color}`; `bulletIcon` (select) → `ul{list-style-type:<glyph>}` from the hardcoded `RICH_TEXT_BULLET_ICONS` map (`RICH_TEXT_BULLET_OPTIONS` feeds the dropdown: default/circle/square/dash/arrow/chevron/check/star/diamond/dot - keyword or quoted-string glyph, ordered lists untouched); `bulletColor` → `ul li::marker{color}`. Stylesheet rules not inline styles: the `.puck-richtext …` rules in `app/globals.css` set explicit descendant colours a wrapper `color` couldn't beat. All colours run through `cssColourValue` (strips `[<>{};]`); bullet glyphs are hardcoded so nothing user-typed reaches `list-style-type`. Fields: `textColor`/`linkColor`/`linkHoverColor`/`bulletColor` are `SiteColourField allowManual` swatch pickers (defaults `''`), `bulletIcon` a select (default `'default'`). NO in-editor colour toolbar - these are block settings, not toolbar marks. The `richtext` field's mark toolbar IS extended (2026-07-15) via its `renderMenu` hook to add a Link button (`lib/puck/RichTextLinkMenu.tsx` `RichTextMenuWithLink`, wired on `content`'s field def and reached through the field-widget registry) - Puck's default toolbar omits the link control despite the Link mark being on. The RSC path's `withSafeRichText` swaps the richtext field for a textarea but keeps other fields (`...base.fields`), so all styling props carry through; `renderMenu` is editor-only and never runs on the RSC path.
- Section vertical padding "Full view height" (2026-07-14): `SECTION_PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` (= shared `PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` + `{value:'screen', label:'Full view height (100vh)'}`) is Section-only so CTABanner et al, which reuse `PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` + `PADDING_Y_MAP`, don't offer an option their render ignores. In `SectionBlock`, `screen` → `min-height:100vh` with the `lg` (6rem) padding as its spacing; `min-height` is emitted on EVERY breakpoint in the `responsiveMediaCssFor` decl (`auto` when not screen) because those media rules only fire when a breakpoint differs from desktop - without the explicit `auto` reset, a desktop `100vh` inline base would leak onto a narrower breakpoint that set a normal padding. Desktop base carries `minHeight` inline too.
- Section content vertical alignment (2026-07-14): `contentAlign` field, a responsive select (`ResponsiveSelectField`, top/middle/bottom, default top) on the Section block, sitting next to `maxWidth` in the sidebar. Applied to the inner content box (`[data-section-id]`), the same element that already owns the max-width/vertical-padding/min-height, so it works with "Full view height" (`paddingY: 'screen'`) - which is the case where a section actually has spare vertical room to distribute. `top` deliberately stays `display:block` rather than a flex column with `justify-content:flex-start`: block flow keeps the children's normal margin collapsing, so every Section saved before the field existed renders byte-identically; `middle`/`bottom` switch the box to `display:flex; flex-direction:column` and push the stack with `justify-content:center|flex-end`.
- Section "Edge to edge" width (2026-07-15): `maxWidth` gained an `edge` option (value `'edge'` → 100% width, listed after "Full bleed"). Every other width keeps the standing 1.5rem horizontal gutter; `edge` drops it to 0 for true edge-to-edge content (heroes, maps, full-width media). The gutter is now a per-breakpoint `pxAt(d)` helper (`pickResponsive(mwRv, d) === 'edge' ? '0' : '1.5rem'`), used in the same `responsiveMediaCssFor` call and desktop inline padding as `pyPad`, so a section can be edge-to-edge on one breakpoint only. "Full bleed" (value `none`) is unchanged - still 100% width WITH the gutter - so existing full-bleed sections don't re-flow. The declaration is folded into the SAME `responsiveMediaCssFor` call as padding/max-width/min-height (one rule per breakpoint), and every branch emits an explicit `display:` so a desktop `flex` can't leak into a breakpoint set back to `top`, the same leak the `min-height:auto` reset guards against.
- Section side padding (2026-07-17): `paddingX`, a responsive unit field (`ResponsiveUnitValueField`, units px/rem/%/vw, default `''`) sitting under `maxWidthCustom`, makes the horizontal gutter an owner setting instead of a constant. `pxAt(d)` now returns the explicit per-breakpoint value when one is set and otherwise falls back to the previous rule (`'0'` for `maxWidth: 'edge'`, `'1.5rem'` for everything else), so blank - the default, and the value every saved Section already has by omission - renders byte-identically and no data migration is needed. The reason it exists: the inner content box is border-box, so the gutter eats into the max-width rather than sitting outside it, and a "Custom max-width" of 1920px silently yielded 1872px of usable width with no control anywhere to reclaim it. Dropping the gutter for `custom` outright was rejected - `custom` is per-breakpoint, so a width chosen for desktop would have left mobile text kissing the viewport edge. Field stays visible for every width (an explicit override is meaningful over `edge` too), so `resolveFields` is untouched. Blank vs zero is distinguishable because `UnitValueInput` emits `undefined` for an empty box and `'0px'` for a typed `0`.
- Section border resolveFields fix (2026-07-14): `borderStyle: 'none'` now also strips `borderColor` + `borderWidth` from the sidebar (previously they showed regardless). Border radius stays visible either way - it rounds the section's background/image even with no border. The trim composes with the pre-existing background-mode trim (both run in one `resolveFields`, mutating a shared `result`).
- Section as in-page anchor target (2026-07-15): `SectionBlock`'s outer band `<div>` now emits `id={id || undefined}` - so the section's Puck component id doubles as an HTML anchor, and an in-page link (`ButtonLink`/`Heading` `href="#<section-id>"`) scrolls to it. Nothing rendered a real `id` before, only `data-section-id` on the inner content box, so no `#hash` link could scroll anywhere. Puck component ids are unique, so no duplicate-id risk; hand-authored ids (e.g. `home-range-section`) make readable anchors. Outer style gained `scrollMarginTop: '5rem'` so the scrolled-to top clears a sticky header. Paired with a new global `html { scroll-behavior: smooth }` in `app/globals.css` (with a `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` override back to `auto`) so same-page anchor jumps glide rather than snap. Shared render, so editor + RSC paths stay identical.
- SiteLogo alignment (2026-07-14): `align` field, a responsive select (`ResponsiveSelectField`, left/center/right, default left) rendered via `lib/puck/siteLogoAlign.ts` - `LOGO_ALIGN_OPTIONS` + `siteLogoAlign(id, align)` returning `{ justifyContent, css }`. The helper is a shared module *precisely because* `SiteLogoClient` (editor) and `SiteLogoRsc` (live) are two separate implementations of the same markup ("Mirrors SiteLogoClient exactly") and are therefore a standing drift hazard - both call it, so the two halves cannot disagree. No wrapper element: the logo's `<a>` is already a block-level flex container (`display:flex`), so it spans the width it is given and `justify-content` moves the logo inside it; the desktop value is the inline base and tablet/mobile ride a per-instance `<style>` keyed on `a[data-sitelogo-id="<id>"]` via `responsiveMediaCssFor`. Unset resolves to `flex-start`, which is what the `<a>` already did (`justify-content`'s initial `normal` behaves as `flex-start` in a flex container), so backfilling the `left` default into pre-existing blocks is a no-op - and unlike `cellHeight` above, `align` has no legacy key for the backfill to shadow. Inside a header column the `<a>` is a flex *item*, sized to its content, so there is no free space to distribute and the field is inert there; header placement stays the column's own alignment setting. `SiteHeaderBlock` renders `SiteLogoRsc` directly with neither `id` nor `align`, which the helper handles (no `data-sitelogo-id` attribute, no emitted CSS).
- Responsive (per-breakpoint) field values: beyond Grid columns + MenuBlock nav, ~25 CSS-mappable fields (alignment, text/icon/logo size, gap, vertical padding, max-width, min-height, thickness across Heading/TextBlock/Caption/Section/Spacer/Divider/Split/Grid/Group/Hero/SocialLinks/Trustline/Logos/Copyright/ButtonLink/SiteLogo - the last two added 2026-07-14) store a `ResponsiveValue<T>` and render per breakpoint via `responsiveMediaCssFor` + `pickResponsive` (`lib/puck/responsiveValue.ts`): a per-instance `<style>` keyed on Puck's `id` (a `data-*` attribute on the block root), emitting `!important` `@media` rules at 640/1024 only when tablet/mobile differ from desktop - so legacy flat data renders byte-identically. Fields that size per-item children drive them through a shared custom property (`--social-icon`/`--logo-h`/`--copy-fs`). Field UIs: `ResponsiveSelectField`/`ResponsiveNumberField`/`ResponsiveTextField` (`ResponsiveValueField.tsx`, sharing `ResponsiveFieldShell`) and the generic `ResponsiveCustomField` (`ResponsiveCustomField.tsx`, atomic per-breakpoint object). MenuBlock's `alignment`/`spacing`/`itemFontSize`/`itemFontWeight`/`textTransform` are now `ResponsiveValue<string>` via `ResponsiveSelectField` too (desktop base inline, tablet/mobile as `!important` @media rules - horizontal path keyed on the ul's `data-menu-id`/`.cactus-nav-link`, vertical path on the existing `menu-vlist-shrink-<id>`/`menu-vlink-shrink-<id>` classes; font-size media skipped when the fluid clamp owns it, gap media skipped when fluid item spacing does). Content/URL/variant/colour/boolean/animation fields, Grid `col*Align`/Group `justify` (header-centring reads them in JS), Split `ratio`, and SiteLogo dimension fields are intentionally left flat/deferred. NOT visually confirmed (static checks only).
- Shared field helpers: `paddingField` (padding presets), `aosFields`/`aosDefaults` (AOS scroll-animation type/duration/delay on visual blocks), `SiteColourField` (site-palette colour picker fetching `/api/admin/appearance`).
- Editor-only field overrides applied in the editors (not in the base config): `OgImagePickerField` (root OG image, stores Media id) + the media-library picker applied via the shared `withImagePickerFields(config)` helper (`lib/puck/MediaPickerField.tsx`), which swaps every known image URL text field in a config for `ImageUrlPickerField` in one place - covers `ImageBlock`/`Card`/`ImageChipPanel` `mediaUrl`, `Hero` `bgImage` + `imageUrl` (side image), and `Section` `bgImage`; both `PuckEditor` (pages) and `LayoutPuckEditor` (layouts/header) run their config through it, so a new image field only needs adding to the helper's `IMAGE_PICKER_FIELDS` map. `MenuCheckboxField` (page menu assignment), `MenuSelectField` + `MenuBlockEditorPreview` (MenuBlock). The shared `MediaPickerModal` now browses folders: it fetches the folder tree from `/api/admin/media/folders`, shows a breadcrumb + clickable subfolder tiles, and scopes its media fetch to the current folder (`?folder=<id|root>&type=image`) - previously it called `/api/admin/media?perPage=50` with no `folder` param, which `parseLibraryQuery` treats as root-only (`folderId: null`), so any image organised into a folder was invisible in the Puck picker. Search now spans every folder server-side (`?folder=all&q=…&type=image`, 250ms debounced) instead of the old client-side filter over the 50 loaded root items.
- Both `app/cactus-admin/pages/[id]/PuckEditor.tsx` and `app/cactus-admin/layouts/[id]/LayoutPuckEditor.tsx` fetch `/api/admin/appearance` on mount and inject the site's real `buildTokenStyles`/`buildFontHref` (`lib/design/tokens.ts`) as a `<style>`/`<link>` into `document.head` - without this the canvas only inherits the admin shell's own `buildAdminThemeStyles` (just its `--color-primary` family), so token-driven props (`--btn-bg`, heading/caption font tokens, image border/radius tokens) render wrong in the editor even though they're correct live. The pages editor was missing this injection until 2026-07-04 - button variants that read `--btn-bg` (ButtonLink `primary`) rendered as the admin's own colour instead of the site's configured button colour. **Leak caveat:** this injected `<style>` sets `:root{…--radius-lg: 9999px…}` (site large-radius default from `buildTokenStyles`' `fixed` string), which clobbers admin globals.css's own `:root --radius-lg: 12px` for the whole document. Admin chrome that portals to `document.body` (the `NotificationBell` `.admin-bell-dropdown`) therefore inherited the pill radius and rendered as a circle on editor pages. Fix: admin chrome uses a dedicated `--admin-radius-lg` var (globals.css `:root`, 12px) that the token injector never emits, so it stays put.
- Data shape read/written: Puck `Data` JSON (`{content: Block[], root: {props}, zones}`). Storage fields - `InfoPage.builderData` (working draft, written by autosave), `InfoPage.publishedData` (live copy, written only by the publish endpoint), `InfoPage.history` (previous published blobs, cap 10), `Layout.builderData` (working draft), `Layout.publishedData`/`publishedAt`/`publishedById`/`history` (mirrors InfoPage's publish/archive pattern, written by the layouts PATCH route when `status: 'published'` is set). Page metadata (title/slug/status/metaDescription/ogImageId/menuIds) is mirrored into `root.props` for editing and reconciled back to real columns on save; `status` in root.props is never trusted from the client.
- Editor left sidebar: both editors pass a `plugins` prop to `<Puck>` (`@puckeditor/core`'s extension point - a `Plugin` with `label`/`icon`/`render` becomes a new sidebar tab, added alongside the built-in Blocks/Outline tabs; `usePuck()` inside a plugin's `render()` gives `{appState, dispatch, selectedItem}`, root props are edited via `dispatch({type:'replaceRoot', root})`). Shared factory `lib/puck/tabs/createPanelPlugin.tsx`. Tabs: Settings (`PageSettingsTab`/`LayoutSettingsTab`), SEO (`SeoTab`, pages only), Conditions (`DisplayConditionsPanel`, layouts only - previously injected via an `overrides.fields` hack, now a real tab), History (`PageHistoryTab`, reused for both pages and layouts), Saved Blocks (`SavedBlocksTab`, both editors - saves the `usePuck().selectedItem` snapshot to the `SavedBlock` table, re-inserts via a `dispatch({type:'insert'})` immediately followed by `dispatch({type:'replace', data: {...snapshot, props:{...snapshot.props, id}}})` to land the saved props under a freshly-generated id, mirroring Puck's own internal `insertComponent` helper. **Both dispatches target `destinationZone: 'root:default-zone'`** - Puck's `rootDroppableId` (`rootAreaId` `'root'` + `rootZone` `'default-zone'`); an earlier bare `'default-zone'` never matched the insert reducer's `zoneCompound === action.destinationZone` check, so Insert silently did nothing).
- Outline sidebar drag-and-drop (both editors, since 2026-07-14): Puck's own Outline tab is select-only - its `Layer` rows are plain `<button>`s with no dnd hooks, so blocks could only be rearranged by dragging on the canvas. Replaced by `lib/puck/outline/OutlineTree.tsx`, wired as `overrides.outline` in both editors. `overrides.outline` is a **wrapper** around Puck's default `LayerTree` (Puck renders `<Wrapper>{<LayerTree/>}</Wrapper>`), so the override simply ignores its `children` and renders its own tree instead. Rules of the road: (1) the tree is built from **public app state only** (`usePuck().appState.data` + `config`) - Puck's `state.indexes` is private and unavailable through `usePuck`, so `lib/puck/outline/tree.ts` walks `data.content` (root), slot props (any config field with `type: 'slot'`, e.g. `Columns.col1`), and legacy `data.zones` (the `puck.renderDropZone` API, still used by `Split`). Zone compound ids are `${parentId}:${slotOrZoneName}`, root is `root:default-zone`. (2) Reordering dispatches Puck's `{type: 'move', sourceZone, sourceIndex, destinationZone, destinationIndex}` - **within one zone Puck removes before it inserts**, so an insertion point below the item's current slot shifts up by one (`computeMove` in `tree.ts`, unit-tested in `tree.test.ts`). (3) Hover-highlight and scroll-to-block parity is kept without importing internals: Puck attaches its own `mouseover`/`mouseout` listeners to each canvas element and tags it `data-puck-component="<id>"` inside the `#preview-frame` iframe, so the outline dispatches synthetic `MouseEvent`s at that element rather than reaching for Puck's private `ZoneStore`. (4) Drops into the dragged block's own subtree are refused (`zoneIsInsideItem`), which is what stops a container being dropped inside itself. Drag is hand-rolled on pointer events (no dnd-kit dependency): 4px threshold for mouse, 220ms hold for touch so the panel still scrolls, Escape cancels, hovering a shut container for 500ms opens it, and the panel autoscrolls near its edges. Alt + arrow keys move a focused block (up/down within its zone, left out to the parent, right into the previous sibling's first slot), so reordering is not mouse-only.
- Editor chrome, both editors: page/layout no longer wrap `<Puck>` in their own topbar (back link, name, status badges, delete button). Instead: (1) `overrides={{header: createBackLinkOverride(backHref, label)}}` (`lib/puck/tabs/headerBackLinkOverride.tsx`) overlays a back-arrow link into the blank gutter Puck's own header already reserves left of its title on desktop (`_PuckHeader`'s `padding-left`, matching the pluginbar's width) - see `.cactus-puck-back-link` in `sidebarOverrides.css` (hidden below Puck's own 638px breakpoint, since that gutter doesn't exist on mobile and the link would overlap the mobile header's own content). (2) `<Puck headerTitle={...}>` sets what Puck's header shows instead of falling back to its default "Page" - layouts pass `getLayoutTypeLabel(layoutType)` (`lib/layout/layout-type-labels.ts`, since layout root props have no `title`), pages need no override (Puck's own fallback already reads the page's real title via `root.props.title`). (3) Name/description/priority/status live in `LayoutSettingsTab` (status is a plain draft/published `<select>`, PATCHing `{status}` directly - the same API-side publish/archive/display-conditions-validation logic in the layouts PATCH route fires regardless of whether `status: 'published'` arrives via this dropdown or Puck's own Publish button); title/slug/status/delete/preview live in `PageSettingsTab` (Delete opens the confirm-modal owned by `app/cactus-admin/pages/[id]/page.tsx`, Preview links to `/page-preview/[id]`). Saving/error feedback that used to live in the removed topbar now renders inline in `LayoutSettingsTab`; `PuckEditor.tsx` (pages) keeps its own inline status strip (saving state, publish errors, Published badge, "View live page" link) below the header, unaffected by this change.
- `_PuckLayout` (Puck's own root layout element) hardcodes `height: 100dvh`, assuming it always fills the full device viewport. Both editors nest it below other chrome (previously the removed topbars; still true generally for any future wrapper), so the real box it sits in is shorter - Puck rendered oversized regardless and the wrapper's `overflow: hidden` clipped the excess off the bottom, silently truncating the right sidebar's field list with no way to scroll to the missing part. Fixed by forcing `height: 100%` on `[class*="_PuckLayout_"]` in `sidebarOverrides.css` (imported by both editors) so it fills its actual parent box.
- Page resolution/rendering: public pages call `renderInfoPageContent` (`lib/puck/renderInfoPage.tsx`) - published pages render `publishedData` (fallback `builderData`), drafts render `builderData`; an `infoPage` Layout is resolved via `resolveThemeLayout` and the page content is injected into the layout's `ContentSlot` (`renderLayoutWithContent`). Markdown-format pages render sanitised HTML inside the same layout mechanism, then run `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` over the result (obfuscate-after-sanitise order invariant - see Email spam-protection).
- Layout resolution: `resolveThemeLayout(type, ctx)` picks the highest-scoring published Layout whose `displayConditions.include` matches the render context; exclusions veto. Scores: page_id 100, page_slug 90, homepage/not_found/coming_soon/maintenance 80, module 50, path_prefix 40, entire_site 10; ties broken by `priority` then `updatedAt` ordering.
- Server-side data resolution before render: `resolveTemplateData` deep-clones the blob and injects live values - MenuBlock/SiteHeader get resolved menu trees (`resolveMenu`/`resolveMainMenu`), SiteLogo/Copyright get siteName/logoUrl/year, LoginButton gets isLoggedIn/adminPath.
- **Changed 2026-07-08**: no background autosave in either Puck editor - content only writes to the DB on an explicit Update/Publish click (was: pages 1.5s debounce → `/autosave`; layouts 1.2s debounce → layout PATCH). Both editors track a local "unsaved changes" flag: warns via `beforeunload` on a real navigation/reload/close, and via a `confirm()` on the in-app "Back to Pages"/"Back to Layouts" link (`createBackLinkOverride` in `lib/puck/tabs/headerBackLinkOverride.tsx`, which a client-side `<Link>` nav would otherwise skip past unnoticed). `doAutosave`/the layout PATCH endpoint themselves are unchanged and still used by explicit actions (Update, History restore). **Fixed 2026-07-08**: `hasUnsavedChanges` was originally threaded into `createBackLinkOverride` as a plain boolean, which meant both editors' `puckOverrides` `useMemo` needed it in their deps - it flips false→true exactly once (the first real edit after page load), which recreated the *entire* overrides object and made Puck reinitialise mid-edit (reported as: first field edit after load kicks focus out and scrolls the sidebar to the top; every edit after that is fine, since the flag never flips again until the next Update/publish resets it to false). `createBackLinkOverride` now reads `hasUnsavedChanges` via a React Context (as of 2026-07-14 `EditorDirtyProvider`/`useEditorDirtyState` in `lib/puck/tabs/editorDirtyState.ts`, formerly `UnsavedChangesProvider` in this file) instead of a constructor argument, so the override factory call - and thus `puckOverrides`'s identity - no longer depends on it at all; the override component just reads the live value on its own render. (Two earlier attempts - a mutable ref read inside the click handler, then a `useCallback` wrapping that ref - both got flagged by the `react-hooks/refs` lint rule, which treats any ref-derived value passed into a function called during render as unsafe regardless of when it's actually invoked.) Publish flows: pages via `/publish` (history snapshot), layouts via PATCH `status: 'published'` (requires include rules).
- Module-declared layout types (generic mechanism, first used by Directory/Gazette/Boards, later also Shop): a module manifest can declare `layoutTypes: { groupLabel, types: [{key, label, starterImport?, starterExport?, editorPreview?}] }`, extending the core `Layout.type` enum (`header|footer|infoPage|notFound|statusPage|<module-type>`) with camelCase types like `directoryCategory`/`directoryEntry`/`shopProduct`. `scripts/generate-module-layout-types.mjs` collects these into two gitignored files: `lib/layout/module-layout-types.ts` (`moduleLayoutTypeGroups`, `moduleLayoutTypeToGroup` lookup) and `lib/setup/module-starter-layouts.ts` (`moduleStarterLayouts: Record<type, () => Template[]>`). `puckBlocks[]` entries gain an optional `layoutTypes: string[]` tag (a block can be tagged into more than one type - e.g. Shop's `ShopProductGrid` serves `shopIndex`/`shopCategory`/`shopCollection` at once, `ShopUpsellProducts` serves both `shopProduct`/`shopCheckout`); `scripts/generate-module-puck.mjs` additionally buckets tagged blocks into `moduleComponentsByLayoutType`/`moduleRscComponentsByLayoutType` (both exported from `lib/puck/module-components.ts` alongside the existing flat maps - purely additive, untagged blocks are unaffected). `lib/puck/config.tsx`'s `getModuleLayoutPuckConfig(type)`/`getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig(type)` build a scoped Puck config per module layout type: that type's tagged blocks plus the shared layout/typography/actions/media/content categories (deliberately excludes site/members - chrome-only concerns). The admin Layouts list/wizard (`app/cactus-admin/layouts/{page,new/page}.tsx`) render one extra top-level tab per module group, with a second-level `TabStrip` for that group's sub-types (e.g. Directory → Category/Entry, Shop → Shop Home/Category/Collection/Product/Checkout/Confirmation) when selected - **but only for modules the site has actually installed**. The two generated files above list every module the *build* cloned, which is every module in `modules.json`, on every install; the tabs are fed instead from `lib/layout/installed-layout-types.ts` `getInstalledModuleLayoutGroups()` (`Module.status IN ('active','update_available')` - the same gate the admin sidebar applies to nav entries), resolved by the server shell `app/cactus-admin/layouts/layout.tsx` and passed to the two client screens via `components/admin/ModuleLayoutGroupsContext.tsx` (`useModuleLayoutGroups()`). `isInstalledLayoutType()` is the matching server gate on `POST /api/admin/layouts` + `PATCH /api/admin/layouts/[id]`. `isKnownLayoutType()` stays build-time on purpose - an existing module layout must still open in its editor. `LayoutPuckEditor.tsx` and `app/layout-preview/[id]/page.tsx` fall back to `getModuleLayoutPuckConfig`/`Rsc` for any type found in `moduleLayoutTypeToGroup`; `DisplayConditionsPanel.tsx` offers only `entire_site` for unmapped types (one shared template per type, no per-instance targeting yet). Module starter templates are **not seeded at setup** - they are offered in the new-layout picker like core's, and nothing on a module's pages changes until the owner creates a layout from one and publishes it (most module pages already render a fully-working hardcoded fallback). A template can set `publishByDefault: true` to have `seedModuleDefaultLayouts(db, name)` create one ordinary published `<template-id>-live` Layout **when that module's install deploy lands** (`markModulesDeploySucceeded()`, guarded once by `Module.layoutsSeededAt` **and** by `isModuleInBuild(name)`), for a module page with **no** hardcoded fallback - Shop's `shopIndex`/`shopProduct`/`shopCheckout`/`shopConfirmation` are Puck-only end to end (formerly served by Shop's own now-retired single-layout table), so exactly one starter per type sets this flag and the storefront keeps working out of the box, same principle as core's header/footer. Seeding cannot happen any earlier than that deploy: a module's code only reaches the build with it, so until then its templates do not exist to copy. **`isModuleInBuild()` is the load-bearing half of that guard** (2026-07-16): `markModulesDeploySucceeded()` does **not** necessarily run on the deploy it is reconciling - the webhook/status-poll is served by whichever instance is live, routinely the *previous* build, which has no copy of the module's code. There `moduleStarterTemplates(name)` is empty, so seeding wrote nothing while the caller stamped `layoutsSeededAt`, turning "seed once" into **never**: on dwoffice.furniture the Shop was stamped 17s *before* its own migrations first ran, so `shopProduct`/`shopIndex`/`shopCheckout`/`shopConfirmation` never existed and every product URL 404ed (Puck-only, no fallback). "No templates" cannot tell a module that has none from one whose code is absent, so the check asks about the code directly, via the new `modulesInBuild: string[]` export that `generate-module-layout-types.mjs` emits into `lib/layout/module-layout-types.ts` (every module dir with a parseable manifest, recorded *before* the `layoutTypes` filter). A module absent from this build is skipped **unstamped**, so the deploy carrying its code seeds it properly. Recovery for already-mis-stamped installs is `seedPendingModuleLayouts(db)` (see `lib/setup/` below), not reconcile, which only runs when a module deploy finishes. (Before 2026-07-14 this ran inside `seedDefaultLayouts` at **setup**, when a site has *no* modules installed at all - which is how every fresh install ended up with Shop cart/checkout/product layouts in its database whether or not it had a Shop. `seedDefaultLayouts` is now core-only.) Layouts belonging to a module the site does not have are deleted by `pruneUninstalledModuleLayouts()` - from `ensureLayoutsCurrent()` (once per core version) and on uninstall; "does not have" means **no `Module` row AND no `ModuleMigration` rows**, so a `code_only` uninstall (which keeps both the module's tables and its migration ledger for a reinstall) keeps its layouts too. A module's `lib/starterLayouts.ts` **must stay pure data** (no server-only imports): core's picker imports the merged catalogue in the browser to draw each template's preview. Content-rendering model: the module's public page calls `resolveThemeLayout(type, ctx)`, and if a layout is published, clones `builderData` and injects live request context (slug/id/filter values) into specific tagged blocks' props via a per-module `lib/inject-*-context.ts` helper (the pattern this mechanism generalises from - Shop's original, module-specific `injectProductContext` - now itself just one more per-type helper alongside `inject-category-context.ts`/`inject-collection-context.ts`), then renders with `<Render config={getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig(type)}>` - otherwise falls through to the original hardcoded JSX byte-for-byte (Shop's Category/Collection pages only - its other four types have no hardcoded path left to fall back to, see publishByDefault above).
- **`editorPreview` - block-internal layout types.** Most layout types render as a whole page; a block-internal one (only `shopProductCard` today) is a flat list of parts that a module surface stamps into a container of its own, and that container is what arranges them (`.shop-card` picks the look from the Image part's class via `:has()` + child rules). It exists only on the surface, so editing or previewing the layout standalone had nothing around the parts: all three card templates rendered identically and `fill`'s absolutely-positioned image escaped to the canvas. A type now declares its container as pure data - `editorPreview: {className?, maxWidth?}` - carried through `moduleLayoutTypeToGroup` and read by `getModuleLayoutEditorPreview(type)` (`lib/puck/config.tsx`). Core learns a class name and a width, never CSS; the parts still emit the stylesheet themselves when no context says a surface already did.
  - The class must land on the parts' **direct parent**, and which element that is differs by path, so there are two roots rather than one shared wrapper. Editor (`moduleLayoutEditorRoot`, config.tsx): Puck's `Page` passes `children: <DropZonePure zone={rootDroppableId}/>`, a live element that renders a zone div around the parts - so the class is cloned **onto** it via DropZone's public `className` prop, and `maxWidth` goes on an outer div. RSC (`moduleLayoutStandaloneRoot`, config.rsc.tsx): ServerRender's `DropZoneRender` returns a Fragment, so a plain `<div className>` already is the direct parent.
  - **Opt-in on the RSC side**: `getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig(type, {standalone: true})` - only `app/layout-preview/[id]` passes it. Every other RSC caller IS the host surface and supplies its own container (`renderCards`' `<a class="shop-card">`, product-attributes' filter grid mirroring it), so wrapping by default would nest a second `.shop-card` inside each card. The editor config wraps unconditionally - its only caller is the standalone layout editor.
  - **Parts of such a type must set `inline: true` and attach `puck.dragRef`** to their own root element. Puck wraps every non-`inline` component in a `<div ref={dragRef}>`, which would sit between the container and the part: the part stops being a grid item, `~` stops matching siblings, and that wrapper (Puck forces `position: relative` on it) becomes the containing block an absolute part stretches to. Puck also sets `position: relative` **inline** on the `dragRef` element, outranking any stylesheet rule - hence `!important` on `.shop-card-badge` and `.shop-card-img.fill-mode`, the only two parts that must position against the card. Live pages have no wrapper and no inline style, so this is also what holds editor/RSC markup identical.
- Email spam-protection (auto, published site only): every email address an owner puts on a page is obfuscated on the live site but stays plain in the editor (`!puck.isEditing`), via `lib/email-obfuscate.tsx`. Two techniques combined: the *visible* address is emitted as numeric HTML entities, so a bulk harvester scanning raw HTML for an "@" finds nothing; and the clickable `mailto:` href is never in the served markup at all - the address rides in a `data-eml` attribute (base64 of the reversed string) which `components/EmailDeobfuscator.tsx` decodes after hydration and turns back into `href="mailto:…"`. Two surfaces are covered:
  - **Text an owner typed** - *every* block, not just the five dedicated text ones. `linkifyEmails` returns `<ObfuscatedEmail>` nodes (Heading, TextBlock, Quote, Caption); `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` rewrites text runs for RichTextBlock; and `protectText(text, obfuscate)` (a thin gate over `linkifyEmails`, in `config.tsx`) covers the free-text props on every other block: CTABanner heading/subtext, Hero heading/subheading, Card heading/body, Callout title/body, ImageBlock caption, Eyebrow, Trustline, Chip label/value, Badge, Accordion answers, Stats value/label, FeatureList title/description, SpecPanel title/rows/badges, Ticker phrases, Copyright text. Two special cases: Accordion *questions* use `maskEmailText`, not `linkifyEmails` (a click anywhere in a `<summary>` toggles the panel, so a real link there would open the mail app *and* fold the answer away); and Chip takes an explicit `obfuscate` prop, because ImageChipPanel renders it from a plain array field with no `puck` to read.
  - **Links an owner pointed at their inbox** - `emailSafeHref(href, obfuscate)` (spread in place of `href={…}`) and `maskEmailText(label, obfuscate)` (for label text sitting *inside* the anchor, which can't be linkified - a nested `<a>` is invalid HTML). Applied to every block carrying an owner-typed href: ButtonLink, CTABanner, Hero (both CTAs), Card, Copyright (footer links), SocialLinks, Logos, linked Heading, and menu items (all four anchors in `MenuBlockClient.tsx`, which obfuscates unconditionally - it has no access to Puck's editing flag and needs none). A literal `mailto:` in an href is the single easiest thing on a page for a harvester to grep, so this was the biggest hole while it was open.
  - `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` tracks three contexts: ordinary text (wrap in a protected anchor), inside `<a>` (entity-mask the text only, and swap a hand-written `href="mailto:…"` for `data-eml` via `protectMailtoAttr`), inside `<code>/<pre>` (leave verbatim - a code sample is not a contact detail).
  - **Not covered, and can't be**: `alt`/`title`/`aria-label` attributes. React escapes attribute values, so an entity-encoded address would render as the literal text `&#64;`. Attributes are the hard edge of this technique. Also skipped: the sign-in/register labels on the Members blocks (owner-typed, but an address there isn't a real scenario, and the RSC mirror in `MembersBlocksRsc.tsx` would have to move in lockstep).
  - No-JS visitors still read the entity-encoded address (just not clickable). Editor keeps the raw address so it stays editable. `a[data-eml]{cursor:pointer}` in `globals.css` keeps a protected button looking clickable in the moment before the JS lands (no href means no pointer cursor from the UA stylesheet).
  - `lib/email-obfuscate.test.ts` guards the lot - the core assertion is "no '@', no `mailto:`, no address in the rendered markup". A regression here type-checks, lints and renders perfectly; the only symptom would be a quiet rise in the owner's spam, so nothing else in the toolchain can catch it.
  - **Order invariant with the sanitiser**: on the published RichText path, sanitise FIRST, obfuscate AFTER (`sanitizeAndObfuscateRichText` in `lib/sanitize.ts`, used by `RichTextBlockRsc` in `config.rsc.tsx`). DOMPurify parses and re-serialises its input, which decodes numeric entities - so obfuscate-then-sanitise silently puts the plain address back into the served HTML. `lib/sanitize-obfuscate.test.ts` guards the order (and proves the wrong order leaks).
  - **Module client props are a third surface**: anything passed as a prop to a `'use client'` component lands verbatim in the RSC flight payload, i.e. in view-source. The contact-form block leaked `notificationEmail`/`ccEmails` this way until 0.1.28 (`ContactFormPublicConfig` display subset now crosses the boundary; the submit route re-derives the full config server-side from stored block props). Same audit applies to any new module block: never hand a client component a config object with addresses in it.

### GitHub API Integration

Client resolution (`lib/github/client.ts`): GitHub App installation token (from the `GithubAppConnection` row, private key decrypted with ENCRYPTION_KEY) → `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` PAT → throw "not configured". `getGithubToken()` returns a bearer token for raw fetches; `getAppOctokit()` gives app-level JWT auth.

**A connection row is not a connection.** `loadConnection()` resolves one of four states - `none`, `unreadable` (row present, but this install's ENCRYPTION_KEY cannot decrypt its private key), `not-installed`, `ready` - and only `ready` authenticates. `unreadable` is the normal state after restoring a backup onto a fresh install, because setup mints a new ENCRYPTION_KEY per site and the backup's ciphertext was written under the old one. Treating "a row exists" as "connected" is what made a restored site report GitHub as set up and then fail every call with OpenSSL's `Unsupported state or unable to authenticate data` (surfaced as "Update failed: ..." and "Failed to load module directory"). `getGithubConnectionStatus()` exposes the state to the admin UI; `GET /api/admin/github-app` returns `connected` (ready or not-installed), `unreadable`, and `hasInstallation`. Anything reading a stored secret it did not write must use `tryDecryptSecret()` from `lib/crypto/secrets.ts`, never `decryptSecret()`.

Octokit endpoints called:

- `repos.listForOrg` - module directory listing (org `cactus-foundation-modules`).
- `repos.getLatestRelease`, `repos.listReleases` - module and core update checks (public vs beta channels); `git.getRef`/`git.getTag` to resolve release tags to commit SHAs.
- `repos.getContent` - read `modules.json`, `.gitmodules` existence; raw `raw.githubusercontent.com` fetch (with bearer token) for `cactus.module.json` manifests, guarded by strict `parseGitHubRepo` hostname validation.
- `git.getRef`, `git.getCommit`, `git.getBlob`, `git.createBlob`, `git.createTree`, `git.createCommit`, `git.updateRef` - Git Data API commits: module registry sync (`syncModulesJson`, commit message `chore: sync module registry\n\n[cactus-deploy]`, also deletes a legacy `.gitmodules`) and core updates (`syncCoreFromUpstream`: raw tree-diff of upstream tags - no ancestry assumption - copying changed core files into the admin repo, skipping `modules/`, `.gitmodules`, `modules.json`; upstream bytes read via `git.getBlob` by sha, no 1 MB cap; text files inlined into the tree via the `content` field so their blobs are written atomically with `createTree` - dodging the blob-replication race that surfaced as `GitRPC::BadObjectState` - and only binaries go through `createBlob`; optional modules.json pin in the same commit; BadObjectState retry with backoff on the residual binary path).
- `apps.getInstallation` - resolve the installation account after install.
- Raw REST (fetch): `POST /app-manifests/{code}/conversions` (App creation), `PUT /app/logo` (logo upload with app JWT).

Credential storage/encryption: the GitHub App's private key, webhook secret, client id/secret are AES-256-GCM encrypted (`lib/crypto/secrets.ts`, format `iv:authTag:ciphertext` hex) with `ENCRYPTION_KEY` and stored in the `GithubAppConnection` table - the stated single exception to "secrets live in env vars". The PAT alternative lives in the `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` env var.

### Media Layer

Provider types (`lib/media/providers.ts`):

- PROXIED (served via the Cloudflare Worker): B2, R2, S3, SPACES, WASABI, MINIO, VERCEL_BLOB, SUPABASE_STORAGE.
- DIRECT (own CDN + URL transforms; Worker never involved): CLOUDINARY, IMAGEKIT.
- Endpoint scheme tolerance: `B2_ENDPOINT`/`MINIO_ENDPOINT` are user-supplied and often pasted scheme-less (e.g. `s3.eu-central-003.backblazeb2.com`), which made the AWS SDK's internal `new URL()` throw `Invalid URL` and fail **every** upload (surfaced as "Upload failed: Invalid URL"). Both the Node upload path (`normalizeS3Endpoint` in `lib/media/upload.ts`, B2 + MINIO branches of `getS3Config`) and the Worker serving path (`normalizeEndpoint` in `workers/media-worker/index.ts` `fetchS3Compatible`) now prepend `https://` when no scheme is present (an explicit `http://` is kept for self-hosted MinIO). Fix applies at read-time so an already-stored scheme-less value works with no re-entry.
- Credential whitespace tolerance: S3 credential env vars (`*_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`B2_APPLICATION_KEY_ID`, `*_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`/`B2_APPLICATION_KEY`, `*_BUCKET_NAME`, `*_REGION`, `R2_ACCOUNT_ID`) pasted from a provider console often carry a trailing space/newline, which S3 request signing rejects (surfaced as "Upload failed: Malformed Access Key Id" for the key id, "SignatureDoesNotMatch" for the secret) and fails **every** upload/download/delete. `getS3Config` (`lib/media/upload.ts`) now reads every credential through `s3Env(key)` = `(process.env[key] ?? '').trim()`, so an already-stored tainted value works with no re-entry (read-time fix, mirrors the endpoint tolerance above). Write paths also trim before storing so nothing dirty is persisted again: `POST /api/admin/env` and `POST /api/setup/configure-env` now `.map(({key,value}) => ({key, value: value.trim()}))` instead of trusting the client-side trim in `ConfigPageClient.tsx`.
- The PROXIED/DIRECT distinction is app-code only, never a DB column. `SiteConfig.mediaProvider` selects the active provider for new uploads; each Media row records the provider it actually lives on.
- Console help data (also `lib/media/providers.ts`): `PROVIDER_SETUP_LINKS` (per-provider `SetupLink[]` deep-linking each provider's own console for buckets/keys), `CLOUDFLARE_DASH_URL` (account-agnostic `?to=/:account/workers-and-pages`), `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKENS_URL` (`/profile/api-tokens`, where both the scoped token and Global API Key live), `CLOUDFLARE_TOKEN_PERMISSIONS` (the two scoped-token perms), `CLOUDFLARE_CREDENTIAL_KEYS`/`ALL_CLOUDFLARE_CREDENTIAL_KEYS` (Vercel env keys `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`CLOUDFLARE_GLOBAL_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`/`CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID`), and `WORKER_SECRET_KEYS` (per-provider Worker secret names, mirrors the wiki's `wrangler secret put` list; empty for DIRECT; Vercel Blob uses `BLOB_BASE_URL` not the Vercel env token).
- Config Media tab (credentials card, proxied only) renders: a "Where to find these" link row; a **Set up the Worker automatically** box (paste a scoped API token *or* Global API Key + email + optional Account ID → `POST /api/admin/media/deploy-worker`), which uploads the Worker to the user's Cloudflare account and writes `CLOUDFLARE_WORKER_URL`. Once a credential is saved (`envStatus[CLOUDFLARE_CREDENTIAL_KEYS.*]`) every field there goes optional, is badged **Set**, and the Deploy button un-gates on blank input (`cfCredentialReady`) - re-running the setup needs nothing retyped, and a hasty re-paste of the wrong token was the cause of the 10000 rejections. There's also and a "Prefer to set it up yourself?" `<details>` fallback with a plain-English dashboard walkthrough (create Worker, Edit code, add Variables and Secrets, copy `.workers.dev` URL). No wrangler/terminal shown on screen.
- Auto-deploy internals: `lib/media/cloudflare-deploy.ts` (Cloudflare API client: `resolveAccountId` via `GET /accounts`, `uploadWorker` PUT multipart `main_module` + `secret_text` bindings, `enableWorkerUrl` claims/enables the `workers.dev` subdomain; auth = Bearer token OR `X-Auth-Email`/`X-Auth-Key`). Worker script uploaded is `cactus-media-worker`, compat date `2024-01-01`. Worker source is transpiled from `workers/media-worker/index.ts` to `lib/media/worker-source.generated.ts` (string export `MEDIA_WORKER_SOURCE`) by `scripts/generate-media-worker.mjs` (uses the `typescript` devDep; single-file type-strip, zero imports), run in `dev`/`build`, git-ignored via `.git/info/exclude`. Route `app/api/admin/media/deploy-worker/route.ts` (isAdmin, `maxDuration 60`) sources each `WORKER_SECRET_KEYS[provider]` value **and** the CF credential/account id from the request body (freshly-typed), then `getVercelEnvValues` (the project's saved values), then `process.env`; derives `ALLOWED_ORIGIN` from `SITE_URL`, deploys, then persists the CF creds (two sensitive) + URL via `upsertVercelEnvVars` + `recordDeploymentNeeded`. `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`CLOUDFLARE_GLOBAL_API_KEY` added to `SENSITIVE_KEYS` (`lib/vercel/env.ts`); all four CF keys added to `ALLOWED_KEYS` (`app/api/admin/env/route.ts`).
- `getVercelEnvValues(token, projectId, keys, target='production')` (`lib/vercel/env.ts`) reads values back off the project via `GET /v10/projects/{id}/env?decrypt=true`, for code that needs a value saved *after* the running deployment was built. **Vercel only decrypts `plain` vars: anything in `SENSITIVE_KEYS` comes back as an empty string** and maps to `null` ("set, but unreadable - only a redeploy can supply it"); keys absent from the result aren't set at all. The deploy-worker route uses that distinction to split its 400 into "never entered → enter and save it above" vs "saved write-only + site not redeployed since → redeploy from the Status tab".
- `uploadWorker` special-cases Cloudflare error **10000** ("Authentication error"): listing accounts needs far less permission than writing a script, so a credential that clears `resolveAccountId` can still be refused here. The thrown message names `CLOUDFLARE_WORKERS_EDIT_PERMISSION` (`lib/media/providers.ts`, also first entry of `CLOUDFLARE_TOKEN_PERMISSIONS`) and the account id rather than parroting Cloudflare's two words.

Upload path (`lib/media/upload.ts`): 10 MB cap; JPEG/PNG/WebP/GIF only; sharp decodes the bytes and rejects content/type mismatches. S3-compatible providers use `@aws-sdk/client-s3` with per-provider endpoints; Vercel Blob via `@vercel/blob`; Supabase via `@supabase/storage-js`; Cloudinary/ImageKit via their SDKs (key = public_id / fileId). Object keys: `media/<PROVIDER>/<folderPath>/<nanoid>-<filename>.<ext>` (legacy B2 keys have no provider segment). `uploadMedia`/`relocateMediaBlob`/`buildKey` take an opt-in `exactName` flag: when set, the sanitised filename becomes the key basename verbatim with **no nanoid** (`…/<folderPath>/<name>.<ext>`) - the caller owns uniqueness within the folder. Used by the Shop's product-image filing (see Shop module) so image urls read `shop/<category>/<product>/<slug><n>.<ext>`; `moveOrRenameMedia` forwards the same flag. **Basename clipping lives in the pure, unit-tested `lib/media/keys.ts` (`exactBaseName`, `nanoidLabel`, `MAX_EXACT_BASENAME=120`) - the two key forms carry uniqueness differently and must NOT share a clip rule.** A nanoid-form label is decoration and is clipped to 40 chars; an exact name is the only unique thing in the key, so it is kept whole to 120 chars and, past that, becomes `<prefix>-<sha256[0:10]>` (deterministic, so re-filing stays a no-op).
