- `core.admin-dashboard-widgets` (id `directory-summary`) - dashboard summary widget.
- `core.menu-entity-provider` (id `directory`, `lib/menu-entity-provider.ts` → `directoryMenuEntityProvider`) - lets the admin Menus builder link to a category or a listing.
- `core.media-usage-providers` (id `directory`, `lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) - contributes `dir_entries.images` (JSONB, returned whole as text) + `dir_categories.icon` to core's media usage index, so the library's Unused tile and delete warning can see them.

**Puck Blocks**

- No manifest-registered `puckBlocks` (nothing site-embeddable, unlike Gazette's `GazetteFeed`/`GazetteFeatured`).
- Module-private only (not in the manifest, only used inside the entry editor's own embedded Puck config and the public/preview RSC render): `DirectoryProse` - one block, richtext only (heading levels 2-4, code/codeBlock/strike/underline/horizontalRule/textAlign all disabled), same minimal single-block shape as Gazette/Boards' own prose blocks but with no pull-quote/code/image/divider siblings, since the spec only calls for one rich-text field per entry.

**Configuration**
Global, in the `dir_settings` singleton row (see Database), edited via the "Directory" tab on core `/cactus-admin/config` (`DirectorySettingsTab.tsx`, `settingsTabs` manifest entry, `directory.manage`). No `requiredEnvVars` - geocoding needs no API key, just a `User-Agent` header built from the site's own configured name.

**External Integrations**
OpenStreetMap Nominatim (free geocoding, no key, `User-Agent: "<siteName> (Cactus Directory)"` per Nominatim's usage policy), OpenStreetMap tile server (public map tiles, no key), core media (`Media.id` for the ordered `images` array, no FK), `leaflet` + `leaflet.markercluster` (new **core** runtime dependencies - modules compile inside core's Next build so map-rendering deps had to land in core `package.json`, the only core code diff this module needed besides `FIELD_NOTES.md`/wiki, precedent: `shiki` was added the same way for Gazette).

**Cron Jobs**
`0 1 * * *` → `/api/m/directory/cron/expire-featured` (clears `featured`/`featured_until` on any entry whose `featured_until` has passed); registered via `cronJobs` in `cactus.module.json`, emitted into the generated `vercel.json`. `CRON_SECRET` bearer-gated, same pattern as Boards' digest cron.

**Scripts**
None.

**Known Limitations**

- CSV import validation (required fields, lat/lng ranges, email/website format, parseable `featured_until`, duplicate-name-within-file) runs entirely client-side against the parsed file before the "ready" rows are POSTed; the server re-validates via the same zod schema but does not repeat the duplicate-within-file check (a DB-level clash is impossible anyway since `ensureUniqueEntrySlug` auto-suffixes).
- The multi-image picker (`EntryImagesField.tsx`) has no existing multi-select precedent anywhere else in the codebase to follow - it's a from-scratch generalisation of `lib/puck/MediaPickerField.tsx`'s single-select `MediaPickerModal` overlay, not a shared core component.
- `leaflet`/`leaflet.markercluster` default marker icon assets are deliberately not used (they resolve via relative image paths that don't survive Next's bundler without extra webpack config) - pins are plain CSS-coloured `L.divIcon` circles instead, sidestepping the issue entirely rather than configuring asset resolution.

### Shop

- Slug: `shop` (table prefix `shp_`), repo `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/shop`, manifest version 0.1.43, pinned in `modules.json` to v0.1.43.
- **Product image filing (v0.1.36, fixed v0.1.41):** images belong in `Shop / <master category> / <product> / <slug><n>`, and v0.1.36 filed them there on save via `reorganiseProductMedia`. In practice they sat in the library root, because two things fought it: the editor's `MediaPickerModal` POSTed to core `/api/admin/media` with **no `folderId`**, so every upload landed in the root by definition; and the same modal listed the library with no `folder` param, which `parseLibraryQuery` defaults to the **root scope**, so any image the save did file correctly then vanished from the picker - making the root look like the only place an image could live. v0.1.41: `getProductMediaFolderId(productId, {folderProductId?, masterCategoryId?})` is split out of `reorganiseProductMedia` (one definition of the target folder, shared by both paths) and exposed as `POST app/api/admin/products/[id]/media-folder` (gate `shop.products`, optional `masterCategoryId` query so a first upload follows the category picked on screen, not the last-saved one). POST, not GET, because it creates the folder: `MediaPanel` hands the picker a `resolveFolderId` callback that it calls **per upload** rather than on mount, so nothing is created for a product whose Images tab was merely opened and no upload can race ahead of a pre-fetched id. The picker appends the answer to the upload FormData and lists with `folder=all&type=image`. **Folder-aware browsing (working tree):** the same route gained a **GET** (same gate, same optional `masterCategoryId`) backed by new `findProductMediaFolderId(productId, {folderProductId?, masterCategoryId?, segments?})` in `modules/shop/lib/media/product-media.ts` - the identical path walk but look-only (mirrors `getOrCreateFolderByPath`'s cleanFolderName/skip-blank treatment), returning the deepest folder of the path that already exists, so browsing creates nothing. `MediaPickerModal` now browses per-folder like core's Puck picker (folder tree from `/api/admin/media/folders`, breadcrumb + subfolder tiles, `folder=<id|root>` scoping, search switches to `folder=all&q=`), opens at the caller's `resolveInitialFolderId` (MediaPanel and shop-variations' `VariationsPanel` pass the GET above), and keeps the selection in an id→item Map so picks survive navigating between folders. Upload still files via the POST resolver and the grid then jumps to that folder with the new image pre-ticked. Save-time filing stays as the backstop for renames, reorders and category changes, but its per-image `catch` now `console.warn`s instead of swallowing silently - that silence is why every image sat in the root with nothing reporting a problem. Relies only on core media APIs from v0.5.338 (`folderId` on the media POST, `folder=all` on the GET), the same release `reorganiseProductMedia` already needed, so no new core-version floor.
- **Picker paging + sort (v0.1.66):** `MediaPickerModal` listed a single hardcoded `perPage=50` page with no way past it and no sort control, so a folder with more than 50 images stranded the rest. Core's `GET /api/admin/media` already took `sort` and `page` and already returned `hasMore` (`parseLibraryQuery`/`queryMediaLibrary` in `lib/media/library-query.ts`) - the picker just never asked, so the fix is module-only, zero core diff. Now: a `Sort images` `<select>` in the modal header (`newest`/`oldest`/`name`/`name_desc` - core's size sorts are omitted, irrelevant when hunting a photo), a **Load more** button under the grid appending the next page (id-deduped, since an upload mid-browse shifts rows between pages), and `pageRef` reset to 1 whenever folder/search/sort changes. The upload path's hand-rolled duplicate re-fetch is replaced by a `reloadKey` counter that re-runs the listing effect, so there is one fetch shape. Inherited by every caller: shop's own media panel, `shop-variations`' variation images and `product-attributes-for-shop`'s `SwatchImagePicker`.
- **Variations hooks (v0.1.26):** shop gained three generic, reusable capabilities with `shop-variations` as the live consumer (nothing variations-specific in shop): (1) the `catalogue_hidden` product flag + `excludeHidden` filter on `listProducts` (public grid/search, admin product list, sitemap and product export all pass `true`; the public product page/route 404 a hidden row); (2) a `shop.product-editor-sections` component slot rendered below `<ProductEditor/>` on `app/cactus-admin/shop/products/[id]/page.tsx` (mirrors `shop.order-messages`); (3) a `shop.cart-line-resolver` **server-function** extension point (precedent: `contact-form.thread-messages`) consumed in `lib/checkout.ts` - `lib/line-meta.ts` collects registered resolvers, and `resolveCartLines` calls each with `(product, line.meta)`, folding a server-authoritative `priceAdjust` into `unitPrice` and a normalised `persistMeta` onto the line (failing the line on invalid input). `CartLine` gained `lineId?`/`meta?` (personalised lines merge by `lineId`, plain lines by `productId` as before), `shp_order_items.line_meta` persists it, and shop renders the `{label,value,href?}` pairs generically wherever it lists line items (cart, order confirmation, confirmation email, admin order detail, member order detail).
- Full ecommerce foundation: catalogue (products - physical/digital/service, categories, tags, collections), checkout with a pluggable payment-provider interface (Stripe, PayPal, bank transfer, cash - all four fully built), orders with per-item refunds and a manual-order-entry route, customers (derived from orders by email, no dedicated table), discounts (coupon codes + priority-ordered automatic discounts), tax (per-zone rates, inclusive/exclusive mode) and shipping (postcode-prefix zones, flat/weight-banded/free rates), back-in-stock email subscriptions, pre-orders, CSV product import/export, and related-products/upsells (manual curation with an automatic same-category fallback). Optional integration with Members (guest checkout always works; saved addresses, order history, post-purchase account prompt when Members is enabled) and Reply Catcher (shop's side of a Customer Communications tab only - see Extension Points).
- Layout system integration (core mechanism, see Puck Integration above - Shop is the 4th module on it, joining Directory/Gazette/Boards): declares `layoutTypes` group "Shop" with seven types - `shopIndex` ("Shop Home"), `shopCategory` ("Category"), `shopCollection` ("Collection"), `shopProduct` ("Product"), `shopCheckout` ("Checkout"), `shopConfirmation` ("Confirmation"), `shopCart` ("Cart", added later when the cart page joined the layout system) - more types than any other module since Shop has more distinct page kinds than a category/entry pair. 2 new blocks in `components/puck/`: `ShopCategoryHeader`, `ShopCollectionHeader` (both `[ANCHOR]`, same shape as `DirectoryCategoryHeader` - re-fetch their own data from an injected slug, nothing else to inject). Existing blocks retagged by page: `ShopProductGrid`/`ShopProductCard` → `shopIndex`+`shopCategory`+`shopCollection` (one grid block reused across all three listing contexts, exactly like Gazette's `gazetteCategory` reuse); `ShopFeaturedCollection`/`ShopCategoryBrowser`/`ShopPromoBanner` → `shopIndex` only; `ShopProductDetail`/`ShopBackInStockForm`/`ShopRelatedProducts` → `shopProduct`; `ShopCheckoutContact`/`Shipping`/`Payment`/`Review` → `shopCheckout`; `ShopUpsellProducts` → `shopProduct` + `shopCheckout` + `shopCart` (later); `ShopOrderConfirmation` → `shopConfirmation`; `ShopCartFull` (later) → `shopCart`. `ShopCartSummary` stays untagged (header-placement mini-cart widget, not part of any of these page types). `lib/inject-category-context.ts`/`lib/inject-collection-context.ts` inject `{categorySlug}`/`{collectionSlug}`; `lib/inject-product-context.ts` (pre-existing) injects `{productSlug, productId, inStock}` - unchanged, just now called from the generic path instead of the retired bespoke one. `lib/starterLayouts.ts` provides 3 starters per type (21 total) - `shopCategory`/`shopCollection` seed all-draft with the pre-existing hardcoded plain-grid pages as fallback (new templating, same principle as Directory/Gazette/Boards); `shopIndex`/`shopProduct`/`shopCheckout`/`shopConfirmation` have **no** hardcoded fallback (they were Puck-only from day one via the old table) so exactly one starter per type sets `publishByDefault: true`, carrying over the old table's default block arrangement so the storefront looks identical to before on first seed. `shopCart` is the hybrid: it KEEPS its hardcoded cart (`CartPageClient`) as a fallback like category/collection, yet still ships one `publishByDefault` starter (Cart block + upsells) so the basket is designable out of the box but can never go blank if the layout is unpublished. This replaced Shop's own pre-existing bespoke mechanism entirely (see "Retired" note under Database below) rather than running the two side by side.

**Database**
Table prefix: `shp_` (32 tables total, incl. addendum and the two shipment tables from `008`). Full DDL in `modules/shop/migrations/001_initial.sql`; later per-change files are numbered (`002_master_category.sql` adds the product master category to existing installs, idempotently; `003_category_nesting.sql` adds `shp_categories.product_display_mode` and flips the `parent_id` FK to ON DELETE CASCADE for the nested-category feature; `004_variations_hooks.sql` adds `shp_products.catalogue_hidden` BOOLEAN (purchasable but hidden from grid/search/sitemap/own URL - backs the shop-variations child rows) + index, and `shp_order_items.line_meta` JSONB (normalised per-line personalisation, `{fields:[{label,value,href?}]}`) - both mirrored in 001 for fresh installs; `008_shipments.sql` adds the `shp_shipments`/`shp_shipment_items` pair and the `PARTIAL_SHIPPED` email template for part-dispatch, likewise mirrored in 001).

- `shp_products` - name/slug(unique)/type(PHYSICAL\|DIGITAL\|SERVICE)/status(DRAFT\|ACTIVE\|ARCHIVED)/description/short_description/sku(unique)/barcode, pricing (price mandatory + optional sale_price/retail_price/trade_price/cost_price, tax_class_id FK - `compare_at_price` was retired by `migrations/005_price_types.sql`, which carries its values into sale_price/price or retail_price before dropping it; which optional types are offered is the `enabledPriceTypes` config key, and `sale_price` is the only one that changes what gets charged), inventory (track_inventory/stock_count/low_stock_threshold/out_of_stock_behaviour BLOCK\|BACKORDER, `low_stock_alerted_at` dedupe marker for the daily cron - cleared on any stock_count write so a restock re-arms it), physical dimensions, digital_file_id FK + download_limit/download_expiry, SEO fields + `og_image_id` (no FK, core Media table), `master_category_id` (FK shp_categories ON DELETE SET NULL - the product's lead category; one per product, drives its media folder path; FK added via `ALTER` after shp_categories exists since it's a forward ref, plus idempotent `migrations/002_master_category.sql` for existing installs), pre-order fields (is_pre_order/pre_order_dispatch_date/pre_order_note/pre_order_max_quantity/pre_order_count), recommendation fields (related_mode/upsell_mode AUTOMATIC\|MANUAL, related_limit/upsell_limit default 4), timestamps.
- `shp_product_media` - product_id FK cascade, type(IMAGE\|VIDEO_FILE\|VIDEO_URL), url, alt_text, position, is_primary.
- `shp_categories` - self-referencing parent_id (**ON DELETE CASCADE** since `003` - deleting a category deletes its whole sub-tree, unlike Directory's RESTRICT; product links go via `shp_product_categories`' own CASCADE, the products themselves survive since `master_category_id` is SET NULL), name/slug(unique)/description/position/`product_display_mode` (`'rollup'|'exact'|NULL`=inherit the shop default)/SEO fields. Unlimited nesting depth. `shp_product_categories` join table (no position). A product stays a member of any number of categories here; the single lead one is `shp_products.master_category_id`. `getPrimaryCategoryId()` returns the master when set, else falls back to first membership (used by automatic recommendations). Tree helpers in `lib/db/catalogue.ts`: `getCategoryDescendantIds` (recursive CTE, cycle-safe via UNION - powers roll-up listing), `getCategoryAncestorPath` (breadcrumbs), `categoryReparentWouldCycle` (reparent guard), `reorderCategories(orderedIds, parentId?)` (writes `position` = array index for the group; when `parentId` is passed - `null`=top level - also writes `parent_id`, so one call both re-parents a dragged node and reindexes its destination siblings; omitted = position-only, used by the ↑/↓ arrows), `resolveCategoryProductFilter` (slug+default → exact vs roll-up product filter), `getCategoryProductCount` (one category) / `getCategoryProductCounts` (bulk `GROUP BY` map of direct product counts, powers the admin tree's per-row count badge).
- `shp_tags` - name/slug both unique. `shp_product_tags` join table.
- `shp_collections` - name/slug(unique)/description/image_id/position/SEO fields. `shp_product_collections` join table (has its own `position` - product order within that collection).
- `shp_tax_classes` (name/code unique), `shp_shipping_zones` (name, postcodes JSONB array of prefixes - not `TEXT[]`, matches Directory/Gazette's existing JSONB-array precedent), `shp_tax_zone_rates` (zone+class unique, rate NUMERIC(5,4)), `shp_shipping_rates` (zone_id FK, type FLAT\|WEIGHT_BASED\|FREE, flat_rate/weight_rates JSONB array of `{upToKg,rate}`/free_threshold/estimated_days/position/is_active).
- `shp_digital_files` (filename/url/size/mime_type) + `shp_digital_downloads` (order_id/order_item_id/file_id FKs, unique `token`, download_count, expires_at).
- `shp_coupons` (code unique, type PERCENTAGE\|FIXED_AMOUNT\|FREE_SHIPPING, value/minimum_order_value/usage_limit/usage_count/per_customer_limit/starts_at/expires_at/is_active) + `shp_automatic_discounts` (same shape minus code/usage tracking, plus free_shipping_threshold/priority).
- `shp_orders` - order_number (unique, generated from a dedicated `shp_order_number_seq` Postgres sequence, not a COUNT(*) scheme, so concurrent checkouts can never collide), status (8-value CHECK), member_id (nullable, no FK - Members is optional), customer snapshot (email/name/phone), shipping_address/billing_address JSONB (`ShpAddress` shape), financials (subtotal/discount_amount/shipping_amount/tax_amount/total/tax_mode snapshot/currency), coupon_id FK + coupon_code snapshot, payment_method/payment_status/payment_reference/paid_at, shipping_rate_id (no FK, snapshot only) + shipping_rate_name.
- `shp_order_items` - order_id FK cascade, product_id FK **SET NULL** (product may later be deleted, snapshot fields survive it), product_name/sku/type snapshot, quantity/unit_price/tax_rate/tax_amount/total, refunded_qty, is_pre_order + pre_order_dispatch_date snapshot.
- `shp_refunds` (order_id FK, amount/reason/provider_refund_id/status/created_by) + `shp_refund_items` (refund_id FK cascade, order_item_id FK restrict, quantity/amount).
- `shp_shipments` (**migration `008_shipments.sql`**) - `order_id` FK cascade, `shipped_at` (when the parcel actually left, which is not always when it was recorded), `tracking_number`, `carrier`, `notes`, `created_at`, `updated_at`; index on `order_id`. Plus `shp_shipment_items` (`shipment_id` FK cascade, `order_item_id` FK **RESTRICT** - exactly as `shp_refund_items` does, a dispatched line is not something to lose quietly - `quantity` with a `> 0` CHECK); indexed on both `shipment_id` and `order_item_id`, the latter because the dispatched-per-line total is the hot read and it groups by that column. Same shape as the refund pair on purpose: a header row per event and a line per order item with the quantity that moved. **Dispatched quantity is DERIVED by summing `shp_shipment_items`** - there is deliberately no `dispatched_qty` counter on `shp_order_items`, so one writer, one truth, and nothing to drift when a shipment is deleted. The `ShpOrderStatus` list is unchanged: "partly/fully dispatched" is a computed display state, not a status value. Everything in 008 is idempotent (`CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`, `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`, `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS`) because 001 now creates the same tables for fresh installs.
- `shp_order_notes` (is_internal flag - false = customer-visible) + `shp_order_emails` (send log: subject/to/sent_at/trigger - `trigger` values incl. `MANUAL` for admin-composed sends and `REPLY_CATCHER` reserved for the extension point).
- `shp_saved_addresses` - member_id (no FK, bare string), label, is_default (single-default enforced app-side in a transaction), address JSONB.
- `shp_email_templates` - trigger(unique)/subject/body_html/is_active. Seeded (INSERT...ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING) with all 10 triggers: `ORDER_CONFIRMED` (has the one `{{#if hasPreOrderItems}}` conditional block the renderer supports), `STATUS_PROCESSING`/`STATUS_SHIPPED`/`STATUS_COMPLETED`/`STATUS_CANCELLED`, `PARTIAL_SHIPPED`, `ADMIN_NEW_ORDER`, `LOW_STOCK`, `BACK_IN_STOCK`, `IMPORT_COMPLETE`. `PARTIAL_SHIPPED` ("Part of an order dispatched" in the admin template list) is seeded in **both** `001_initial.sql` and `008_shipments.sql`, with `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` on each side, because the 001 seed only ever reaches fresh installs while existing shops get the row from 008 on their next deploy - whichever runs first wins and an owner's edits are never overwritten by the other. Its subject and body use two mutually exclusive `{{#if}}` flags, `hasOutstanding` and `isFinalPart`, so the same template also covers the parcel that finishes an order off.
- `shp_back_in_stock_subscriptions` - product_id FK cascade, email, member_id nullable, unique(product_id,email) (idempotent subscribe), notified_at (null = pending, retained after fulfilment for reporting).
- `shp_import_jobs` - status(PENDING\|PROCESSING\|COMPLETED\|FAILED), filename, total/processed/created/updated/skipped row counts, errors JSONB array of `{row,reason}`, column_map JSONB, created_by, started_at/completed_at.
- `shp_related_products`/`shp_upsell_products` (product_id+related_id or product_id+upsell_id composite PK, position, both self-FK cascade to shp_products) + `shp_auto_exclude_products` (per-product exclusions from the automatic-recommendation fallback).
- `shp_suppliers` (**migration `007_suppliers.sql`, v0.1.74**) - `name`, `account_number`, `discount_percent` NUMERIC(5,2) (CHECK 0-100; NULL = none recorded, which is not the same as a recorded 0%), `status` (CHECK ENABLED\|DISABLED), `contact_name`/`phone`/`email`/`address`/`notes`, timestamps. Unique index on `LOWER(name)`, since the name **is** the link to products - two suppliers differing only in case would split one supplier's product count in two. No FK from `shp_products`: the link is `shp_products.supplier` matched on name, so `renameSupplier` updates both tables in one transaction and `deleteSupplier` deliberately leaves the products' names alone (re-adding the name picks them all back up). Counts come from one grouped pass over `shp_products` split on `catalogue_hidden` - false = catalogue products, true = variation child rows - so the products/variations split works whether or not shop-variations is installed. Helpers in `lib/db/suppliers.ts`; shared create/edit validation in `lib/supplier-schema.ts`. Added to `teardown`.
- `shp_supplier_catalogues` (**migration `010_supplier_catalogues.sql`, v0.1.91**) - a supplier's own catalogues/price lists: `supplier_id` (FK -> `shp_suppliers` ON DELETE CASCADE - unlike products, which are name-linked, a catalogue only exists inside its supplier row), `name`, `sheet_url` (nullable; the Google Sheet the catalogue lives in), `position` INTEGER for the owner's ordering, timestamps. Unique index on `(supplier_id, LOWER(name))`. Written by `replaceSupplierCatalogues(supplierId, list)` - delete-then-insert in one transaction, because the editor always hands over the whole list and no id is ever shown to the owner; read by `listSuppliersWithCounts` (admin screen, one extra query for all suppliers' catalogues) and `listSupplierCatalogues` (export shape: name + status + catalogues, no count aggregate). Validation is `SupplierCatalogueInput` + the `catalogues` array on `SupplierBody` (absent = leave alone, `[]` = none; case-insensitive duplicate names rejected in Zod so the unique index never surfaces as a 500; URL must match `^https?://\S+$`). Added to `teardown` (before `shp_suppliers`, though the DROP is CASCADE anyway).
- `shp_settings` - singleton (`id='singleton'`), single `config` JSONB column holding the whole `ShpConfig` blob (Q2 decision - no `shopConfig` column added to core `SiteConfig`, everything lives in this one module-owned row instead).
- **Retired**: `shp_page_layouts` (key(unique: `index`\|`product`\|`checkout`\|`confirmation`)/builder_data JSONB) - the original single-layout-per-page mechanism, superseded by the generic `Layout` model (see Layout system integration bullet above and Puck Integration section). Dropped from `001_initial.sql` and from the shared test DB; its default block arrangements were carried forward as each type's `publishByDefault` starter so on-site appearance didn't change.

**Permissions**

`shop.access` (read-only GETs across orders/products/customers - every admin route below marked "or access" accepts this in place of its normal key), `shop.manage` (supersedes every other shop key - settings, email templates, tax/shipping config), `shop.products` (products/categories/tags/collections/CSV import-export CRUD), `shop.orders` (orders/refunds/manual payment confirmation), `shop.customers` (customer list/detail), `shop.discounts` (coupons/automatic discounts), `shop.reports` (tax/revenue reports, no read-only fallback). Enforced via `modules/shop/lib/access.ts`'s `requireShopUser(key, {allowAccess?})`/`hasShopPermission`. Page-layout editing is **not** one of these any more - since it moved onto the core Layout system, it's gated by core `layouts.manage` instead (same as Directory/Gazette/Boards' own layout types), not any `shop.*` key.

**API Routes** (all served through `/api/m/shop/…` via the generated router)

Public (`/api/m/shop/public/…`, unauthenticated unless noted; mutating ones rate-limited via a module-owned in-memory limiter in `lib/rate-limit.ts` - not table-backed like contact-form's, since a rate-limit-only IP column on shp_back_in_stock_subscriptions would be a schema change for a secondary guard; resets on cold start, doesn't share state across serverless instances):
- `GET /products` (filters: category/tag/collection/type/search/pagination, ACTIVE only), `GET /products/[slug]`, `GET /products/[slug]/related`, `GET /products/[slug]/upsells`, `GET /categories`, `GET /categories/[slug]`, `GET /collections`, `GET /collections/[slug]`, `GET /tags`.
- `GET /config` (client-safe config slice: currency, tax mode, enabled payment methods filtered by actual env presence, Stripe publishable key, checkout steps, shop status).
- `POST /cart/validate` (re-checks stock/price/status for client localStorage cart lines).
- `POST /checkout/session` (server-only totals - subtotal/discount/shipping/tax/total, never trusts client maths), `POST /checkout/apply-coupon`, `POST /checkout/payment-intent` (**PROTECTED** - creates the PENDING `shp_orders` row + item snapshot per Q8, then the provider's payment intent), `POST /checkout/confirm` (**PROTECTED** - confirms via the provider, idempotent PAID transition, triggers `fulfillPaidOrder`).
- `GET /orders/status?orderNumber=&email=` (guest lookup, both must match - no enumeration), `GET /downloads/[token]` (**PROTECTED** - token/expiry/download-limit checks, then streams the file bytes through this endpoint rather than redirecting, so the permanent underlying storage URL is never exposed to the client). Three things about the response are deliberate: `Content-Disposition` is built by `lib/download-name.ts`, never interpolated from `shp_digital_files.filename` (the upload route writes that verbatim from the admin's `file.name`, and a quote or a CR/LF in it rewrites the header); `Content-Length` is relayed from the upstream response, never the `size` column, since a row disagreeing with its bytes truncates the transfer or hangs it; and `incrementDownloadCount` runs in the stream's `flush()`, so only a transfer that finished costs a customer one of their limited downloads. Always `attachment` + `nosniff`, as its sibling is: the attachment stops a browser rendering the bytes, and nosniff stops it overriding the stored `Content-Type` and rendering them anyway - worth more here than in the sibling, since this route's upload allowlist is by *declared* MIME type rather than by extension.
- `POST /back-in-stock` (idempotent subscribe), `DELETE /back-in-stock?token=` (**PROTECTED** - HMAC-signed unsubscribe token via `ENCRYPTION_KEY`, no DB lookup needed to validate it).

Member (`/api/m/shop/member/…`, `getMemberFromCookie()` gated): `GET /orders`, `GET /orders/[id]`, `GET/POST /addresses`, `PUT/DELETE /addresses/[id]`, `GET /gdpr-export` (internal-bearer only, `verifyInternalExportBearer` - called self-origin by core's member data-export assembler, feeds the `memberExtensions.dataExportPath` manifest entry).

Webhooks (`/api/m/shop/webhooks/…`, unauthenticated, signature-verified, **PROTECTED**): `POST /stripe` (verifies `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`, handles `payment_intent.succeeded`/`payment_intent.payment_failed`/`charge.refunded`), `POST /paypal` (verifies via PayPal's own verify-webhook-signature endpoint using `PAYPAL_WEBHOOK_ID`, handles `PAYMENT.CAPTURE.COMPLETED`/`PAYMENT.CAPTURE.REFUNDED`). Both idempotent - `markOrderPaid`'s `WHERE payment_status != 'PAID'` clause makes a replayed event a no-op.

Cron (`/api/m/shop/cron/…`, `CRON_SECRET` bearer): `GET/POST /low-stock-alerts` - daily 07:00, also covers Q11 import-job retention (30 days) and Q8 abandoned-PENDING-order pruning (24h).

Admin (`/api/m/shop/admin/…`, session + permission gated per route above): full CRUD for `products` (+ `[id]/related`, `[id]/upsells`, `[id]/duplicate` (POST, clones the row + media/categories/tags/collections/manual-recommendation lists into a fresh DRAFT with a new slug and no SKU, returns `{id,slug}`), `bulk` (POST `{action:'delete'|'status', ids[], status?}` - capped at 200 ids, FK-violation → friendly 409), `export`/`import-template`/`import`(+`[id]` status poll)). The `GET` list now also takes `sort` (`newest`/`oldest`/`name-asc|desc`/`price-asc|desc`/`stock-asc|desc`, whitelisted to a fixed `ORDER BY` map, never interpolated) and `stock` (`in`/`low`/`out`), and its response carries `images` (one primary-image url per product for the list thumbnails, batched via `getPrimaryProductImages`); the single-row `DELETE` catches FK violations the same way as `bulk`. Order-line history survives any delete (`shp_order_items.product_id` is ON DELETE SET NULL). Sibling admin routes: `categories` (GET returns `{categories, productCounts}` - the latter a per-category direct-product-count map for the admin tree; POST/PUT accept `parentId` + `productDisplayMode`; PUT cycle-guards a reparent; DELETE cascades the sub-tree; `+ reorder` persists a sibling order), `tags`, `collections`, `tax-classes`, `tax-zone-rates`, `shipping-zones`(+ nested rates GET), `shipping-rates`, `coupons`, `automatic-discounts`; `orders` (list+manual-create, `[id]` detail, `[id]/status` (**PROTECTED** - decrements stock for pre-order items on SHIPPED per addendum B.4, now only on a genuine transition, and refuses SHIPPED with a 409 + plain-English explanation while `preOrderMixedCartBehaviour` is HOLD_ALL and pre-order lines are outstanding; a genuine transition to CANCELLED releases the pre-order allocation), `[id]/notes`, `[id]/email`, `[id]/refund` (**PROTECTED** - per-item, delegates to `processRefund`, which validates under an order-wide advisory lock and calls the provider outside any transaction), `[id]/dispatch` (**PROTECTED**, part-dispatch: **POST** records one dispatch of a subset of the order's lines (`items[]`, optional `trackingNumber`/`carrier`/`notes`/`shippedAt` - a plain date string is coerced, since owners back-date a parcel that went out on Friday - and `emailCustomer`; every cap is enforced inside `createShipment` and its rejections are handed back verbatim because they already read as plain English; a failed dispatch email is logged and stepped over rather than rolling the shipment back). **GET** returns everything the order screen needs in one call: the per-line dispatch summary, the shipments already recorded, and `preOrderHold` (whether the shop's hold-everything policy currently applies, how many lines are outstanding and the latest expected date) - it rides on this route rather than the main order GET so the dispatch block can refresh itself without re-fetching the whole order. This route only EXPLAINS the hold; `[id]/status` ENFORCES it, and both read the same `outstandingPreOrderItems`. **DELETE** `?shipmentId=` undoes a dispatch recorded by mistake, scoped to this order so an id from elsewhere cannot be deleted through it - the totals fall back out on their own because they are summed from the shipment's lines), `[id]/confirm-payment`); `customers` (list, `[id]` keyed by URL-encoded email - no dedicated table); `reports/tax`(+`?format=csv`)/`reports/revenue`; `dashboard-widget`; `email-templates`; `back-in-stock`; `suppliers` (GET list with per-supplier product/variation counts, or `?for=picker` for just the enabled names - the picker form skips the count aggregate, which is the right cost for the Suppliers screen and the wrong one for opening a product; POST create with a friendly 409 on a duplicate name; `[id]` PUT - a name change routes through `renameSupplier` - and DELETE. Both writes also accept an optional `catalogues[]` (`{name, sheetUrl}`) which is persisted with `replaceSupplierCatalogues`; omitted leaves the existing catalogues alone, `[]` clears them. `SuppliersScreen` edits them as a repeating name+URL block in the supplier form, blank rows dropped client-side, and lists them per supplier on the table as links); `settings` (shopConfig read/merge-update, and syncs the Suppliers sidebar link on both GET and PUT). Layout editing for all six page types goes through the core `/api/admin/layouts*` routes now (see Layout system integration bullet above) - there is no shop-specific layout-editing route any more (`admin/page-layouts/[key]` retired along with the table it served).

**Payment providers** (`modules/shop/lib/payments/`, **PROTECTED - entire directory**)
- `provider.ts` - the `ShpPaymentProvider` interface (`createIntent`/`confirmPayment`/`refundOrder`/optional `handleWebhook`) every provider implements.
- `stripe.ts` - `stripe` npm SDK (new core dependency, see below), no `apiVersion` pinned (uses the account's dashboard default rather than guessing a literal date string the installed major might reject), server always re-fetches the PaymentIntent and validates its own status **and** amount/currency against the order before trusting a client "confirmed" claim.
- `paypal.ts` - raw REST, no SDK (spec's own instruction, keeps the bundle lean), OAuth token cached in-memory with expiry, sandbox/live base URL switches on `PAYPAL_MODE`, capture amount/currency checked against the order on confirm.
- `bank-transfer.ts`/`cash.ts` - instructions-from-config intents, `confirmPayment` always fails (admin confirms manually via the order detail page's "Confirm payment" action), refunds are manual-only.
- `registry.ts` - `paymentProviders: Record<ShpPaymentMethod, ShpPaymentProvider>` lookup used by every route above.

**Sanctioned core diffs** (all outside `modules/shop/`, each minimal/isolated, flagged PROTECTED in-code):
- `package.json`/`package-lock.json` - added `stripe` (^22.x) as a core runtime dependency. Modules can't add their own npm dependencies (they compile inside core's Next build); precedent: `shiki` for Gazette, `leaflet`/`leaflet.markercluster` for Directory.
- `proxy.ts`'s `buildCsp()` - added `https://js.stripe.com` to `script-src`, `https://api.stripe.com` to `connect-src`, and a new `frame-src 'self' https://js.stripe.com https://hooks.stripe.com` directive (didn't exist before - Stripe Elements renders card fields and 3D Secure challenges in hidden iframes). **`blob:` joined `connect-src` in v0.5.484** for product-3d-views-for-shop's GLB textures (full reasoning in that module's section) - a `blob:` URL is same-origin, unguessable and readable only by the document that minted it, so it widens nothing. **A `worker-src 'self' blob:` directive joined it in v0.5.612** for the same module's Draco decoder, which three builds as a Worker from a Blob URL; it had to be spelled out because `worker-src` falls back to `child-src` then `script-src`, and `script-src` carries no `blob:`. Note `img-src` has carried `blob:` since long before and is **not** the directive a `fetch()` of a blob URL consults; that near-miss is exactly what made the bug read as a bad model file. **`'wasm-unsafe-eval'` joined `script-src` in the working tree (unreleased)** for product-3d-views-for-shop's WebAssembly mesh decoder (Draco/Meshopt) - without it the admin "Detect from model" button died with a CSP refusal on live sites. It permits only `WebAssembly.compile`/`instantiate`, not JS `eval()`; `'unsafe-eval'` stays banned.
- Product image filing (`lib/media/product-media.ts`, `reorganiseProductMedia(productId, {folderProductId?})`): runs on every product `PUT` after the media/category writes. Files each `IMAGE` in `shp_product_media` into the core media library under **Shop / <master category> / <product name> / <product-slug><n>** (`<n>` = 1-based position; no master → "Uncategorised"), via core's `getOrCreateFolderByPath(['Shop', <category>, <product name>])` + `moveOrRenameMedia(id, {targetFolderId, newName, exactName:true, collision:'replace'})`. Only urls resolving to a managed core `Media` row are moved (external urls / video embeds left as-is); the row's `url` is rewritten to the relocated one. Idempotent (an already-filed image is a no-op) and best-effort per image (one relocate failure doesn't fail the save). The editor refetches after save so thumbnails follow the moved blobs. `exactName` keeps the stored key nanoid-free so the url reads `…/shop/<category>/<product>/<slug><n>.<ext>` exactly - this filing is the **only** consumer of `exactName`, so it owns the uniqueness contract `lib/media/keys.ts` now keeps (a shared 40-char clip used to break it; see the Media section). `folderProductId` files a product's images under a **different** product's folder while still naming them from its own slug - the one consumer is shop-variations' variant `PATCH`, which passes the parent so variant images land beside the parent's (a variant child is a hidden, category-less product, so unaided it would file under "Uncategorised"). Two products sharing a name share a folder; filenames stay unique because the slug is.
- `lib/media/upload.ts` - purely additive `NonImageUploadMode` type + `validateNonImageUpload(mimeType, sizeBytes, mode)` export for the digital-file upload path (declares its own mime/size allowlist, skips the sharp image-decode sniff entirely since there's no universal "valid PDF/zip" magic-byte check the way there is for images). The existing image-only `validateUpload`/`uploadMedia`/`deleteMedia`/`downloadMedia`/`saveMediaRecord` are untouched. Shop's digital files are **not** wired into the core `Media` table at all (no `saveMediaRecord` call) - they're stored in shop's own `shp_digital_files` table via `uploadMedia()`'s returned key/url only, since they're not part of core's page/logo Media referencing system.
- `.env.example` - added the seven Stripe/PayPal env var rows (all optional; a payment method with unset keys is filtered out of `enabledPaymentMethods` server-side, never offered at checkout - `modules/shop/lib/env.ts`'s `isStripeConfigured`/`isPayPalConfigured`).
- `app/api/admin/env/route.ts`'s `ALLOWED_KEYS` - added the same seven Stripe/PayPal vars so they're settable through the core env-var UI/API (Vercel project env vars, admin-only per `isAdmin()`). `lib/notifications/deployment.ts` gained a `PAYMENT_KEYS` set feeding `labelForEnvKeys()` → "Payment provider keys updated" on the existing deployment-needed notification.

**Admin pages** (`/cactus-admin/m/shop/…`)

`products` (**redesigned list, `ProductsScreen.tsx` + `products-screen-css.ts` prefix `sps-`, tokens only**: 40px thumbnails from the GET response's `images`, coloured type/status/stock badges (stock badge derives In/Low/Out/Not-tracked from `trackInventory`+`stockCount`+`lowStockThreshold`), a pre-order chip, compare-at strike-through price, and a per-row `⋯` menu (fixed-positioned so the table's overflow container never clips it - Edit / Duplicate / Delete). A filter toolbar drives the server: debounced name/SKU search, a status segmented control (All/Active/Draft/Archived), type + stock selects, and a sort select; results paginate 20/page (server `page`/`perPage`, `total` shown as "Showing X–Y of Z"). Row checkboxes + a select-all (indeterminate) header raise a sticky **bulk bar** - Set active / Set draft / Archive / Delete - posting to `admin/products/bulk`; selection is dropped on every reload so a bulk action can never touch an off-page row. Delete (single via the row menu, or bulk) confirms through the shop's own `useConfirm` dialog. Distinct empty states for no-products-at-all vs no-filter-match. Still carries the back-in-stock "N waiting" link, Export/Import-template buttons, and the "Import CSV" button opening `ImportModal.tsx` - upload → auto-detects header mismatches via `headerMatchesFormat()` and only then shows a column-mapping step → polls job progress, recent-imports log), `products/[id]` (**tabbed editor, rebuilt v0.1.38** - see "Product editor" below), `categories` (indented tree: search box, collapsible branches, **drag-and-drop** to reorder among siblings or re-nest under any category plus ↑/↓ arrows and an inline edit panel that renames/reparents/sets the per-category display mode), `collections` (flat list + inline rename/delete, no drag-reorder UI yet), `orders` (status-tab filters incl. a `PRE_ORDER` tab), `orders/[id]` (items table, a "Refund items" button opening `RefundModal.tsx` (per-item quantity inputs pre-filled against remaining refundable qty, reason field, provider-aware copy for manual methods, one batched call to `POST .../refund`), financial summary, shipping address, "Confirm payment" for bank-transfer/cash, notes, email log, digital download tokens, and a Customer Communications section that renders only when another module - e.g. Reply Catcher - actually contributes to the `shop.order-messages` extension point), `customers`, `customers/[id]`, `discounts` (Coupons/Automatic tabs via the shared core `TabStrip`, real forms - not `prompt()` - covering type incl. fixed-amount/free-shipping, expiry window, usage/per-customer limits, minimum order value, free-shipping threshold, priority; edit + delete on both coupons and automatic discounts), `reports` (Revenue/Tax tabs via the shared core `TabStrip`), `back-in-stock` (no nav entry - reached from the products list), `tax-shipping` (`TaxShippingScreen.tsx` - tax classes CRUD (new tax class's `code` auto-slugs from `name`, read-only until unlocked via a pencil button), zones (name + postcode-prefix list, empty list = catch-all matched when no other zone's prefix matches, so one zone can cover a whole country without listing postcodes) picker+detail, per-zone tax rate per class, per-zone shipping rates (flat/weight-banded/free) picker+detail). `ShopSettingsTab` renders on core `/cactus-admin/config`, internal `TabStrip` sub-tabs (General/Checkout/Payments/Notifications/Email templates) covering the full `ShpConfig` shape: store identity+units/SEO/shop status, tax mode+checkout rules (guest checkout, min/max order value, phone requirement, per-step checkout-steps editor, back-in-stock account prompt, pre-order mixed-cart behaviour), payment methods w/ env-presence indicators, order/low-stock alert emails, and the email-templates editor. **Publishes two hosted-panel slots** (v0.1.53) for other modules' `settingsTabs` `host` entries: `shop.payments` (merged into the Payments sub-tab, below Stripe/PayPal - GoCardless) and `shop.settings-sub-tabs` (each contributed panel gets its own labelled sub-tab after shop's own, in module-load order - product-3d-views-for-shop's "3D Viewer"). Contributed sub-tabs save through their own module's API, so shop's own "Save settings" button stands down while one is showing. Both slots are empty (render nothing) on a shop with no such add-ons. `requiresCoreVersion` **0.5.490** from v0.1.53 (imports `lib/modules/hosted-settings.ts`).

**Product editor** (`components/admin/ProductEditor.tsx` + `components/admin/product-editor/`, rebuilt v0.1.38)

Tabbed shell with a sticky sidebar, replacing the single 700px column of stacked sections. Sidebar (collapses above the tabs under 1100px) carries status, a "View on the shop" link, cover thumbnail, at-a-glance price/stock/SKU, **the only Save button on the page**, and a **Manage card** (Duplicate product → POST `[id]/duplicate` then navigates to the new draft; Delete product → `useConfirm` then DELETE then back to the list). Both clear `dirtyRef` before their hard navigation so the unsaved-changes guard doesn't prompt - the product is being replaced or removed, so in-progress edits are moot. Own tabs: Details, Images, Pricing, Stock & delivery, Organisation, Recommendations, Search, plus Download (only when `type === 'DIGITAL'`). Files: `model.ts` (form shape, `toEditorState`/`toProductBody`, per-tab dirty compare, validation), `fields.tsx` (Field/Control/Select/Switch primitives; every field has a real `<label>`, hint and inline error wired through `aria-describedby`), `editor-css.ts` (prefix `spe-`, tokens only, injected once - real CSS so focus rings/hover/responsive work), `panels/*.tsx`, `context.tsx`.

- **Fields the old editor never exposed, all already accepted by the `PUT` and stored**: `barcode`, `weight`+`weightUnit`, `dimensionL/W/H`+`dimensionUnit` (these feed weight-priced shipping rates), and `regenerateSlug` (a "rebuild the web address from the name on save" switch; the API takes the flag, not a free-text slug). `catalogueHidden` is deliberately **not** exposed - it is the internal marker for variant child products, not a "hide from catalogue" toggle, and the page refuses to open a `catalogueHidden` product at all.
- **Numeric fields are held as strings** and converted once in `toProductBody`, so a half-typed `12.` or a cleared box stays what was typed. Validation is computed from the first keystroke but only shown after a save is attempted (`showErrors`); a failed save jumps to the offending tab via `tabForField`.
- **Position is the only cover.** `toProductBody` re-stamps `isPrimary: i === 0` from the array order. `setProductMedia` honours a supplied `isPrimary` over order and `card-template.tsx` reads `media.find(m => m.isPrimary) ?? media[0]`, so round-tripping the loaded flag unchanged would have meant drag-to-reorder moved the image but not the cover.
- **Save races.** The form stays interactive during a save. The post-save reload (needed because images may be re-filed server-side) only takes the server's copy wholesale when nothing was touched since the save started (`prev === current`); otherwise the admin's edits stand and the new baseline just marks them unsaved again. Silently binning what someone typed is the worst kind of bug.
- **`shop.product-editor-sections` is now a tab contract.** Manifest entries gained optional `label` (tab name; falls back to a prettified id) and `order` (sorted among the editor's own via `SHOP_TAB_ORDER`, default 999 = last). The page renders each contributed **server** component and passes it as a `ReactNode` into the client shell, which renders it inside `ProductEditorTabScope`. All panels stay mounted (`hidden` on the inactive ones) so a half-finished edit survives a trip to another tab and contributed tabs can report state while unopened.
- **`product-editor/context.tsx` is the public API for contributed tabs** (`shop-variations` and `product-attributes-for-shop` are the live consumers): `useProductEditorSave({dirty, save})` registers a tab's unsaved edits with the single Save button (throw an `Error` from `save` to fail it; the message is shown, prefixed with the tab name, and one failing tab does not roll the others back); `useProductEditorTabBadge(text)` puts a count on the tab label; `useProductEditorCurrency()` hands over the already-loaded currency symbol so a tab need not re-fetch shop config. All three are inert outside the editor. Registration keys off `useId()` + the scope's tab id, so a tab never names itself. Dirty tabs get an amber dot and a chip in the sidebar; errored tabs get a red one. Navigation away while dirty is guarded by core's `useUnsavedChanges` + `UnsavedChangesModal`.
- Tab selection mirrors to `?tab=<id>` via `replaceState` (deep-linkable; `tab` is read once on the server and passed as `initialTab`, so no `useSearchParams` Suspense boundary). The active tab is **derived**, not stored, so a `?tab=` naming an uninstalled module, or a tab that vanishes when a product stops being digital, falls back to the first tab instead of stranding the view.
- **Panels must be allowed to shrink (v0.1.39).** `.spe-panel>*,.spe-grid>*{min-width:0}` in `editor-css.ts` is load-bearing for any tab holding something wide. Grid children default to `min-width:auto` (their content-based minimum), and a scroll container still propagates its contents' min-content size up through block flow, so without the floor a wide panel overflows the `minmax(0,1fr)` main column and the sticky sidebar paints over it - `shop-variations`' nowrap variants table hit exactly this. A contributed tab wanting a wide surface should wrap it in its own `overflow-x:auto`, which only works because of this rule. Note `minmax(0,1fr)` on `.spe-grid-2/3/4` floors the track, not the item, hence the separate `.spe-field{min-width:0}`.

**Public pages** (`/shop/…`, via `publicBasePath: "shop"`)

**CLOSED gate (v0.1.51).** `getShopGate()` (`modules/shop/lib/access.ts`) is the single check for `shopStatus === 'CLOSED'`, and **every** public page above calls it first, rendering `<ShopClosedNotice message={gate.message} />` (`components/public/ShopClosedNotice.tsx`) when `gate.blocked`. Staff who pass `canPreviewClosedShop()` (`shop.access`/`shop.manage`, and any protected role via `hasPermission`) instead get `gate.staffPreview` and see the real page with a `<ShopStaffPreviewBanner />` on top. Until v0.1.51 only `/shop` itself had this check inline, so a closed shop's product/category/collection/cart/checkout/order/account/download pages all rendered in full to anyone with the URL. The gate is per-page by necessity: module public pages are dispatched individually through `resolveModulePublicPage`, so there is no shared Next layout to hang it on - **a new page under `app/public/shop/` is unprotected until it calls `getShopGate()` itself.** `generateMetadata` on the product/category/collection pages checks it too, so a closed shop does not publish its product names. The same check backs the public data routes as `shopClosedResponse()` (503 + the owner's closed message), on `products`(+`[slug]`/`related`/`upsells`), `categories`(+`[slug]`), `collections`(+`[slug]`), `tags`, `cart/validate`, `orders/status`, `downloads/[token]`, and back-in-stock `POST` - otherwise the catalogue stayed readable as JSON while the shop was shut. Deliberately **not** gated: `config` (carries `shopClosedMessage` itself and feeds the sitewide header cart), back-in-stock unsubscribe (`GET`/`DELETE` - links already in inboxes must keep working), and `checkout/confirm` (must not strand a payment already taken); `checkout/payment-intent` + `checkout/session` keep their own stricter `!== 'OPEN'` rejection, which also blocks staff.

`/shop` (index, resolves the `shopIndex` layout via `resolveThemeLayout`, honours `shopStatus` CLOSED), `/shop/products/[slug]` (resolves `shopProduct`, 404s if none published; `productSlug`/`productId`/`inStock` injected into `ShopProductDetail`/`ShopRelatedProducts`/`ShopUpsellProducts`/`ShopBackInStockForm` block props via `lib/inject-product-context.ts` - mirrors core's `resolveTemplateData` context-injection pattern for MenuBlock etc, since these blocks have no per-instance slug of their own in the stored template), `/shop/categories/[slug]` (resolves `shopCategory`, falls back to the original hardcoded plain grid when none published), `/shop/collections/[slug]` (resolves `shopCollection`, same fallback pattern), `/shop/cart` (resolves the `shopCart` layout via `resolveThemeLayout` and renders it with `getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig('shopCart')`; the `<h1>Your cart</h1>` stays in the page shell; falls back to the original hardcoded client-side cart UI + coupon field + `ShopUpsellProducts` when no `shopCart` layout is published, so never blank), `/shop/checkout` (resolves `shopCheckout`), `/shop/checkout/confirmation` (resolves `shopConfirmation`), `/shop/orders/[orderNumber]` (guest lookup form), `/shop/downloads/[token]` (friendly expired/limit-reached states, real download via the API route), `/shop/account/orders`(+`[id]`)/`/shop/account/addresses` (member-session-gated, 404 when Members disabled, redirect to `{memberAreaPath}/login?redirect=` when signed out).

**Extension Points**
- `core.admin-dashboard-widgets` (id `shop-summary`) - 30-day revenue/orders/AOV, low-stock chip, pending-manual-payment chip, active-pre-order chip.
- `members.account-section` (id `shop-orders`, **first module to use this point** - it existed in core unused until now) - "Orders & addresses" card linking to the member-area pages above.
- `core.menu-entity-provider` (id `shop`, `lib/menu-entity-provider.ts` exporting `shopMenuEntityProvider`) - lets the admin menu builder's "Module content" picker link to shop pages. Four kinds: Shop home (`/shop`), Product (`/shop/products/{slug}`, `publiclyVisible` only when status `ACTIVE`), Category (`/shop/categories/{slug}`), Collection (`/shop/collections/{slug}`). Same shape as Gazette/Directory/Boards providers; URL scheme mirrors `lib/sitemap.ts`.
- `core.media-usage-providers` (id `shop`, `lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) - contributes `shp_product_media.url`, `shp_digital_files.url`, `shp_products.og_image_id`, `shp_collections.image_id`/`og_image_id`, `shp_categories.og_image_id` - the catalogue's entire photography used to read as unused in the media library to core's media usage index, so the library's Unused tile and delete warning can see them.
- `shop.order-messages` (shop is the **consumer** here, not a publisher - no manifest entry needed) - the order detail page looks up any active module's `extensionPoints` for this point name and renders its contributed component with `orderId`/`orderNumber`/`customerEmail` props, mirroring the exact mechanism `members.admin-member-detail` already uses. Reply Catcher does not currently publish to this point (Q12 - shop builds only its own side; the reply-catcher-side contribution is out of scope), so the section never renders out of the box today.
- `shop.product-detail-parts` (**published by shop, v0.1.35**; contract + resolver in `lib/detail-slot.ts`, precedent `lib/line-meta.ts`; live consumer `shop-variations`) - a **claim-and-replace** point, unlike the additive ones above. `resolveShopDetailSlot(product)` is awaited once per product page inside `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx` (in the existing `Promise.all`, one extra query) and asks each active provider's `claimsProduct(product)`; the first to claim supplies optional `Gallery`/`Price`/`PurchaseArea` components, which ride to the parts as `DetailPartContext.slot` via the existing `_ctx` injector (`inject-part-context.ts`, attached by reference so components survive). `ShopDetailGalleryRsc`/`ShopDetailPriceRsc`/`ShopDetailAddToCartRsc` render the slot component instead of their own markup when `slot` is set, and shop's own markup unchanged when it is null (shop-only site, or any unclaimed product) - the starter layout's block list is **not** touched, which is how a variations-aware default PDP stays free of variations-specific blocks. Shop hands the provider its own `.spd-*` class names plus its server-loaded images/price so a replaced part looks native and paints on first byte. Replace (not render-alongside) because a claimed product has no single price/stock of its own - both rendering would show two prices and two buttons. **A claimed product's `PurchaseArea` owns availability outright: shop's `outOfStock` gate is deliberately skipped**, since stock lives on the chosen combination and gating on the parent row would strand a parent that tracks no stock of its own (`ShopDetailBadges` still reads the parent's `outOfStock`, so a mis-configured parent can show an out-of-stock badge above a working buy button). Nothing in shop names variations; the point is generic and the `git grep` leak check stays clean.

- `shop.product-detail-tabs` (**published by shop, v0.1.50**; contract + resolver in `lib/detail-tabs.ts`; live consumer `product-downloads-for-shop`) - **additive**: a module contributes a tab to the product page's own tab strip, beside Description/Specification/Dimensions, rather than a block bolted underneath. Modelled on `shop.gallery-media` line for line, and additive for the same reason - a tab replaces nothing, so every provider resolves and one whose `load` throws is dropped and logged rather than taking the product page down. `resolveShopDetailTabs(productId)` is awaited once per page in `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx` (in the existing `Promise.all`) and rides to the parts as `DetailPartContext.detailTabs`, **not** awaited inside `ShopDetailTabsRsc` - the parts render synchronously, and `detail-parts.tsx` is dual-compiled into the client editor bundle, so it cannot import the extension-point registry (which reaches prisma) at all. Provider supplies `label`, optional `order`, `load(productId)` (server-only; payload crosses the RSC boundary so must be JSON-serialisable; **null means no tab**, which is what keeps the strip unchanged on products with nothing to add) and a `Panel` **client** component. `label`/`order` live on the provider object rather than in the manifest - unlike `shop.product-editor-sections`, whose manifest `label` is stripped by the install-time zod schema and only restored by `sync-module-manifests.mjs` on the next deploy, leaving a tab named after its own id in the meantime. Shop's own tabs are numbered in `detail-parts.tsx` (`TAB_ORDER`: desc 10, spec 20, dims 30, downloads 40); an unordered contribution lands at 50 and ties keep shop's own first (stable sort). Shop never learns what a tab holds.
- `shop.gallery-media` (**published by shop, v0.1.43**; contract + resolver in `lib/gallery-media.ts`; live consumer `product-3d-views-for-shop`) - **additive**, the counterpart to the claim-and-replace point above: a module contributes extra items to a product's gallery (a 3D model) that appear as further thumbnails and take over the stage when picked. It exists *because* `shop.product-detail-parts` is winner-takes-all - shop-variations already claims Gallery on every product with options, so a second claimant could never reach exactly the products that need it most. Being additive, nothing replaces a part of shop's, so there is no two-prices failure to design around and **every** provider is resolved, not just the first; one whose `load` throws is dropped and logged rather than taking the product page down. `resolveShopGalleryExtras(productId)` is awaited once per page in `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx` (in the existing `Promise.all`) and rides to the parts as `DetailPartContext.galleryExtras` - resolved by the injector, **not** awaited inside the part, because `wrapResponsiveRender` (`lib/puck/config.tsx`) calls a block's `render` as a plain function. Provider supplies `load(productId)` (server-only; the returned payload crosses the RSC boundary so must be JSON-serialisable) plus `Thumbs`/`Stage` **client** components - a function cannot cross that boundary, which is why filtering by the chosen variation is the provider's own job rather than a callback shop calls into. Shop hands over its `.spd-thumb` class names and owns the strip, the stage box and which item is picked; it never learns what the item is. Rendered by **all three** galleries - shop's `ProductGallery`, shop-variations' `VariantSlotGalleryClient` (which passes the chosen child's id as `activeProductId`, the bit shop cannot know) and shop-variations' granular `ShopVariantGallery` block (which covers shop's Gallery slot, so it is the only strip on those layouts and must resolve extras itself).

**Contributed media leads the strip and opens the stage (shop v0.1.54, shop-variations v0.1.21, product-3d-views-for-shop v0.1.6).** In all three galleries the `extras.map` now renders **before** the photo thumbnails, so a 3D thumbnail sits at the front of the strip rather than trailing the photos. Order only - the host still owns the strip and the pick, and pick behaviour is unchanged. The opening view is the provider's call: `Gallery3dThumbs` (`product-3d-views-for-shop`) picks its first visible item once, on first paint, when nothing else is picked - so a product that carries a model opens the stage on the model instead of a photo. It fires only on mount (`ledWithModel` ref guard), so a later variation change that brings a model in does not yank the stage off a photo the shopper chose; a variation change that drops the picked model still hands the stage back to the photos via the existing `stale` guard.

**Puck Blocks** (all 18, registered in the generated `lib/puck/module-components.ts`)

`ShopProductGrid`, `ShopProductCard`, `ShopFeaturedCollection`, `ShopCategoryBrowser`, `ShopPromoBanner` (colour prop is a semantic token name, never hex), `ShopCartSummary` (client, reads localStorage cart, untagged - header-placement widget, not part of any `layoutTypes` page), `ShopCartFull` (client, full editable cart display - `CartFullClient` localStorage island wrapped by `components/puck/ShopCartFull.tsx`; ~33 look/behaviour options: rows/cards/table layout, spacing/dividers, optional heading, product-image toggle+size+radius, unit/line-price toggles, quantity control style (stepper/number/read-only), remove button text-or-bin, stock + pre-order badges, coupon field labels, item-count/subtotal toggles + labels, checkout button label/colour/text-colour via core `SiteColourField`/full-width/radius, empty-state copy + continue-shopping link, price-accent + panel colours; tagged `shopCart` (its layout type) but ALSO present on every core page via the all-module-blocks "Modules" category, so still droppable anywhere; ONE render path shared by editor and live for parity - editor render passes `preview` to seed sample lines with inert controls and no fetch, RSC render is a server wrapper passing only plain props into the client island, same trick as `ShopCartSummary`; no new API - reuses `/api/m/shop/public/cart/validate`, `/config`, `/checkout/apply-coupon`), `ShopCheckoutContact`/`ShopCheckoutShipping`/`ShopCheckoutPayment`/`ShopCheckoutReview` (all `[ANCHOR]` - `permissions:{delete:false,duplicate:false}` - client components sharing state via a sessionStorage-backed `checkout-state.ts` store since Puck blocks don't share React state; the Payment block owns the mounted Stripe Elements instance and listens for a `cactus-shop-place-order` window CustomEvent the Review block dispatches, since only Payment has access to `stripe.confirmPayment()`), `ShopOrderConfirmation`, `ShopProductDetail` (`[ANCHOR]`, add-to-cart non-removable; RSC render also emits the schema.org Product JSON-LD script tag), `ShopBackInStockForm` (auto-hidden via an `inStock` prop the product page injects), `ShopRelatedProducts`, `ShopUpsellProducts` (client, resolves upsells for every product currently in the cart client-side by calling the per-product upsells route once per cart line and merging/deduping), `ShopCategoryHeader`/`ShopCollectionHeader` (both `[ANCHOR]`, added with the layout system integration above - breadcrumb + name + description, re-fetched server-side from an injected `categorySlug`/`collectionSlug`).

**Configuration**

`ShpConfig` (`modules/shop/lib/config.ts`, Zod-validated, stored as the single `config` JSONB column on the `shp_settings` singleton, Q2): `currency`/`currencySymbol`/`storeEmail`/`orderNumberPrefix`/`weightUnit`/`dimensionUnit`, `enabledPriceTypes` (subset of sale\|retail\|trade\|cost, default `['sale','cost']`) + `showRetailPrice` (default false - prints the RRP beside the price on cards/detail when it beats the charged figure), `taxMode` (INCLUSIVE\|EXCLUSIVE), `weightBasedShippingEnabled` (default true - the switch at the top of the Tax & shipping screen, saved through `PUT admin/settings` like any other config key and exposed on `public/config` so the product editor can read it alongside the price types; off drops the `WEIGHT_BASED` option from the shipping-rate Type dropdown, the Weight field from the product editor's Stock tab, and the Weight column from shop-variations' grid. Nothing is blanked: stored weights and existing weight-based rates are untouched, and an existing weight-based rate still lists its own type when opened for editing so it can't silently become a flat rate), `guestCheckoutEnabled`/`postPurchaseAccountPrompt`/`minimumOrderValue`/`maximumOrderValue`/`requirePhone`/`checkoutSteps` (ordered step array), `enabledPaymentMethods` (filtered by env presence at read time via `getAvailablePaymentMethods()`), `bankTransferInstructions`/`cashInstructions`, `adminOrderAlertEmail`/`lowStockAlertEnabled`/`lowStockAlertEmail`, `shopStatus` (OPEN\|BROWSE_ONLY\|CLOSED)/`shopClosedMessage`, `shopTitle`/`shopMetaDescription` (`shopBasePath` dropped per Q3 - fixed to `"shop"` via the manifest's `publicBasePath` instead of being runtime-configurable), `backInStockAccountPrompt`, `preOrderMixedCartBehaviour` (HOLD_ALL\|PROMPT_SPLIT - a fulfilment policy, wired up 2026-07-23, see the Part-dispatch subsection below; also returned by `POST /public/checkout/session` so the checkout review step can word its pre-order notice), `supplierFieldEnabled` (default false) + `supplierLabelPreset` (Supplier\|Manufacturer\|Retailer\|Importer\|custom, default Supplier) + `supplierLabelCustom` (default '') + `supplierShowOnFrontend` (default false) + `supplierFieldScope` (PRODUCTS\|PRODUCTS_AND_VARIATIONS, default PRODUCTS) - the supplier field block on the General tab. `resolveSupplierLabel(config)` (same file) is the one place the preset/custom pair resolves to a display string, falling back to "Supplier" when custom is blank. Enabled adds the **Suppliers** sidebar entry and screen (see `shp_suppliers`) and a supplier dropdown to the product editor's Details tab; `supplierShowOnFrontend` additionally puts it on the Product Detail Specification tab (via `DetailPartContext.supplierLabel`, null when either switch is off); `supplierFieldScope` = PRODUCTS_AND_VARIATIONS adds the column to shop-variations' grid. Nothing is blanked by switching any of them off. Exposed on `public/config` as a `supplierField` object (enabled/label/showOnFrontend/scope) because the admin product editor reads its config from there.

`imageZoomOnHover` moved out of `ShpConfig` into the Puck "Product: Gallery" block itself (`shopDetailGalleryPuckComponent`, `modules/shop/components/puck/parts/detail-parts.tsx`) as a per-block `zoomOnHover` radio field (default off), so it's set per layout in the shop layout editor rather than shop-wide in admin settings. Flows straight from the block's own prop into the `zoom` prop on `ProductGallery`/`ShopDetailGallerySlotProps`, same as before - `DetailPartContext.zoomImages` is gone, `ShopSettingsTab`'s "Product images" section is gone.

**Product photos are square everywhere; the `shape` prop is gone (shop v0.1.44, shop-variations v0.1.11)**
One ratio, 1:1, for every product photo: the Product Detail stage (`.spd-stage`) and the card image (`.shop-card-img` in `card-parts.tsx`, `.spc-img` in `product-card-css.ts`, both previously `4/3`). The per-instance `shape` select (square/portrait/landscape) is **removed** from both the `ShopDetailGallery` and `ShopCardImage` Puck blocks, from `GalleryProps`/`ImageProps`/`ProductGallery`, from `ShopDetailGallerySlotProps` (so `shop-variations`' `VariantSlotGalleryClient` stopped reading it and no longer sets `aspectRatio` inline - it inherits the ratio from shop's `.spd-stage` via `classNames`, one definition rather than two modules agreeing to keep saying `1/1`), and from every `starterLayouts.ts` block (two set `landscape`). The `.shape-*` CSS classes are gone. Its only real effect was letting one shop's photos be three shapes depending on the layout a page used. Saved `Layout` rows may still carry `props.shape`; Puck passes unknown props through and nothing reads it, so they resolve square with no data migration - correct on this fresh-install platform. **Exempt: Overlay cards** (`.shop-card-img.fill-mode`, `aspect-ratio:auto` inside a `3/4` card) - the photo being the whole card is that design, not a shape. Non-square originals crop rather than distort (`object-fit:cover` in an `overflow:hidden` box). `shop-variations` declares `requiresModules: shop >= 0.1.44`, since its gallery now leans on shop's square `.spd-stage`.

**Product: Tabs strip - own background colour, and the active tab scrolls itself into view**
Two per-block fields on `shopDetailTabsPuckComponent` (`modules/shop/components/puck/parts/detail-parts.tsx`): `bgColour` (custom field, core `SiteColourField`, so it carries the light and dark arms in one stored `light-dark(l, d)` value - `lib/puck/lightDark.ts`) and `bgOpacity` (number, 0-100, default 100). `navBgVars()` folds the opacity into **each arm separately** via `color-mix(in srgb, <arm> N%, ...)` rather than wrapping the whole `light-dark()`, matching what `SectionBgColorField` already writes; `rgba()` can't wrap a `var(--color-N)` swatch, hence `color-mix`. It emits **two** custom properties on `.spd-tab-shell`: `--spd-tabnav-bg` (mixed over `transparent`, the strip's own fill) and `--spd-tabnav-fade` (the same colour mixed over `var(--color-page-bg, var(--color-bg))`, i.e. already composited onto the page). The edge fades and arrow buttons use the **fade** var, because they paint over the shell's own fill - a see-through colour applied twice would darken both edges relative to the middle. A blank colour sets neither var, so the CSS falls back to `transparent` / page-background exactly as before, and sticky still fills so the panel can't show through as it scrolls under. Editor preview (`ShopDetailTabs`) sets the same vars on the same wrapper for markup/class parity.

The mobile bug it shipped with: on a small phone the strip is an `overflow-x:auto` row, and the scroll-spy would light a tab (Downloads, typically last) that sat off the right-hand edge - the highlight was correct and invisible. `ProductSectionTabs` (`modules/shop/components/public/ProductDetailIslands.tsx`) now tags every pill `data-spd-anchor` (including the leading CTA, whose anchor is `spd-buy`) and, on `active` change only, nudges `nav.scrollTo` so the lit pill clears the 32px arrow/fade overlay at whichever edge it came in from. Guarded on `scrollWidth > clientWidth`, so it is a no-op on desktop and on the larger-phone shrink-to-fit tier, and it never fights a shopper dragging the strip by hand. Honours `prefers-reduced-motion` (jumps instead of smooth-scrolling). The standalone **Section links** block is static server markup and is untouched.

**Product Detail gallery, viewport fit (v0.1.42, reworked v0.1.44)**
The gallery column (`.spd-stage-col`, CSS in `galleryCss()`, `modules/shop/components/puck/parts/detail-parts.tsx`) is `position:sticky` so the photo stays with a shopper scrolling a taller buy column, and the stage fits the leftover viewport **by giving up width** - `aspect-ratio` takes the height with it, so it stays square and merely gets smaller. `--spd-fit` (`calc(100dvh - var(--spd-header-h) - 32px - var(--spd-thumbs-h))`) is that width budget; the stage is `flex:none;align-self:center;width:min(100%,var(--spd-fit));min-width:140px`. **v0.1.42 capped the column's height instead and let the stage flex-shrink into it, which squashed the square stage into a letterbox and cropped the photo** - the bug the square rule exists to prevent. `beside` mode overrides `--spd-fit` (the strip sits alongside, costing the stage no height) and uses `flex:1 1 auto;max-width:var(--spd-fit)`, since the strip is spending some of the row's width too.

Both numbers need measurements CSS cannot get. The site header's height: core does **not** publish it - the header is the Site Header Puck block (`lib/puck/config.tsx`), whose height is a per-site prop that may be `auto`, whose stickiness is a second prop, and which a site may omit. So `modules/shop/components/public/GalleryViewportFit.tsx` (client island, renders null) measures it and publishes `--spd-header-h` on `:root`, counting only `<header>` elements computing to `position:sticky|fixed` with `top <= 4px` (a static header scrolls away and costs the column nothing) and summing `height + top` (a header parked below an announcement bar). It also publishes `--spd-thumbs-h` - the stacked strip's height plus the column's `gap:12px`, `0` when there's no strip (no strip, no gap). Re-measures on `ResizeObserver` (headers + strip) and `resize`: late-decoding logo, wrapping nav, condense-on-scroll header, strip rewrapping rows. Fallbacks `96px`/`76px` cover pre-hydration and the editor canvas.

**The strip's width is deliberately NOT tied to `--spd-fit`.** Its height feeds that sum, so sizing it from the result would let a narrower strip wrap to more rows → taller strip → smaller budget → narrower strip: a loop the ResizeObserver would chase. It keeps its full column width (`flex:none`); only the stage moves. Rendered by `ShopDetailGalleryRsc`, **not** by `ProductGallery`, so a `shop.product-detail-parts` provider's replacement gallery gets it too - it wears `.spd-stage-col`. No `overflow` on the column: it would clip `.spd-thumb.on`'s `box-shadow: 0 0 0 1px` ring on the edge thumbnails of every page, to catch only a ~35-image outlier. Below `tabletBp` the column goes `position:static` and the stage back to `width:100%` - stacked, it has the width to itself and shouldn't shrink for a viewport it no longer shares.

**Thumbnail strip overflow affordance (`GalleryThumbStrip`, v0.1.48)**

The strip below the stage is one nowrap `overflow-x:auto` row (above), which on a product with a dozen photos simply looked like it ended at the column's edge - nothing said the row ran on. `modules/shop/components/public/GalleryThumbStrip.tsx` (client) wraps it in `.spd-thumbs-wrap` and renders, at whichever end still has scroll left in it, a `.spd-thumbs-fade` gradient and a `.spd-thumbs-arrow` button - the same affordance, geometry (2rem fade inboard of a 1.5rem arrow) and 160px step as core's admin `components/admin/TabStrip.tsx`. State is `scrollLeft` vs `scrollWidth - clientWidth` on a `scroll` + `resize` + `ResizeObserver` check; both ends start "at" so the server's markup carries no arrows and the effect earns them. Keyed on `Children.count`, **not `children`**: the gallery re-renders on every pointer move while the magnifier is tracking, and keying on the nodes would tear the listeners down and rebuild them on each one.

`beside` strips pass straight through unwrapped - left/right means nothing to a column - so that layout's markup and CSS are exactly as before. `ShopDetailGallery` (editor preview) mirrors the same wrapper for markup/class parity; its four placeholders never overflow, so no arrows are earned there.

**The new rules are scoped to `.spd-thumbs-wrap`, not to `.spd-thumbs`, and that is load-bearing.** A `shop.product-detail-parts` provider's replacement gallery (shop-variations' `VariantSlotGalleryClient` / `ShopVariantGallery`) wears the `.spd-thumbs` class it is handed via `classNames` but renders it straight into `.spd-stage-col` with no wrapper. `flex:1 1 auto` reaching it there would read as grow-to-fill on the **vertical** axis (the column's main axis) and stretch its strip down the page; hiding the scrollbar would leave it with no overflow hint at all, having no arrows to replace it with. Hence `.spd-thumbs-wrap .spd-thumbs{flex:1 1 auto;scrollbar-width:none}` and an untouched `.spd-stage-col:not(.beside) .spd-thumbs`.

**`VariantSlotGalleryClient` now adopts `GalleryThumbStrip` (shop-variations v0.1.15), which is what actually put the arrows in front of shoppers.** The affordance shipped in shop v0.1.48 and, on a real catalogue, almost nobody saw it: any product with options is claimed by shop-variations' replacement gallery, and that is the half of the catalogue with the most photos. The strip on Deskwell's Chiro Plus overflowed (804px of thumbnails in a 796px column) with no arrow, no fade and a hidden scrollbar. The slot gallery now renders `<GalleryThumbStrip beside={thumbPosition === 'beside'} className={classNames.thumbs}>` - the `className`/`beside` props existed from v0.1.48 for exactly this caller and had no consumer until now - so `requiresModules: shop` moved 0.1.44 → **0.1.48**, the release that carries the component (the `product-downloads` lesson at the top of this file, applied on purpose rather than after the fact). Its thumb buttons gained `role="tab"`/`aria-selected` to earn the wrapper's `role="tablist"`, matching `ProductGallery`. `ShopVariantGallery` (the hand-placed Puck block, own `svr-gallery-thumb` styling, 56px) is a separate surface and is **not** wrapped - no live consumer asked for it. `GalleryViewportFit` is unaffected: it queries `.spd-stage-col:not(.beside) .spd-thumbs` as a **descendant**, so an interposed wrapper changes nothing it measures.

The hidden scrollbar slightly *raises* the photo's budget: its height was being charged to `--spd-thumbs-h`.

**Part-dispatch (shipments)**
An order used to be either shipped or not - the SHIPPED status was the whole record of dispatch, which cannot describe "three of the five went out on Tuesday". Data layer: `modules/shop/lib/db/shipments.ts` exports `createShipment`, `getShipmentsForOrder`, `getDispatchedQtyByOrderItem`, `getOrderDispatchSummary`, `isOrderFullyDispatched`, `deleteShipment`, plus the pure `isFullyDispatched`/`isPartiallyDispatched` so the UI can answer the same question from a summary it already holds. Types in `lib/types.ts`: `ShpShipment`, `ShpShipmentItem`, `ShpShipmentWithItems`, `ShpOrderItemDispatch` (`quantity`/`refundedQty`/`dispatchedQty`/`outstandingQty`, the last being `quantity - refundedQty - dispatchedQty` floored at zero), `ShpOrderDispatchSummary`. Load-bearing details:
- **Dispatched totals are aggregated in a subquery BEFORE the join to the order lines.** Joining `shp_shipment_items` straight onto `shp_order_items` fans a line out once per shipment and any later arithmetic counts it several times - the same trap that caused the real overselling bug in `decrementStockOnShip`.
- **The advisory-lock namespace is shared with refunds** (`0x53485250`, transaction-scoped `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` keyed on the order id). Refunds and dispatch police the same units of the same order, so they have to be mutually exclusive: a refund landing between a shipment's validation and its insert would otherwise refund units the dispatch had just decided were still dispatchable. One of the two simply waits, or is turned away with a 409 and a "something else is updating this order" message.
- **This layer records dispatch and nothing else - it does NOT touch `stock_count`.** Stock still moves in exactly two places: normal lines at payment (`lib/order-fulfillment.ts`) and pre-order lines when an admin sets the order to SHIPPED (`decrementStockOnShip`).
