Adding a decrement here would double-count against one of those and silently oversell. If dispatch is ever meant to own the pre-order decrement, the decrement has to MOVE, not be added alongside.
- Two lines for the same order item in one request are folded together before anything is validated, or each would validate against the same starting figure and together sail past the cap. "Fully dispatched" excludes an order with nothing dispatchable (empty, or refunded down to nothing) - there was never a parcel to send.
Admin UI: new `components/admin/DispatchModal.tsx` (built on `RefundModal`'s bones - a quantity per line capped at what is still owed, optional parcel details, server rejections shown verbatim; the real caps are server-side, so a refund landing while the modal is open is caught there). `components/admin/OrderDetailScreen.tsx` gains a Dispatched column on the items table, a "Dispatch items" action beside "Refund items", a Dispatches list, the HOLD_ALL banner, and a derived "Partly dispatched"/"All dispatched" pill next to the status select - **a marker, not a new `ShpOrderStatus` value**; it fetches `/admin/orders/[id]/dispatch` alongside the order.
Email: `lib/shipment-email.ts`'s `sendShipmentDispatchedEmail({orderId, shipmentId})` renders the `PARTIAL_SHIPPED` template. `STATUS_SHIPPED` says the whole order is on its way and only knows orderNumber/customerName/shopName, so sending it for three of five items would be a straight untruth; this one lists what went and what is still owed. It covers the final parcel too - the copy switches to "the last part of your order" via the `isFinalPart`/`hasOutstanding` flags - so the dispatch route calls it for EVERY shipment and never has to choose between templates. Item lists go in as ONE plain-text variable (`- name xN`, newline-joined) because `lib/email.ts` HTML-escapes every `{{variable}}`, so any `<br>`/`<li>` built here would reach the customer as visible angle brackets - the same trade-off `ORDER_CONFIRMED` already makes. Silent no-op when the order, shipment or its lines cannot be found: an email is not worth failing a dispatch that has already committed.
**`preOrderMixedCartBehaviour` is now actually implemented, as a FULFILMENT policy rather than a checkout restriction.** Neither value forbids a mixed basket, and nothing on the storefront blocks the Place order button - the payment-intent route carries an explicit comment saying so, since "add the gate here" is the obvious wrong fix. HOLD_ALL: `[id]/status` refuses SHIPPED with a 409 while any pre-order line is outstanding, naming how many items and the latest expected date and pointing at the two ways out (take the products off pre-order, or switch the setting to split shipping); the checkout review step tells the shopper the whole order is sent together once everything has arrived. PROMPT_SPLIT: part-dispatch is permitted and the shopper is told anything in stock can be sent straight away with the pre-order to follow. The shared rule is `outstandingPreOrderItems(items)` in `lib/db/orders.ts` - the line's snapshotted dispatch date is the primary signal, a line with no date falls back to the product's own `is_pre_order` flag (so unticking it once stock lands is the owner's escape hatch), and a line whose product row has gone is treated as ready rather than jamming the order shut for good. It lives in the data layer precisely because the status route enforces the policy and the dispatch route explains it, and two copies would drift into disagreeing about whether the shop is holding the order.

**Order, stock and money correctness (2026-07-23)**
- `decrementStockOnShip` aggregates `SUM(quantity) GROUP BY product_id` before joining to the product row. The plain join updated each product once however many order-item rows pointed at it, so a basket with two lines of the same product (which personalised lines deliberately allow) decremented by the larger line only - qty 1 + qty 3 took 3 off, not 4 - and silently oversold.
- Coupon usage is keyed on the resolved `coupon_id`, never the raw code: `fulfillPaidOrder` bumps `usage_count` only when `order.couponId` is set, `countPriorCouponOrdersByEmail` takes a coupon id (also immune to a later rename), and the payment-intent route stores `couponCode` only when a coupon genuinely resolved. A rejected or expired code previously burned the coupon's usage and the customer's per-customer allowance against an order it never discounted.
- Refunds go through `processRefund` (`lib/db/refunds.ts`), split into a short validation transaction and a settle transaction with the provider call between them. The validation half takes the order's transaction-scoped advisory lock, re-reads every cap under it and commits a PENDING refund row that reserves the order; a second overlapping request sees the live reservation and gets a 409 instead of validating against quantities that are about to move (the old code read the caps, called the provider and wrote afterwards, so two requests could both slip past). A PENDING row older than 5 minutes can only have been left by a request that died mid-flight - module routes are capped at 60 seconds - so it stops blocking, but its amount still counts against the caps because the provider may well have refunded it. The provider HTTP call runs with NO database transaction open, so a slow provider never pins a pooled connection, and the refund row id is passed as the idempotency key (Stripe's `idempotencyKey` request option, PayPal's `PayPal-Request-Id` header, GoCardless's equivalent) so a retried call cannot refund twice. A FAILED provider refund no longer increments `refunded_qty`.
- `markOrderPaymentFailed(id, reason)` takes `'FAILED' | 'CHARGEBACK'`. FAILED (the default, used by the Stripe/PayPal failure webhooks and the confirm route) still only touches a PENDING order, so a stray late failure cannot undo a paid one. CHARGEBACK (the GoCardless settle handler, when a settled payment is later charged back or fails at the bank) moves an already-PAID order to ON_HOLD with `payment_status='FAILED'` and writes an internal note telling the owner to check whether anything shipped against money that has since been clawed back - previously that case was a silent no-op, because the guard only matched PENDING.
- Stripe's `charge.refunded` handler resolves the order through `charge.payment_intent` and the new `getOrderByPaymentReference`. The `shpOrderId` metadata it used to read only ever exists on the PaymentIntent; Stripe does not copy it onto the Charge, so a dashboard refund matched nothing and the order was never marked refunded.
- `minimumOrderValue`/`maximumOrderValue` are enforced at `POST /public/checkout/payment-intent` as well as at `/checkout/session`. The session route only advises the browser, while the payment-intent route is what actually creates a payable order, so a direct POST skipping the session step produced a chargeable below-minimum order.
- `updateOrderStatus` is idempotent (`WHERE … AND status != status`) and returns whether the row changed; every once-per-transition side effect now hangs off that boolean. SHIPPED → COMPLETED → SHIPPED used to decrement the pre-order stock a second time, and `decrementStockOnShip` clamps at zero rather than erroring, so the shop quietly undercounted itself.
- `decrementPreOrderCount` (`lib/db/products.ts`) is the counterpart to `incrementPreOrderCount`, called by `releasePreOrderAllocationForOrder` on a genuine transition to CANCELLED; the refund settle path runs the identical statement inlined, because it has to execute on the transaction client rather than the shared one. `pre_order_count` previously only ever went up, so a cancelled pre-order kept its slot forever and, once the count had touched `pre_order_max_quantity`, the auto-flip left `is_pre_order = false` permanently - quietly taking a product out of pre-order mode with nobody actually waiting on those units. One statement, so the counter and the flag cannot disagree; re-enabling is deliberately narrow (only a product that was sitting at its cap, which is precisely the state the increment creates, and never one with no cap), so a product the owner switched off by hand is never switched back on. The release is guarded on `paid_at IS NOT NULL` (the allocation is only ever consumed by `fulfillPaidOrder`, so an order cancelled before it paid never took a slot) and on `quantity - refunded_qty`, so units a refund has already returned cannot be double-released.
- The CSV import engine rejects a negative price (`lib/import-engine.ts`), matching the same fix in google-sheet-products-for-shop's preview.

**Admin dialogs**
The shop admin no longer calls the browser's `confirm()`/`prompt()`/`alert()`. `modules/shop/components/admin/dialogs.tsx` exports three promise-based hooks - `useConfirm()`, `usePrompt()`, `useAlert()` - each returning `[invoke, node]`: call `await invoke(...)` and render `{node}` once in the screen. Styling matches the module's other overlays (colour tokens only, `role="dialog"`/`aria-modal`, Escape cancels, Enter confirms, delete confirms use the `btn-danger` class). Wired through CategoriesScreen, CollectionsScreen, ProductsScreen (new-item name prompts), DiscountsScreen (delete confirms + save-error alerts), TaxShippingScreen (delete confirms), ProductEditor (upload/save-error alerts).

**Money formatting**
All prices render through one helper - `modules/shop/lib/money.ts` `formatMoney(amount, symbol='£')` - which coerces the string/number a price arrives as and always emits `symbol` + 2dp (e.g. `£7.99`). Storefront pages/blocks and order emails pass `config.currencySymbol`; admin screens (client-rendered, no server config) read it via `components/admin/use-currency-symbol.ts` `useCurrencySymbol()` (fetches `/api/m/shop/public/config` once, module-cached, `£` fallback). Prices are decimal pounds end to end (`NUMERIC(10,2)`); nothing is stored or displayed in pence (the Stripe `×100` in `lib/payments/stripe.ts` is API-only). Discount "value" cells format per type: `%` for PERCENTAGE, `formatMoney` for FIXED_AMOUNT, `—` for FREE_SHIPPING.

**External Integrations**
Stripe (Payment Intents + Elements + webhooks, `stripe` npm SDK), PayPal (Orders v2 REST API directly, no SDK), core Members system (optional, guest checkout always works regardless), core Media/upload pipeline (`uploadMedia()` reused for digital files, but not `saveMediaRecord` - see core diffs above), core email (`sendEmail` via `lib/email/index.ts`, shop owns its own `shp_email_templates` table rather than reusing core's `EmailTemplate`).

**Cron Jobs**
`0 7 * * *` → `/api/m/shop/cron/low-stock-alerts` - low-stock digest email (deduped via `low_stock_alerted_at`, re-arms on any stock_count write) + `shp_import_jobs` retention (30 days) + abandoned-PENDING-order pruning (24h, Q8). `CRON_SECRET` bearer-gated.

**Scripts**
None.

**Known Limitations** (v0.1.2 - flagged here rather than silently shipped as if finished)

- Categories have an indented nested-tree admin UI with ↑/↓ sibling reorder, reparent, and per-category display-mode override; collections still have no reorder UI (the `position` column and API support it; only rename/delete are wired up in the collections screen). Neither uses drag-to-reorder (↑/↓ buttons only, like Directory).
- `shop.products-toolbar` (**published by shop, v0.1.61**; live consumer `google-sheet-products-for-shop`) - a module hangs a control beside the Products **list** header buttons (Export/Import-template/Import/New product). Resolved server-side in `app/cactus-admin/shop/products/page.tsx` (`resolveToolbarExtras`: reads each active module's manifest `extensionPoints`, permission-filters per entry, looks the component up in `moduleExtensionPointComponents['shop.products-toolbar']`) and passed as a single `toolbarExtras` `ReactNode` into the client `ProductsScreen`, which renders it after the New product button. Empty (renders nothing) on a plain shop. google-sheet uses it for its Google Sheet dropdown.
- Reply Catcher's contribution to the `shop.order-messages` extension point is out of scope of this build (Q12) - the Communications tab section is real and will render the moment another module publishes to that point, but nothing does yet.
- The module-side rate limiter (`lib/rate-limit.ts`) is in-memory, not table-backed - resets on a cold start and doesn't share state across concurrent serverless instances. Acceptable for a secondary guard behind normal validation, but weaker than contact-form's DB-backed one.

v0.1.1 fixed five review findings from the original v0.1.0 build: Stripe/PayPal `confirmPayment` now validates charged amount/currency against the order (not just status/reference); `GET /downloads/[token]` streams the file through the endpoint instead of redirecting to the permanent storage URL; the `product`/`checkout` default page layouts now seed `ShopBackInStockForm`/`ShopUpsellProducts` (new installs only, per `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`); the product editor gained a real Recommendations panel, image picker, and digital-file upload; the Discounts screen, refund flow, CSV import, and page-layouts editor were all rebuilt from `prompt()`/raw-JSON placeholders into proper UI (see the Admin pages entry above for each).

### Shop Variations

- Slug: `shop-variations` (table prefix `svr_`), repo `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/shop-variations`, manifest version 0.1.61 (registry pin v0.1.61). `requiresModules: shop >= 0.1.52` (`GalleryThumbStrip` needed v0.1.15; previously 0.1.44, and before that 0.1.43 for `shop.gallery-media` - `product-editor/context` needed only 0.1.38 and `shop.product-detail-parts` only 0.1.35), `requiresCoreVersion 0.5.493`. Reuses shop's `shop.products`/`shop.reports` permissions (declares none of its own) and joins the existing **Shop** admin nav group with one entry ("Product options").
- `core.media-usage-providers` (`lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) - contributes `svr_option_values.swatch` + `svr_uploads.media_ref`/`media_key` to core's media usage index.
- Adds product options to the shop: fixed **variant matrices** (e.g. Size × Colour, each combination its own price/SKU/barcode/stock/weight/image) and free-form **personalisation add-ons** (text, long text, number, priced dropdown, checkbox, date, file upload). A variant is a real but `catalogue_hidden` child `shp_products` row created through shop's own `createProduct`, so basket, checkout, inventory, orders and refunds work unchanged; the storefront selector resolves the chosen combination to that child id and calls shop's `addToCart(childId, qty, {meta})`. Personalisation rides in the generic `line_meta` carrier, priced server-side by the registered resolver.

**Database**
Table prefix: `svr_` (7 tables). Full DDL in `modules/shop-variations/migrations/001_initial.sql` (idempotent); later per-change files are numbered (`002_image_option_type.sql` widens the `svr_options.control_type` CHECK to admit `IMAGE`, also mirrored in 001; `003_requires_previous_option.sql` adds `svr_options.requires_previous_option`, also mirrored in 001; `004_option_source.sql` adds `svr_options.source_provider`/`source_ref` + `svr_option_values.source_ref` and the `(option_id, source_ref)` index, also mirrored in 001; `005_option_name_overridden.sql` adds `svr_options.name_overridden`, also mirrored in 001). Cross-module FKs to `shp_products` are safe because shop installs first.

- `svr_options` - `id`, `product_id` FK→shp_products (cascade, the parent), `name`, `control_type` (DROPDOWN\|SWATCH\|PILL\|IMAGE - IMAGE added by `002_image_option_type.sql`, which drops and re-adds the CHECK constraint, and mirrored in 001 for fresh installs), `position`, `requires_previous_option` (BOOLEAN, default false - added by `003_requires_previous_option.sql`, mirrored in 001; when true the storefront holds this option back until **every** option before it by position has a value chosen, not just the one immediately before - see `isOptionVisible`), `source_provider?`/`source_ref?` (TEXT, both added by `004_option_source.sql`, mirrored in 001 - the extension-point provider id that built this option and that provider's own opaque ref for the source; both null on a hand-typed option, set together or not at all), `name_overridden` (BOOLEAN, default false - added by `005_option_name_overridden.sql`, mirrored in 001; true once the owner named the option something other than the source's own name, set on create when the two differ and on every PATCH rename. Suppresses the refresh's `nameDiffers` report, so a deliberately renamed copy is never nagged - which is what makes adding one source to a product twice, under two names, liveable).
- `svr_option_values` - `id`, `option_id` FK (cascade), `label`, `swatch?` (hex colour for SWATCH, image url for IMAGE, null otherwise and for a value nobody has styled yet), `position`, `source_ref?` (TEXT, added by `004_option_source.sql`, mirrored in 001 - the source value this one was copied from, opaque here; null on a hand-added value, which a refresh then never touches. Indexed `(option_id, source_ref)` because a refresh matches on that pair).
- `svr_variants` - `id`, `product_id` FK (parent, cascade), `child_product_id` FK→shp_products (cascade, unique - the hidden child), `enabled`, `position`.
- `svr_variant_values` - composite PK (`variant_id` FK cascade, `option_value_id` FK cascade) - which values define a variant.
- `svr_addons` - `id`, `product_id` FK (cascade), `type` (TEXT\|TEXTAREA\|NUMBER\|SELECT\|CHECKBOX\|DATE\|FILE), `label`, `required`, `position`, `config` JSONB (max length, min/max, flat/per-char price, priced choices, file limits).
- `svr_uploads` - `id`, `token` (unique), `media_ref` (public url, used as the line_meta href), `media_provider?`/`media_key?` (for orphan blob cleanup), `filename?`, `size`, `mime_type`, `order_item_id?` (unused link, retained), `ip_hash?`, `created_at`. Not FK'd to order items - orphan cleanup cross-checks `media_ref` against `shp_order_items.line_meta`.
- `svr_settings` - singleton (`id='singleton'`): `max_upload_mb` (10), `allowed_upload_types`, `upload_retention_days` (30), `max_variants` (200).

**Permissions**: none of its own - admin writes gate on `shop.products` (via shop's `requireShopUser`), the report on `shop.reports`.

**API Routes** (through `/api/m/shop-variations/…`)

- Admin (`shop.products`): `GET admin/products` (variation-enabled product list), `GET admin/products/[id]` (deep-editor payload), `POST admin/products/[id]/options`, `POST admin/products/[id]/generate-matrix`, `POST admin/products/[id]/clear-variants`, `POST admin/products/[id]/delete-variants` (bulk delete a chosen set - `{variantIds: string[]}` → `deleteVariants(parentId, ids)`, each id verified to belong to the parent before its hidden child is deleted; backs the grid's select-all + **Delete selected**), `POST admin/products/[id]/variants` (create one hand-picked combination - `{optionValueIds: string[]}` → `createSingleVariant`; rejects a partial combination or a duplicate value-set, builds a hidden child like the matrix does, then `resequenceVariantPositions` renumbers every row so the new variant lands in the slot a full generate would have given it), `POST admin/products/[id]/addons`, `PATCH/DELETE admin/options/[id]`, `POST admin/options/[id]/values`, `POST admin/options/[id]/refresh` (re-read a sourced option from its provider - additive only, see the option-source point below), `GET admin/option-sources` (every contributed source with its values + a suggested control type, for the picker; empty list when no module contributes one), `PATCH/DELETE admin/option-values/[id]`, `POST admin/products/[id]/resequence-variants` (0.1.61 - renumber a parent's existing variants into matrix order after an option/value drag, and re-compose the child names option order feeds; a renumber, never a regenerate, so ids and their stock/prices/photos/orders are preserved), `PATCH/DELETE admin/variants/[id]` (PATCH edits the child product via shop's `updateProduct`/`setProductMedia` + `enabled`, and as of 0.1.52 carries the **optional price types** as well as `price` - `salePrice`/`retailPrice`/`tradePrice`/`costPrice`, each `.nullable()` so clearing a variant's sale price stays distinct from setting it to zero; the image field is **`imageUrls: string[]`**, not a single url - the whole ordered set is written to `shp_product_media` (index 0 `is_primary`, `position` = index, duplicates dropped) and an empty array clears them; on a non-empty set, calls shop's `reorganiseProductMedia(childProductId, {folderProductId: parentId})` so the variant images file into the parent product's media folder. DELETE removes one variant by deleting its hidden child product, which cascades the `svr_variants` + `svr_variant_values` rows away - the same path `clear-variants` takes per row), `PATCH/DELETE admin/addons/[id]`, `GET admin/export` (CSV), `POST admin/import` (CSV). `GET admin/reports` gates on `shop.reports`.
- Public: `GET public/by-slug/[slug]/variations` (storefront selector payload - options, per-variant price/stock/image, base images, add-ons; looked up by slug so no product-context injection is needed in shop), `POST public/upload` (anonymous, rate-limited, size/type-validated personalisation file upload → core media provider + `svr_uploads` row, returns a token).
- Member: `GET member/gdpr-export` (internal bearer; the member's personalisation from their orders' `line_meta`).
- Cron: `GET/POST cron/cleanup-uploads` (`Bearer $CRON_SECRET`, daily 03:00) - prunes orphaned uploads past the retention window, deleting the blob then the row.

Admin pages (`/cactus-admin/m/shop-variations/…`): `products` (cross-product list; its "Manage" links to `/m/shop/products/[id]?tab=variations-inline`), `reports` (parent-grouped variant sales), `import` (CSV import/export). A shared `VariationsTabs` sub-nav keeps the module to one Shop-group nav entry. **There is no standalone per-product editor** (`products/[productId]` was deleted in v0.1.6): the whole thing is now the **Variations tab** on shop's product editor, contributed via `shop.product-editor-sections` → `ProductVariationsSection` (server wrapper; returns `null` for a `catalogue_hidden` variant child, since a variant of a variant is not a thing) → `VariationsPanel` (client: options builder with inline rename and drag-to-reorder (v0.1.18 - options are draggable cards, values draggable pills within their own option; only a grab handle is `draggable`, so the inline rename/swatch/delete controls keep their click and text-select behaviour, and a value drag is pinned to its option id and never crosses; a drop reassigns `position` on the moved rows through the existing `PATCH admin/options/[id]` / `PATCH admin/option-values/[id]` routes, then refreshes. **"No variant re-sync is needed" was wrong and is fixed in 0.1.61**: the grid *label* is indeed composed live from option order in `getEditorPayload`, but `svr_variants.position` is stored, so a drag left every variant sitting in the running order the old value order implied - visible as a grid whose rows no longer match the options above them, until the next generate. `persistPositions` now fires one `POST admin/products/[id]/resequence-variants` after all the moved rows have landed, which calls `resequenceVariantPositions` + `syncVariantChildNames`. **Once per drag, not once per PATCH**: the row PATCHes go out concurrently, and hanging the resequence off each one would both repeat the work N times and race - every call re-reads the option order to recompute slots, so a slow early one could write its now-stale answer last. Names are re-composed on both drags even though only an *option* reorder can move one (a child is named from its value labels joined in option order), because the sync only writes rows whose name actually differs), matrix generate/rebuild/clear, bulk variant grid, personalisation fields). **The grid carries every price type the shop has switched on** (0.1.52): the panel takes an `enabledPriceTypes` prop, read server-side by `ProductVariationsSection` from shop's `getShopConfigCached()` (rather than a second config fetch of the panel's own), and renders a column per switched-on type - Sale, RRP, Trade, Cost - beside the mandatory Price. The same wrapper reads `weightBasedShippingEnabled` off that config and passes it down (0.1.58): false drops the Weight column and its inputs, matching what shop's own Stock tab does, while per-variant weights already stored are left alone. Emptying one of those boxes writes `null`, not `0`: a blank sale price means "not on offer" and a zero one means free. Two save models on purpose: structural work (add option, generate matrix, add addon) applies immediately because it is an action, while per-variant grid edits are held locally and written by the product editor's single Save via `useProductEditorSave` (dirty rows tint, and only the rows actually written are cleared, so a row edited mid-save survives). Tab badge = variant count. A stale-matrix warning appears when the option combinations no longer match the variant count; because `generateMatrix` only fills the gap (existing rows kept), a big matrix that timed out part-built is resumable, so the action button reads **Continue building options** while the count is short of expected (and the warning says as much, "build a batch at a time, keep pressing Continue"), falling back to **Rebuild from options** when there are more variants than the options now call for. The grid also offers a per-row **Delete** (the DELETE route above) for the odd variant a big matrix throws up that is never actually sold, and its first column (the variant label) is `position: sticky; left: 0` so it stays put while the rest of the grid scrolls sideways. An **Add a single variant** control below the grid (`AddSingleVariant` in `VariationsPanel.tsx`) builds one hand-picked combination - a dropdown per option, each defaulting to its first value - via `POST admin/products/[id]/variants`, for the site owner who wants to grow the list one row at a time rather than generate the whole matrix. Ordering is the point: the server's `resequenceVariantPositions` (`variants-service.ts`) recomputes every variant's `position` as its canonical cartesian index (mixed-radix over the options in display order, the last option moving fastest - the same order `generateMatrix` walks), written back in one bulk `setVariantPositions` statement, so an individually-added variant appears exactly where the full auto-generate would have placed it, not tacked on the end.

**Option control types: DROPDOWN, PILL, SWATCH, IMAGE (v0.1.16).** All four are one column, `svr_options.control_type`, and the two swatch types share one nullable `svr_option_values.swatch` column - a hex colour for SWATCH, an image url for IMAGE. No second column: the column already meant "whatever the control shows beside the label", so IMAGE only needed the CHECK constraint widening (`002_image_option_type.sql`). The API-edge cap on it is `SWATCH_MAX_LENGTH` (`lib/types.ts`, 1000), shared by the three routes that accept a swatch - it was 200, which is roomy for `#ff0000` and too tight for a hosted media url carrying a folder path.
- Admin: `InlineImageSwatch` (`VariationsPanel.tsx`) sits where `InlineSwatch` sits for colours - a 22px thumbnail on the value pill, click to open shop's `MediaPickerModal` (the shared core media library, `GET/POST /api/admin/media`, with its own upload button, so picking a filed image and uploading a new one are the same two clicks). It saves on the pick rather than behind a tick, because unlike the colour control there is no hand-typed hex box to half-finish and therefore no draft to hold.
- A value's picture is set **after** the value exists, not while adding it: `AddValueInline`'s extra field stays colour-only, so the comma-separated "S, M, L" flow still works for an IMAGE option and each value is then given its picture from the dotted placeholder. A value with no picture renders as the bare label on the storefront - the same fallback an uncoloured SWATCH value gets.
- Storefront (`OptionControl` in `VariantParts.tsx`, shared by the granular blocks and the slot path): SWATCH, IMAGE and PILL are all one row of buttons; IMAGE adds a 28px thumbnail and **keeps the label** beside it, because a shopper who can't see the picture would otherwise have nothing to go on.

**Dependent options - "reveal in order" (`requires_previous_option`).** Any option from the second onward can be flagged to stay hidden on the storefront until the option immediately before it (by display order) has a value chosen, so a shopper works through them one step at a time. Pure progressive disclosure: it changes nothing about the variant matrix or `resolveVariant`, only which controls are on screen. The gate is one pure helper, `isOptionVisible(payload, selection, index)` (`lib/selection-logic.ts`), surfaced on the hook as `sel.isOptionVisible(index)` and applied in both storefront render paths (`VariantOptionsPart` in `VariantParts.tsx` and `VariantSlotPurchaseClient` in `DetailSlotPartsClient.tsx`). It chains: if the option before is itself hidden and unchosen this one stays hidden too, and it is dormant on the first option (nothing before it to wait on), so a flag left on an option later dragged to the front simply does nothing. Admin: a checkbox on each option card from the second onward (`VariationsPanel.tsx`, gated on `oi > 0`), labelled with the previous option's name, saving through `PATCH admin/options/[id]` (`requiresPreviousOption` boolean).

**Pinned mobile gallery (`lib/use-sticky-mobile-gallery.ts`, working tree).** On a stacked (mobile) product page, and only for a product that actually has options, `VariantSlotGalleryClient` pins the gallery under the site header while the shopper scrolls the option pickers: the hook flips the column to `position:fixed` via the `svr-mstick` class (CSS emitted by the client, restyling shop's `spd-*` classes at equal specificity but later in the document - stage at half width, thumbnails beside it as a 2×2 grid whose overflow scrolls vertically; the `spd-thumbs-wrap` collapses to `display:contents` so the same rules land whether the strip arrives wrapped (below) or bare (beside)), while a hidden sibling spacer holds the column's slot in the flow so pinning never jumps the scroll. The options' extent is found through the `svr-options` marker class worn by both option hosts (`VariantSlotPurchaseClient`'s inline area and the granular `VariantOptionsPart`). It releases both ways: scrolled back toward the top the gallery drops back into the flow unchanged; scrolled on past the options' bottom edge it lets go and leaves with them. "Mobile" is detected from geometry (options stacked below the gallery in the same column) rather than a breakpoint, so per-site breakpoint settings are honoured without widening shop's slot contract; the pin's top edge rides shop's live-measured `--spd-header-h`, so shrink-on-scroll headers stay snug. Desktop layouts (options beside the gallery) never match and keep shop's own sticky column.

**Extension point published: `shop-variations.option-source` (v0.1.49, working tree).** Another module offers ready-made options - "here is a Colour list with twelve values" - which the Variations tab turns into a real `svr_options` row. Live consumer: `product-attributes-for-shop` v0.1.9 (`lib/option-source-provider.ts`, `productAttributesOptionSourceProvider`), offering each attribute as a source and each attribute value as a source value.

- **Data-only by design.** A provider contributes no UI at all: `listSources()` / `getSource(ref)` return plain `{ref, name, groupLabel?, values: [{ref, label, swatch}]}`, and shop-variations owns the whole picker (`components/admin/OptionSourcePicker.tsx`). That keeps the word "attribute" out of this module entirely and keeps the provider free of admin-UI code. Contrast `variant-columns`/`variant-field-provider`, which do cross a component over.
- Resolver `lib/option-sources.ts` (`resolveOptionSourceProviders` / `resolveOptionSourceProvider`, same manifest-read + permission-filter + registry-lookup shape as the variant-field resolver), plus `suggestControlType(values)` - all-hex swatches suggest SWATCH, all-non-hex suggest IMAGE, mixed or none falls back to DROPDOWN rather than rendering half a swatch grid as blanks.
- **The browser never supplies the labels.** `POST admin/products/[id]/options` takes `source: {provider, ref, valueRefs[]}` and re-reads the source server-side, so what lands in the DB is what the provider says now; only the option name, control type and the picked refs come from the client. The name is the deliberate override - it starts as the source's name and is the shop owner's from then on.
- **Refresh is additive, never destructive** (`lib/option-refresh.ts`, `POST admin/options/[id]/refresh`). Matching is by `source_ref`, not label, so a renamed source value updates its copy rather than orphaning it. New source values are appended; copies whose source value is gone are **kept and reported as stale**, never deleted, because each option value has real variants (hidden child products with their own price/stock/SKU) hanging off it; hand-added values (`source_ref` null) are always left alone; the option's own name is never overwritten, only reported as differing. Renames that would collide with an existing label on the same option are skipped, matching the rename endpoint's own duplicate refusal. The route re-runs `fileSwatchImage` for any swatch that came across and `syncVariantChildNames` when anything changed, since variant child names are composed from value labels.
- **One source may be added to a product more than once** (v0.1.50, working tree) - a frame colour and a seat colour off one Colour attribute. Nothing keys on `source_ref` per product, so the only constraint is the option-name one, now enforced on **create** as well as rename: `POST admin/products/[id]/options` trims the name and 409s on a case-insensitive duplicate (previously unchecked, so the typed-in path could make the duplicates the importer and the rename endpoint both refuse). The picker takes `existingOptions` (name + source refs) instead of `existingNames`, badges a source that is already on the product with the names it uses, starts the name box **empty** when the source's own name is taken, warns live and disables Add while the typed name clashes. `name_overridden` is set on create when the chosen name differs from the source's and on every PATCH rename, and `refreshOptionFromSource` reports `nameDiffers` only when it is false - otherwise every refresh of a deliberately renamed copy would nag about a name the owner chose.
- **A source is now the only way in** (shop-variations v0.1.55). The typed-in "Add an option" form (name + control type + comma-separated values) is gone from `VariationsPanel`; the tab offers `Add from attributes` alone, so every option on every product traces back to one source row and one colour cannot exist under three spellings across three products. `POST admin/products/[id]/options` still accepts its `{name, controlType, values}` shape - the CSV importer and `lib/csv.ts` build options through the db layer, and the route's manual branch is left as the documented contract - so the gate is the UI, not the route.
- **New values travel back to the source** (shop-variations v0.1.55 + product-attributes-for-shop v0.1.15). `OptionSourceProvider` gains an **optional** `createValue(ref, {label, swatch})` returning the stored `OptionSourceValue`. `POST admin/options/[id]/values` calls it on the hand-typed branch whenever the option is sourced and the provider implements it, then copies the returned `ref`/`label`/`swatch` down - so a value typed on the Variations tab lands on the attribute too and is **sourced from birth**, matching on a later Refresh instead of being an orphan. The source is the authority on what it stored: a reused label comes back with the source's own spelling and swatch. A provider that refuses (source deleted, blank label) is a **hard 400, not a quiet local write** - a local-only row would look saved while the attributes screen silently disagreed. Providers without `createValue` keep the old local-only behaviour. `attributes` implements it with the same reuse-by-label rule its own `reuseExisting` POST body uses, plus `ensureUniqueValueSlug` / `nextValuePosition` / `fileSwatchImage` so a value made this way is indistinguishable from one made on the Attributes screen. `VariationsPanel.addValue` now surfaces the refusal in `optionError` instead of ignoring the response.
- Degrades to a dead end rather than to nothing: no contributing module means an empty `GET admin/option-sources`, and since the typed-in form has gone, the tab now says so in words and points at setting attributes up first, rather than showing a button with nothing behind it. shop-variations still does **not** declare `requiresModules: product-attributes-for-shop` (that would invert the dependency - attributes is the optional companion), so a variations-only install can price and edit existing options but cannot add a new one. Uninstalling the provider later leaves the copied options fully working - they are the product's own rows - and only removes the Refresh and Add affordances.

**Extension point published: `shop-variations.variant-columns` (v0.1.12)** - another module hangs an extra column on the variants grid, one cell per variant, resolved in `ProductVariationsSection` (manifest read + permission filter + registry lookup, none of which can happen in the browser) and passed to `VariationsPanel` as `columns: VariantColumn[]`. **No live consumer as of the current working tree**: `product-3d-views-for-shop`'s **3D** column used to ride this point, but moved to the dynamic `variant-field-provider` sibling (below) so its 3D files round-trip through the CSV/Google Sheet. The static point stays published for any column that genuinely needs no CSV presence.

- It exists because the alternative broke module isolation: setting a variation's picture and its 3D model are the same errand, but the grid belongs to this module and the model to one this module has never heard of and does not depend on. So the grid learned about *columns*, not about 3D - there is **no 3D code in shop-variations**, and without that module installed there is no such column.
- Contract: a cell gets `productId`, `variantId`, `childProductId` (the knowledge only this module has - a variation IS a hidden child product) and `label`, and owns its own storage, fetching and saving.
- **A contributed cell must be a client component.** `VariationsPanel` is a client island that fetches its own variants, so cells render per row in the browser and only client references survive the crossing - same rule as `shop.gallery-media`'s `Thumbs`/`Stage`.
- Contributed cells **save themselves** and are deliberately not wired into the editor's Save button: this point exists for uploads, and holding a 40 MB file as a pending in-memory edit would be a lie that costs the admin their upload.
- `label`/`order` ride along on the manifest entry (the `shop.product-editor-sections` trick), each with a fallback for manifests written before they existed.

**Extension point published: `shop-variations.variant-field-provider` (v0.1.29)** - the *dynamic* sibling of `variant-columns`. A static variant-column is one manifest entry = one column resolved without knowing the product; a **field provider** returns a set of columns that **depends on the product** (`listColumns(productId)`), so one module can contribute a different number of columns per product - e.g. one per attribute a product uses for its variations. `lib/variant-field-providers.ts` holds the contract + `resolveVariantFieldProviders(user?)` (manifest read + optional permission gate). The provider object is one export carrying: `listColumns`, `getValues(productId, childIds)` (per-child column values, for CSV export), an **optional** `beginImport(productId, childIds)` (v0.1.37 - preload once per parent, returns an opaque ctx), `applyImportedRow(productId, childId, row, ctx?)` (CSV import writes its own columns back, using the preloaded ctx), an **optional** `rowChanged(productId, childId, row, ctx?)` (v0.1.64-to-be, working tree - **read-only** twin of `applyImportedRow`: would applying this row write anything? Must create/update/delete nothing, including the lazily-created rows `applyImportedRow` may make - an attribute value for an unseen label counts as a change without being created. Lets the google-sheet Pull preview count changed provider columns instead of always previewing "0 to update" for them then applying anyway. A provider without it is invisible to the preview, as all were before), and a client `Cell` (the admin grid control, `columnKey` telling it which column it is). **Import batching (v0.1.37):** `applyImportedRow` used to be one round-trip *per row* per provider - the last per-row DB ceiling after the v0.5.519 shop/shop-variations batch. `csv.ts` now calls each provider's `beginImport` once per parent (child ids from `upsertCtx.existing`) and threads the returned ctx into every `applyImportedRow`, so provider reads drop from O(rows) to O(parents). Fully back-compatible: a provider with no `beginImport` gets `ctx === undefined` and behaves as before. A variant **created mid-import** is absent from the preload snapshot, so a ctx miss MUST default to empty current state - a brand-new variant still gets its values written (contract spelled out in `variant-field-providers.ts`, covered by each provider's `variant-field-provider.test.ts`). The **same object drives three surfaces**: `ProductVariationsSection` builds dynamic `VariantColumn`s from it for the grid, and `csv.ts` appends the columns to `exportVariationsCsv` (union of labels, after Weight) and feeds every row of `importVariationsCsv` back through `applyImportedRow`. Because the columns live in the CSV, **the Google Sheet sync carries them with no google-sheet code change** (`gridToImportCsv` is generic; the importer round-trips whatever the header names). `upsertVariantForCombination` now returns `childProductId` for the import path. **This module knows nothing of what the columns mean** - no `pat_` reference - exactly the isolation `variant-columns` was built for. Live consumers: `product-attributes-for-shop`'s per-variant attribute columns (its **Use for variations** attributes), and `product-3d-views-for-shop`'s **3D Files** column (a `|`-separated list of the variant's model urls, always offered - any variant can carry a model; attach-by-url on import, `deleteModelCascade` for a url the sheet dropped).

**The variant's own image also rides the CSV (shop-variations' own column, not a provider).** `exportVariationsCsv` emits an **Image** column carrying `VariantEditorRow.imageUrls[0]` (the hidden child product's primary media url; the CSV/Sheet carries **one** image per variant, so a variant with several exports only its first, and a changed cell replaces the lot) after Weight and before the provider columns; `importVariationsCsv` reads it (`imageCol`) and writes it via shop's `setProductMedia` + `reorganiseProductMedia(child, {folderProductId: parent})` - the same write `PATCH admin/variants/[id]` makes. Empty cell clears the image; a value failing the `http(s)` `isHttpUrl` guard is pushed to `errors`, not stored; and the whole block is skipped when the sheet carries no Image column, so a sheet made before this column existed never wipes an image. This is what makes the Google Sheet's Variations tab carry variant pictures.

**Puck Blocks** (editor + RSC parity, colour tokens only): composite `ShopVariantPurchase` (layout `shopProduct` - gallery + options + personalisation + live price + variant-aware add-to-cart) and five granular parts on `shopProductDetail` mirroring shop's `ShopDetail*`: `ShopVariantOptions`, `ShopVariantPersonalisation`, `ShopVariantPrice`, `ShopVariantAddToCart`, `ShopVariantGallery`. Each is a server wrapper → a client island; editor render is a labelled skeleton (preview), RSC render is live. Parts share one selection per product keyed by slug (`lib/use-variation-selection.ts`), so they sync when placed independently. `ShopVariantOptions` carries one field, **Option name position** (`labelPlacement`, radio, `above` | `beside`, default `above`): `above` is the long-standing stacked look, `beside` puts each option's name on the same row as its choices for a narrow column. It threads block → `VariantOptionsPart` → `OptionControl`; the slot host (`DetailSlotPartsClient`) passes nothing and so keeps `above`, since a slot render has no block props to read. **`beside` is a float, not flex, and cannot become one** (v0.1.44): the name is `float: left` inside a `flow-root` container and the choices stay inline-level, so the first row clears the name and every wrapped row after it runs the full width. Flex was tried twice and is wrong in both directions - as a flex item the choices div is measured at its full unwrapped width when the row breaks its lines and gets pushed below the name entirely (v0.1.43 patched that with `flex: 1 1 0` + `min-width: 0`), and even once it sits beside the name a flex container is a block formatting context, so it is shoved aside by the float whole instead of flowing around it, leaving every wrapped row in a column beside the name with the space beneath the name wasted. Consequences: the choices' `gap` moves onto the buttons as margins (`gap` does nothing to inline layout) with a `-0.5rem` bottom margin on the wrapper swallowing the last row's, buttons get `vertical-align: top` so an image swatch's baseline cannot drag its row about, and containment is `flow-root` rather than `overflow: hidden` because hidden would clip the image swatch's absolutely positioned hover peek. Indicative storefront pricing and the authoritative server pricing use the same pure `computeAddonPricing` (`lib/addon-pricing.ts`), so they can't disagree.

**The page opens with nothing chosen (v0.1.13).** `firstPreselect` is gone from `lib/selection-logic.ts` and neither entry path (`seededEntry`, `ensureLoaded`) seeds a selection: the opening `optionValues` is `{}`, so the price shows the parent's `basePrice`, `resolveVariant` returns null and `canAdd` is false until the shopper picks. Preselecting the first buyable variant meant a combination nobody had chosen sat in the controls looking chosen, and the buy button was live over it. Two consequences worth knowing:
- **"Out of stock" must gate on `allOptionsChosen`, not just `!inStock`** (`VariantPricePart`). `inStock` is `hasOptions ? !!(variant && enabled && inStock) : true`, and with nothing chosen there is no variant - so the unguarded check labelled *every* options product sold out on load. The purchase parts were already safe: their `reason` chain tests `!allOptionsChosen` first and says "Choose your options".
- **`ResetOptionsLink`** (exported from `VariantParts.tsx`) renders after the last option in **both** hosts - the granular `VariantOptionsPart` and the slot path's `VariantSlotPurchaseClient` - and calls `resetOptions()` → `resetOptionValues(slug)`, clearing `optionValues` only. Personalisation (`addonValues`) survives on purpose: it's typing, not a click. It renders only when `anyOptionChosen`, which is also why RSC and hydration agree - a server render never has a selection, so neither emits the link.

- **The RSC halves live in their own files (v0.1.7): `components/puck/variant-parts.rsc.tsx` and `ShopVariantPurchase.rsc.tsx`, pointed at by the manifest's `rscImport`** (same split, same reason, as shop's `ShopProductDetail.rsc.tsx`). They resolve the selector payload server-side via `lib/variation-bootstrap.ts` and pass it to the island as `initial`, so the option controls are in the page's first HTML. Before this the RSC halves were pass-throughs that rendered nothing but the editor's skeleton, and every island waited for hydration → read the slug off `window.location` → `GET public/by-slug/[slug]/variations` + `GET /api/m/shop/public/config`, which is why the options arrived a beat after the rest of the page.
- **`lib/variation-bootstrap.ts` (server-only, pulls prisma - never import from a `'use client'` file).** `getVariationBootstrap(slug)` is React-`cache`d, so all six blocks share one query per request; it returns the payload plus shop's currency symbol (killing the second fetch). Puck's `<Render>` gives a block only its own saved props and shop injects context into its own part types alone (`inject-part-context.ts`), so there is no prop carrying the slug - instead `rememberProductSlug` records it into a `cache()`-scoped, therefore per-request, slot from the detail-parts provider's `claimsProduct`, which shop calls once per product page before any block renders. `currentProductSlug()`/`bootstrapForCurrentProduct()` read it back. A null is survivable, not fatal: the island falls back to the old fetch-after-mount path (the composite block on a bare `shopProduct` layout, say).
- **The selection store must not be written during a server render.** Module state is per-tab in the browser but per-process on the server, outliving the request: an entry seeded into `store` server-side would sit there marked loaded and hand the *next* shopper of that product whatever price and stock that render happened to see, until the instance recycled. So `useVariationSelection` builds a throwaway entry from `initial` when `typeof window === 'undefined'` and touches no module state; the browser seeds the shared store as normal (first seed per slug wins, so a re-render can't discard a live selection). The currency symbol rides on the entry rather than the module-level `let` for the same reason - otherwise a server render prints the `£` default and hydrates into the real symbol.

**Extension points provided**: `shop.product-editor-sections` → `ProductVariationsSection` (component); `shop.cart-line-resolver` → `resolveVariationLineMeta` (server function; maps a variant child back to its parent, loads the parent's add-ons, re-resolves file tokens from `svr_uploads` server-authoritatively, prices via `computeAddonPricing`); and `shop.product-detail-parts` → `shopVariationsDetailParts` (`lib/detail-parts-provider.ts`, an object, id `variations-detail-parts`) - **this is what makes shop's default Product Detail layout handle options with no layout editing**. `claimsProduct` runs server-side once per product page and returns true when the product has options or add-ons and is not itself a `catalogue_hidden` variant child; shop then renders this module's `Gallery`/`Price`/`PurchaseArea` in place of its own `ShopDetailGallery`/`ShopDetailPrice`/`ShopDetailAddToCart`. Those slot components are distinct from the granular Puck blocks below: they render into shop's own `.spd-*` class names (handed down as props) and from shop's server-loaded images/price, so the swap is invisible and paints on first byte. As of v0.1.7 they are split like the Puck blocks: `components/public/DetailSlotParts.tsx` holds **async server** halves that await `getVariationBootstrap(props.slug)` (shop hands the slug down on every slot prop, so no request-scoped lookup is needed here) and pass it to the islands in `DetailSlotPartsClient.tsx` as `initial`. Awaiting is within shop's contract - it types the slots as plain components but only ever renders them from its own RSC halves (`ShopDetail*Rsc`). `OptionControl`/`AddonControl` are shared with `VariantParts.tsx` so the hand-placed blocks and the automatic slot render the identical control. Unclaimed products, and shop-only sites, are untouched.
  - **`coveredSlots(blockTypes)` - not claiming a job the layout already does by hand.** The point assumed shop's part was the only thing doing each job. Layouts written before it existed do the same job with this module's granular blocks (Deskwell's product page carries `ShopVariantPrice` and `ShopVariantOptions` beside shop's `ShopDetailPrice`/`ShopDetailAddToCart`), so taking the slot as well rendered the price and the option picker twice. Shop now passes every block type in the layout (`collectLayoutBlockTypes`, walks `content` **and** `zones` - the default Product Detail keeps its parts in a Split's zones) and this module returns the covered slots: `ShopVariantGallery`→Gallery, `ShopVariantPrice`→Price, `ShopVariantAddToCart`→PurchaseArea. Shop then renders **nothing** for those (`ctx.slot.covered`), rather than falling back to its own part - a static parent price beside a live variant price is two different figures for one product. Only applies to claimed products; an unclaimed one never consults `covered`, so shop's parts render normally.
  - **A replaced part inherits none of shop's behaviour, only its classes (v0.1.9).** Shop's `imageZoomOnHover` setting (shop settings > General) reached `VariantSlotGalleryClient` as the optional `zoom` prop from shop 0.1.40 and was simply ignored, so the shop-wide zoom silently did nothing on exactly the products this module claims - anything with options. The island now implements it: pointer-tracked `transformOrigin` + `transform: scale(2.5)` on the stage image, mouse magnifying on hover, touch on tap-drag-tap, reset when the variant image or thumbnail pick changes. Shop's behaviour is **reimplemented, not imported** - its copy lives inside `ProductGallery`, which knows nothing of variant images, and the `zoomable`/`zoomed` modifier classes behind it are shop CSS the `classNames` contract does not hand over; the two declarations they carry (cursor, and `touch-action` while magnified) go on inline instead, keeping the fix inside this module. The scale constant is duplicated deliberately and must stay level with shop's, or one setting means two things depending on the product. Generalises: any future prop shop adds to a slot is inert until a provider reads it, and nothing fails loudly when it doesn't.
  - Options and personalisation have no shop part to replace, so they can't be handled that way: they ride inside `VariantSlotPurchase`, which drops them itself when `layoutBlockTypes` (on every slot prop) shows `ShopVariantOptions`/`ShopVariantPersonalisation` already placed. Shop only ever passes block-type strings it attaches no meaning to; this module is the only side that knows what they mean. Resolution is split - `resolveShopDetailProvider(product)` (the claim, still parallel with the template fetch) then the pure `narrowShopDetailSlot(provider, blockTypes)` once the template's blocks are known.

**Cron Jobs**: `0 3 * * *` → `cron/cleanup-uploads`.

**Known Limitations**: a layout that *hand-places* a granular `ShopVariant*` block next to shop's equivalent (`ShopVariantPrice` beside `ShopDetailPrice`, etc.) now double-renders on a claimed product, because shop's own part is variant-aware via the slot as of shop 0.1.35 - the two can't see each other (the slot is per-product, the blocks are per-layout, and shop knowing about `ShopVariant*` types is exactly the coupling the point exists to avoid). Stock layouts are unaffected (they contain shop's parts only); the fix for a hand-built one is to drop the now-redundant `ShopVariant*` block. Also: a variant's image set can only be cleared wholesale (the × drops all of them) - there is no per-image remove in the grid cell; `svr_settings` has no admin UI (defaults only) in v1; CSV import requires the parent product to exist by slug (creates options + child variants, not parents); deleting a parent product leaves its hidden children orphaned (retention cleanup covers uploads; child-product cleanup on parent delete / uninstall is a documented follow-up); a hidden child 404s on its own URL rather than redirecting to its parent.

### Product Attributes for Shop

- Slug: `product-attributes-for-shop` (table prefix `pat_`), repo `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/product-attributes-for-shop`, manifest version 0.1.17 (registry pin v0.1.17). `requiresModules: shop >= 0.1.65` (raised in 0.1.6 for `MediaPickerModal`'s `resolveInitialFolderId`), `requiresCoreVersion 0.5.493` (raised in 0.1.6 for `core.media-reference-rewriters` + `moveOrRenameMedia`). Reuses shop's `shop.products` permission (declares none of its own) and joins the existing **Shop** admin nav group with one entry ("Product attributes").
- Adds shop-wide **filterable attributes** (Material, Colour, Room) with values. Each product carries a **set** of them (`pat_product_attributes`, v0.1.3): tick values for ordinary attributes, or flag one **Use for variations** to set its value per variant (a column on the Variations tab) and **Show in shop filters** off to keep it internal to that product. A storefront Puck block filters the catalogue by them. shop-variations is an **optional** companion, not a `requiresModules` entry: every `svr_` read goes through `lib/variations-bridge.ts` as raw SQL guarded by a `to_regclass` probe (30s cache, `resetVariationsProbeCache()` test seam), because `@/modules/shop-variations/...` does not resolve on an install without it and a static import would break that build. It also registers a **field provider** on shop-variations' `variant-field-provider` point (see below), likewise inert without shop-variations.

**Database**
Table prefix: `pat_` (6 tables). Full DDL in `modules/product-attributes-for-shop/migrations/001_initial.sql` (idempotent); later per-change files numbered (`002_product_attribute_sets.sql` adds `pat_product_attributes`; `003_image_control_type.sql` widens the control-type CHECK - no new column; `004_attribute_groups.sql` adds `pat_attribute_groups` + `pat_attributes.group_id`; `005_repeatable_product_attributes.sql` swaps both composite PKs for surrogate ids, adds `pat_product_attributes.name_override`/`position` and `pat_product_values.assignment_id`, and backfills each existing product-level tick onto the one helping it can have come from; `006_variation_columns_per_helping.sql` adds **no DDL at all** - it stamps `assignment_id` onto the per-variant rows 005 deliberately left NULL, so a variations column can belong to a helping rather than to an attribute; `007_swatch_size.sql` adds `pat_attribute_values.swatch_size`. 001/002 are **not** mirrored for these - both are idempotent and run on a fresh install too, so the end state is the same either way. 006 skips itself via `to_regclass('public.svr_variants')` when shop-variations is absent). Cross-module FKs to `shp_products` are safe because shop installs first.

- `pat_attribute_groups` (v0.1.7) - `id`, `name`, `slug` (unique), `position`, `created_at`. Admin-side folders only; nothing public reads them.
- `pat_attributes` - `id`, `name`, `slug` (unique; the storefront filter's query key), `control_type` (CHECKBOX\|SWATCH\|DROPDOWN\|IMAGE - IMAGE added 0.1.6), `position`, `show_in_filters` (shop-wide gate), `group_id?` FK → `pat_attribute_groups` **ON DELETE SET NULL** (v0.1.7 - deleting a folder must tip its attributes back onto the ungrouped pile, never cascade them and every product assignment away), `source_option_name?` (the shop-variations option name it was imported from, so a re-import updates rather than duplicates), `created_at`.
- `pat_attribute_values` - `id`, `attribute_id` FK (cascade), `label`, `slug` (unique per attribute), `swatch?` (**one column, two mediums as of 0.1.6**: a hex colour for a SWATCH attribute, a media url for an IMAGE one - same arrangement as `svr_option_values.swatch`), `swatch_size?` (**`007_swatch_size.sql`, v0.1.14** - the real-world size of the picture swatch, free text as typed: "20cm", "200mm", "0.2m" or a bare number; NULL/empty means "not given", which every value written before 007 is, so nothing may read a missing size as an error), `position`.
- `pat_product_values` - `id` PK (surrogate, added by `005_repeatable_product_attributes.sql`; was a composite PK on `(product_id, value_id)`), `product_id` FK→shp_products cascade, `value_id` FK cascade, `assignment_id?` FK→`pat_product_attributes` cascade, UNIQUE **NULLS NOT DISTINCT** `(product_id, value_id, assignment_id)`. `product_id` covers **both** parent products and shop-variations' hidden variant children - that is what makes per-variant attributes work with no second table. `assignment_id` says which *helping* of an attribute a tick belongs to. Since `006_variation_columns_per_helping.sql` that includes rows on a **variant child** (they carried NULL under 005, when one attribute meant one column and the row needed no further identity) - it is the only thing telling "Oak on the main finish" from "Oak on the edge", which are otherwise the same product, value and attribute. Still **nullable**: a row whose parent no longer uses that attribute for variations, or one written before 005, has no helping to name. The `NULLS NOT DISTINCT` clause keeps those de-duplicating properly.
- `pat_product_attributes` (v0.1.3) - `id` PK (surrogate, added by `005_repeatable_product_attributes.sql`; was a composite PK on `(product_id, attribute_id)`), `product_id` FK→shp_products cascade, `attribute_id` FK cascade, `name_override?` (TEXT, 005 - the name this helping goes by; NULL means "call it whatever the attribute is called"), `position` (INTEGER, 005), `use_for_variations` (bool, default false), `show_in_filters` (bool, default true - **per-product** filter gate, narrower than `pat_attributes.show_in_filters`; both apply), UNIQUE **NULLS NOT DISTINCT** `(product_id, attribute_id, name_override)`. The product's attribute "set" plus its per-helping flags. **A product may hold the same attribute several times** (005) - "Top material" and "Frame material" both off Material - with all but one carrying a `name_override`; the unique constraint is what enforces that, and the editor + PUT both state it in words first so the constraint is never what the owner meets. Membership is *not* a filter gate on its own - an assigned value still filters unless hidden here, and `getEffectiveValueIdsByProduct` only counts an attribute hidden when **every** helping of it on that product is (`HAVING bool_or(show_in_filters) = false`).
- `pat_settings` - singleton (`id='singleton'`): `hide_empty_values` (true), `include_variant_values` (true).

**A picture swatch carries its own real-world size (working tree, v0.1.14, unreleased)**: `007_swatch_size.sql` adds `pat_attribute_values.swatch_size` (nullable TEXT), surfaced as `PatAttributeValue.swatchSize` and validated at `SWATCH_SIZE_MAX_LENGTH` (40) in `lib/types.ts` - a length cap only, since the units are the reader's problem, not the store's. Set on the **Attributes** screen and, crucially, **editable afterwards**: an IMAGE attribute's add-value row gains a "Size, e.g. 20cm" box, and every existing value chip gains a small size button (shows the size, or "size?" when unset) that prompts for a new one and clears on blank - the figure usually arrives from the supplier after the photograph does, and deleting the value to re-add it with a size would drop every product ticked against it. Routes: `POST /attributes/[id]/values` and `PATCH /values/[id]` both take an optional `swatchSize`, normalising `''` to NULL so a cleared box and a never-filled one are one thing downstream; `createAttributeValue`/`updateAttributeValue` carry it (`!== undefined` guard on the update, so an explicit null clears). Column is deliberately **not** constrained to IMAGE attributes - an attribute can be switched between control types and losing the size on the way through would be a data-loss trap, the same reasoning `swatch` already follows. Not imported from shop-variations (no such field there) and not propagated to `svr_option_values` by `syncSourcedOptionValues` - the size is this module's fact about its own picture. Consumed by product-3d-views-for-shop's material configurator (see below).

**Permissions**: none of its own - all reads/writes gate on `shop.products` via shop's `requireShopUser` (GETs pass `allowAccess: true`).

**API Routes** (through `/api/m/product-attributes-for-shop/…`, all admin, all `shop.products`)

- `GET/POST admin/attributes`, `PATCH/DELETE admin/attributes/[id]` (rename re-slugs; case-insensitive duplicate name **within the same group** → 409 - see Attribute groups), `POST admin/attributes/[id]/values`, `PATCH/DELETE admin/values/[id]`. The values POST takes an optional `reuseExisting: true` (v0.1.5) that turns the duplicate-label 409 into "return the value that already has that label" - set by the two in-context add boxes on the product editor, left off by the attributes screen so a duplicate typed *there* is still reported as the mistake it is. Either way the response now carries the whole value row (`{ id, slug, value, reused }`), so a client can splice it into its list without a refetch. Both the values POST and the value PATCH validate `swatch` through `isValidSwatch` (hex **or** picture url, `SWATCH_MAX_LENGTH` 1000) rather than the old hex-only regex, and file a picked picture via `fileSwatchImage` before responding - filing can rewrite the url, so both re-read the row and hand back the **stored** url (`value.swatch` / `{ ok, swatch }`) instead of echoing what was sent.
- `POST admin/attributes/[id]/values/reorder` (v0.1.17) - whole-list drag reorder for one attribute's values; also pushes the order into any variation option copied from the attribute and renumbers the variants already generated from it. See "Value ordering" below.
- `POST admin/attributes/reorder`, `POST admin/groups/reorder` (v0.1.7) - take `{ ids: string[] }`, the **whole** running order, and write `position = index` in one transaction (`setAttributePositions` / `setAttributeGroupPositions`). Whole-list rather than "move this one up" because `position` is not unique-enforced, so two rows on the same number would make a swap a silent no-op; restating every row repairs the order as a side effect. A list with duplicates is 400; one that does not exactly match the ids on record is **409** ("reload the page") - a partial list would renumber the named rows to 0..n and leave everything else on its old number, shuffling rows nobody touched. Static-vs-dynamic precedence is safe: `scripts/generate-module-router.mjs` sorts static segments above `[param]` ones, so `attributes/reorder` cannot be swallowed by `attributes/[id]`.
- `GET/POST admin/groups`, `PATCH/DELETE admin/groups/[id]` (v0.1.7) - the attribute folders. POST/PATCH slugify and refuse a case-insensitive duplicate name with 409, same shape as attributes. PATCH on a rename and DELETE both **re-file the picture swatches** of every attribute involved (the group name is a folder segment); DELETE reads the membership *before* dropping the row, because the FK nulls `group_id` on the way out and there would be nothing left to walk. `PATCH admin/attributes/[id]` gains `groupId` (`string | null`, `null` meaning ungrouped - the zod field is `.nullable().optional()` so "take it out" and "leave it alone" stay distinct), 404s an unknown group, and re-files that attribute's pictures afterwards; `POST admin/attributes` takes the same optional `groupId` to create straight into a folder.
- `GET/POST admin/attributes/[id]/media-folder` (v0.1.6) - where the picture picker opens (GET, look-only, creates nothing) and where an upload should be filed (POST, creates). Same two-verb split, same reasoning, as shop's `products/[id]/media-folder`.
- `POST admin/refile-swatches` (working tree, unreleased) - walks every attribute and runs `refileAttributeSwatches`, moving each picture swatch into its `Shop/Attributes/[group]/<attribute>` folder. Idempotent (already-filed pictures are no-ops). Surfaced as a **Tidy picture folders** button on the attributes screen. Exists to repair pictures that older shop-variations builds dragged into product `colours` folders (see the swatch-filing invariant below).
- `GET/PUT admin/products/[id]/assignments` - one round trip returning the vocabulary + this product's `own` assignments + its **set** (`membership`) + its variants. `assignments.own` is a **`Record<assignmentId, valueId[]>`**, not a flat list: two helpings of one attribute hold separate ticks, including the same value ticked under both. PUT takes `{membership}` alone - each entry is `{id?, attributeId, nameOverride?, useForVariations, showInFilters, values[]}`, so the set and its ticks are submitted together and an existing helping keeps its id (recreating it would cascade its ticks away mid-save). It 409s on two helpings of one attribute sharing a name. It **no longer** refuses a repeated attribute that is also marked use-for-variations (**v0.1.13**): the Variations column is now per helping, so a product can raise Finish as both a "Main finish" and an "Edge finish" column, and the name rule is the only thing needed to keep the two (and their CSV headers) apart. It still **clears assignments for any attribute dropped from the set** - only genuinely gone attributes count, not one that merely lost a second helping - and **strips a use-for-variations attribute's value off the parent** (that value belongs per variant, not to the product).

**A variations column belongs to a helping, not an attribute (v0.1.13)** - `listVariationColumns` groups by `pat_product_attributes.id` (heading = `COALESCE(NULLIF(TRIM(name_override),''), a.name)`, ordered by `ppa.position`), `getVariantAttributeValues` joins `pat_product_values.assignment_id`, and `setVariantAttributeValue(childProductId, assignmentId, valueId)` scopes its clear-out to the assignment. That last one is the whole fix: scoped to the attribute, as it was, saving the edge finish deleted the main finish on the same variant. The field provider's `VariantFieldColumn.key` is therefore the assignment id, `PatVariationColumn` carries both `assignmentId` and `attributeId` (values and any newly-typed one still belong to the attribute, so `addLocalColumnValue` and `ensureAttributeValueByLabel` stay attribute-keyed - a finish typed into the edge column is offered by the main one too), and `variation-attributes` returns both ids per column. `importVariationOptions` files its per-variant links against the assignment `upsertProductAttribute` now returns. Covered by `lib/variant-field-provider.test.ts`, whose fixture is deliberately one attribute standing up as two columns.
- `GET admin/products/[id]/variation-attributes` (v0.1.3) - the use-for-variations columns (with their selectable values) + each variant's current value, keyed child→attribute; feeds the Variations-tab cells in one fetch.
- `POST admin/products/[id]/variant-attribute-value` (v0.1.3; body takes `assignmentId` not `attributeId` since **v0.1.13**) - sets (or clears) one variant's value for one use-for-variations **helping**; single-select per (variant, helping). Every id checked against the product: variant belongs to it, the helping is used-for-variations **on this product** (which is also what stops a crafted request writing against someone else's helping), value belongs to that helping's attribute.
- `POST admin/products/[id]/import-variations` - turns the product's `svr_options`/`svr_option_values` into attributes (matched by option **name**, so two products' "Colour" feed one shop-wide filter), attaches values to the variant children carrying them, and (v0.1.3) adds each to the set marked **use-for-variations** so it shows as a column. Idempotent: clears prior imported assignments for the touched attributes first. 409 when shop-variations is absent or the product has no options.

Admin pages (`/cactus-admin/m/product-attributes-for-shop/…`): `attributes` (define the vocabulary + values). The per-product `ProductAttributesSection` is the **Attributes tab** on shop's product editor via `shop.product-editor-sections` (server wrapper → `ProductAttributesEditor` client island, **redesigned v0.1.3**: add attributes to the product's set, per-attribute **Use for variations** / **Show in shop filters** tick-boxes, value ticks for ordinary attributes, "Copy from variations"; the old collapsible per-variant tick-grid is gone - per-variant values live on the Variations-tab column). It has **no save button of its own**: it registers with the product editor's single Save through `useProductEditorSave`, diffing set + ticks against a baseline. Tab badge = count of attributes in the set. The Variations-tab column is a **client cell** (`ProductAttributesVariantCell.tsx`) fed by a server field provider (`lib/variant-field-provider.ts`) and its own `lib/db/membership.ts`; fifty variants share one `variation-attributes` fetch via a module-scoped store and each cell saves itself on change (`variant-attribute-value`), not through the grid's Save.

**Values added in context (v0.1.5)** - a value no longer has to be created on the attributes screen first. `ProductAttributesEditor` renders an `AddValueBox` under every attribute in the product's set (label + a colour input when `controlType === 'SWATCH'`, `preventDefault` on Enter so the product editor's form does not submit); the variant cell's dropdown gains a `+ New value…` option (sentinel `__new__`, safe against value ids because those are uuids) that swaps the `<select>` for an input, Escape cancelling. Both POST `attributes/[id]/values` with `reuseExisting: true` and splice the returned row into local state - the editor into `data.attributes[].values` (and ticks it in `own` unless the attribute is use-for-variations, where the value belongs to a variant), the cell into the shared store's `columns` via `addLocalColumnValue` so every row in the grid offers it at once, then saves the assignment through the usual `variant-attribute-value` POST. **The value itself is written immediately, not deferred to the product's Save**: it is a change to the shop-wide vocabulary, not to this product, and the deliberate choice is that a value stays global rather than being scoped per product - a private "Oak" per product would give the storefront filter one option per product carrying it. The cost is that abandoning a product edit leaves the value behind (documented on the wiki page).

**Picture swatches (IMAGE control type, v0.1.6)** - a fourth control type whose values are offered as picture tiles. No new column: the value's one visual lives in `swatch` either way, and `lib/types.ts` gains `SWATCH_MAX_LENGTH` (1000) plus `isHexSwatch` / `isImageSwatch` / `isValidSwatch`. `isImageSwatch` accepts `http(s)://…` and site-relative `/…` **only** - it is the sole guard between the API and an `<img src>`, so `javascript:`/`data:` are refused. `isValidSwatch` deliberately accepts *either* medium regardless of the attribute's current control type, so switching an attribute from colours to pictures and back is a change of mind rather than a data-loss trap; each render site picks what it can show and falls back (an image-typed value holding a hex renders the empty tile, label intact).

**Swatch-filing invariant (working tree, unreleased)** - a sourced variation value's picture belongs to the attribute, never the product. Three co-ordinated changes: (1) shop-variations' `fileSwatchImage` now no-ops when the value carries a `source_ref` (it used to move the shared attribute picture into the product's `colours` folder, rewriting the url under the attribute and every other copy); (2) product-attributes' `fileSwatchImage` calls `syncSourcedOptionValues(valueId, { swatch })` after a move that rewrites the url, so `svr_option_values` copies follow it; (3) the option-source provider's `listSources` now returns attributes in attributes-screen order (each group's attributes together, ungrouped last) - the picker draws one heading per consecutive run, so the old flat position order repeated a group's heading once per run (the "three Dynamic groups" bug), and shop-variations' `groupSources` additionally merges any repeated non-null heading into its first section as a belt-and-braces guard.

Admin: one shared `components/admin/SwatchImagePicker.tsx` client component (shop's `MediaPickerModal` + `uploadOneFile`/`preflightUploadError`, drag-and-drop onto the thumbnail, dashed box when empty) used by both the attributes screen (add-value row, and per-value so an existing picture can be swapped) and `AddValueBox` on the product editor. The Variations-tab cell is unchanged - a `<select>` cannot hold a picture, and the label is the identifier there.

**Attribute groups (v0.1.7)** - folders for the attribute vocabulary, **admin-side only**: `listAttributes()` ordering, the filter block, `matchesSelection` and every public read are untouched, so grouping cannot change what a shopper sees. `lib/db/groups.ts` holds the CRUD plus `listAttributeIdsInGroup`. The attributes screen fetches `attributes` and `groups` in one `Promise.all`, renders one section per group in `position` order followed by a **Not in a group** section (drawn only when non-empty, and it also catches any attribute pointing at a group row that has gone), gives every card a Group `<select>` that PATCHes `groupId`, and puts Rename/Delete on each group heading (delete confirms with the count and says the attributes stay put). Empty groups render a prompt rather than vanishing, otherwise a freshly-made group would look like it failed.

**Attribute names are unique per group, not shop-wide (v0.1.8).** The duplicate-name guard was global, so a shop that wanted "Size" under both Chairs and Desks simply could not create the second one - the whole point of folders. `attributeNameTaken(name, groupId, exceptId)` now scopes the check with `"group_id" IS NOT DISTINCT FROM ${groupId}::text` (the ungrouped pile counts as one group; the `::text` cast is needed or Postgres cannot resolve the operator for an untyped null parameter). `POST admin/attributes` resolves and validates `groupId` **before** judging the clash, and `PATCH admin/attributes/[id]` now checks on a `groupId` change too, against the post-patch `(name, group)` pair - moving an attribute into a folder that already has that name is as much a duplicate as renaming it into one. **No schema change**: nothing ever enforced name uniqueness in the DB, only the API, and slugs stay globally unique via `ensureUniqueAttributeSlug` so the storefront filter's query key is still unambiguous. The attributes screen's "Add an attribute" row gains a Group `<select>` (hidden when no groups exist, falls back to "No group" if the chosen folder has since been deleted, and deliberately **not** reset after an add - filling one folder in a row is the common case); without it every new attribute landed ungrouped and was judged against the ungrouped pile, so the second "Size" was still unreachable. Picture-swatch folders need no change - the group name is already a path segment, so two same-named attributes in different groups file to different folders.

**Ordering (v0.1.7)** - up/down buttons on every attribute card and group heading (`MoveButtons`, `aria-label`ed per row; buttons rather than drag-and-drop, which gets keyboard and screen-reader support for free on lists this short). Groups reorder among themselves. An attribute moves **within its section**, but the POST carries the flattened order of *every* section - the attribute `position` is global (it is the storefront filter order), so sending only one group's slice would let a move inside "Materials" leapfrog an attribute in another group on the shop. Both handlers go through the screen's existing `send()`, so a failure surfaces in the same banner and the list re-reads from the server.
