**Value ordering (v0.1.17)** - attribute values get native HTML5 drag-and-drop instead of up/down buttons: a value list (colours, materials) commonly runs far longer than the attribute list itself, where the short-list case for buttons made sense, and a chip has no spare room for two more controls anyway. `draggable` sits on a small handle (`⠿`) inside each value chip, not the chip itself, so a drag gesture starting on the rename/delete buttons or the colour input is never misread; `onDragOver`/`onDrop` are on the chip, tracked via a per-card `draggedValueId` state. Same whole-running-order contract as attributes/groups: `POST admin/attributes/[id]/values/reorder` takes `{ ids: string[] }` scoped to one attribute, 400s on a duplicate id, 409s ("reload the page") on a list that doesn't exactly match the attribute's known value ids, then `setValuePositions(ids)` rewrites `position = index` for the whole list in one transaction (`lib/db/attributes.ts`, mirrors `setAttributePositions`). New `listAttributeValues(attributeId)` backs the 409 check. No new DB column - `pat_attribute_values.position` already existed and `listAttributes()` already ordered by it. The product Attributes tab, the Variations column dropdown (`listVariationColumns` orders `av."position"`) and the storefront filter block all re-read live and inherit the new order with no further work.

**A value reorder follows through to shop-variations (v0.1.17)** - `syncSourcedValueOrder(orderedValueIds)` in `lib/variations-bridge.ts`, called by the values reorder route, the third sibling of `renameSourcedOptions` / `syncSourcedOptionValues` and guarded by the same `hasVariationsTables()` probe. **Needed because shop-variations' own "refresh from source" syncs labels and swatches but never `position`** (`shop-variations/lib/option-refresh.ts:84-87` updates label/swatch; `nextPosition` at :72/:95 only numbers *newly added* values), so without this a copy keeps whatever slot it was created in for ever and a PAT reorder would move the filter and the product editor while every variations dropdown stayed as it was. Two set-based statements, no per-product loop, because a popular attribute can be an option source on hundreds of products and module routes share a hard 60s dispatcher ceiling:
- **Option values** - one `UPDATE ... FROM (WITH src(ref,rank) AS (VALUES …))` that renumbers **every** value on a touched option via `ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY option_id ORDER BY (src.rank IS NULL), src.rank, position, id)`. Renumbering the whole option, not just the sourced rows, is what guarantees a clean collision-free 0..n; `src.rank IS NULL` sorting last parks **hand-typed values (no `source_ref`) after the sourced block in their existing relative order** - PAT owns the values it supplied and nothing else, and interleaving them by a rule nobody wrote down would be worse than a documented tail. The VALUES list casts `${id}::text, ${index}::int` explicitly, since an untyped bind in a VALUES list arrives as text and would sort "10" below "9".
- **Variants** - `resequenceVariants(productIds)` renumbers `svr_variants.position` from `ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY product_id ORDER BY array_agg(ov.position ORDER BY o.position, o.created_at, o.id))`. Postgres compares arrays element by element, which **is** the odometer `generateMatrix` used (options left to right, last option fastest), so this reproduces the order a fresh generation would give. Deliberately a **renumber, never a regenerate**: a variant carries stock, price, photographs and any order placed against it, so ids are preserved absolutely. Child product **names are not touched** - a name is built from option order, and reordering values *within* an option cannot change any variant's label.
- Route returns `{ optionValuesMoved, variantsResequenced }`; the screen reports it through the existing `renameNote` line, staying silent at 0 so the common no-variations case says nothing.
- **Verified by real execution, not just tsc**: the two statements were run against a throwaway Neon project with a 2-option / 3-value / 6-variant fixture (one hand-typed value, one wholly local option). Result: sourced values took PAT order, the hand-typed one settled last, the local option was untouched, all six variant ids survived, positions came out a clean 0..5 in the new odometer order. Project deleted afterwards. Raw SQL of this shape is invisible to `tsc`/`eslint`, so a fixture run is the only check that means anything.

The equivalent gap on shop-variations' own screen is fixed in shop-variations 0.1.61 (see its section). The two odometers agree: PAT's SQL sorts on `array_agg(position ORDER BY option position)` and shop-variations' JS sums `value_index * radix[option_index]`, and mixed-radix ordering is lexicographic tuple ordering, so a reorder driven from either screen leaves the variants in the same order. That equivalence holds because both paths renumber values to a clean 0..n before resequencing; it would not survive duplicate positions within one option.

**Groups move the picture swatches with them** - the folder path became `shop / attributes / [group name /] <attribute name>`, so `attributeFolderSegments(attributeName, groupName?)` takes an optional group segment and the private `segmentsForAttribute(attributeId)` resolves it from the row (both `resolveAttributeFolderId` and the look-only `findAttributeFolderId` go through it). The group segment is **omitted entirely** when an attribute is ungrouped, so an existing install's folders are byte-identical to before and nothing shuffles on upgrade. `refileAttributeSwatches(attributeId)` walks that attribute's values (new `listAttributeSwatches` - returns every non-null swatch, hex ones filtered out in JS by `isImageSwatch` rather than by a LIKE pattern, so the validator stays the single authority on what a picture is) and re-runs `fileSwatchImage` on each, moving the file and rewriting the stored url; `refileGroupSwatches(groupId)` does the lot for a group. Called on: move into/out of/between groups, group rename, group delete, **and attribute rename** - that last one had quietly stranded pictures in the old folder since 0.1.6. Per-picture failures stay swallowed-and-warned inside `fileSwatchImage`, so one unmovable file cannot strand the rest.

**Media filing is by attribute, not by product** - `lib/media-folder.ts` files pictures under `shop / attributes / [group /] <attribute name>` (lower-cased through `sanitizeFolderSegment`, same as shop's tree), NOT the product folder that shop-variations, the 3D module and the downloads module all use. Deliberate: an attribute value is shop-wide vocabulary (one "Oak" picture serves every product carrying it), so filing it under whichever product happened to be open would mislead, and would strand the picture the day that product is deleted. `fileSwatchImage` is a no-op unless the url resolves to a managed `Media` row, so the folder is never created for an attribute that only uses colours; a filing failure is warned and swallowed rather than failing the save. Pictures **imported** from shop-variations keep that module's filing - re-filing them would move a file shop-variations owns and break its own swatch. `lib/import-service.ts` now carries url swatches across instead of dropping everything non-hex, and infers the control type as IMAGE if any value has a picture, else SWATCH if any has a hex, else CHECKBOX (pictures win when an option holds both - picture tiles with an empty tile or two beat colour dots for the minority that have one). A bare media id, which shop-variations may also hold there, is still dropped: nothing renderable can be made of it.

**`core.media-reference-rewriters` (v0.1.6)** - `lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts` repoints `pat_attribute_values.swatch` when core moves a blob (optimise/resize/crop/replace/rename), matching on url **equality** (for an image swatch the column is the whole url, so it cannot hit a hex colour). Without it the tile 404s while the library looks healthy. Registered in the manifest under this module's own id, alongside shop-variations' rewriter for its equivalent column.

**`core.media-usage-providers`** - `lib/media-usage-provider.ts` returns every `pat_attribute_values.swatch` (colour swatches come back too - a hex string matches no media item) so picture swatches stop counting as unused library clutter.

**Puck Blocks**: `ShopAttributeFilterGrid` ("Shop: Filtered Product Grid", layouts `shopIndex`/`shopCategory`/`shopCollection`, editor + RSC split via `rscImport`, colour tokens only). RSC renders every matching product up front with shop's **own** Product Card template (`resolveCardTemplate` + `buildCardContext` + `injectShopProductCardEmbed`), tagging each `.shop-card` anchor `data-pat-product`/`data-pat-values`; the `AttributeFilterShell` client island then shows/hides them in place. It deliberately mirrors shop's `renderCards` rather than calling it - the only difference is the data tag, which shop's helper has nowhere to hang. Facet semantics: OR within an attribute, AND across attributes - the rule itself is the pure `matchesSelection()` in `lib/filter-logic.ts` (7 tests in `lib/filter-logic.test.ts`), which the shell calls rather than keeping its own copy. Selection mirrors into the URL via `replaceState` (read post-mount only, so hydration cannot mismatch the server-rendered cards). Filter CSS in `components/public/filter-css.ts` (prefix `pat-`, tokens only, site breakpoints baked in like shop's grids; `.pat-images`/`.pat-image*` added in 0.1.6 for the picture tiles).

**Variant rollup**: `getEffectiveValueIdsByProduct()` unions a parent's own values with those of its **enabled** variants (disabled ones excluded - not buyable, so a filter hit would be a dead end), then (v0.1.3) **drops any value whose attribute the product has hidden** (`pat_product_attributes.show_in_filters = false` for that `(product, attribute)`); `countProductsByValue()` counts the same way, powering the per-option counts and `hide_empty_values`. Both are consumed only by the public filter grid (`ShopAttributeFilterGrid.rsc.tsx`), so the hide never touches admin. **`countProductsByValue(productIds, opts)` now takes the same `includeVariantValues` the grid builds its matrix with (2026-07-23)** and passes it through to `getEffectiveValueIdsByProduct`. Left to its own devices it rolled variants up regardless of the setting, so with the setting off a variant-only value showed a non-zero count, survived `hide_empty_values` on the strength of it, and then matched nothing when a shopper ticked it - a dead-end filter option. The counts and the matrix must see products the same way or the panel lies about itself.

**Extension point consumed**: `shop-variations.variant-field-provider` (id `product-attributes`) → `productAttributesVariantFieldProvider`. The provider is inert (no columns) unless the product has use-for-variations attributes, and unreachable unless shop-variations hosts the point, so an install without it sees no change. **Import batching (v0.1.4):** implements the optional `beginImport(productId, childIds)`, preloading every child's current variation-attribute value via `getVariantAttributeValues` in one query. `applyImportedRow` now (a) resolves each label once via a per-import cache over `ensureAttributeValueByLabel`, and (b) only calls `setVariantAttributeValue` when the resolved value id **differs** from the preloaded current one - killing the old unconditional per-row write. A ctx miss (new variant) reads as no current value, so its first non-empty cell still writes. **Preview `rowChanged` (v0.1.19-to-be, working tree):** read-only twin resolving each cell via new `findAttributeValueByLabel` (a non-creating lookup added beside `ensureAttributeValueByLabel` in `lib/db/membership.ts`) and comparing to the preloaded value; an unseen label resolves to null ≠ stored, so it counts as a change without materialising the value. Behaviour tested in `lib/variant-field-provider.test.ts`.

**Known Limitations**: filtering only covers what the block rendered, and `listProducts` clamps `perPage` to 100 - so 100 products is the honest ceiling per grid (a larger catalogue wants a paginated, server-filtered grid). `pat_settings` has no admin UI (defaults only) in v1. No `settingsTabs` entry. Renaming an attribute re-slugs it, breaking any bookmarked filter URL. Imported swatches take hex only (shop-variations also allows a media id there).

### Product Downloads for Shop

- Slug: `product-downloads-for-shop` (table prefix `pdl_`), repo `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/product-downloads-for-shop`, manifest version 0.1.2 (registry pin v0.1.2, landed in core v0.5.540).
- `core.media-usage-providers` (`lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) - contributes `pdl_files.url`/`media_key`/`media_id`, so attached downloads aren't counted as unused media.
- `requiresCoreVersion` **0.5.472**, `requiresModules` **shop >= 0.1.50** (the release adding `shop.product-detail-tabs`). Manifest v0.1.0 named 0.1.47 - the shop of the day it was written against, which shipped without the point; corrected in module v0.1.1, since a min version naming a release that lacks the feature installs cleanly and then silently renders no tab at all.
- Free downloadable literature on a product - manuals, spec sheets, care cards, drawings - each named in plain English, shown on the product page under a **Downloads** tab that anyone can take them from. Distinct from shop's `shp_digital_files`, which is the product being *sold* and is delivered post-purchase behind a token with an expiry and a download count.

**Database**
Table prefix: `pdl_`

- `pdl_files` - `id` (text PK, gen_random_uuid), `product_id` FK → `shp_products` (cascade), `name` (what the shopper reads and saves it as), `filename` (as uploaded), `url`, `media_provider?`, `media_key?`, `media_id?` (the core `Media` row, nullable), `mime_type`, `size` (int), `position` (int), `created_at`. Index: product_id.

**Extension points consumed**: `shop.product-editor-sections` (id `product-downloads-inline`, label "Downloads", order 50, permission `shop.products`) and `shop.product-detail-tabs` (id `product-downloads`, label "Downloads", order 45).

**Routes**: `GET|POST|PATCH /api/m/product-downloads-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/files` (list / upload / save order - PATCH scopes the renumber to the product in the WHERE clause, so a posted foreign id renumbers nothing), `PATCH|DELETE /api/m/product-downloads-for-shop/admin/files/[id]` (rename / drop our row + the `Media` row + the blob), `GET /api/m/product-downloads-for-shop/public/files/[id]` (the download).

**Upload path - through the server, and it has to be (4 MB)**: the direct-to-Worker path photographs and 3D models use is **closed to a document**. The Worker types an upload from its object key's extension (`contentTypeForKey`) and 415s anything that is not a raster image or a 3D model, so a signed PDF key is refused no matter what. The bytes therefore go multipart through the serverless function, where Vercel's ~4.5 MB body cap applies, so the module advertises `MAX_UPLOAD_BYTES` (4 MB) and preflights on the client rather than promising more and dying on the doorstep - the exact failure `product-3d-views-for-shop` v0.1.2 was released to fix, and the reason shop's own `digital-files` route claiming `maxSizeBytes: 200 MB` is a lie the platform overrules. Lifting it needs a core release teaching the Worker about document types **plus** every install redeploying its Worker.

**Why downloads are proxied rather than linked (`app/api/public/files/[id]`)**: core's `extensionForMimeType` derives a key's extension from the MIME **subtype**, so a `.docx` is stored under a key ending `.vnd.openxmlformats-officedocument.wordprocessingml.document`, with a nanoid prefix. Link the shopper at storage and they save a file their machine cannot open; the `<a download>` attribute would rename it but is ignored cross-origin, and storage is always another origin. So the route sets `Content-Disposition` itself from `lib/download-name.ts` (owner's name + the *original* file's extension, so "Instructions.exe" cannot rename a PDF, and a typed ".pdf" does not double). Also: reads by `provider`+`key` via core's `downloadMedia` rather than fetching the stored url, so a site that later moves its Worker keeps working (shop's digital files store only a url and every link dies at that point); `Content-Length` from the bytes in hand, never the `size` column; always `attachment` + `nosniff`.

**Self-healing storage details (`lib/db/heal.ts`, `withFreshStorage`)**: `pdl_files` copies `media_provider` / `media_key` / `url` off the core `Media` row at upload time so the download route needs no join - a snapshot the core library then invalidates behind its back. Renaming a product renames its media folder, the folder path is baked into the object key, so every file inside gets a new key **and a new nanoid**, and core updates only its own `Media` rows. Both of `chiro-plus-high-back-ergonomic-posture-24-hour-office-chair`'s assembly PDFs went to "That file could not be retrieved." this way (stale key 404s at the Worker, live `Media.key` 200s; verified against the Deskwell library). `media_id` is the column that survives a move, because it names the row rather than the address, so the public GET and the admin DELETE both resolve through it first: mismatch → serve/delete the live key and write it back to `pdl_files`. Repair is per-request and needs nobody to press anything - the next click on a stale download fixes it and serves it. Rows with no `media_id`, or whose `Media` row is gone, pass through untouched. Write-back is best-effort (a lost race just heals again next time). The DELETE side matters separately: deleting by a dead key leaves the real bytes billed forever with nothing pointing at them. `p3d_models` and `svr_uploads` cache the same three columns beside a `media_id` and have the same latent exposure (0 stale rows on Deskwell today).

**Status gating**: the public route loads the owning product and 404s unless `status === 'ACTIVE' && !catalogueHidden` - the same line `app/public/shop/products/[slug]/page.tsx` draws. Without it an id would hand out an unlaunched product's manual or a withdrawn one's spec sheet; the uuid makes it unguessable, not access-controlled.

**Type policy** (`lib/file-kinds.ts`, single source for server and browser): pdf, zip, doc(x), xls(x), ppt(x), rtf, txt, csv, dwg, dxf, jpg/jpeg, png. **No html/svg/xml/js, deliberately** - the module serves stored bytes from the site's own origin, and a type the browser renders markup from is stored XSS rather than a download. The extension decides, not the declared MIME (a .zip arrives as `application/zip` or `application/x-zip-compressed`; a .dwg as nothing).

**Known limitations**: 4 MB per file (above). No per-variation downloads - files attach to the product only. On a DIGITAL product that also carries free literature, shop's own "Downloads" tab and this module's sit side by side, both labelled "Downloads"; rare (it means an ebook with a manual) and cosmetic, but a per-product label would need the point's contract to grow.

### Product 3D Views for Shop

- Slug: `product-3d-views-for-shop` (table prefix `p3d_`), repo `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/product-3d-views-for-shop`, manifest version 0.1.50 (registry pin v0.1.49; 0.1.50 unreleased, in the working tree).
- `core.media-usage-providers` (`lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) - contributes `p3d_models.url`/`media_key`/`media_id` plus `p3d_fabric_configs.config` returned whole as text (core scans it for any embedded texture reference, exactly as it scans Puck builder JSON).
- `requiresCoreVersion` **0.5.490** (the release adding `lib/modules/hosted-settings.ts` and the labelled hosted-panel forwarding), `requiresModules` **shop >= 0.1.53** (the release publishing the `shop.settings-sub-tabs` slot). Was 0.5.468 / shop 0.1.43 before the settings tab.
- A 3D model on a product or one of its variations, shown as an extra auto-rotating gallery thumbnail badged "3D"; picking it replaces the gallery's main image with an orbit/pan/zoom viewer.

**Database**
Table prefix: `p3d_`

- `p3d_models` - `id` (text PK, gen_random_uuid), `product_id` FK → `shp_products` (cascade), `url`, `media_provider?`, `media_key?`, `media_id?` (the core `Media` row, nullable - a model whose library row is deleted still renders), `owns_media` (bool, default **false**, **migration `005_owns_media.sql`, v0.1.32**), `filename`, `format` (check: glb | gltf | obj | fbx | 3ds), `size` (int), `position` (int), `created_at`. Index: product_id.
- `p3d_settings` (**migration `002_settings.sql`, v0.1.5**) - `id` (text PK, default `'singleton'`, CHECK = `'singleton'`), `config` (jsonb, default `{}`), `updated_at`. The singleton viewer-settings row, same shape and key as shop's `shp_settings`. No row seeded: absent = defaults, and `updateP3dConfig` upserts so the first save heals it. `to_regclass`-probed by `getP3dConfig` so a product page served before the migration runs falls back to defaults rather than 500ing. Added to `teardown`.
- `p3d_product_settings` (**migration `004_product_settings.sql`, v0.1.30**) - `product_id` (text PK, FK → `shp_products` cascade), `config` (jsonb, default `{}`), `updated_at`. One row per **parent** product holding its viewer-setting overrides as JSON (`lib/db/product-settings.ts`, `P3dProductConfigSchema`); today the only field is `exposure` (nullable, null = use the sitewide value). Merged over the sitewide config by `applyProductOverrides` in the gallery provider (and the fabric admin route, so the material-configurator preview matches the storefront) - everything downstream sees one resolved `P3dConfig`. Admin API `GET/PUT /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/settings` (gate `shop.products`; GET also returns the **whole** sitewide `P3dConfig` as `site` - **v0.1.33**, was just `toneMapping` + `exposure` - the panel needs the rest to light its preview the way the storefront will, and the fabric route already hands the same config to the same admin). UI: "Viewer brightness" panel on the product editor's 3D views tab (`ViewerSettingsPanel` in `Product3dEditor.tsx`), debounced save-as-you-go, greyed while sitewide colour handling is `none`. **Live preview (v0.1.33, registry-pinned).** While the override is ticked (and colour handling is not `none`) the panel mounts a real `Viewer3d` under the slider on the product's own first model, else the first variation's, lit by `{...site, exposure: override}` - so the slider can be judged rather than guessed. Mounted only while ticked, since a WebGL context and a model download are not a fair price for a tab opened to add a file. `Product3dEditor` keeps the tree's models in one `treeModels` state (list and preview both derive from it) rather than a filtered list plus a boolean. In manifest `teardown`.
- `p3d_fabric_configs` (**migration `003_fabric_config.sql`, v0.1.8**) - `product_id` (text PK, FK → `shp_products` cascade), `config` (jsonb, default `{}`), `updated_at`. One row per **parent** product configured for the fabric configurator. Everything inside the JSON (option/value/attribute/model ids) is resolved at read time, so the table carries **no** hard FK to shop-variations/product-attributes rows and stays valid on an install that later removes them. `to_regclass`-probed by `getFabricConfig` (`lib/db/fabric-config.ts`) so a page served before the migration runs treats it as "not configured" rather than 500ing. Read/upsert: `getFabricConfig`/`saveFabricConfig`, zod schema `FabricConfigSchema` (defensive `parseFabricConfig` returns null on corrupt). Added to `teardown`. Migration validated on a throwaway Neon project (idempotent re-apply, FK + cascade) 2026-07-17.

**The configurator picks a HELPING, not just an attribute (working tree, unreleased)**: product-attributes-for-shop 0.1.11+ lets one product use the same attribute more than once, each helping named by `pat_product_attributes.name_override` and each ticked value stamped with `pat_product_values.assignment_id`. The fabric configurator's three attribute dropdowns (**Overall height from**, and per part **Colour from** / **Size from**) were attribute-keyed throughout, so "Fabric" used as both *Seat fabric* and *Back fabric* collapsed to one entry and `resolve.ts`'s `.find()` on `attributeId` took whichever row Postgres returned first. Now: `listSizeAttributes(productId)` and `listColourAttributes(productId)` both take the product (was: site-wide, no argument - the two callers, the admin fabric route and the public `swatches` route, pass it) and go through the new private `listAttributeChoices(productId)`, which lists the product's helpings by `position` and then every attribute it has no helping for (keeping the old site-wide behaviour for a product whose values were set per-variation without the attribute being declared on the parent). **The stored id is the helping's id only where the attribute is used more than once**; used once, it stays the bare attribute id, so no saved `FabricConfig` JSON needs migrating and legacy configs keep resolving - the helping's override name still shows either way. `ChildSizeValue` gains `assignmentId`, the child-values query selects it, and the three lookups go through `matchesSource()` (assignment id **or** attribute id). Guarded by a new `hasAttributeHelpings()` probe (`information_schema` column check for `name_override` + `assignment_id`, 30s TTL beside the existing probes): on an older product-attributes install the second query shape is skipped and the module behaves exactly as before, since it pins no version of that module. Covered by three cases in `lib/fabric/resolve.test.ts`.

**Why product_id covers variations too**: a shop-variations variation IS a hidden child `shp_products` row (`svr_variants.child_product_id`), so a model on a variation is a model on that child's id. The module therefore holds **no** notion of options or variants and depends on shop alone.

**shop-variations is optional, not required**. `lib/db/models.ts` reads the `svr_` tables through raw SQL and never imports `@/modules/shop-variations/...` - that path does not exist on an install without it, and a static import would break the build there. Presence is probed with `to_regclass` (30s TTL cache), not the `Module` table, since a module row can exist before its migration has run. Same bargain and the same reasoning as `product-attributes-for-shop/lib/variations-bridge.ts`. Read-only: this module adds no column to shop-variations' schema, and its Variations-tab column is contributed through a generic point rather than built into shop-variations (below).

**Extension points consumed**: `shop.product-editor-sections` (id `product-3d-views-inline`, label "3D views", order 60, permission `shop.products`), `shop.gallery-media` (id `product-3d-views`), and `shop-variations.variant-field-provider` (id `product-3d-views-variant`, permission `shop.products` - **moved here from `variant-columns` in the working tree** so the 3D files round-trip through the CSV/Google Sheet; `lib/variant-field-provider.ts` exports `product3dVariantFieldProvider`, whose `Cell` is the same `Product3dVariantColumn`). Also `core.media-usage-providers` (id `product-3d-views-for-shop`, `lib/media-usage-provider.ts`) and, **new 2026-07-23, `core.media-reference-rewriters`** (id `product-3d-views-for-shop`, `lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts` exporting `product3dMediaReferenceRewriter`).

**Media addresses are kept in step, and healed when they were not (2026-07-23)**: `p3d_models` snapshots a blob three ways - the public `url`, the provider storage `key` and the core `Media` id - so the storefront can hand the viewer a url without a join, and the fabric configurator files each model's measured real-world size inside `p3d_fabric_configs.config` keyed by the model's url (query string stripped, see `lib/fabric/calibration.ts`'s `modelScaleKey`). Every one of those is an address, and the core library moves blobs about underneath them: optimise to WebP, resize, crop, replace-file, and renaming a product or a folder, which re-keys every file inside it. Without a rewriter the row went on naming the old, now-deleted address - the storefront thumbnail and viewer 404 permanently, the orphaned blob is billed forever, and the calibration key no longer matched the model url so every fabric surface silently dropped back to repeat 1. Two halves: (1) `lib/media-reference-rewriter.ts` is the provider for `core.media-reference-rewriters`, which core runs from `rewriteMediaReferencesInContent` (`lib/media/upload.ts`) **before** it deletes the superseded blob - so a throw aborts the whole move with the old blob still serving, a loud recoverable failure rather than a silent 404. (2) `lib/db/heal.ts`'s `withFreshStorage(model)` is the safety net for rows a move stranded BEFORE the rewriter existed: `media_id` points at the library row rather than at the address, so it survives the move, and the next read of a stale model quietly brings its `key` and `url` back into line. Model rows only, on purpose.

**Settings tab (v0.1.5)**: manifest `settingsTabs` entry id `product-3d-views`, label "3D Viewer", permission `shop.manage`, `host: "shop.settings-sub-tabs"` - so it renders as a sub-tab inside **admin > Shop**, not a top-level Settings tab (see the hosted-panels note in the config-page section). `components/admin/Settings3dTab.tsx` is the panel (four cards: Lighting, Stage, Handling, Speed); `lib/config.ts` owns the zod schema (`P3dConfigSchema`), the singleton read/write (`getP3dConfig`/`getP3dConfigCached`/`updateP3dConfig`, 5s cache like shop) and `P3D_CONFIG_DEFAULTS`. **Every default is the value the module hardcoded before the tab existed**, so an install that upgrades into v0.1.5 with no saved row looks byte-identical. `GET|PUT /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/settings` (gated `shop.manage` - the module has no permission key of its own and shop is a hard dep) reads/writes it. The settings ride to the storefront **inside `P3dPayload.settings`** (resolved once server-side in `lib/gallery-provider.ts`, only when a product actually has a model), never a client fetch. `components/public/Viewer3d.tsx` applies them (renderer antialias/pixel-ratio cap, tone mapping + exposure, background transparent/colour/environment, shadows via `addShadowCatcher`, and every OrbitControls dial) - all at **build** time, since the build effect's deps are `[item.url, item.format]` alone and the settings never move on the storefront; the one exception is **exposure (v0.1.33)**, mirrored onto the live renderer (`rendererRef.current.toneMappingExposure`) by its own effect so the admin's brightness preview updates on the next animation frame instead of tearing down the WebGL context and re-downloading the model on every step of a slider drag; `lib/three/load-model.ts` `addLights` takes the four light intensities + environment intensity and returns the key light so the viewer can make it a shadow caster; `lib/three/thumb-stage.ts` honours `thumbnailAutoRotate`, `antialias`, `pixelRatioCap`, `toneMapping`/`exposure` and the lighting on the shared thumbnail renderer (tone mapping added later - see the brightness-parity note below). **Shadows are the main viewer's alone** - never the 64px thumbnails (cost with nothing to show, and the thumbnails spin their pivot which would drag a baked shadow round). A shopper's OS "reduce motion" still overrides `autoRotate`/`thumbnailAutoRotate`.

**Thumbnail brightness parity**: the shared thumbnail renderer in `lib/three/thumb-stage.ts` was built with no tone-mapping setup at all, so the strip drew at three's own defaults (`NoToneMapping`, exposure 1) while `Viewer3d` drew the same model through the owner's `toneMapping`/`exposure` - visibly different brightness between the small picture and the big one next to it on any site not using `toneMapping: 'none'`. `getRenderer` now sets both from `thumbSettings` (captured in `mountThumb` before the renderer is built, same as `antialias`/`pixelRatioCap`), so the context-loss rebuild path picks them up too. Lighting, environment intensity, anisotropy and fabric paint already matched; the tone curve was the whole gap.

**Thumbnail strip froze on its first frame (regression fix)**: `tick()` in `lib/three/thumb-stage.ts` decided whether to schedule another rAF with `spin > 0 || pending`, where `spin = SPIN_RATE * delta` and `delta` is **0 on the first frame of any run** (no previous timestamp). So the very first tick drew each thumbnail once, found `spin === 0` and nothing pending, scheduled no successor and reset `lastTime = 0` on the way out - which made every later `start()` repeat that same dead first frame. Net effect: no thumbnail on any site ever rotated, with `thumbnailAutoRotate` on and no error anywhere. Introduced by the draw-on-demand (`needsDraw`) change, which added the `pending` continuation condition. Fix: the loop continues on the **intent** (`spinning`, the settings-and-reduced-motion boolean) rather than on the computed step. The same trap is now covered from the other side by `lib/nudge.test.ts` ("turns nothing on a zero-length frame, and is not finished by it").

**Idle motion styles (`autoRotateStyle`, `autoRotateSweep`)**: `autoRotate` says whether the stage moves on its own; `autoRotateStyle` says what that motion is. `'continuous'` is **the default** (unchanged behaviour on upgrade); `'nudge'` turns the model once through `autoRotateSweep` degrees (default 40, range 5-180) with an easeInOutQuad tween over a fixed `NUDGE_DURATION_MS = 1600`, then stops for good; `'continuous'` is the historic endless turn and is the only style `autoRotateSpeed` still means anything for (the settings tab greys the speed slider otherwise, and greys the sweep slider under `'continuous'`). The nudge is armed by an `IntersectionObserver` on the host (threshold 0.25, disconnected on first hit, straight to armed where the API is missing), so a gallery below the fold spends its sweep when the shopper can see it rather than on load. Driven by the viewer's own tween rather than `controls.autoRotate` because it has to serve both viewer kinds - `pivot.rotation.y` in spin mode, `orbitBy(step, 0)` otherwise - and because a sweep needs a finish line: each frame applies (eased position - already applied), so a dropped frame costs smoothness, never the final angle. `takeHold` cancels it, `resetRef` replays it from zero without waiting for the observer, and `carriedView.spinning` includes `nudgeRunning` so an option change mid-nudge resumes it. The render loop now takes the rAF timestamp (`elapsed` clamped to 100ms, so a backgrounded tab does not teleport through the sweep on its first frame back). The **thumbnail strip follows the same style**: per-entry `nudgeElapsed`/`nudgeApplied`/`nudgeDone` on the `Entry`, advanced only while `isVisible(entry.canvas)` (so a thumbnail below the fold still has its turn waiting), and an unfinished nudge counts as `pending` so the shared loop stays alive; `SPIN_RATE` now paces `'continuous'` only. The tween itself lives in `lib/nudge.ts` (`NUDGE_DURATION_MS`, `easeNudge`, `nudgeStep`) and is shared by both surfaces so the strip and the stage read as one gesture and the constants cannot drift apart; `lib/nudge.test.ts` covers it (lands on exactly the sweep at any frame rate, no overshoot on a backgrounded tab's enormous gap, a zero-length frame is not "finished"). Reduced motion still wins over the lot. **No default changes on upgrade** - `'continuous'` is what the module always did; `'nudge'` is there for owners whose shoppers are on older phones.

**Stage viewer parks its loop when unseen**: the same `IntersectionObserver` (now `threshold: 0`, kept connected for the viewer's life rather than disconnected after first sight, with `nudgeSpent` stopping the nudge replaying on every scroll-back) drives `setOnScreen`, which `cancelAnimationFrame`s the loop outright when the stage leaves the viewport and restarts it - re-basing `lastFrameAt` and forcing one `invalidate()` - when it returns. A backgrounded tab was always free (browsers stop serving rAF), and a viewer scrolled past was not: the endless turn kept rendering into a canvas nobody could see for as long as the shopper read the description below it. Nobody can be mid-drag on an off-screen stage, so no motion state needs preserving across the park. The `AnimationMixer` delta is now clamped (`Math.min(clock.getDelta(), 0.1)`) for the same reason `elapsed` is: the clock runs on while parked, and an unclamped resume fast-forwards the clip through time nobody watched. **The thumbnail strip is deliberately NOT parked** - its shared loop keeps ticking (rAF only, `isVisible` already suppresses every draw) because that tick is the only thing that notices a thumbnail scrolling back in; parking it would need per-thumbnail observers to wake it.

**Spin-model mode (v0.1.21, fixed for real in 0.1.26)**: `spinModel` picks WHAT moves. Off (default): the camera does everything - auto-rotate orbits it and a drag swings it round a still model; the shadow map is baked once (`shadowMap.autoUpdate=false` + one `needsUpdate`) since nothing in the world ever moves, saving the per-frame shadow pass. On: the MODEL turns - idle spin and horizontal drag alike - while camera, light and floor hold still, so the shadow stays anchored beneath it with a LIVE shadow map whose silhouette follows the turning shape. Implementation in `Viewer3d`: camera azimuth locked (`min/maxAzimuthAngle = getAzimuthalAngle()`), own pointer handlers turn the pivot (2π per stage height, matching OrbitControls' orbit ratio; release glides, decayed by `dampingFactor`; a non-primary pointer cancels the drag so pinch stays the controls'); vertical drag tilts via OrbitControls as before; idle-spin step matched to `autoRotateSpeed`. `spinModel` governs drag as well as idle, so the settings tab no longer disables it when `autoRotate` is off. History: v0.1.24 had frozen the map in spin mode ("pin the shadow") - that anchored the shadow by petrifying its shape and the silhouette never followed the model; 0.1.26 inverted it. Related 0.1.26 fixes: `loadModel` deep-clones MATERIALS per clone (`.clone(true)` shares them, so one viewer's fabric paint mutated the cached master - colour leaked onto thumbnails and the next clone of the same file arrived pre-painted; textures stay shared), and the repaint effect `prefetchTexture`s + re-checks `cancelled` before stamping so a stale colour's slow fetch can no longer overwrite a newer pick.

**Baked GLB animations play in the viewer (working tree, unreleased)**: `parseRaw()` in `lib/three/load-model.ts` now assigns `gltf.scene.animations = gltf.animations` before returning the scene - GLTFLoader hands the clips back **beside** the scene, so returning `gltf.scene` alone silently dropped them. `Object3D.copy()` copies `animations` by reference (three 0.180, `Object3D.js:1567`), which is what carries the clips through `loadModel`'s `.clone(true)`; clips bind to nodes **by name**, which cloning preserves, so no retargeting is needed. `Viewer3d.tsx` builds an `AnimationMixer(model)` when `wantsMotion && model.animations.length > 0`, plays every clip, and advances it with a `Clock` delta inside the existing rAF loop (real elapsed time, so a dropped frame costs smoothness rather than desynchronising the file's authored timing). Cleanup calls `stopAllAction()` + `uncacheRoot(model)` - three caches bindings per root, so without it a shopper flicking between variations leaks one binding set per model. **Gated on `wantsMotion` (the reduced-motion + `settings.autoRotate` check) but deliberately NOT on the touch latch** that kills the idle turn: the idle turn stops on touch because it fights someone inspecting a corner, whereas an animation is usually the thing they opened the viewer to watch, and freezing it mid-travel parks the model in a state the real product never sits in. No per-product setting and no code that knows what moves - motion is data in the file. Thumbnails (`lib/three/thumb-stage.ts`) run no mixer, so they render the file's bind pose. Verified against three's own `GLTFLoader.parse` on a real animated GLB (clip survives clone, mixer drives the node, loop start/end match to the micron).

**Carried view - a model swap keeps the shopper's viewing angle and zoom (working tree, unreleased)**: `Viewer3d.tsx` holds a module-scope `carriedView` (camera position, `controls.target`, `pivot.rotation.y`, the `touched`/`moved` latches, capture timestamp). The build effect's `dispose` writes it first, while the scene still holds the view; the next build reads it via `takeCarriedView()` **synchronously at effect start** (the freshness window measures the dispose-to-rebuild gap, not the model download) and re-applies it AFTER `OrbitControls` is constructed, so the controls' saved state - and therefore **Reset view** - still means the opening framing. Safe across different models because `frameModel` normalises everything into the same 2-unit box at the origin. Module-scope rather than a ref because a fabric product's stage remounts across the `PaintedStage`/plain-`Viewer3d` branch in `Gallery3dStage`; the 3-second freshness window keeps a later client-side navigation from inheriting the old product's view, and the carry is deliberately NOT consumed on read (a rapid option flick can cancel a build before it owns a disposer, and the next build still deserves the view). Carried `touched` suppresses the idle turn and the drag hint on the new model; carried `moved` keeps the Reset button up; an untouched auto-rotating model simply carries on turning from where it was. Local `latchTouched`/`latchMoved` booleans shadow the React state inside the build closure because `dispose` would otherwise read mount-time values.

**The 3D column on the Variations tab (v0.1.2; round-trips via the field provider, working tree)**: the column is now contributed through `lib/variant-field-provider.ts` (`product3dVariantFieldProvider`) on shop-variations' `variant-field-provider` point, so **one object drives the admin grid, the CSV export and the CSV import**. `listColumns` always returns a single **3D Files** column (any variant can carry a model); `getValues` joins each child's model urls with `|` (one `getModelsForProducts` query for all children); `applyImportedRow` treats the sheet as truth - a url in the cell that is not yet attached is attached (`createModel`, filename off the url path, format via `formatFromFilename`, `size:0` and null media keys so a sheet-attached model never owns a stored blob it did not upload; a url with no 3D extension is skipped), and a model whose url has left the cell is removed via `deleteModelCascade`. **Import batching (v0.1.14):** the diff logic is unchanged, but the per-row `getModelsForProducts([childId])` read is gone - the provider now implements the optional `beginImport(productId, childIds)`, preloading every child's models in **one** query keyed by child, and `applyImportedRow` diffs against that ctx (a ctx miss - a variant created mid-import - reads as no models, so a new variant still gets its urls attached; with no ctx at all it falls back to the old per-row read). **Preview `rowChanged` (v0.1.59-to-be, working tree):** the attach/drop decision moved into a shared read-only `planRow` helper that both `applyImportedRow` and the new `rowChanged` call, so the google-sheet preview's count and the import's effect cannot drift; `rowChanged` is true when `planRow` would attach or drop any model, writes nothing, and ignores a non-3D url (nothing to render, not a change). Behaviour tested in `lib/variant-field-provider.test.ts`. Because the column lives in shop-variations' CSV, the Google Sheet sync carries a variant's 3D files with **no google-sheet change**. The grid cell is still `components/admin/Product3dVariantColumn.tsx`, a **client** component (only client references cross to shop-variations' client panel). Drop a model on a variant row, or click the `＋`; clicking it opens `components/admin/Model3dPickerModal.tsx` - the 3D answer to shop's image `MediaPickerModal`: browse the library's existing 3D files (media `type=other`, client-filtered to renderable extensions with `formatFromFilename`) and pick one, or upload a new file, both attaching to that variant. Dropping a file straight on the row still uploads it directly. Picking an existing file moves no bytes: the models route gained a third POST shape `{ mediaId, targetProductId }` (`attachExisting`) that reads the `Media` row and writes a `p3d_models` row pointing at the same object. Uploads and picks save immediately rather than via the editor's Save button, same reasoning as the 3D tab. The cells share one fetch through `lib/use-product-models.ts` (module-scoped store + `useSyncExternalStore`, keyed by the PARENT id): the route already returns the whole tree, so fifty variants must not mean fifty identical requests. The 3D views tab (`Product3dEditor`) opens the **same** `Model3dPickerModal` from its **Add a 3D model** button (target = its "Attach to" dropdown), so pick-existing and upload work identically on both surfaces from one component; the dropdown stays as the only way to reach the whole product rather than a variation. **Folder-aware browsing (working tree):** `Model3dPickerModal` now browses one folder at a time (breadcrumb + subfolder tiles, `folder=<id|root>&type=other` + the extension filter; search spans `folder=all`), opening at the product's `Shop/<category>/<product>/3d` folder via new module route `GET app/api/admin/products/[id]/models/folder` (gate `shop.products`, parent product id) - a look-only resolve through shop's `findProductMediaFolderId(id, {segments:['3d']})` that returns the deepest existing folder of that path and never creates one, unlike upload-time `resolve3dFolderId`.

**Routes**: `GET|POST /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/models` (list + record/upload; GET returns `{models, targets, options}` - each target carries its `valueIds`, and `options` is the product's `svr_options` + values, both for the brightness preview's option picker), `POST /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/models/upload-url` (**v0.1.2**, signs a direct-to-Worker target), `DELETE /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/models/[id]` (drops our row, the `Media` row and the blob - a 50 MB model left in the bucket is a bill - now via the shared `deleteModelCascade` in `lib/db/models.ts`, the same cascade the Google Sheet import calls when a variant's url leaves its cell). On all of them `id` is the PARENT; the target travels as `targetProductId` and is checked against the parent's tree via `isValidTarget` - without it an admin could hang a model off any product. Fabric configurator (v0.1.8): `GET|PUT /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/admin/products/[id]/fabric` (gated `shop.products`; GET returns `{config, options, attributes, models, settings}`, PUT validates + upserts) and the **public, unauthenticated** `GET /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/fabric/[child]?parent=&child=` (catalogue data, `Cache-Control: public, max-age=300`, resolves one variant child to a `FabricBundle` or `null`; errors return `null` so the stage falls back to the default model). Draco decoder assets (v0.1.57): the **public, unauthenticated** `GET /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/draco/[file]` serves the two files in `assets/draco` off an allowlist (see the Draco paragraph below). Background preload (v0.1.23): the **public, unauthenticated** `GET /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/swatches?parent=` returns `{urls: string[]}` - the distinct http(s) swatch texture urls the parent's fabric colour options could paint (from `getFabricConfig` + `listColourOptions`, deduped; `Cache-Control: public, max-age=300`, `{urls: []}` on any error or a non-fabric product). Scales with distinct colours, not variation count, which is why it is one endpoint rather than the storefront prefetching one `/fabric/[child]` bundle per child. Consumed by `lib/preload.ts` (`preloadProductAssets`), fired once from `Gallery3dThumbs` on `requestIdleCallback` (setTimeout fallback) after first paint and aborted on unmount: it warms the module-scoped model cache from `payload.items` (`prefetchModel`, no clone) and then the fabric texture cache from this endpoint's urls (`prefetchTexture`), both at concurrency 3, so a later variation switch clones/paints from memory instead of fetching. A real pick landing mid-preload shares the same cached promise (`load-model.ts`), so preloading never competes with the shopper.

**Upload path - direct to the Worker (v0.1.2, was broken before it)**: the browser PUTs the model straight to the media Worker and never sends the bytes through a serverless function. It **had** to change: the old form upload advertised 50 MB while Vercel 413s any body over ~4.5 MB *before* the handler runs, and that 413's body is not JSON - so `res.json()` threw and the editor's `?? 'Upload failed'` fallback was the only thing the admin ever saw. Every model worth selling died there. Two halves, mirroring core's `/api/admin/media/upload-url` + `/record`, but module-owned because only this module knows the folder and the ownership rule: `upload-url` gates on `shop.products`, resolves the folder, `buildKey`s and `signUploadToken`s; the JSON POST to `models` verifies that same token, reads the format from the **key** (the only claim the signature covers), and writes the `Media` + `p3d_models` rows. The folder is re-resolved server-side rather than carried back through the browser - the path is already baked into the signed key. `lib/upload-model-client.ts` owns the client half for both surfaces.

- **Fallbacks are honest, not silent.** `{ available: false }` (non-S3 provider, or no Worker URL) falls back to the multipart path and says up front that a model over `MAX_UPLOAD_MB` cannot get in on this install, naming R2/B2/S3 as the fix. A **415 from the Worker** means a Worker deployed before it learned about 3D keys: the client says "Settings → Media, deploy the Worker again" rather than showing a bare refusal. The Worker only picks up new source on redeploy, so **every existing install must redeploy before 3D uploads work**.
- The multipart POST on `models` survives as that fallback; `Product3dEditor` and the variant column both go through the client helper and never touch it directly.
- **Models are named after the product, not a nanoid (working tree, unreleased).** `lib/model-key.ts` `buildModelKey({provider, mimeType, filename, folderPath, parentProductId})` returns `{key, nameForKey, exactName}` and is used by **both** halves - `upload-url` takes the `key` (it has to be right first time, being what the token signs), the multipart fallback passes `nameForKey`/`exactName` to `uploadMedia` so it rebuilds the identical key. The basename is `<parent-product-slug>-<uploaded filename>` via core's `exactName` flag, matching how the shop names product images (`reorganiseProductMedia`), so a variation model files as `…/oslo-back-to-back-office-desks/3d/oslo-back-to-back-office-desks-120cm-natural-wood-2-person-1.glb` rather than `…/3d/<nanoid>-120cm-natural-wood-2-person-1.glb` - the folder used to be the only thing identifying the file. The **parent's** slug, not the variation's, for the same reason the folder is the parent's: a variation is a hidden child product whose name the owner is never shown, and the uploaded filename already says which variation it is. A filename already leading with the slug is not prefixed twice. **Exact-name keys overwrite in storage**, which is right for a re-filed product image and wrong for a model (two variations both given `model.glb` would share one object, so deleting either model would take the other's file), so a basename already held by a different `Media` row gets `-2`, `-3`… up to 50 attempts, then falls back to core's nanoid form rather than clobbering anything. Existing models keep their nanoid keys - nothing is renamed.

**Deleting a model only deletes a file it owns and nobody else wants (v0.1.32)**: `deleteModelCascade` used to drop the `Media` row and the blob unconditionally, on two assumptions that both turned out to be false. **One file, several rows:** the picker attaches an existing object by writing a second `p3d_models` row over it (`attachExisting`), so a model on the product and on one of its variations is two rows and one blob - deleting either row deleted the blob, and the survivor was left with a row, no file, no entry in the picker (which lists `Media`, not `p3d_models`) and a 404 on the shop. Confirmed on live Deskwell: `p3d_models.media_id` `cmrqo5kwx…` naming a `Media` row that no longer existed, its key 404ing at the Worker while a sibling GLB 200'd. **Not every file is ours:** a model picked from the library was the owner's file before this module pointed at it. So the cascade now deletes our row always, and the `Media` row + blob only when `owns_media` **and** no other `p3d_models` row names the same file - matched on `media_id` **or** `media_key` **or** `url`, the last because the Google Sheet import's rows carry no ids at all. `owns_media` is written true by both upload paths (`recordDirect`, `uploadThroughServer`), false by `attachExisting` and by the sheet import, and defaults false in the column and in `createModel`: a wrong false orphans a blob (a bill), a wrong true destroys a file (gone). `005_owns_media.sql` backfills true from `media_key LIKE '%/3d/%'`, since `resolve3dFolderId` is the only thing that ever wrote there. Covered by `lib/db/models.test.ts` - typecheck, lint and render all pass happily while this destroys data, so it needed a test.

**Format policy** (`lib/formats.ts`, the single source for server and browser): glb, gltf, obj, fbx, 3ds. **DWG and USDZ are rejected at upload**: DWG is proprietary AutoCAD with no JS loader (needs a paid Autodesk/ODA conversion service) and USDZ renders only via Apple AR Quick Look, so neither can drive an inline viewer - accepting them would store a file nothing on the page could draw. The **extension decides**, not the declared MIME: browsers report .glb as `application/octet-stream`, .fbx as an empty string. Safe because nothing server-side parses these files. Cap is `MAX_DIRECT_UPLOAD_BYTES` (50 MB) - taken from core rather than declared here, since the Worker is the real ceiling and promising more than it accepts is how the 50 MB became a lie in the first place.

**Why models are no longer `application/octet-stream`** (`mimeForFormat`, v0.1.2): core builds an object key's extension from the MIME type, so every model used to land under a `.octet-stream` key - and the Worker reads an upload's type back out of the key's extension, that being the only claim a client cannot forge. A key naming no type is a key the Worker refuses. The type here is not a description of the bytes so much as the thing that carries the extension. Core owns the map (`MODEL_EXTENSION_TYPES`); a format core has not heard of **throws** rather than falling back to a near-enough type.

**Visibility rule**: the pure `visibleItems()` in `lib/visible-items.ts` (10 tests in `lib/visible-items.test.ts`). A model on the product itself always shows; variation models are narrowed to the chosen variation, and before a choice is made all of them show *unless* the product has its own (which then stands in). Deduplicated **by url**, so a size run pointing every variation at one file is one thumbnail, not one per variation.

**One WebGL context for all thumbnails** (`lib/three/thumb-stage.ts`): a renderer per thumbnail hits the browser's ~8-16 live-context cap, past which the oldest are silently killed - blank thumbnails on someone else's machine. Instead one off-document `WebGLRenderer` is resized per thumbnail, rendered, and `drawImage`'d into that thumbnail's plain 2D canvas; one rAF loop drives the lot, skips off-screen thumbnails, and honours `prefers-reduced-motion`. The full viewer (`Viewer3d.tsx`) gets its own context - only one is ever on screen - with OrbitControls, bounded zoom, and auto-rotate that stops for good on first touch. `three` is **dynamically imported** throughout, so a product page with no model never carries it.

**A PBR scene needs an environment or every metal renders black (`addLights`, v0.1.4).** `addLights(scene, renderer)` now sets `scene.environment` from three's procedural `RoomEnvironment` via `PMREMGenerator`, and the light rig drops to ambient 0.6 / key 1.2 / fill 0.4 (was 2 / 2.5 / 1). **A `metallic: 1` material has NO diffuse term - a metal's colour is entirely what it reflects** - so lights alone give it nothing but a pinprick specular and it renders BLACK. Deskwell's Chiro Plus has a "Chrome polished" base (metallic 1, roughness 0) that came out black on the site and silver in every desktop viewer. Measured against the real module code: chrome base brightness **9.3 → 180.5**, and **the model file makes no difference either way** (9.3 with the original file, 9.3 with a repaired one). Every other viewer - macOS Quick Look, Blender, the pCon catalogue - supplies a default environment as a matter of course; we were the odd one out, and had been since v0.1.0. The old lights were cranked that high *because* they were carrying the scene alone, which also flooded out the shading a normal map needs to read as texture. The env map is generated **once per renderer** (`environments` WeakMap) because the thumbnail strip builds one scene per thumbnail off a single shared renderer; `disposeEnvironment(renderer)` must be called before disposing a renderer, since a GPU texture is not something the collector can see. **This was found only because a human noticed the chair base was the wrong colour and pushed back on two confident wrong diagnoses - it is the bug that the white-fabric and flat-weave symptoms were hiding behind.**

**The flat weave is a *separate*, file-side defect, and the env map does not fix it.** Measured: fabric weave detail 0.088 (original) → 0.096 (original + env map, still flat) → 0.478 (transform stripped). EGEO bakes correct tiling into the UVs (**texel density 0.9645 UV units per cm**, i.e. ~1 tile/cm ≈ a 10.4mm tile) and *then* also writes a `KHR_texture_transform` with `scale 33.33` that multiplies it again, driving the weave cell to 0.033mm - finer than a thread, so it mipmaps to flat grey. Per spec `scale` multiplies (verified against the Khronos README), so three is correct and the file is not. macOS ignores the extension and lands on the right answer by not looking. **Measure texel density per triangle, never the global UV span**: the mesh is unwrapped into islands spread across a 177-unit UV space, and reasoning from that span produced a confident, wrong answer (and a proposed "fix" that would have made each tile 34.5cm and *looked* plausible). Repaired per-file by stripping the transform, **not** in code - one supplier, one defect, and a throwaway script beats a permanent vendor quirk in a module others install.

**Spin the pivot, never the model (`frameModel`, v0.1.3).** `frameModel(scene, model)` now wraps the model in a `Group`, centres the model **inside** it, adds the pivot and **returns the pivot**; `thumb-stage.ts` turns `entry.pivot.rotation.y` and `Viewer3d`/`thumb-stage` `scene.remove(pivot)` on teardown. An `Object3D`'s matrix is `T * R * S`, so rotating the model spins it about **its own file's origin** and then translates - and a real product file's origin is nowhere near the object. Deskwell's Chiro Plus GLB (authored by EasternGraphics EGEO, node matrices carrying the showroom's coordinates) put its origin ~1.5 units off the chair, which after framing meant the model's centre swept a **4.79-unit** circle while the camera at distance 4 could see ±1.46: the thumbnail was empty most of the turn. Centring inside the pivot puts the axis through the model's middle - measured excursion **0.087 units**, i.e. framed throughout. The old code's `model.position.sub(centre)` was doing the *centring* correctly, which is why the static first frame always looked right and only the rotation gave it away.

**`connect-src` must allow `blob:` or every embedded texture dies** (core `proxy.ts`, v0.5.484 - see Sanctioned core diffs). A GLB carries its textures inside the file; three's `GLTFLoader` unpacks each to a `Blob`, takes a `URL.createObjectURL` on it, and **fetches it back** through `ImageBitmapLoader`. That fetch answers to **`connect-src`**, not `img-src`, however image-shaped its cargo - `img-src blob:` was already present and is not the directive being consulted. Without it the loader logs `Couldn't load texture blob:…`, leaves `material.map` null, and the mesh falls back to `baseColorFactor`, which glTF defaults to **white**. On the Chiro Plus only the fabric took its colour from a texture (every other material carried an explicit near-black factor), so a black chair rendered snow-white seats while its arms and base looked perfect - a symptom that reads like a broken model file and is not. Verified by A/B: same file, same code, `connect-src 'self'` → `map=null`, fabric `rgb(255,255,255)`; `connect-src 'self' blob:` → `map=LOADED (256x256)`, fabric `rgb(63,62,63)`. Safari <17 and Firefox <98 were never affected - `GLTFLoader` hands those a `TextureLoader` (an `<img>` load, so `img-src`) instead.

**Draco decompression (v0.1.57)** - `KHR_draco_mesh_compression` is the *other* compressed-glTF scheme and by a distance the more common one (Blender's "Compression" tick, gltf-pipeline's default, most "optimise my GLB" tools); meshopt was handled from v0.1.x, Draco was not, so `GLTFLoader` threw "No DRACOLoader instance provided" and the model never appeared. Registered unconditionally in `parseRaw`'s glb/gltf branch via a module-scoped, promise-held `getDracoLoader()` (one `DRACOLoader` per page, three's own guidance - each instance keeps its own worker pool with a compiled wasm copy each); it costs nothing on an uncompressed file because the decoder is fetched lazily on the first compressed primitive. **The decoder is a served file, not an import**: `DRACOLoader` fetches `draco_wasm_wrapper.js` as *text* (it builds a Web Worker out of the source) and `draco_decoder.wasm` as bytes, from a directory url - so a bundler-emitted hashed asset cannot satisfy it. Both are committed to `modules/product-3d-views-for-shop/assets/draco/` (copied verbatim from `three/examples/jsm/libs/draco/gltf/`, Apache-2.0) and served by `app/api/draco/[file]/route.ts` at `GET /api/m/product-3d-views-for-shop/draco/<file>` - public, unauthenticated, `Cache-Control: public, max-age=86400` (deliberately **not** `immutable`: the wrapper and the wasm are two halves of one decoder and a three upgrade replaces both, so a browser must not be able to hold one half across it). The filename is an **allowlist**, not a sanitised path. This is the first user of core's pre-existing generic `outputFileTracingIncludes` entry `'app/api/m/[module]/[...path]/route.ts': ['./modules/*/assets/**']` (no module named in core), which is what gets the files into the deployed function. **Required core diff**: `proxy.ts`'s `buildCsp()` gained `worker-src 'self' blob:` - `worker-src` falls back to `child-src` then `script-src`, and `script-src` has no `blob:`, so without it the decoder worker is blocked and every compressed model fails with a console error about a worker rather than about a model. **`requiresCoreVersion` raised to `0.5.612`** (the release that ships `worker-src`) in the same breath as this module's own release, for exactly that reason - a module shipped ahead of that core is a module whose compressed models fail on every install that has not caught up.

**KTX2 / Basis textures + parallel fetch (working tree, unreleased)** (`lib/three/load-model.ts`). Two changes to `parseRaw`, both about the time before a shopper sees anything.

- **`KHR_texture_basisu` now decodes.** The third compression a glTF can arrive under and the only one that compresses *textures*; like Draco and meshopt before it, `GLTFLoader` refused such a file outright ("setKTX2Loader must be called before loading KTX2 textures") and the model never appeared. `getKtx2Loader()` mirrors `getDracoLoader()` (module-scoped, promise-held, one worker pool per page). Nothing in Cactus writes KTX2 yet - this is for models a site owner optimised with gltfpack/gltf-transform themselves, and for the GPU-memory saving a compressed texture keeps at *draw* time (a 2048px map costs ~16 MB of VRAM as PNG/JPEG whatever its file size, a fraction of that as KTX2 - the difference between a phone rendering the page and running the tab out of memory).
  - `detectSupport(renderer)` needs a live WebGL context to ask which compressed formats the GPU takes. Contexts are capped ~16/page and the browser silently drops the **oldest** past that, so spending one here can kill the thumbnail strip's shared context. Hence `warmKtx2Support(renderer)`, exported and called by `Viewer3d` and `thumb-stage` as they build theirs: the check runs **immediately, while that renderer is demonstrably alive**, and no reference is retained (an earlier draft stored the renderer and would have queried a disposed context after unmount). A caller with none - `prefetchModel` at idle, no viewer mounted - gets a throwaway renderer built and disposed inside `getKtx2Loader`.
  - `tryKtx2Loader()` wraps it so registration can never be what stops a model loading: on a machine with no working WebGL, every ordinary GLB (nearly all of them) must still parse. Failure logs, clears the cached promise (a full context budget is a passing condition) and returns null. A file that genuinely carries KTX2 textures still fails, with GLTFLoader's own message - honest, since there is no rendering it there either way.
  - Assets: `assets/basis/basis_transcoder.{js,wasm}` copied verbatim from `three/examples/jsm/libs/basis/` (Apache-2.0, Binomial LLC), same served-file-not-import reasoning as Draco. **New shared `lib/decoder-assets.ts` `serveDecoderAsset(file)`** holds the allowlist (four filenames → content type + subdirectory) and is called by both `app/api/decoders/[file]/route.ts` (new, serves both decoders; `DECODER_PATH` in `load-model.ts` now points here) and `app/api/draco/[file]/route.ts`, **kept as a deprecated alias**: the decoder path is baked into a shopper's JS bundle, so someone who loaded a product page moments before the deploy would 404 on it. Deletable one release after `/decoders` ships.
- **The fetch starts before the loader imports resolve.** `loadAsync(url)` does the two in series - the dynamic import of the loader chunk (and, for glTF, the meshopt decoder) must resolve before a single byte of the model is requested. They are independent waits (a script on our origin vs a large file from the media Worker), so `parseRaw` now kicks off `fetchModelBytes(url)` first and hands the buffer to `parseAsync`/`parse` after. Worth the most on a slow mobile link, where the loader chunk's round trip is dead time the download now fills. Applies to all four formats (OBJ decodes the buffer as UTF-8 text; FBX/3DS take the ArrayBuffer). `LoaderUtils.extractUrlBase(url)` is passed as the path argument - `loadAsync` derived that itself, and a loader told nothing resolves relative references against the *page*, which for a `.gltf` pointing at a sibling `.bin` is a blank stage. Deliberately a plain `fetch`, not three's `FileLoader`, so no second copy of the raw bytes lands in three's cache (this module caches *parsed* models, the expensive half).

**The stage viewer renders on demand (v0.1.57)** (`Viewer3d.tsx`). The rAF loop stays; the `renderer.render` inside it is now earned. A still model - no idle turn, no animation, nobody touching it - was being redrawn 60fps to produce identical frames, paid for the whole time the page was open. A `needsRender` flag gates the draw; `controls.addEventListener('change', invalidate)` covers every camera move OrbitControls makes itself (drag, wheel, each auto-rotation step, the whole damped tail), and the things that move the picture *without* going through the camera each invalidate by hand: the spin-mode pivot (`onPointerMove`, the idle-spin and flick-glide branches), `resize` (a resized drawing buffer is cleared), the arrow keys, and - via a new `invalidateRef` nulled on dispose - the exposure effect and the fabric repaint effect. `controls.update()` and `mixer.update(clock.getDelta())` still run every frame regardless, or damping would never settle and a dropped frame would put an animation clip out of step with its own clock. **The thumbnail strip does the same** (`thumb-stage.ts`): `Entry.needsDraw`, and when `spin === 0` (reduced motion, or `thumbnailAutoRotate` off) each thumbnail is drawn once and left alone - its 2D canvas is still holding the picture. The tick reschedules only while `spin > 0 || pending`, so a still strip stops the loop entirely; `pending` deliberately stays true for an entry that is offscreen or zero-sized and has never been drawn, so it still gets its first frame when it scrolls in.

**Surviving a lost WebGL context (v0.1.57)** - the most common way a working viewer stops working, and it never happens on the machine of whoever built it (backgrounded tab on a phone, driver reset, another tab exhausting the context budget). Both surfaces `preventDefault()` on `webglcontextlost`, which is what entitles the browser to fire `webglcontextrestored` at all, and both rebuild rather than resume: a restored context hands back the ability to draw but not the geometry, textures or shaders that were on the dead one. **Stage** (`Viewer3d.tsx`): a `generation` state in the build effect's deps, bumped on restore *or* after `CONTEXT_RESTORE_TIMEOUT_MS` (1500ms) since some browsers never fire the restore; `key={generation}` on the `<canvas>` remounts the element so the new renderer gets a genuinely fresh context rather than inheriting the dead one. `carriedView` is captured by the outgoing dispose as usual, so the shopper's angle and zoom survive it. **Thumbnails** (`thumb-stage.ts` `watchForContextLoss`): same timer, disposes and rebuilds the shared renderer, and **must** re-point every entry's `scene.environment` at the new one - the PMREM studio is keyed to the renderer in a `WeakMap`, so a scene left holding the dead renderer's environment renders every metal surface black. That is what new `applyEnvironment(scene, renderer, intensity)` in `load-model.ts` is for (split out of `addLights`, which now calls it): the environment without the lights, since re-running `addLights` would add a second rig to every surviving scene. `rendererFailed` is explicitly cleared on this path - a lost context is not "this browser cannot do WebGL".

**Keyboard control of the stage (v0.1.57)** (`Viewer3d.tsx`). The canvas is `tabIndex={0}` with an `aria-label`; arrow keys turn/tilt, `+`/`=` and `-`/`_` zoom, `Home` resets. OrbitControls' own `listenToKeyEvents` is not used, twice over: its arrow keys **pan** rather than orbit, and it wants to listen on `window`, which would eat the arrow keys a shopper is scrolling the product page with. The maths is the public OrbitControls surface (`target`, `min/maxPolarAngle`, `min/maxDistance`) plus a local `Spherical`/`Vector3`, never a reach into its internals, and clamps to the same limits a drag obeys. Horizontal keys follow the drag's rule: in spin mode the **pivot** turns (camera azimuth is pinned, so the shadow stays anchored), otherwise the camera orbits. `Home` returns early before the shared `takeHold()` (which stops the idle motion and trips the touched/moved latches), or it would set `moved` straight back and leave the Reset button offering to undo nothing. Modifier guard is meta/ctrl/alt only - **not shift**, since `+` is shift-and-minus on most layouts and filtering it would have removed half the zoom. Which hint shows (`.p3d-hint-keys` vs `.p3d-hint-drag`) is decided by CSS `:focus-visible ~` sibling selectors rather than a React `onFocus`, because only `:focus-visible` knows whether the focus arrived by keyboard or by a mouse click - `onFocus` would have told someone mid-drag to try the arrow keys. The three duplicated inline style blocks (`Gallery3d.tsx`, `Product3dEditor.tsx`, `FabricConfigPanel.tsx`) all carry the focus ring (`--color-border-focus`, `outline-offset:-2px` since the canvas fills its box) and the hint rules. **No role is claimed** on the canvas: `img` would misdescribe something operable and `application` would swallow every key. The honest limit, documented rather than papered over: a screen reader in browse mode takes the arrow keys before the page sees them, so these serve sighted keyboard and alternative-input users.

**Material configurator (v0.1.8)** - named "Fabric configurator" in the admin until v0.1.29; the panel's user-facing copy now says **material** throughout (upholstery, wood, laminate, metal - anything the shopper chooses), while every stored name (`FabricConfig`, `p3d_fabric_configs`, `FabricConfigPanel`, `lib/fabric/*`) is unchanged. One model re-textured live from a shopper's variation choices, instead of a model file per variant. All diffs stay inside the module; `shop`, `shop-variations`, `product-attributes-for-shop` and core are untouched. Lights up only when a saved `p3d_fabric_configs` row (naming a default model) **and** the `svr_`/`pat_` tables are all present; otherwise the gallery behaves exactly as before.
- **Data reused, none added**: colour texture = `svr_option_values.swatch` (a full https url to the `.webp`); swatch size = `pat_product_values` → `pat_attribute_values.label` ("20x20cm"). No new column in shop-variations or product-attributes.
- **Config shape** (`FabricConfig`, `lib/db/fabric-config.ts`): `models: [{modelId, optionId, valueId}]` (structural option → model file, e.g. Headrest on/off), `defaultModelId`, `scaleAxis: 'height' | 'width'` (zod default `'height'` - which real dimension pins the model's scale; **one or the other, never both**, since a second measurement could only disagree with the first), `heightAttributeId` (the `pat_attributes` id whose per-variation value gives the model's REAL overall size in cm **along `scaleAxis`**, or `MANUAL_SIZE_ID` with the measurement typed into `heightManual`; still named for the height because that is what every pre-width config stored and renaming a stored key buys only a migration), `modelHeights: {modelId → bbox height in the model's OWN units}` and `modelWidths: {modelId → bbox X extent}` (both measured at config time, both written on every save whatever the axis, so switching axis re-scales on the spot instead of dropping to repeat 1 until someone presses Detect; `modelWidths` is empty on a pre-width config, which is harmless as such a config is on the height axis), `slots: [{materialName, colourOptionId, colourManual, sizeAttributeId, sizeManual, texelDensity, rotationDeg}]` (`texelDensity` = UV units per model-unit, also measured at config time). `materialName` is the exact glTF material name - the contract with the file. `colourOptionId` may hold the sentinel `MANUAL_COLOUR_ID` (`'__manual_colour'`, also from `lib/fabric/constants.ts`, deliberately a different value from `MANUAL_SIZE_ID` so the two can never be read for one another), in which case the part is painted the flat colour in `colourManual` rather than from a shopper's choice - `parseHexColour` (same file, shared by panel and resolver) normalises `#rrggbb`/`rrggbb`/`#rgb` to `#rrggbb` and returns null for anything else, and a slot whose colour will not parse is dropped rather than painted a guessed shade. `rotationDeg` turns that part's texture about the middle of its tile, added to whatever rotation the model's own map carried (ignored by a flat-colour part, which has no direction). Both zod-defaulted (`''`, `0`), so every saved config reads back unchanged. `sizeAttributeId` may hold the sentinel `MANUAL_SIZE_ID` (`'__manual'`, exported from `lib/fabric/constants.ts` - a leaf file precisely so the client panel does not import prisma via `lib/db/fabric-config.ts`), in which case the slot's swatch size is the hand-typed `sizeManual` string instead of a per-variation attribute value; it goes through the same `parseSwatchCm`, so "20cm"/"200mm"/"20" all read alike, and an empty one leaves the slot at repeat 1.
- **Scale is derived, not eyeballed (changed after v0.1.10).** The original build had a per-slot `uvSpanCm` "cm/tile" slider + a `defaultSwatchCm` fallback; both are **gone**. The model file carries geometry but not reliably its unit (mm vs metres), so one real dimension pins it: the **Overall Height or Overall Width attribute** (per variation, cm - whichever `scaleAxis` names) over the model's measured `modelHeights[id]` / `modelWidths[id]` gives cm-per-model-unit; the mesh's per-material `texelDensity` supplies the rest. `tileRepeat({realCm, modelUnits, texelDensity, swatchCm}) = realCm / (modelUnits · texelDensity · swatchCm)` (dimensionless, unit-tested - the axis does not appear in the formula, only the ratio, which is exactly why either dimension will do so long as both halves are taken along the same one; `resolveFabricForChild` picks the map and `composeFabricBundle` takes the resolved number); any term missing → repeat 1 (colour right, scale neutral - there is deliberately **no** default size, since size is a per-variation fact).
- **Resolver** (`lib/fabric/resolve.ts`): `to_regclass` probes `hasVariationsTables`/`hasAttributeTables` (30s cache, never imports the companion modules); `parseSwatchCm("20x20cm")=20` / `"137cm"=137` (first integer, v1 assumes square); pure `composeFabricBundle(config, selected, sizes, models)` + `tileRepeat` (unit-tested, 21 tests in `resolve.test.ts`, four of them covering the Manual sentinel on the per-slot size and on the overall height) do model selection + per-slot texture and true-scale repeat, skipping a slot whose swatch is not http; `resolveFabricForChild(childId, config)` does the `svr_`/`pat_` joins keyed by **child product id** (all shop's gallery contract hands us - the height attribute rides in the same `pat_product_values` query as the swatch sizes) and returns a `FabricBundle` (`{modelId, modelUrl, format, slots}`).
- **Payload/flow**: `P3dPayload` gains `fabric: FabricConfig | null` (set in `gallery-provider.ts` only when `defaultModelId` is present). `Gallery3d.tsx` collapses the configurator's models into a **single** synthetic thumbnail (`key: 'fabric-configurator'`, never stale); `FabricStage` fetches `/fabric/x?parent=&child=` on `activeProductId` change (cached by child id, derives the displayed bundle in render), renders one `Viewer3d` with the model url + paints.
- **Live re-texture** (`lib/three/load-model.ts` `applyFabricPaint`, `Viewer3d.tsx`): paints a named material's baseColor (`map`) only - normalMap/roughness untouched, so the model keeps its own relief. Textures cached by url (master, never disposed, ~48 colours bounded); each paint is a `clone()` so a viewer owns disposable per-slot tiling (`SRGBColorSpace`, `RepeatWrapping`, `flipY` copied from the existing map or `false` for glTF). A **colour** change repaints in place (second effect keyed on the slots' JSON signature - no context rebuild); a **headrest** change alters the model url and rebuilds through `build()`. A `Viewer3d` with no `fabric` prop behaves exactly as before.
- **Client mesh measurement** (`lib/three/load-model.ts`): `collectMaterialNamesFrom`, `measureModelHeight` (world-space Y extent, model units), `measureTexelDensity(model, name)` (area-weighted per-triangle √(ΣUVarea/Σworldarea), NOT the global UV span - the flat-weave-saga lesson; world-space 3D area so a node scale counts; raw UVs since the repeat we set replaces any `KHR_texture_transform`).
