The server never parses a GLB, so these run in the browser at config time and bake into the saved config.
- **Admin** (`components/admin/FabricConfigPanel.tsx`, mounted below the model list in `Product3dEditor` when the product has variations; no longer hides itself when no size attributes exist, since both measurements can be typed by hand): material names + per-material texel densities + per-model heights **and widths** are measured client-side whenever the configured-model set changes (and on a "Detect from model" button - one `loadModel` per file, both bbox extents off it); colour/size/height dropdowns fed from the admin GET (which also returns viewer `settings` for the preview). Name-matching pre-fills slots. **No** scale slider and **no** default-size field - the admin only picks the colour option, size attribute and one **Overall size** attribute. The **Overall size** section leads with a **Scale by** select bound to `scaleAxis` (Overall height / Overall width); the label and placeholder of the two fields beside it follow the axis, so the box never says "height" while a width is wanted. Width is the model's X extent as exported - deliberately not "whichever of X and Z is larger", which would scale a deep narrow cabinet by its depth without saying so. Both the per-slot **Size from** and the **Overall height/width from** dropdowns offer **Manual** below the attribute list; picking it reveals a free-text box bound to `sizeManual` / `heightManual` (for a finish whose repeat is the same across the whole range, or a product whose variations all stand the same height, where an attribute is pure admin overhead - and the only route at all on a site without product-attributes, which is why a new part defaults to Manual when the attribute list is empty). The per-slot **Colour from** dropdown offers **Manual** the same way: picking it swaps the Size-from/Size/Rotation fields for a native colour picker + hex box (both bound to `colourManual`) and the row's tag becomes "fixed colour" / "not a colour - use #rrggbb", since a flat colour has nothing to scale, measure or turn. Every texture-driven slot also carries a **Rotation** number box (degrees, step 15) bound to `rotationDeg`. A new part defaults to Manual colour when the product has no variation options at all. A rough colour/placement `Viewer3d` preview (scale approximate; true scale is per-variation). Saves via the admin PUT (own button), merging the measured densities into the slots at save.
- **A slot's colour may come from an ATTRIBUTE, not only a variation option (working tree, unreleased).** `pat_attribute_values.swatch` holds a picture url for an `IMAGE` attribute (product-attributes-for-shop v0.1.6), which is where a range's finishes often live when they are shop-wide vocabulary rather than one product's options - so `colourOptionId` now accepts a `pat_attributes` id, stored with the `ATTRIBUTE_COLOUR_PREFIX` (`'attr:'`, `lib/fabric/constants.ts`) because both sources are cuids out of different tables and a bare id would be ambiguous. `readColourSource(id)` is the one reader (`{kind:'manual'|'option'|'attribute'}`) shared by panel, resolver and swatch preloader; an unprefixed id is an option, so **every config saved before this reads back unchanged - no migration**. Resolver: the existing `pat_product_values` query now also selects `av."swatch"` (so `ChildSizeValue` gains an optional `swatch`) and an attribute-sourced slot reads its texture from the child's own attribute value. Admin GET returns a new `colourAttributes` array from `listColourAttributes()` (site-wide, only attributes with at least one non-empty swatch value, ids already prefixed); the panel renders **Variation options** and **Attributes** as two `<optgroup>`s and keeps a flattened `colourSources` for lookups/name-guessing. `/swatches` preloads both lists.
- **A hex swatch now paints flat rather than being skipped (working tree, unreleased).** Both modules store one visual per value in the same `swatch` column (hex for `SWATCH`, media url for `IMAGE`), and the resolver previously dropped any non-http swatch. A value whose swatch is a hex is now painted as a flat colour (`repeat 1`, `rotationDeg 0`, same path as `MANUAL_COLOUR_ID`); only a swatch that is neither a url nor a parseable hex drops the slot. Applies to option- and attribute-sourced slots alike, and the panel's preview does the same with the source's first hex value standing in for the shopper's choice. `resolve.test.ts` covers it (31 tests).
- **The swatch brings its own size, and "Colour from" is picture swatches or nothing (working tree, v0.1.49, unreleased).** The per-slot **Size from** dropdown and its Manual size box are **gone from the panel**. A material's picture and how big that material really is are one fact about one thing, so they now live together on the attribute value (product-attributes-for-shop `swatch_size`, its v0.1.14): pointing a part at a finish settles its scale along with its colour, and there is no second dropdown to keep in step. `ChildSizeValue` gains `swatchSize`; the child-values query selects `av."swatch_size"` behind a new `hasSwatchSizes()` probe (`information_schema` column check, 30s TTL beside the other probes) - and that query is now **one statement** with `assignment_id`/`swatch_size` selected as `NULL::text` where the companion module is too old, rather than a branch per combination. `composeFabricBundle` reads the size from the attribute value that supplied the swatch, falling back to the stored `sizeAttributeId`/`sizeManual` **only** when the swatch has none, so a config saved before this goes on scaling as it did; nothing writes those two fields any more and both are now zod-optional (`.default('')`). **`listColourAttributes` is narrowed to `control_type = 'IMAGE'`** and the panel's dropdown drops the "Variation options" optgroup entirely: only a picture swatch carries both halves (picture + size), and a colour-dot attribute or a variation option would paint at an unknown scale. A slot already pointing at a variation option keeps it - the panel offers the stored one back as a "(variation option)" entry so opening the panel cannot silently re-point a working product, and `colourSources` still includes options so the preview and the resolver both go on painting it. Three new cases in `resolve.test.ts` (37 tests): size read off the swatch, swatch size winning over a stored `sizeManual`, and a sizeless swatch leaving repeat 1.
- **An option-painted part is scaled by matching its picture (working tree, v0.1.50, unreleased).** v0.1.49 read the new `swatch_size` only where a slot pointed at an ATTRIBUTE, which missed the arrangement most live products actually use: **the finishes live in variation options**, whose values carry the picture but no size. Found on live Deskwell's Chiro Plus - `colourOptionId` on both slots is a bare `svr_options` id (Upholstery Colour / Back Colour), and its `sizeAttributeId` pointed at a `pat_attributes` row that **no longer exists**, so the legacy fallback resolved to nothing and every colour tiled at repeat 1 (a tile every ~0.93cm - the flat-grey mipmap symptom). `resolveFabricForChild` now also builds `swatchSizeByUrl` (every `pat_attribute_values` row with an http swatch and a non-empty `swatch_size`, keyed by the picture url, first row wins on a contradiction) and passes it to `composeFabricBundle` as an optional 6th argument. Lookup order per slot: the painted attribute value's own `swatchSize` → `swatchSizeByUrl[textureUrl]` → the legacy `sizeAttributeId`/`sizeManual`. **Matching on the picture is exactly as strong as the claim being made** - the size describes the photograph, so the same photograph in an option value and an attribute value is the same real material. Verified against live Deskwell: all 44 of that product's option values join 1:1 to an attribute value on `swatch`, with **zero** urls carrying two different sizes; resulting repeat 0.047 for a 20cm swatch (1 model unit ≈ 90.5cm), against 1.0 before. Three more cases in `resolve.test.ts` (40 tests), including two swatch sizes on one product - which a per-product size could not express at all. **A DB fix was considered and rejected**: re-pointing the config at the attribute would have painted nothing, since the variant children carry no `pat_product_values` for the colour attributes (only Overall Height).
- **Out of scope (v1)**: fabric↔leather (a material-*type* change, not baseColor), non-square swatches (parser takes the first number), independent U/V tiling. **Data-entry prerequisite**: swatch **size** and **overall height** attributes filled on all variant children; where missing, that slot stays at repeat 1 (colour applied, scale neutral) until filled.

**Known Limitations**: OBJ carries no materials (the `.mtl` sibling is never uploaded) so it renders plain white; a `.gltf` referencing external `.bin`/textures loads geometry only - GLB is the format to recommend and the editor says so. No settings tab. No reorder UI (models append). A model is not shown on product cards or in the cart, only on the product page. `loadModel`'s cache hands every caller `.clone(true)`, which **shares materials and textures** with the cached parse, so `disposeModel` on any one instance disposes them for all - benign today (three re-uploads from the surviving `ImageBitmap` on the next frame, confirmed by probe) but a real trap for anything that later assumes it owns its materials.

### Google Sheet Products for Shop

- Slug: `google-sheet-products-for-shop` (table prefix `gsp_`), repo (at release) `github.com/cactus-foundation-modules/google-sheet-products-for-shop`, manifest version **0.1.19** (0.1.8 was the resumable-Pull + Products-page-toolbar bump; 0.1.19 adds the Supplier Catalogues tab, working tree). `requiresCoreVersion` 0.5.486 (re-confirm at tag time). `requiresModules`: **`shop >= 0.1.91`** (raised from 0.1.68 for `listSupplierCatalogues`; 0.1.61 was the release that published the `shop.products-toolbar` extension point this module's dropdown needs) and `shop-variations >= 0.1.65` (a hard dependency - a shop-without-variations site cannot install this).
- **Status: built and green in the working tree; NOT yet registered in `modules.json` and NOT released.** No GitHub repo/tag exists yet, so registering it (or a repo-linked README/wiki push) is a release step, deliberately deferred. `modules.json` intentionally left untouched to avoid a shared-tree sweep pinning a non-existent tag into a deploy.
- A hand-synced Google Sheet mirror of the shop catalogue. Two human-pressed buttons: **Push** (DB → sheet) and **Pull** (sheet → DB, after a diff preview and confirm). No crons, no background polling. It is a transport adapter: it moves grids between Google and shop's existing CSV export/import functions and shop-variations' `exportVariationsCsv`/`importVariationsCsv`, and writes no product-field mapping of its own. Adds no columns to `shp_*`/`svr_*`. Because it round-trips whatever those CSVs name, the Variations tab **automatically** gained the variant **Image** and **3D Files** columns when shop-variations/product-3d-views added them (working tree) - no change here.

**Database** (table prefix `gsp_`)

- `gsp_connection` - singleton (`id` keyed `'singleton'` by every writer). Encrypted (`lib/crypto/secrets`) `oauth_client_id_encrypted`, `oauth_client_secret_encrypted`, `oauth_access_token_encrypted`, `oauth_refresh_token_encrypted`; `oauth_token_expires_at`, `google_account_email` (display only), `spreadsheet_id`, `spreadsheet_url`, `include_cost_price` (bool, default true), `last_push_at`, `last_pull_at`, `created_at`, `updated_at`.
- `gsp_sync_log` - one row per push/pull per tab. `direction` (PUSH|PULL), `tab` (PRODUCTS|VARIATIONS), `status` (COMPLETED|FAILED), `created_count`/`updated_count`/`skipped_count`/`archived_count`, `errors` (jsonb), `run_by` (admin user id, no FK), `created_at`. Index on `created_at DESC`. All three CHECK constraints idempotent (`DO $$ … duplicate_object`). No row-id mapping table by design: products match by `sku`, variants by parent slug + value-set. Backup round-trip re-run (real PASS, not skipped); schema-coverage backstop parses the migration - all column types (TEXT/BOOLEAN/TIMESTAMP(3)/INTEGER/JSONB) already supported, no sequences.
- `gsp_pull_job` (migration `002_pull_job.sql`) - one row per Pull, the resumable job the browser drives step by step. `status` (RUNNING|COMPLETED|FAILED|CANCELLED), `phase` (PRODUCTS|DELETIONS|VARIATIONS|DONE), `products_grid`/`variations_grid` (jsonb sheet snapshots, nulled once finished), `last_push_at` (deletion baseline captured at start), `shop_import_job_id` (the `shp_import_jobs` row that carries live products progress), `detected` (jsonb, the confirm dialog's headline counts, display-only), `products_total`/`variations_total`/`variations_done` (the last doubles as the resume cursor), accumulated `prod_*`/`var_*` counts, `prod_errors`/`var_errors` (jsonb), `error`, `run_by`, `created_at`/`updated_at`. Two CHECK constraints (status, phase) idempotent; index on `(status, created_at DESC)` for the "latest unfinished job" lookup. In `teardown`. Backup gate re-run for the new table: schema-coverage green, round-trip **real PASS (3/3)**.

**Permissions**: `googlesheets.manage` (single; gates the settings tab and every route).

**API Routes** (served through `/api/m/google-sheet-products-for-shop/admin/…`)

- `GET /oauth/google/start` - mints state (cookie `cactus_gsp_oauth_state`), returns the Google authorize URL (scope `openid email drive.file`, `access_type=offline` + `prompt=consent`).
- `GET /oauth/google/callback` - verifies state, exchanges the code, stores tokens + account email, redirects to `…/config?tab=google-sheet-products-for-shop`.
- `GET/PATCH /settings` - status booleans + display fields (never secrets) / save client id+secret (paired) and cost-price toggle.
- `POST /disconnect` - null the tokens + email (keeps client creds + spreadsheet).
- `POST /sheet` - create the workbook (idempotent: returns the existing one). `POST /reset` - create a fresh workbook and repoint (old one left in Drive, not deleted).
- `POST /push` - DB → sheet, products then variations then supplier catalogues, RAW writes. Returns `{ok, products, variations, supplierCatalogues, formulasKept}`. **Formula preservation** (`lib/push-grid.ts` + pure planner `lib/formula-preserve.ts`, tested in `lib/formula-preserve.test.ts`): each tab is read first with `readGridWithFormulas` (`spreadsheets.get?includeGridData=true&fields=sheets.data.rowData.values(userEnteredValue,effectiveValue)` - one call for both the formula text and its result), then written RAW as before, then the surviving formulas are put back with `writeFormulaRuns` (`values:batchUpdate`, `valueInputOption=USER_ENTERED`, contiguous cells grouped into runs). A formula survives only when **row index, column index and computed result are all unchanged**: written formula text does not shift its references the way a copy-paste would, so a preserved `=B5*1.2` in a moved row would point at the wrong product. Header comparison is prefix-based, so an owner's extra columns to the right do not block preservation; any header difference within the pushed width disables it wholesale. Numeric results compare with a 1e-9 *relative* tolerance (`=12.5*1.2` really is 15.000000000000002); text compares exactly with no numeric fallback (`"0100"` is not `100` in a barcode); an erroring formula is never preserved. `clearTab` is no longer used by Push - `clearRange` clears only rows the catalogue has given up (across the pushed columns only) and only columns it has given up that the tab **owns** (`ownsColumn`: `CSV_COLUMNS` for Products, the fixed names + `/^(Option|Value) \d+$/` for Variations). Known gap: a Variations column contributed by a variant-field provider module that has since been uninstalled has an unrecognisable label and is left behind as a stale column (Pull ignores unknown columns). Row identity for matching is SKU-then-slug (Products) and Variant SKU-then-(Parent Slug + option values) (Variations), the same fallbacks Pull matches on. **Overwrite guard**: before writing, reads the sheet's Drive `modifiedTime` (`getSheetModifiedTime` in `lib/sheets.ts`, `drive.file` scope covers metadata on the app's own file) and, unless the body carries `{force:true}`, 409s (`{error, needsConfirm:true, modifiedAt}`) when it is newer than `max(last_push_at, last_pull_at)` by more than a 120s clock-skew margin - i.e. the owner edited the sheet since Cactus last synced it. The toolbar turns that 409 into a `confirm()` and re-POSTs with `{force:true}`. The app's own syncs stamp their timestamps *after* their sheet writes, so they never trip it.
- `POST /pull` - **start a resumable Pull.** Reads+validates both tabs, snapshots the grids into a new `gsp_pull_job` row, creates the linked `shp_import_jobs` row, returns `{pullJobId, productsTotal, variationsTotal}` (202). No heavy work here, no `after()`. 409s (`{error, pullJobId}`) if an unfinished job already exists. Optional body `{detected}` (the preview summary, stored display-only).
- `POST /pull/step` `{pullJobId}` - run one bounded batch (`lib/pull-run.ts` `stepPullJob`) and return the live `PullStatus`. The browser loops this until `done`; a failed/errored step is **auto-retried by the browser loop** (up to 5 consecutive failures, backoff 2s..8s, counter reset whenever the phase/cursor advances) and reopening the modal onto an unfinished job auto-resumes - the Continue button is only the last resort once retries are exhausted. Phases: PRODUCTS (whole products CSV through `processImportJob`, one step) → DELETIONS (status pass + `planPullDeletions` + `applyProductDeletions`/`applyVariationDeletions`, one step) → VARIATIONS (60 rows/step via `importVariationsCsv`) → finalize (two `gsp_sync_log` rows + stamp last-pull + clear grids). Every phase idempotent, so a replay after a failure/closed tab is safe. A failed step marks the job FAILED with the cursor intact. **Steps are now serialised (2026-07-23):** `withPullStepLock` wraps the step in a `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` on `(0x67737001, hashtext(jobId))`, returning without running when another worker already holds it, so the browser's retry loop plus a reopened modal (or two tabs) cannot run two batches of the same job at once and double-apply a cursor. A transaction-scoped lock, deliberately, not a session-level one: a step killed at the module dispatcher's 60s ceiling takes its lock down with the request rather than stranding a lease, and it behaves correctly through connection pooling. The transaction's own `timeout` is therefore 60s (a step runs right up to the ceiling) with a 10s `maxWait` to get a pooled connection.
- `GET /pull/status?pullJobId=` - the live snapshot the progress UI polls (products-done read from the `shp_import_jobs` row during the PRODUCTS phase). With no id, returns the latest unfinished job (RUNNING|FAILED) for the toolbar's Continue prompt, or null.
- `POST /pull/cancel` `{pullJobId}` - mark an unfinished job CANCELLED (whatever batches landed stay; they were idempotent writes).
- `POST /pull/preview` - dry-run diff (creates/updates/rowErrors, `products.toDelete` list, `variations.toDelete` count, staleness), computed via the same `planPullDeletions`, writes nothing. Row validation rejects a **negative** price as well as a missing or non-numeric one (2026-07-23, matching shop's own `lib/import-engine.ts`) - `Number('-5')` is neither falsy nor NaN, so a minus sign in a sheet cell previously sailed through and created a product with a negative price. Variations "to update" is a **real field diff** (`variationRowChanged` in `lib/preview.ts` mirrors `upsertVariantForCombination`'s changed check + the importer's image compare, column-present-only); a matched row whose values are identical counts as nothing, so Push→Pull with no edits previews 0 updates instead of the whole catalogue. It **also asks each variant-field provider** (`resolveVariantFieldProviders(...).rowChanged`, preloaded per parent via `beginImport`) so a changed **3D Files** or **attribute** cell counts as an update too - previously the preview only diffed the seven built-in columns, so editing a provider column previewed "0 to update" while the Pull then applied it (the counts lied, the data still landed). Providers report changes read-only (they never create the attribute value a new label would need); a provider without `rowChanged` is simply invisible to the preview, as all were before.
- `GET /log` - recent `gsp_sync_log` rows.

**Supplier Catalogues tab (v0.1.19, working tree)** - a fourth workbook tab, `TAB.SUPPLIER_CATALOGUES = 'Supplier Catalogues'`, written by `lib/push-supplier-catalogues.ts` (`pushSupplierCataloguesTab`) at the end of a Push. **One-way**: Push writes it, Pull never reads it, and no `gsp_sync_log` row is written for it (the table's `tab` CHECK is `PRODUCTS|VARIATIONS` and this tab does not warrant a migration to widen it). Columns `Supplier | Status | Catalogue | Google Sheet URL`, one row per catalogue plus a catalogue-blank row for a supplier with none, sourced from shop's `listSupplierCatalogues()`. Goes through the same `pushGrid` as the other tabs purely for the **stale-row clear** - a deleted supplier or catalogue shortens the grid and the abandoned rows have to be cleared; row identity is `['Supplier','Catalogue']`, so a supplier with no catalogues forms no key and keeps no formulas. Workbooks created before the tab existed grow one on their next Push: `ensureSupplierCataloguesTab` (`lib/workbook.ts`) calls the new `addTab` (`lib/sheets.ts`, `batchUpdate.addSheet`, returns null when the title already exists) at index 2 and then applies the shared `headerFormattingRequests` (freeze/bold/protect/width, extracted from `createWorkbook` so creation and back-fill format identically). `TAB_ORDER` and the Read me both updated.

**Settings tab**: `google-sheet-products-for-shop` ("Google Sheet"), component `GoogleSheetSettingsTab`, permission `googlesheets.manage`. **Setup-only now** (Google connection, create/reset sheet, cost-price toggle); Push/Pull/Open/Logs moved to the Products page.
**Products-page toolbar**: `extensionPoints` entry `{ point: "shop.products-toolbar", id: "google-sheet-products-toolbar", permission: "googlesheets.manage", component: GoogleSheetProductsToolbar }` (`components/ProductsToolbar.tsx`) - a **Google Sheet ▾** dropdown (Open sheet / Push / Pull… / Sheet logs) rendered beside the Products header buttons, shown only once a sheet is connected. Pull opens the preview→confirm→live-progress→Continue modal; Sheet logs opens the Recent-syncs table as a modal. The point is published by shop (see Shop → `ProductsScreen.toolbarExtras`, resolved in `products/page.tsx`).
No nav entries, no Puck blocks, no public pages, no cron.

**Env vars**: `ENCRYPTION_KEY` (required, token encryption), `SITE_URL` (required, OAuth redirect URI).

**Key design points**: `drive.file` scope only (non-sensitive - no Google verification), which is why the module *creates* its own sheet rather than accepting a link. Owner registers their own Google Cloud OAuth client. The Testing-mode 7-day-refresh-token trap is surfaced inline in the settings tab and as a plain-English error on refresh failure (`GoogleAuthError`). Push builds the products grid directly (no CSV escaping, RAW write); pull converts the grid to import CSV with structural escaping only (no formula guard, so cells starting with `= + - @` aren't corrupted with a stray `'`). **Pull deletes on the sheet's say-so** (changed from the original archive-on-tick design): a product absent from the sheet is hard-deleted (cascading its variants); a variant absent from the sheet is pruned - partial (some rows removed) and full (a parent's whole block cleared) both handled. All deletion logic lives in one shared planner `lib/deletions.ts` (`planPullDeletions`), used by both the preview and the pull so their counts cannot diverge; execution helpers in `lib/delete-pass.ts` (`applyProductDeletions`/`applyVariationDeletions`, both `bulkDeleteProducts`). **Safety anchor**: only ever removes something whose `created_at <= last_push_at` - Push mirrors the whole catalogue, so anything created in the admin after the last push was never in the sheet and is spared; with no push on record, Pull deletes nothing. Uses shop `bulkDeleteProducts` and shop-variations `getEditorPayload` + `getProductIdsWithVariations` (the latter finds parents whose whole block was cleared). Order history survives deletion via `shp_order_items.product_id` ON DELETE SET NULL. Replaced files: `archive-pass.ts` and `reconcile-variations.ts` deleted; `pull-variations.ts` (create/update import) kept.

**Shop-side (Phase 0, in shop's own working tree, `shop` v0.1.55-to-be)**: three silent-data-loss bugs on a plain CSV export→import round trip, fixed in shop because they are shop's independently of this module. (1) `tax_class` was exported empty → import nulled every product's tax class; now exports the real code via new `getTaxClassCodesByIds` (`lib/db/tax-shipping.ts`). (2) media flattened to `IMAGE` and alt text dropped; now type-prefixed cells `TYPE:url` in `image_urls` with a new positionally-aligned `image_alt` column, backwards-compatible (un-prefixed → IMAGE), via `serializeMedia`/`parseMediaCells` (`lib/csv.ts`). (3) export clamped to 100 products (listProducts' public-list guard); now paginated via new `collectPaged` (clamp untouched). `CSV_COLUMNS` gains `image_alt`; `headerMatchesFormat`/new `missingFormatColumns` treat `image_alt` + `cost_price` as optional. Pure round-trip test `lib/csv-roundtrip.test.ts` (17 cases).

**The format now carries every owner-editable product field (working tree, shop + google-sheet-products-for-shop, unreleased).** `CSV_COLUMNS` was 24 columns and had drifted well behind `shp_products`, so the sheet (and the CSV) silently omitted `slug`, the dimensions, the digital-download rules, the pre-order fields and the related/upsell settings. Now 39 columns; everything added after the original 24 is in `OPTIONAL_CSV_COLUMNS`, so a pre-existing export still passes `headerMatchesFormat`. Deliberately still absent, and pinned by a test: id-shaped FKs (`digital_file_id`, `og_image_id`, `master_category_id`), derived counters (`pre_order_count`), and `catalogue_hidden` (shop-variations' own system state). Row-building moved to one place, new `modules/shop/lib/csv-rows.ts` (`buildProductCsvRows`), consumed by both the export route and the module's `push-products.ts` - the two hand-maintained copies are what let the drift happen. `import-engine.ts`: `ImportFields` is now `Partial`, and a field is only written when the CSV **carries its column** (absent = leave alone, present-but-blank = clear); row identity prefers the `slug` cell over `slugify(name)`; a slug edit renames the product (uniqueness excludes itself); `status` is now honoured on update as well as create (blank/invalid leaves it alone). `createProduct` gained the columns it accepted but never inserted (`weight_unit`, `meta_title`, `meta_description`, dimensions, download rules, pre-order, related/upsell) - imported products were losing them until re-saved in the admin. Module side: `NUMERIC_CSV_COLUMNS`/`BOOLEAN_CSV_COLUMNS` drive `typedCell` in `push-products.ts` so prices/stock/weights land as real numbers rather than text cells Sheets shows as `'100` (sku/barcode stay text - leading zeros); `writeGrid` takes `CellValue = string | number | boolean`; `sheetProductIdentity` (`deletions.ts`) counts **both** the row's slug cell and `slugify(name)`, without which a name edit would have made the Pull delete the product; `preview.ts` matches on the same identity and diffs the new fields; `related_mode`/`upsell_mode` gained sheet dropdowns and the Read me tab a slug section.

### Twilio

Module `twilio` (repo `cactus-foundation-modules/twilio`), tablePrefix `tw_`, v0.1.22 (requiresCoreVersion 0.5.303 - needs the `admins.account-section` extension point). Twilio account integration: call forwarding for the account's incoming numbers, per-number voicemail with opening hours, per-number call/message logs with recording playback, two-leg click-to-dial, and SMS delivery of login codes (via the core `smsProviders` hook, see Scripts above). No Puck blocks, no public pages. One cron job as of v0.1.22 (`/api/m/twilio/cron/retention`, `20 4 * * *`).

- Env vars (manifest `requiredEnvVars`, all `required: false` so install isn't blocked before configuration): `TWILIO_HOME_REGION`, `TWILIO_ACCOUNT_SID`, `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN`, `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN_US1`, `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN_IE1`, `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN_AU1`. Managed through the module's core settings tab via `/api/admin/env` (module-declared keys are allowlisted generically). `TWILIO_HOME_REGION` + `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN_US1` added in v0.1.13 - see home-region note below. `TWILIO_PHONE_NUMBER` removed in v0.1.4 - the from-number is now picked from the account's numbers and stored in `tw_site_numbers` (default SMS number), not typed as an env var. `TWILIO_REGION` existed only in v0.1.7 and is gone - see below.
- **Per-number regions / v0.1.8.** Twilio Regions (`us1`/`ie1`/`au1`) are isolated instances for data residency. Three facts shape the implementation, each learned the hard way in v0.1.7:
  1. **Numbers are a single global pool** administered from the account's home Region, and each number's *inbound processing Region* is set **per number** via the Routes API. **v0.1.13:** the home Region is no longer hardcoded to `us1` - `getHomeRegion()` reads `TWILIO_HOME_REGION` (default `us1`, validated against `TWILIO_REGIONS`). This exists because a Twilio account is itself provisioned in one Region for data residency: an Ireland-homed account is `ie1`, and `api.twilio.com` (us1) **rejects its credentials outright with error 20003 "Authenticate"** - the exact symptom that drove this change. `listIncomingNumbers`, `setNumberVoiceUrl`, the Routes API and the connection test all run against the home Region.
  2. **A token is only valid in the Region it was created in** ("Any given Auth token or API key is only valid for the Twilio Region in which it was created"), so each Region needs its own token. Account SID is shared. `regionTokenEnvVar(region)` (v0.1.13, replaced the static `REGION_TOKEN_ENV` map) returns `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN` for the **home** Region and `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN_<REGION>` (e.g. `_IE1`, `_AU1`, `_US1`) for every other - so a `us1` home yields the historical layout unchanged. `MissingRegionTokenError` (exported, message shown to admins verbatim) names the missing var. Failed REST calls now throw `TwilioApiError` (exported) carrying region/host/HTTP-status/Twilio-code, and its `message` (shown verbatim on the settings tab) names the likely cause for code 20003.
  3. **FQDNs are `{product}.{edge}.{region}.twilio.com`** - the bare `{product}.{region}` form (`api.ie1.twilio.com`) was switched off 28 April 2026 and omitting the edge silently routes back to `us1`. `REGION_EDGE` = `ie1`→`dublin`, `au1`→`sydney`; `regionHost(product, region)` builds it, with `us1` staying the plain `api.twilio.com`/`routes.twilio.com`.
  Records follow the routing (a call to an `ie1`-routed number is processed and stored in `ie1` only, and querying `us1` returns an empty list rather than an error), so **every log/recording/outbound path resolves the number's Region first**: `listCallsForNumber`/`listMessagesForNumber`/`fetchRecordingAudio`/`placeCall`/`sendSms` all take a `TwilioRegion`. `lib/twilio.ts` exports `TWILIO_REGIONS`, `TWILIO_REGION_LABELS`, `getHomeRegion`, `isTwilioRegion`, `isRegionConfigured`, `getConfiguredRegions`, `regionTokenEnvVar`, `getNumberRegion`, `setNumberRegion`, `TwilioApiError`, `MissingRegionTokenError` (v0.1.13 renamed the `HOME_REGION` const to the `getHomeRegion()` function - all default `region` params now default to `getHomeRegion()`). Routing uses **Routes API v3** (`GET`/`POST https://routes.twilio.com/v3/PhoneNumbers/{e164}`, form params `voiceRegion`/`messagingRegion`, response `voice_region`/`messaging_region`) run against the home Region's host + credentials, covering both voice and messaging - so reading/writing routing needs only the home token. This module keeps voice and messaging together (one Region per number); `getNumberRegion` reads `voice_region` and treats unset/unknown as the home Region. Twilio takes up to 5 minutes to apply a routing change. `validateTwilioSignature` now tries **every configured Region's token** (no early exit) because a webhook is signed with the token of the Region that processed the call - a number routed to `ie1` arrives signed with the `ie1` token.
- Permission: `twilio.manage` (settings tab, nav entry, admin API routes).
- Manifest surfaces: `settingsTabs` → `TwilioSettingsTab` (account-country picker + credentials + per-region tokens for the non-home regions + connection status + phone-numbers picker: lists the account's incoming numbers with a Texts/No-texts capability badge, add/remove to site, per-number Country select, radio choosing the default send-texts-from number - SMS-capable numbers only); `navEntries` → `/m/twilio` admin page; `smsProviders` → `lib/sms-provider.ts` `twilioSmsProvider` (`isConfigured` = credentials set AND an SMS-capable default site number selected, `sendSms` = `sendSiteSms`); `extensionPoints` → `members.account-section` `TwilioMemberSmsSection` (member SMS 2FA enrolment card) + `admins.account-section` `TwilioAdminSmsSection` (same card for the signed-in admin on the admin account page, no permission - self-service).
- Tables: `tw_forwarding_rules` (`phone_sid` unique, `phone_number`, `forward_to`, `enabled`, `greeting_message`, `greeting_voice`, `record_calls`, `show_called_number` - added by module migration `002_show_called_number.sql`; plus the voicemail columns added by `004_voicemail.sql` and also in `001_initial.sql` for fresh installs: `voicemail_enabled` BOOLEAN DEFAULT false, `ring_timeout` INTEGER DEFAULT 20 (seconds the forwarded leg rings first, form-bounded 5-120), `voicemail_greeting` TEXT, `voicemail_voice` TEXT, `closed_voicemail_greeting` TEXT DEFAULT `''` (added by module migration `006_closed_voicemail_greeting.sql` and also in `001_initial.sql` for fresh installs - said instead of `voicemail_greeting` when the call arrives outside opening hours; empty = say the usual greeting; only the words differ, the voice and recording behaviour are shared), `business_hours` JSONB DEFAULT `'[]'` - a JSON array of `{day, closed, open, close}` entries, day 0 = Sunday, `"HH:MM"` in the site timezone, empty array = no schedule so the number is available at any hour; plus the three v0.1.20 uploaded-audio columns from `007_greeting_audio.sql`, also in `001_initial.sql`: `greeting_audio_media_id` / `voicemail_audio_media_id` / `closed_voicemail_audio_media_id` TEXT DEFAULT `''` - core media library ids of MP3/WAV files played with `<Play>` instead of the `<Say>` pair when set), `tw_site_numbers` (account numbers added to the site: `phone_sid` unique, `phone_number`, `friendly_name`, `sms_capable`, `is_default_sms` with a partial unique index enforcing at most one default, `region` TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT `'us1'` - the number's Twilio Region mirrored from the Routes API, added by module migration `003_number_regions.sql` and also in `001_initial.sql` for fresh installs; metadata refreshed from Twilio on every listing, rows pruned when the number leaves the account, first/oldest SMS-capable number auto-promoted to default), `tw_verification_codes` (enrolment codes: `subject_type` 'user'|'member' + `subject_id` unique pair, `phone_encrypted`, sha256 `code_hash`, 5 attempts, 10-min TTL) and `tw_voicemails` (one row per voicemail message, added by module migration `005_voicemails.sql` and also in `001_initial.sql` for fresh installs: PK `recording_sid` (Twilio's `RE...` SID, so a repeated callback is an idempotent no-op), `call_sid` (indexed - the call log matches on it), `from_number`/`to_number` E.164, `duration_seconds`, `created_at`. Twilio's own `Recordings.json` listing cannot distinguish a voicemail from a recorded forwarded call, so this table is the record of which recordings are voicemails; only messages left from v0.1.10 on have a row). All four in `teardown`.
- API routes (all under `/api/m/twilio/`): `admin/status` (GET, connection test **per Region** - every Region is tested separately via `fetchAccountName(region)` since a working main token says nothing about the Ireland one; returns `regions: [{ region, configured, connected, accountName?, error? }]` plus `configuredRegions`, and `fromNumber` = the default SMS site number or ''), `admin/numbers` (GET, Twilio incoming numbers merged with forwarding rules; v0.1.19 also each number's `region` via `resolveNumberRegion`, null on lookup failure, feeding the region-aware voice pickers), `admin/site-numbers` (GET account numbers merged with site state + capability flags + each on-site number's `region` and a `regionTokenMissing` flag so the UI can warn before the admin finds an empty log, also syncs stored metadata; POST `{ action: 'add'|'remove'|'set-default-sms'|'set-region', sid, region? }` - add validates the sid against the live account listing, takes the capability flag from Twilio, never the client, and adopts the number's existing routing rather than assuming `us1`; set-default-sms rejects non-SMS-capable numbers; set-region goes through `setSiteNumberRegion`, which writes to Twilio **first** so a rejected change never leaves the stored value lying), `admin/forwarding` (PUT, upserts rule and points the number's `VoiceUrl` at the voice webhook when forwarding **or voicemail** is on / clears it only when both are off - voicemail on its own is reason enough to keep answering calls; validates `ringTimeout` 5-120, both voices against the curated list, and the `businessHours` array through `parseBusinessHours`, rejecting a malformed schedule rather than storing one that would silently mis-route calls), `admin/greeting-preview` (POST, places an outbound call via `placeCall` from the row's Twilio number to a given number that `<Say>`s the unsaved greeting/voice - test-email-style preview; v0.1.19: applies `voiceForRegion` so the preview says exactly what a live call would), `admin/greeting-audio` (POST multipart `file`, v0.1.20 - files an MP3/WAV into the media library's root `twilio` folder on the active provider and returns `{ mediaId, name }` for the forwarding form to store; `twilio.manage` + configured-media-provider gated, browser mime aliases normalised via `GREETING_AUDIO_TYPES`, 10 MB cap), `public/audio/[mediaId]` (GET, v0.1.20, unauthenticated - Twilio's `<Play>` and the admin's inline player fetch greeting bytes here; 404s any id not referenced by a rule's audio columns so it cannot proxy arbitrary media, reads by provider+key via `downloadMedia`, serves the stored mimeType with `nosniff` + 5-min cache), `admin/sms-2fa` (GET/POST send|verify/DELETE - self-service admin enrolment, writes `User.smsOtpPhoneEncrypted`; gated on `isSmsReady`, not just credentials), `member/sms-2fa` (same shape for members, upserts the `SMS` `MemberTwoFactor` row, same `isSmsReady` gate), `admin/calls` (GET `?number=`, recent calls to and from that number - two filtered `Calls.json` listings merged newest-first, completed recording SIDs attached from an account-wide `Recordings.json` listing keyed by call SID; each call also carries `voicemailSids`, the subset of its recording SIDs that `filterVoicemailSids` (`lib/voicemail-log.ts`) finds in `tw_voicemails`, so the UI can badge voicemail messages apart from recorded calls), `admin/messages` (GET `?number=`, same merge shape over `Messages.json`), `admin/recordings/[sid]` (GET `?number=`, streams the recording MP3 through the site with the Region's Basic auth so the browser never sees credentials; validates the `RE...` SID shape, `Cache-Control: private`. The `number` query is load-bearing, not decorative: a recording lives in the Region its call was processed in and the SID alone doesn't say which, so `TwilioAdminScreen`'s `CallLogCard` passes the active tab's number and the route resolves the Region from it - guess wrong and it reads as "Recording not found"), `admin/make-call` (POST `{ fromNumber, to, callMeAt }` - two-leg click-to-dial: validates both numbers E.164 and `fromNumber` against the live account listing (must be voice-capable), places a call to the admin from that number whose TwiML `<Gather>`s one digit then hits `webhooks/outbound-connect?to=`), `webhooks/outbound-connect` (POST, X-Twilio-Signature-validated over the full URL including the query string; on any digit returns `<Dial callerId="<From = the site's Twilio number>">` to the E.164 `to`, else `<Hangup/>`), `webhooks/voice` (POST, X-Twilio-Signature-validated, returns TwiML: optional `<Say voice="...">` greeting (XML-escaped `greeting_message`, voice from the curated `lib/voices.ts` list, both rule voices passed through `voiceForRegion` for the number's Region first - v0.1.19, us1-only Generative voices are Twilio 13520 elsewhere) then `<Dial>` to the enabled rule's target - with `record="record-from-answer-dual"` when `record_calls`, and `callerId="<called number>"` when `show_called_number` so the forwarded leg shows the site's Twilio number instead of the caller's. Looks the rule up with `getRuleForNumber` (**not** enabled-only: a number can have forwarding off and voicemail on, and the webhook still has to answer). When the call can't be forwarded - forwarding off, no valid E.164 target, or `isRuleOpenNow` says the number is shut - it returns the voicemail TwiML if `voicemail_enabled`, else `<Reject/>`; that path deliberately skips the call greeting, which promises a forward that isn't going to happen. With voicemail on, the `<Dial>` also carries `timeout="<ring_timeout>"` and `action="<voicemail webhook>"`; with voicemail off it keeps Twilio's default timeout and no action, so the pre-v0.1.9 behaviour is byte-identical), `webhooks/voicemail` (POST, X-Twilio-Signature-validated **over the full URL including the query string**, the follow-on step for a dialled call. Twilio hits it twice over a voicemail's life and **the URL says which stage it is** - the `<Record>`'s `action` carries `?stage=recording` (`RECORDING_STAGE`/`voicemailRecordingUrl()`), the `<Dial>`'s doesn't. All the branching is the pure `planVoicemailRequest` (`lib/voicemail.ts`), the route only does the IO: `log-message` → `recordVoicemail` then `<Hangup/>`, `take-message` → re-read the rule (hang up if voicemail was switched off mid-call), swap a us-only voicemail voice via `voiceForRegion` (v0.1.19) and return `voicemailTwiml`, `hangup` → `<Hangup/>`. The hangup on the recording stage is **load-bearing**, since a `<Record>` left without an explicit `action` re-requests the current document's URL and would loop. The `recordVoicemail` call is wrapped in a try/catch that only logs: the caller has already rung off and Twilio would just retry the webhook, so a DB failure must not turn a recorded message into an error. The recording SID comes from `RecordingSid`, falling back to the trailing `RE...` segment of `RecordingUrl`).
- `lib/twilio.ts` is a dependency-free REST client (Basic auth, `AbortSignal.timeout(15s)`), Region-aware throughout - every account-API call takes an optional `region` defaulting to `HOME_REGION`: `sendSms(to, body, from, region)`, `listIncomingNumbers` (global pool, always `us1`; includes `smsCapable`/`voiceCapable` from Twilio's capability flags), `listCallsForNumber(number, region, limit)`/`listMessagesForNumber(number, region, limit)` (To+From listings merged newest-first, capped 50; calls carry completed recording SIDs from a Region-wide `Recordings.json` listing), `fetchRecordingAudio(sid, region)` (30s timeout), `setNumberVoiceUrl` (account-level, `us1`), `fetchAccountName(region)` (doubles as the per-Region credential check), `placeCall(to, from, twiml, region)`, `getNumberRegion`/`setNumberRegion` (Routes v3, `us1`), `escapeXml`, `validateTwilioSignature` (HMAC-SHA1, timing-safe, tried against every configured Region's token). `lib/numbers.ts` owns the site-number store: `getSiteNumbers`, `addSiteNumber` (takes `region`), `removeSiteNumber`, `setDefaultSmsNumber`, `setSiteNumberRegion` (Twilio first, then the row), `syncSiteNumbers` (refreshes name/capability **and** re-reads each on-site number's Region from the Routes API in parallel, so a change made directly in the Twilio console is picked up; a failed lookup keeps the stored value rather than wiping it), `resolveNumberRegion` (stored value for on-site numbers, live Routes lookup otherwise - the admin log tabs cover every account number, not just on-site ones, so the fallback is load-bearing), `getDefaultSmsNumber` (now returns `{ phoneNumber, region } | null`), `isSmsReady`, `sendSiteSms` (throws when no text-enabled number is selected; sends through the default number's own Region).
- **Voicemail / v0.1.9.** Per number: switch voicemail on, set how long the forward-to number rings before it takes over (`ring_timeout`), write its own greeting with its own voice (separate from the forwarding notice - reuses `admin/greeting-preview` unchanged for the "call me to hear it" button, since that route already takes an arbitrary message + voice), and optionally restrict the number to opening hours. Recordings need **no new storage**: `<Record>` attaches to the call SID, and `listCallsForNumber` already merges a Region-wide `Recordings.json` listing keyed by call SID, so voicemails appear in the existing call log player for free. Max message length is a fixed `MAX_VOICEMAIL_SECONDS = 120` in `lib/voicemail.ts`, not a setting. `lib/voicemail.ts` holds the shared `<Say>`+`<Record>` builder, `voicemailUrl()`/`voicemailRecordingUrl()`, the `planVoicemailRequest` planner and its constants, used by both the voice and voicemail webhooks; an empty greeting falls back to a stock line so voicemail-on-with-no-message still works. `lib/voicemail-log.ts` owns the `tw_voicemails` store and the notification: `recordVoicemail` (idempotent `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` + `upsertAlert`), `filterVoicemailSids` (the call log's SIDs that are voicemails).
- **Voicemail marking + admin notification / v0.1.10.** The one thing Twilio's flat `Recordings.json` listing can't tell you is whether a recording is a voicemail message or a recorded forwarded call - both are just recordings against a call SID. The distinction only exists at the moment the voicemail `<Record>` finishes, a request `webhooks/voicemail` already handles, so that stage now writes a `tw_voicemails` row (`recordVoicemail` in `lib/voicemail-log.ts`) and raises an admin notification via the core `upsertAlert` (`lib/notifications/alerts.ts`, `type:'message'`, `dedupeKey` `twilio-voicemail:<recordingSid>` so each message rings the bell once and reading one doesn't hide the next, `link:'/m/twilio'`, title `New voicemail from <caller>` with a withheld/anonymous From shown as "a withheld number"). The call log API marks the voicemails among a page's recordings (`filterVoicemailSids`, an `IN (...)` over the page's SIDs rather than listing the table) and `CallLogCard` shows a **Voicemail** badge (`--color-primary` outline) beside those recordings' Listen buttons. Recordings made before v0.1.10 have no row and read as ordinary recordings - the log isn't back-filled because Twilio never knew the difference either. Migration `005_voicemails.sql` (mirrored into `001_initial.sql`); `tw_voicemails` added to `teardown`. Backup round-trip re-run green (3/3).
- **Voicemail marking: two false-positive fixes / v0.1.11.** v0.1.10 decided "this is the recording stage" by looking for `RecordingSid`/`RecordingUrl` in the payload. Both halves of that were wrong. (1) **A `<Dial record="...">` sends `RecordingUrl` to its own `action` URL** (Twilio documents it as included "only if record is set on `<Dial>`"; `RecordingSid`/`RecordingDuration` are not sent there, only to a `recordingStatusCallback`) - so on a `record_calls` number every answered forwarded call's dial callback read as a finished voicemail, tagging the *conversation's* recording as a voicemail and ringing the admin's bell for it. The stage is now stated on the URL instead of inferred: `voicemailRecordingUrl()` puts `?stage=recording` on the `<Record>`'s action and the route matches on that (signature validation now covers `request.nextUrl.search`, as `webhooks/outbound-connect` already did). Branch order matters - the dial stage is checked by `DialCallStatus`, which every dial callback carries, so a recorded-but-unanswered dial still reaches voicemail instead of having its recording params swallow the message. (2) **Twilio saves silent recordings by default** ("By default, silent recordings are saved by Twilio"), so a caller who rings off at the beep still produces one; `trim-silence` shrinks it to ~0-1s rather than to nothing. New `MIN_VOICEMAIL_SECONDS = 2` (a named constant beside `MAX_VOICEMAIL_SECONDS`, not a setting): a shorter recording is a hang-up, gets no row and no notification. That is deliberately the cheap direction to be wrong in - an unlogged recording still sits in the call log with its Listen button, it just isn't announced as a message. The decision logic moved into the pure `planVoicemailRequest(req): {action:'log-message'|'take-message'|'hangup'}` in `lib/voicemail.ts`, covered by `lib/voicemail.test.ts` (13 tests, incl. both regressions above and the no-stage-marker in-flight-across-a-deploy case, which hangs up rather than looping). No schema change.
- `lib/business-hours.ts` - opening-hours type, validator (`parseBusinessHours`), `defaultBusinessHours()` (Mon-Fri 09:00-17:00), `MIN_RING_TIMEOUT`/`MAX_RING_TIMEOUT` (5/120) and the pure `isOpenAt(hours, timezone, at)`. **Deliberately free of DB imports** so the admin form can share the type, the validator and the defaults; the `SiteConfig.timezone` lookup that feeds it lives in `forwarding.ts` (`isRuleOpenNow`), which is server-only. Semantics, all covered by `lib/business-hours.test.ts` (16 tests): empty schedule = always open (so every pre-v0.1.9 rule behaves exactly as before); the clock is read in the site timezone via `Intl.DateTimeFormat` with `hourCycle: 'h23'` (`hour12: false` emits `24` for midnight on some ICU builds); an unknown timezone falls back to UTC rather than throwing mid-call; closing time is exclusive; a window whose close is earlier than its open runs **overnight** and belongs to the day it starts on (a Monday 18:00-02:00 window still counts at 01:00 Tuesday, and does not spill out of a day marked closed); `open == close` is a zero-length window = shut (use the Closed toggle); and a day **missing** from an otherwise-populated schedule is treated as unrestricted, not closed - an absent rule should never be the thing that stops a call getting through. The admin form always writes all seven days.
- Admin page `/m/twilio` (`TwilioAdminScreen`): one core `TabStrip` tab per account number (label `phoneNumber · friendlyName`, logs lazy-loaded per tab, Refresh button in the strip's trailing slot), each tab holding a "Make a call" card (number to call + "your phone" input remembered in localStorage `twilio-call-me-at`, hits `admin/make-call`), a call log table (when/direction/from/to/status/length + a Listen button per completed recording swapping to an inline `<audio controls autoPlay>` on the `admin/recordings/[sid]` proxy, with a **Voicemail** badge beside recordings that are voicemail messages) and a message log table (when/direction/from/to/status/body). Forwarding configuration moved to the Settings Twilio tab in v0.1.6: `TwilioForwardingSection` (rendered by `TwilioSettingsTab` below the phone-numbers picker once connected) keeps the per-number rows - forward-to, on/off, greeting textarea (max 500 chars), voice `<select>` (optgroups from `lib/voices.ts` `TWILIO_VOICES` - Basic/Polly Standard/Neural/Generative; server validates via `isValidVoice`; v0.1.19 `VoicePicker` takes the number's `region` and disables us-only Generative voices off-us1, noting the substitute callers actually hear), record-calls checkbox (recordings playable from the Twilio page's call log), show-this-number-as-caller-ID checkbox (with a you-won't-see-who-rang note), "Call me to preview" (shown when a greeting is typed: number input + button hitting `admin/greeting-preview`). The admin's own SMS login-code card moved off this `twilio.manage`-gated page to the admin account page via `admins.account-section` (`TwilioAdminSmsSection`, wrapping the shared `SmsTwoFactorCard` also used by the member section) so every admin can enrol, not just Twilio managers.

- **Settings redesign + call features / v0.1.22.** `TwilioSettingsTab` was one endless scroll (credentials card, phone-numbers card, then the whole per-number forwarding form stacked for every number). It is now five core `TabStrip` sub-tabs, shop-settings style: **Account** (country picker, Account SID, per-region tokens, connection status, and the new Test connection button; the four-step set-up walk-through collapses into a `<details>` once connected), **Phone numbers** (unchanged picker), **Call handling** (`TwilioForwardingSection`), **Texting** (which number texts go out from + Send a test text), **Alerts & data** (the new `tw_settings` row). `TwilioForwardingSection` itself now edits **one number at a time**, picked from a nested `TabStrip` (shown only when the account has more than one number), with the controls grouped under Forwarding / Missed calls / Voicemail / Opening hours headings and a per-number "Unsaved changes" marker (`dirtySids`) so switching numbers never silently loses edits. Nine features landed with it:
  1. **Test connection** - `admin/test-connection` (POST `{ homeRegion, accountSid, tokens }`) calls the new `testCredentials(region, accountSid, authToken)` in `lib/twilio.ts`, which takes credentials as arguments instead of reading the env, so **typed-but-unsaved** values can be checked before the save-and-redeploy round trip. Blank fields fall back to the saved env values; every region with a token in play is tested separately.
  2. **Voicemail + missed-call email alerts** - `lib/notify.ts` `sendVoicemailEmail`/`sendMissedCallEmail`, gated on the `tw_settings` toggles + a `notify_email` address, sent through the core `sendEmail`. Both link to `/{adminPath}/m/twilio` (admin path read from `SiteConfig`). All failures are logged, never thrown: the call itself went fine and Twilio must not be told otherwise. The voicemail email only fires on the request that actually inserted the row (`$executeRaw` rowcount), so a repeated callback cannot double-send.
  3. **Auto-text on missed call** - per number (`missed_call_sms_enabled`/`missed_call_sms_message`, 320 chars, stock line when empty). `sendMissedCallText` sends from the called number where it is SMS-capable, else the site default sender. Withheld callers are skipped - there is nowhere to text.
  4. **Holiday dates** - per number `holiday_dates` JSONB, an array of `"YYYY-MM-DD"`. `parseHolidayDates` (same reject-don't-guess contract as `parseBusinessHours`, sorts + dedupes) and the pure `isHolidayOn(dates, timezone, at)` in `lib/business-hours.ts`, matched on the calendar date **in the site timezone** (`Intl.DateTimeFormat('en-CA')`, same UTC fallback as `clockIn`). `isRuleOpenNow` checks holidays before the weekly schedule; a holiday closes the whole day regardless of hours.
  5. **Send a test text** - `admin/test-sms` (POST `{ to }`) sends one fixed test message through `sendSiteSms`, proving credentials + number + region without going near a sign-in code.
  6. **Voicemail transcription** - per number `transcribe_voicemail` adds `transcribe="true" transcribeCallback=...` to the voicemail `<Record>`; the new `webhooks/transcription` route (signature-validated, returns 204) files the text onto `tw_voicemails.transcription_text`/`transcription_status` via `recordTranscription`. `admin/calls` returns a `transcriptions` map per call and `CallLogCard` prints the words (or "on its way" / "could not make out") under the Listen button. Twilio only transcribes 2-120s recordings, which is exactly the `MIN`/`MAX_VOICEMAIL_SECONDS` window already enforced.
  7. **Anonymous callers** - per number `anonymous_callers` `'allow'|'voicemail'|'reject'`. The voice webhook treats a non-E.164 `From` (or Twilio's `+266696687` ANONYMOUS marker) as withheld: reject outright, force the voicemail path, or ring through as before (the default, so nothing changes for existing rules).
  8. **Retention** - `tw_settings.retention_days` (0 = forever, the default and the historical behaviour; ceiling `MAX_RETENTION_DAYS` 3650). `lib/retention.ts` `runRetentionSweep` lists recordings older than the cutoff **per configured region** (`listRecordingSidsBefore`), deletes each (`deleteRecording`), then prunes `tw_voicemails` rows by `created_at`. One page (400) per region per night, so a backlog drains over successive runs rather than holding the cron open. Driven by `cron/retention` on the standard `CRON_SECRET` bearer check.
  9. **Sequential ring** - per number `forward_to_second`. The voice webhook's `<Dial>` now gets its action URL whenever there is anything to do after an unanswered ring (voicemail, a second number, an auto-text, or an email alert). `planVoicemailRequest` takes a second argument `{ hasSecondLeg }` and can return the new `dial-second` action; the second leg's own `<Dial>` carries `?leg=2` (`SECOND_LEG`/`secondLegUrl()`) so it cannot loop - same URL-marker trick as `RECORDING_STAGE`, and for the same reason (the two dial callbacks are otherwise indistinguishable). `take-message` is now the single point where a call is known to be definitively missed, so the auto-text and email alert hang off it and fire exactly once.
  10. **Bank-holiday import** (added same release, after the nine above). `lib/holidays.ts` + `admin/holidays` (GET): with no `region` param it returns the picker's own country options (single source of truth for the list); with one it returns that country's public holidays **for the twelve months starting today** - `fetchHolidayWindow(region, from)`, `from` inclusive / `to` exclusive, where `from` is `todayIn(await getSiteTimezone())`. A rolling window, not a calendar year: a calendar year is the wrong window for eleven months of the year (an October import would offer ten months of dates that had already been and none of the spring ones). The window straddles two calendar years so both are fetched - one cached document read twice for gov.uk, two parallel requests for Nager - then filtered by ISO string compare (ISO dates sort correctly as strings, so no parsing). `oneYearOn` builds the end bound through `Date.UTC`, which rolls a 29 February start to 1 March rather than producing a date that does not exist. Five regions: England and Wales / Scotland / Northern Ireland from **gov.uk's own `bank-holidays.json`** (authoritative, one document covering ~2019-2028, filtered by division and year), Republic of Ireland and United States from **Nager.Date** (`/api/v3/PublicHolidays/{year}/{code}`, `global !== false` only so a US state-only holiday cannot shut a line three thousand miles away). Results are deduped by date, sorted, and cached a day (`next: { revalidate: 86400 }`). Nothing is stored by this route - `HolidayImporter` in `TwilioForwardingSection` shows the list with already-added dates ticked-and-disabled, the rest pre-ticked, and the admin adds what they want. A missing gov.uk division **throws** rather than returning `[]`: gov.uk always publishes all three, so absence means the feed changed shape, and an empty list would read as "no bank holidays that year". `getSiteTimezone` is now exported from `lib/forwarding.ts` for the route's use. `lib/holidays.test.ts` (26 tests, `fetch` stubbed) covers both payload shapes, the division/year slicing, the nationwide filter, dedupe, name fallbacks, both failure modes, `todayIn`/`oneYearOn` (leap day included), and the window boundaries - inclusive start, exclusive end, and the two-year merge.
  Schema: module migration `008_call_features_and_settings.sql` (mirrored into `001_initial.sql` for fresh installs) adds the six `tw_forwarding_rules` columns, two `tw_voicemails` transcription columns, and the new singleton `tw_settings` table (`notify_voicemail_email`, `notify_missed_call_email`, `notify_email`, `retention_days`), added to `teardown`. New lib files: `lib/settings.ts` (`getTwilioSettings`/`updateTwilioSettings`, `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`, `MAX_RETENTION_DAYS`), `lib/notify.ts`, `lib/retention.ts`. New API routes: `admin/settings` (GET/PUT - rejects an alert toggle with no address rather than letting it silently do nothing), `admin/test-connection`, `admin/test-sms`, `cron/retention`, `webhooks/transcription`. `getForwardingRules`/`getRuleForNumber` moved to `$queryRawUnsafe` with a shared `RULE_COLUMNS` constant (column list only, no interpolated values). Tests: `voicemail.test.ts` gains the second-leg and transcription cases, `business-hours.test.ts` gains `parseHolidayDates`/`isHolidayOn`.

### Gemini Watermark Remover

Module `gemini-watermark-remover` (tablePrefix `gwr_`, v0.1.7, requiresCoreVersion 0.5.346). Locates the Google Gemini watermark and **erases it by reverse alpha-blend at a pixel-verified candidate position**, saving the cleaned result into a dedicated root `gemini-processed` folder in the core media library under its original filename. No database tables (the `gwr_` prefix is reserved but unused), no Puck blocks, no public pages, no cron, no settings tab. Declares no permissions of its own - reuses the core `media.upload` permission.

- **Why the v0.1.6 rewrite (drops MI-GAN):** v0.1.3-0.1.5 erased the mark with client-side MI-GAN inpainting, but MI-GAN *hallucinates* the hole from its surroundings, so when the sparkle sits on a sharp geometric line (e.g. a desk edge) it smears the edge into a blur. Root cause of the earlier "reverse-blend leaves residual" belief was actually the library's **adaptive detector drifting off the mark** (picking an 80px box above the true 96px mark on a 2816x1536 image), so the reverse-blend was applied at the wrong place. Fix: skip the adaptive detector for placement entirely - reverse-blend at the exact catalog position (`detectWatermarkConfig`+`calculateWatermarkPosition`) with the matching embedded alpha map. Reverse-blend reconstructs the true underlying pixels (edges intact) and never smears; worst case on a non-catalog size is a faint leftover, not a destructive smear.
- **Why the v0.1.7 rewrite (pixel-verified placement):** the v0.1.6 blind catalog erase backfired when Gemini shipped a second geometry for the same size. 2752x1536 exports now carry the mark 192px from the corner (`alphaVariant '20260520'`, weaker blend curve) while the catalog still answers 64px - so v0.1.6 left the real mark AND burnt a black sparkle where it reverse-blended clean pixels (reverse-blend on unmarked pixels = over-subtraction = dark stamp). v0.1.7 never erases blind: it builds candidate boxes (library's own `meta.position` pick, catalog position, 192px new-margin variant), scores each by Pearson correlation between the alpha map and box luminance (real mark ≥ ~0.25, unmarked texture ≤ ~0.17, threshold 0.2), then picks the blend curve by trial erase on a copy (lowest leftover |correlation| wins; the wrong curve leaves 0.4+, the right one ~0). Two rejection gates fall back to the server pipeline instead of touching pixels: presence below threshold (`unlocated`), or best trial residual ≥ 0.3 / ≥ the presence score (erase would burn rather than clean, seen on scaled non-official-size exports).
- **Processing is all client-side** (kills the old >4MB lossy pre-upload re-encode and upload-cap failures). `components/admin/WatermarkRemoverScreen.tsx`: `createImageBitmap` at full res → `detectWatermark` (canvas) → if a box is found, `eraseWatermark` (reverse-blend, no ONNX) → encode under the 4MB cap (output only) → POST with `mode=save-cleaned`. Any browser-path failure falls through to `mode=server-fallback`.
- `lib/detect.ts` - `detectWatermark(canvas, rgba)` calls `removeWatermarkFromImage` for the `meta.applied` yes/no gate **and** takes its `meta.position`/`meta.config` as a candidate, alongside the catalog answer and the 192px new-margin variant. Candidates are deduped, bounds-checked, presence-scored against the pristine pixels, and the winner's blend curve is picked by trial erase (see v0.1.7 note above). Returns `{found:true, box, alphaKey}`, `{found:false, unlocated:false}` (genuinely clean), or `{found:false, unlocated:true}` (mark exists but no safe local erase → caller uses server fallback). `residualVisibility.visible` is unreliable both ways, so it is not used.
- `lib/erase.ts` - `eraseWatermark(rgba,imgW,box,alphaKey)`: pure reverse alpha-blend (`original = (watermarked - a*logo)/(1-a)`), constants copied verbatim from the library's `blendModes.js`. Fetches the embedded alpha map via a cached `WatermarkEngine` (no network, no ONNX). Only pixels the alpha map actually tinted are touched. Also exports the verification maths: `scoreSparklePresence(rgba,imgW,box,alphaKey)` (Pearson correlation between alpha-map magnitude and box luminance over signal pixels) and `pickAlphaMap(rgba,imgW,box,keys)` (trial erase per candidate map on a copied patch, returns the key with the lowest leftover |correlation| plus that residual).
- `lib/remove.ts` - server-fallback reverse-blend wrapper (library `/node` path, unchanged maths), returns `residualVisible` from `meta.detection.residualVisibility.visible`. `lib/pilio-gwr.d.ts` - ambient types for `/node` + `/browser` entry points (`getAlphaMap` widened to accept variant-key strings like `'96-20260520'`).
- API route `POST /api/m/gemini-watermark-remover/remove` (`app/api/remove/route.ts`) - session + `media.upload` gated, media provider required (503 otherwise), multipart `file` (PNG/JPEG/WebP) + `mode`. `save-cleaned`: skip removal, `validateUpload`→`uploadMedia`→`saveMediaRecord`, return `{ status:'erased', media }` 201. `server-fallback`: run reverse-blend; no watermark → `{ status:'clean', reason }` 200 (saves nothing); else save + `{ status: residualVisible ? 'partial' : 'removed', media }` 201. **Honesty gate: never returns a clean `removed` when residual is still visible.**
- Core deps: `@pilio/gemini-watermark-remover` (MIT), `sharp` `^0.34.5` (used by the server fallback). **`onnxruntime-web` was dropped from core `package.json`** (2026-07-14): MI-GAN was its only consumer, and the ONNX runtime the browser actually executes is vendored inside `@pilio/gemini-watermark-remover`'s own bundle. It was 132MB of `node_modules` - roughly half the 290MB Vercel build cache - contributing nothing to any bundle. The About-dialog credit for ONNX Runtime (`lib/about/credits.ts`) stays: the runtime still runs in the browser, just via the vendored copy. The `next.config.ts` `outputFileTracingIncludes[...] = ['./modules/*/assets/**']` glob now matches no module (kept: module-name-agnostic, future-proof).
- Admin page `/m/gemini-watermark-remover` (`app/cactus-admin/gemini-watermark-remover/page.tsx`, `media.upload` gated). `navEntries` → a plain ungrouped sidebar link. Outcome list statuses: erased / removed / partial / clean / error.
- Shipped as `cactus-foundation-modules/gemini-watermark-remover` (registered in `modules.json`; bump the tag pin at release), listed in the core README's Available modules, wiki page at `wiki/Gemini-Watermark-Remover.md`.

### Ultimate SEO

Module `ultimate-seo` (repo `cactus-foundation-modules/ultimate-seo`), tablePrefix `seo_`, v0.1.0 (requiresCoreVersion 0.5.436). The SEO command centre: unified content inventory (core InfoPages + gazette posts + shop products + directory entries when those modules are installed, detected live from the `Module` table - never a hard import), a ~20-rule on-page analyser with 0-100 scoring and one-click fixes for core pages, a live HTTP crawl audit (manual + weekly cron), admin-managed robots disallow rules and extra sitemap entries (served through the standard `lib/robots.ts`/`lib/sitemap.ts` module hooks), and two Puck blocks for JSON-LD structured data. Zero core changes - integration is entirely existing hook mechanisms.

- Permissions: `seo.view` (dashboard/pages/audit read + run analyser), `seo.manage` (apply fixes, run audits, robots/sitemap rules, settings).
- Manifest surfaces: `navGroupLabel: "SEO"` with 4 `navEntries` (`/m/ultimate-seo` Dashboard, `/m/ultimate-seo/pages`, `/m/ultimate-seo/audit`, `/m/ultimate-seo/indexing`); `settingsTabs` → `ultimate-seo` "SEO" tab (`UltimateSeoSettingsTab`); `puckBlocks` → `SeoStructuredData` (Organisation/LocalBusiness/WebSite/custom JSON-LD `<script type="application/ld+json">` in a zero-height wrapper; editor-only `resolveData` pre-fills org fields from saved settings; same sync component both paths so editor/RSC parity is exact) + `SeoFaq` (visible `<details>` accordion + FAQPage JSON-LD); `cronJobs` → `/api/m/ultimate-seo/cron/audit` weekly (`0 4 * * 1`, `CRON_SECRET` bearer).
- Tables (`migrations/001_initial.sql`, all idempotent, all in `teardown`): `seo_settings` (singleton: `organization`/`social`/`targets` jsonb), `seo_page_meta` (per-entity focus keyword + latest analysis, UNIQUE(`entity_type`,`entity_id`); entity types `core-page`/`gazette-post`/`shop-product`/`directory-entry`, no FKs - source tables may not exist on a given install), `seo_audit_runs` + `seo_audit_issues` (FK CASCADE, severity error/warning/notice), `seo_robots_rules`, `seo_sitemap_entries` (NUMERIC priority - Decimal at read time, normalised in the API layer).
- API routes (all `/api/m/ultimate-seo/`, session + permission gated via `lib/auth.ts` `requireSeoPermission`): `admin/overview` GET (dashboard aggregates + hideFromCrawlers/siteStatus), `admin/pages` GET (inventory joined with `seo_page_meta`), `admin/pages/analyze` POST (runs analyser, persists, returns checks + a description suggestion drafted from page copy), `admin/pages/apply` POST (core pages only: writes `InfoPage.title`/`metaDescription` columns AND mirrors into `builderData`/`publishedData` `root.props` so the Puck editor and the next publish don't revert the fix; re-analyses in the same request), `admin/settings` GET/PUT (module settings + takes over `SiteConfig.hideFromCrawlers`), `admin/robots` GET/POST + `admin/robots/[id]` DELETE, `admin/sitemap` GET/POST + `admin/sitemap/[id]` DELETE, `admin/audit` GET/POST (POST 409s if a run younger than 10 min is still `running`), `admin/audit/[id]` GET (run + issues), `cron/audit` GET.
- `lib/`: `analyze.ts` (pure rule engine: title/desc length + uniqueness, slug hygiene, H1 count, content depth, image alts, internal links, focus-keyword title/desc/slug/density checks, readability, published status; score = pass 1 / warn 0.5 / fail 0 over check count), `content.ts` (generic Puck-data text extraction - block-palette-agnostic traversal, HTML stripping, heading/link/image-alt harvesting), `inventory.ts` (source collectors behind `Promise.allSettled` so a half-installed module can't 500 the screen), `run-analysis.ts` (entity loaders incl. gazette `builder_data`, shop `description` HTML, directory `description`), `apply.ts` (core-page write-through), `audit.ts` (crawler: URL list from live `/sitemap.xml` with inventory fallback, concurrency 4, 45s time budget → `partial` status, 10s per-fetch timeout, jsdom parse; checks HTTP status, title, meta description, noindex, H1s, img alts, OG tags, canonical, thin content, response time), `sitemap.ts`/`robots.ts` (the standard module hooks serving the admin-managed rows), `settings.ts` (singleton normalise/save), `db.ts` (raw SQL accessors), `auth.ts`, `types.ts`.
- Admin pages (`app/cactus-admin/ultimate-seo/…`): Dashboard (stat cards, hidden-from-crawlers warning banner, quick wins deep-linking `?focus=type:id`, recent audits), Pages (filterable/searchable table + detail side panel: SERP preview, focus keyword, analyse, inline title/description editing with Use-suggestion for core pages, deep links `/m/gazette/posts/:id` / `/m/shop/products/:id` / `/m/directory/entries/:id` for module content), Site audit (run list, expandable per-run issue tables), Sitemap & robots (both rule CRUDs + links to live `/sitemap.xml` `/robots.txt`).
- Module-to-module isolation: reads other modules' tables for analysis only; never writes them, never adds UI to their screens. One-click apply is core-`InfoPage`-only by design.
- Shipped as `cactus-foundation-modules/ultimate-seo`, listed in the core README's Available modules, wiki page at `wiki/Ultimate-SEO.md`.
